Seeing him, the Blessed One descended from his walk and sat down on a prepared seat. Then the clansman Yasa, not far from the Blessed One, uttered this exclamation: “Afflicted, sirs! Beset, sirs!” Then the Blessed One said to the clansman Yasa: “Here, Yasa, there is no affliction, here there is no besetment. Come, Yasa, sit down; I will teach you the Dhamma.” Then the clansman Yasa, thinking, “Here indeed is no affliction, here is no besetment,” joyful and uplifted, removed his golden sandals and approached the Blessed One. Having approached, he paid homage to the Blessed One and sat down to one side. As the clansman Yasa was sitting to one side, the Blessed One gave him a progressive talk, that is to say, a talk on generosity, a talk on virtue, a talk on heaven; he revealed the danger, degradation, and defilement of sensual pleasures and the benefit of renunciation. When the Blessed One knew that Yasa's mind was fit, pliable, unobscured, uplifted, and clear, then he revealed the teaching unique to the Buddhas: suffering, its origin, its cessation, and the path. Just as a clean cloth, free from stains, would perfectly absorb dye, even so, while sitting in that very seat, there arose in the clansman Yasa the stainless, immaculate Eye of Dhamma: “Whatever is subject to origination is all subject to cessation.”

27. Atha kho yasassa kulaputtassa mātā pāsādaṃ abhiruhitvā yasaṃ kulaputtaṃ apassantī yena seṭṭhi gahapati tenupasaṅkami, upasaṅkamitvā seṭṭhiṃ gahapatiṃ etadavoca – ‘‘putto te, gahapati, yaso na dissatī’’ti. Atha kho seṭṭhi gahapati catuddisā assadūte uyyojetvā sāmaṃyeva yena isipatanaṃ migadāyo tenupasaṅkami. Addasā kho seṭṭhi gahapati suvaṇṇapādukānaṃ nikkhepaṃ, disvāna taṃyeva anugamāsi [anugamā (sī. syā.)]. Addasā kho bhagavā seṭṭhiṃ gahapatiṃ dūratova āgacchantaṃ, disvāna bhagavato etadahosi – ‘‘yaṃnūnāhaṃ tathārūpaṃ iddhābhisaṅkhāraṃ abhisaṅkhareyyaṃ yathā seṭṭhi gahapati idha nisinno idha nisinnaṃ yasaṃ kulaputtaṃ na passeyyā’’ti. Atha kho bhagavā tathārūpaṃ iddhābhisaṅkhāraṃ abhisaṅkharesi. Atha kho seṭṭhi gahapati yena bhagavā tenupasaṅkami, upasaṅkamitvā bhagavantaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘api, bhante, bhagavā yasaṃ kulaputtaṃ passeyyā’’ti? Tena hi, gahapati, nisīda, appeva nāma idha nisinno idha nisinnaṃ yasaṃ kulaputtaṃ passeyyāsīti. Atha kho seṭṭhi gahapati – idheva kirāhaṃ nisinno idha nisinnaṃ yasaṃ kulaputtaṃ passissāmīti haṭṭho udaggo bhagavantaṃ abhivādetvā ekamantaṃ nisīdi. Ekamantaṃ nisinnassa kho seṭṭhissa gahapatissa bhagavā anupubbiṃ kathaṃ kathesi, seyyathidaṃ – dānakathaṃ sīlakathaṃ saggakathaṃ, kāmānaṃ ādīnavaṃ okāraṃ saṃkilesaṃ, nekkhamme ānisaṃsaṃ pakāsesi. Yadā bhagavā aññāsi seṭṭhiṃ gahapatiṃ kallacittaṃ, muducittaṃ, vinīvaraṇacittaṃ, udaggacittaṃ, pasannacittaṃ, atha yā buddhānaṃ sāmukkaṃsikā dhammadesanā, taṃ pakāsesi – dukkhaṃ, samudayaṃ, nirodhaṃ, maggaṃ. Seyyathāpi nāma suddhaṃ vatthaṃ apagatakāḷakaṃ sammadeva rajanaṃ paṭiggaṇheyya evameva seṭṭhissa gahapatissa tasmiṃyeva āsane virajaṃ vītamalaṃ dhammacakkhuṃ udapādi – yaṃ kiñci samudayadhammaṃ, sabbaṃ taṃ nirodhadhammanti. Atha kho seṭṭhi gahapati diṭṭhadhammo pattadhammo viditadhammo pariyogāḷhadhammo tiṇṇavicikiccho vigatakathaṃkatho vesārajjappatto aparappaccayo satthusāsane bhagavantaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘abhikkantaṃ, bhante, abhikkantaṃ, bhante, seyyathāpi, bhante, nikkujjitaṃ [nikujjitaṃ (ka.)] vā ukkujjeyya, paṭicchannaṃ vā vivareyya, mūḷhassa vā maggaṃ ācikkheyya, andhakāre vā telapajjotaṃ dhāreyya – cakkhumanto rūpāni dakkhantīti – evamevaṃ bhagavatā anekapariyāyena dhammo pakāsito. Esāhaṃ, bhante, bhagavantaṃ saraṇaṃ gacchāmi, dhammañca, bhikkhusaṅghañca. Upāsakaṃ maṃ bhagavā dhāretu ajjatagge pāṇupetaṃ saraṇaṃ gata’’nti. Sova loke paṭhamaṃ upāsako ahosi tevāciko.

27.Then Yasa's mother, having ascended to the palace and not seeing the clansman Yasa, approached the wealthy householder and said, 'Householder, your son Yasa is not to be seen.' Then the wealthy householder dispatched messengers in the four directions and himself went to the Isipatana Deer Park. The wealthy householder saw the place where the golden sandals were deposited, and following them, went along that very path. The Blessed One saw the wealthy householder approaching from afar and thought: 'What if I were to exert such an act of psychic power that the wealthy householder, sitting here, would not see the clansman Yasa sitting here?' Then the Blessed One exerted such an act of psychic power. Then the wealthy householder approached the Blessed One and said, 'Venerable sir, has the Blessed One seen the clansman Yasa?' 'Well then, householder, sit down. Perhaps by sitting here you may see the clansman Yasa sitting here.' Then the wealthy householder, joyful and uplifted, thinking, 'Indeed, by sitting here I will see the clansman Yasa sitting here,' paid homage to the Blessed One and sat down to one side. As the wealthy householder sat to one side, the Blessed One gave him a progressive discourse—that is, a discourse on giving, virtue, and the heavens; he explained the danger, degradation, and defilement of sensual pleasures and the benefit of renunciation. When the Blessed One knew that the wealthy householder's mind was fit, pliable, unobscured, uplifted, and clear, he then proclaimed the teaching unique to the Buddhas: suffering, its origin, its cessation, and the path. Just as a clean cloth, free from stains, would readily absorb dye, so too in the wealthy householder, right there on that seat, arose the stainless, immaculate Eye of Dhamma: 'Whatever is subject to origination is all subject to cessation.' Then the wealthy householder, having seen the Dhamma, attained the Dhamma, known the Dhamma, and plunged into the Dhamma, having crossed over doubt, dispelled uncertainty, gained confidence, and become independent of others in the Teacher's dispensation, said to the Blessed One: 'Excellent, Venerable Sir! Excellent, Venerable Sir! Just as one might set upright what was overturned, reveal what was hidden, show the way to one who is lost, or hold up a lamp in the darkness so that those with eyes might see forms—even so has the Dhamma been explained by the Blessed One in manifold ways. Venerable Sir, I go for refuge to the Blessed One, the Dhamma, and the Sangha of monks. May the Blessed One remember me as a lay follower who has taken refuge from this day forward until life's end.' He was the first lay follower in the world to make the threefold declaration of refuge.

28. Atha kho yasassa kulaputtassa pituno dhamme desiyamāne yathādiṭṭhaṃ yathāviditaṃ bhūmiṃ paccavekkhantassa anupādāya āsavehi cittaṃ vimucci. Atha kho bhagavato etadahosi – ‘‘yasassa kho kulaputtassa pituno dhamme desiyamāne yathādiṭṭhaṃ yathāviditaṃ bhūmiṃ paccavekkhantassa anupādāya āsavehi cittaṃ vimuttaṃ. Abhabbo kho yaso kulaputto hīnāyāvattitvā kāme paribhuñjituṃ, seyyathāpi pubbe agārikabhūto; yaṃnūnāhaṃ taṃ iddhābhisaṅkhāraṃ paṭippassambheyya’’nti. Atha kho bhagavā taṃ iddhābhisaṅkhāraṃ paṭippassambhesi. Addasā kho seṭṭhi gahapati yasaṃ kulaputtaṃ nisinnaṃ, disvāna yasaṃ kulaputtaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘mātā te tāta, yasa, parideva [paridevī (ka.)] sokasamāpannā, dehi mātuyā jīvita’’nti. Atha kho yaso kulaputto bhagavantaṃ ullokesi. Atha kho bhagavā seṭṭhiṃ gahapatiṃ etadavoca – ‘‘taṃ kiṃ maññasi, gahapati, yassa sekkhena ñāṇena sekkhena dassanena dhammo diṭṭho vidito seyyathāpi tayā? Tassa yathādiṭṭhaṃ yathāviditaṃ bhūmiṃ paccavekkhantassa anupādāya āsavehi cittaṃ vimuttaṃ. Bhabbo nu kho so, gahapati, hīnāyāvattitvā kāme paribhuñjituṃ seyyathāpi pubbe agārikabhūto’’ti? ‘‘No hetaṃ, bhante’’. ‘‘Yasassa kho, gahapati, kulaputtassa sekkhena ñāṇena sekkhena dassanena dhammo diṭṭho vidito seyyathāpi tayā. Tassa yathādiṭṭhaṃ yathāviditaṃ bhūmiṃ paccavekkhantassa anupādāya āsavehi cittaṃ vimuttaṃ. Abhabbo kho, gahapati, yaso kulaputto hīnāyāvattitvā kāme paribhuñjituṃ seyyathāpi pubbe agārikabhūto’’ti. ‘‘Lābhā, bhante, yasassa kulaputtassa, suladdhaṃ, bhante, yasassa kulaputtassa, yathā yasassa kulaputtassa anupādāya āsavehi cittaṃ vimuttaṃ. Adhivāsetu me, bhante, bhagavā ajjatanāya bhattaṃ yasena kulaputtena pacchāsamaṇenā’’ti. Adhivāsesi bhagavā tuṇhībhāvena. Atha kho seṭṭhi gahapati bhagavato adhivāsanaṃ viditvā uṭṭhāyāsanā bhagavantaṃ abhivādetvā padakkhiṇaṃ katvā pakkāmi. Atha kho yaso kulaputto acirapakkante seṭṭhimhi gahapatimhi bhagavantaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘labheyyāhaṃ, bhante, bhagavato santike pabbajjaṃ, labheyyaṃ upasampada’’nti. ‘‘Ehi bhikkhū’’ti bhagavā avoca – ‘‘svākkhāto dhammo, cara brahmacariyaṃ sammā dukkhassa antakiriyāyā’’ti. Sāva tassa āyasmato upasampadā ahosi. Tena kho pana samayena satta loke arahanto honti.

28.Then, while the clansman Yasa’s father was being taught the Dhamma, contemplating the ground as it had been seen and known, his mind was liberated from the taints without clinging. Then the Blessed One thought: “While the clansman Yasa’s father was being taught the Dhamma, contemplating the ground as it had been seen and known, his mind was liberated from the taints without clinging. It is impossible for the clansman Yasa to return to the lower life and enjoy sensual pleasures as he did before when he was a householder. Why don’t I now withdraw that act of psychic power?” Then the Blessed One withdrew that act of psychic power. The wealthy householder saw the clansman Yasa seated there. Seeing him, he said to the clansman Yasa: “My dear Yasa, your mother is grieving, overcome by sorrow. Give your mother her life.” Then the clansman Yasa looked at the Blessed One. Then the Blessed One said to the wealthy householder: “What do you think, householder? If someone has seen and understood the Dhamma with the knowledge and vision of a trainee, just as you have, and while contemplating the ground as it had been seen and known, his mind is liberated from the taints without clinging—could such a one return to the lower life and enjoy sensual pleasures as he did before when he was a householder?” “No, venerable sir.” “Householder, the clansman Yasa has seen and understood the Dhamma with the knowledge and vision of a trainee, just as you have. While contemplating the ground as it had been seen and known, his mind was liberated from the taints without clinging. It is impossible for the clansman Yasa to return to the lower life and enjoy sensual pleasures as he did before when he was a householder.” “It is a gain, venerable sir, for the clansman Yasa, it is a great gain, venerable sir, that the clansman Yasa’s mind has been liberated from the taints without clinging. Venerable sir, may the Blessed One together with the clansman Yasa as his attendant accept tomorrow’s meal from me.” The Blessed One consented by silence. Then the wealthy householder, understanding the Blessed One’s consent, rose from his seat, paid homage to the Blessed One, circumambulated him, and departed. Then, not long after the wealthy householder had left, the clansman Yasa said to the Blessed One: “Venerable sir, may I receive the going forth in the Blessed One’s presence, may I receive the higher ordination.” “Come, monk,” the Blessed One said, “the Dhamma is well proclaimed; live the holy life for the complete ending of suffering.” That was the venerable one’s higher ordination. At that time there were seven arahants in the world.

Yasassa pabbajjā niṭṭhitā.

The Going Forth of Yasa was concluded.

29. Atha kho bhagavā pubbaṇhasamayaṃ nivāsetvā pattacīvaramādāya āyasmatā yasena pacchāsamaṇena yena seṭṭhissa gahapatissa nivesanaṃ tenupasaṅkami, upasaṅkamitvā paññatte āsane nisīdi. Atha kho āyasmato yasassa mātā ca purāṇadutiyikā ca yena bhagavā tenupasaṅkamiṃsu, upasaṅkamitvā bhagavantaṃ abhivādetvā ekamantaṃ nisīdiṃsu. Tāsaṃ bhagavā anupubbiṃ kathaṃ kathesi, seyyathidaṃ – dānakathaṃ sīlakathaṃ saggakathaṃ, kāmānaṃ ādīnavaṃ okāraṃ saṃkilesaṃ, nekkhamme ānisaṃsaṃ pakāsesi. Yadā tā bhagavā aññāsi kallacittā, muducittā, vinīvaraṇacittā, udaggacittā, pasannacittā, atha yā buddhānaṃ sāmukkaṃsikā dhammadesanā taṃ pakāsesi – dukkhaṃ, samudayaṃ, nirodhaṃ, maggaṃ. Seyyathāpi nāma suddhaṃ vatthaṃ apagatakāḷakaṃ sammadeva rajanaṃ paṭiggaṇheyya, evameva tāsaṃ tasmiṃyeva āsane virajaṃ vītamalaṃ dhammacakkhuṃ udapādi – yaṃ kiñci samudayadhammaṃ, sabbaṃ taṃ nirodhadhammanti. Tā diṭṭhadhammā pattadhammā viditadhammā pariyogāḷhadhammā tiṇṇavicikicchā vigatakathaṃkathā vesārajjappattā aparappaccayā satthusāsane bhagavantaṃ etadavocuṃ – ‘‘abhikkantaṃ, bhante, abhikkantaṃ, bhante…pe… etā mayaṃ, bhante, bhagavantaṃ saraṇaṃ gacchāma, dhammañca, bhikkhusaṅghañca. Upāsikāyo no bhagavā dhāretu ajjatagge pāṇupetā saraṇaṃ gatā’’ti. Tā ca loke paṭhamaṃ upāsikā ahesuṃ tevācikā.

29.Then, in the morning, the Blessed One, having dressed, took his bowl and robe, and accompanied by Venerable Yasa following behind him as his attendant, went to the house of the wealthy householder. Arriving there, he sat down on the prepared seat. Then Venerable Yasa’s mother and his former wife approached the Blessed One, paid homage to him, and sat down to one side. The Blessed One gave them a progressive talk—that is, talk on generosity, talk on virtue, talk on heaven; he revealed the danger, degradation, and defilement of sensual pleasures and the benefit of renunciation. When he knew that their minds were ready, pliable, free from hindrances, uplifted, and confident, he revealed the teaching special to the Buddhas—suffering, its origin, its cessation, and the path. Just as a clean cloth, free from stains, would properly absorb dye, so too, while they sat there, the dust-free, stainless vision of the Dhamma arose in them: "Whatever is subject to arising is all subject to cessation." Having seen the Dhamma, attained the Dhamma, understood the Dhamma, plunged into the Dhamma, having crossed over doubt, rid of uncertainty, having gained confidence, independent of others in the Teacher’s dispensation, they said to the Blessed One: "Excellent, venerable sir! Excellent, venerable sir! ... We go for refuge to the Blessed One, to the Dhamma, and to the Sangha. May the Blessed One remember us as laywomen who have gone for refuge from this day forward for life." They were the first laywomen in the world to declare the threefold refuge.

Atha kho āyasmato yasassa mātā ca pitā ca purāṇadutiyikā ca bhagavantañca āyasmantañca yasaṃ paṇītena khādanīyena bhojanīyena sahatthā santappetvā sampavāretvā, bhagavantaṃ bhuttāviṃ onītapattapāṇiṃ, ekamantaṃ nisīdiṃsu. Atha kho bhagavā āyasmato yasassa mātarañca pitarañca purāṇadutiyikañca dhammiyā kathāya sandassetvā samādapetvā samuttejetvā sampahaṃsetvā uṭṭhāyāsanā pakkāmi.

Then Venerable Yasa’s mother, father, and former wife personally served and satisfied the Blessed One and Venerable Yasa with choice food, both hard and soft. When the Blessed One had finished eating and removed his hand from the bowl, they sat down to one side. Then the Blessed One, having instructed, urged, roused, and gladdened Venerable Yasa’s mother, father, and former wife with a Dhamma talk, rose from his seat and departed.

30. Assosuṃ kho āyasmato yasassa cattāro gihisahāyakā bārāṇasiyaṃ seṭṭhānuseṭṭhīnaṃ kulānaṃ puttā – vimalo, subāhu, puṇṇaji, gavampati – yaso kira kulaputto kesamassuṃ ohāretvā kāsāyāni vatthāni acchādetvā agārasmā anagāriyaṃ pabbajitoti. Sutvāna nesaṃ etadahosi – ‘‘na hi nūna so orako dhammavinayo, na sā orakā pabbajjā, yattha yaso kulaputto kesamassuṃ ohāretvā kāsāyāni vatthāni acchādetvā agārasmā anagāriyaṃ pabbajito’’ti. Te [te cattāro janā (ka.)] yenāyasmā yaso tenupasaṅkamiṃsu, upasaṅkamitvā āyasmantaṃ yasaṃ abhivādetvā ekamantaṃ aṭṭhaṃsu. Atha kho āyasmā yaso te cattāro gihisahāyake ādāya yena bhagavā tenupasaṅkami, upasaṅkamitvā bhagavantaṃ abhivādetvā ekamantaṃ nisīdi. Ekamantaṃ nisinno kho āyasmā yaso bhagavantaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘ime me, bhante, cattāro gihisahāyakā bārāṇasiyaṃ seṭṭhānuseṭṭhīnaṃ kulānaṃ puttā – vimalo, subāhu, puṇṇaji, gavampati. Ime [ime cattāro (ka.)] bhagavā ovadatu anusāsatū’’ti. Tesaṃ bhagavā anupubbiṃ kathaṃ kathesi, seyyathidaṃ – dānakathaṃ sīlakathaṃ saggakathaṃ kāmānaṃ ādīnavaṃ okāraṃ saṃkilesaṃ nekkhamme ānisaṃsaṃ pakāsesi, yadā te bhagavā aññāsi kallacitte muducitte vinīvaraṇacitte udaggacitte pasannacitte, atha yā buddhānaṃ sāmukkaṃsikā dhammadesanā, taṃ pakāsesi dukkhaṃ samudayaṃ nirodhaṃ maggaṃ, seyyathāpi nāma suddhaṃ vatthaṃ apagatakāḷakaṃ sammadeva rajanaṃ paṭiggaṇheyya, evameva tesaṃ tasmiṃyeva āsane virajaṃ vītamalaṃ dhammacakkhuṃ udapādi ‘‘yaṃ kiñci samudayadhammaṃ, sabbaṃ taṃ nirodhadhamma’’nti. Te diṭṭhadhammā pattadhammā viditadhammā pariyogāḷhadhammā tiṇṇavicikicchā vigatakathaṃkathā vesārajjappattā aparappaccayā satthusāsane bhagavantaṃ etadavocuṃ – ‘‘labheyyāma mayaṃ, bhante, bhagavato santike pabbajjaṃ, labheyyāma upasampada’’nti. ‘‘Etha bhikkhavo’’ti bhagavā avoca – ‘‘svākkhāto dhammo, caratha brahmacariyaṃ sammā dukkhassa antakiriyāyā’’ti. Sāva tesaṃ āyasmantānaṃ upasampadā ahosi. Atha kho bhagavā te bhikkhū dhammiyā kathāya ovadi anusāsi. Tesaṃ bhagavatā dhammiyā kathāya ovadiyamānānaṃ anusāsiyamānānaṃ anupādāya āsavehi cittāni vimucciṃsu. Tena kho pana samayena ekādasa loke arahanto honti.

30.The four lay friends of Venerable Yasa in Varanasi—sons of prominent families—Vimala, Subahu, Punnaji, and Gavampati, heard that Yasa, the clansman, had shaved off his hair and beard, put on the ochre robes, and gone forth from the household life into homelessness. Upon hearing this, they thought: "Surely, this is no inferior Dhamma and Discipline, no inferior going forth, where Yasa the clansman has shaved off his hair and beard, put on the ochre robes, and gone forth from the household life into homelessness." They approached Venerable Yasa, paid homage to him, and stood to one side. Then Venerable Yasa took his four lay friends and went to the Blessed One. Having approached, he paid homage to the Blessed One and sat to one side. Sitting to one side, Venerable Yasa said to the Blessed One: "Venerable sir, these are my four lay friends in Varanasi—sons of prominent families—Vimala, Subahu, Punnaji, and Gavampati. May the Blessed One advise and instruct them." The Blessed One gave them a progressive talk: on generosity, on virtue, on the heavens; on the danger, degradation, and defilement of sensual pleasures; and on the benefits of renunciation. When the Blessed One knew that their minds were ready, pliable, free from hindrances, uplifted, and confident, he revealed the teaching special to the Buddhas: suffering, its origin, its cessation, and the path. Just as a clean cloth free from stains would properly absorb dye, so too, while they sat there, the dust-free, stainless vision of the Dhamma arose in them: "Whatever is subject to arising is all subject to cessation." Having seen the Dhamma, attained the Dhamma, understood the Dhamma, plunged into the Dhamma, having crossed over doubt, rid of uncertainty, having gained confidence, independent of others in the Teacher’s dispensation, they said to the Blessed One: "May we receive the going forth, Venerable sir, may we receive the higher ordination in the Blessed One’s presence." "Come, bhikkhus," said the Blessed One, "the Dhamma is well-expounded. Live the holy life for the complete ending of suffering." That was the higher ordination of those venerable ones. Then the Blessed One instructed and advised those bhikkhus with a Dhamma talk. As they were being instructed and advised by the Blessed One, their minds were liberated from the taints through non-clinging. At that time, there were eleven arahants in the world.

Catugihisahāyakapabbajjā niṭṭhitā.

The going forth of the four lay friends is completed.

31. Assosuṃ kho āyasmato yasassa paññāsamattā gihisahāyakā jānapadā pubbānupubbakānaṃ kulānaṃ puttā – yaso kira kulaputto kesamassuṃ ohāretvā kāsāyāni vatthāni acchādetvā agārasmā anagāriyaṃ pabbajitoti. Sutvāna nesaṃ etadahosi – ‘‘na hi nūna so orako dhammavinayo, na sā orakā pabbajjā, yattha yaso kulaputto kesamassuṃ ohāretvā kāsāyāni vatthāni acchādetvā agārasmā anagāriyaṃ pabbajito’’ti. Te yenāyasmā yaso tenupasaṅkamiṃsu, upasaṅkamitvā āyasmantaṃ yasaṃ abhivādetvā ekamantaṃ aṭṭhaṃsu. Atha kho āyasmā yaso te paññāsamatte gihisahāyake ādāya yena bhagavā tenupasaṅkami, upasaṅkamitvā bhagavantaṃ abhivādetvā ekamantaṃ nisīdi. Ekamantaṃ nisinno kho āyasmā yaso bhagavantaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘ime me, bhante, paññāsamattā gihisahāyakā jānapadā pubbānupubbakānaṃ kulānaṃ puttā. Ime bhagavā ovadatu anusāsatū’’ti. Tesaṃ bhagavā anupubbiṃ kathaṃ kathesi, seyyathidaṃ – dānakathaṃ sīlakathaṃ saggakathaṃ kāmānaṃ ādīnavaṃ okāraṃ saṃkilesaṃ nekkhamme ānisaṃsaṃ pakāsesi. Yadā te bhagavā aññāsi kallacitte muducitte vinīvaraṇacitte udaggacitte pasannacitte, atha yā buddhānaṃ sāmukkaṃsikā dhammadesanā, taṃ pakāsesi dukkhaṃ samudayaṃ nirodhaṃ maggaṃ, seyyathāpi nāma suddhaṃ vatthaṃ apagatakāḷakaṃ sammadeva rajanaṃ paṭiggaṇheyya, evameva tesaṃ tasmiṃyeva āsane virajaṃ vītamalaṃ dhammacakkhuṃ udapādi yaṃ kiñci samudayadhammaṃ, sabbaṃ taṃ nirodhadhammanti. Te diṭṭhadhammā pattadhammā viditadhammā pariyogāḷhadhammā tiṇṇavicikicchā vigatakathaṃkathā vesārajjappattā aparappaccayā satthusāsane bhagavantaṃ etadavocuṃ – ‘‘labheyyāma mayaṃ, bhante, bhagavato santike pabbajjaṃ, labheyyāma upasampada’’nti. ‘‘Etha bhikkhavo’’ti bhagavā avoca – ‘‘svākkhāto dhammo, caratha brahmacariyaṃ sammā dukkhassa antakiriyāyā’’ti. Sāva tesaṃ āyasmantānaṃ upasampadā ahosi. Atha kho bhagavā te bhikkhū dhammiyā kathāya ovadi anusāsi. Tesaṃ bhagavatā dhammiyā kathāya ovadiyamānānaṃ anusāsiyamānānaṃ anupādāya āsavehi cittāni vimucciṃsu. Tena kho pana samayena ekasaṭṭhi loke arahanto honti.

31.Then about fifty lay friends of Venerable Yasa, sons of prominent families from the provinces, heard that Yasa, the clansman, had shaved off his hair and beard, put on the ochre robes, and gone forth from the household life into homelessness. Upon hearing this, they thought: "Surely, this is no inferior Dhamma and Discipline, no inferior going forth, where Yasa the clansman has shaved off his hair and beard, put on the ochre robes, and gone forth from the household life into homelessness." They approached Venerable Yasa, paid homage to him, and stood to one side. Then Venerable Yasa took those fifty lay friends and went to the Blessed One. Having approached, he paid homage to the Blessed One and sat to one side. Sitting to one side, Venerable Yasa said to the Blessed One: "Venerable sir, these fifty lay friends of mine are sons of prominent families from the provinces. May the Blessed One advise and instruct them." The Blessed One gave them a progressive talk—that is, talk on generosity, talk on virtue, talk on heaven; on the danger, degradation, and defilement of sensual pleasures and the benefit of renunciation. When the Blessed One knew that their minds were ready, pliable, free from hindrances, uplifted, and confident, he revealed the teaching special to the Buddhas: suffering, its origin, its cessation, and the path. Just as a clean cloth free from stains would properly absorb dye, so too, while they sat there, the dust-free, stainless vision of the Dhamma arose in them: "Whatever is subject to arising is all subject to cessation." Having seen the Dhamma, attained the Dhamma, understood the Dhamma, plunged into the Dhamma, having crossed over doubt, rid of uncertainty, having gained confidence, independent of others in the Teacher’s dispensation, they said to the Blessed One: "May we receive the going forth, Venerable sir, may we receive the higher ordination in the Blessed One’s presence." "Come, bhikkhus," said the Blessed One, "the Dhamma is well-expounded. Live the holy life for the complete ending of suffering." That was the higher ordination of those venerable ones. Then the Blessed One instructed and advised those bhikkhus with a Dhamma talk. As they were being instructed and advised by the Blessed One, their minds were liberated from the taints through non-clinging. At that time, there were sixty-one arahants in the world.

Paññāsagihisahāyakapabbajjā niṭṭhitā.

The going forth of the fifty lay friends is completed.

Niṭṭhitā ca pabbajjākathā.

The account of the going forth is concluded.

### 8. Mārakathā ^8

> [!TIP]- Links to [[mv1-brahmali-pali#^8|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch14|BMC Chapter 14]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-MV1.8" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


8.Discourse on Māra

32. Atha kho bhagavā te bhikkhū āmantesi [saṃ. ni. 1.141 mārasaṃyuttepi] – ‘‘muttāhaṃ, bhikkhave, sabbapāsehi, ye dibbā ye ca mānusā. Tumhepi, bhikkhave, muttā sabbapāsehi, ye dibbā ye ca mānusā. Caratha, bhikkhave, cārikaṃ bahujanahitāya bahujanasukhāya lokānukampāya atthāya hitāya sukhāya devamanussānaṃ. Mā ekena dve agamittha. Desetha, bhikkhave, dhammaṃ ādikalyāṇaṃ majjhekalyāṇaṃ pariyosānakalyāṇaṃ sātthaṃ sabyañjanaṃ kevalaparipuṇṇaṃ parisuddhaṃ brahmacariyaṃ pakāsetha. Santi sattā apparajakkhajātikā, assavanatā dhammassa parihāyanti, bhavissanti dhammassa aññātāro. Ahampi, bhikkhave, yena uruvelā senānigamo tenupasaṅkamissāmi dhammadesanāyā’’ti.

32.Then the Blessed One addressed the monks: "I am freed, monks, from all fetters, both divine and human. You too, monks, are freed from all fetters, both divine and human. Go forth, monks, for the good of the many, for the happiness of the many, out of compassion for the world, for the benefit, good, and happiness of gods and humans. Let not two go by one road. Teach, monks, the Dhamma that is good in the beginning, good in the middle, and good in the end, with the meaning and the wording. Proclaim the holy life that is entirely perfect and pure. There are beings with little dust in their eyes, who decline through not hearing the Dhamma. They will be understanders of the Dhamma. I too, monks, will go to Uruvelā, to Senānigama, to teach the Dhamma."

33. Atha kho māro pāpimā yena bhagavā tenupasaṅkami, upasaṅkamitvā bhagavantaṃ gāthāya ajjhabhāsi –

33.Then Māra the Wicked One approached the Blessed One. Having approached, he addressed the Blessed One in verse:

‘‘Baddhosi sabbapāsehi, ye dibbā ye ca mānusā;Mahābandhanabaddhosi, na me samaṇa mokkhasī’’ti.

"You are bound by all bonds, both divine and human. You are bound by a great bond; ascetic, you will not escape me."

‘‘Muttāhaṃ [muttohaṃ (sī. syā.)] sabbapāsehi, ye dibbā ye ca mānusā;Mahābandhanamuttomhi, nihato tvamasi antakāti.

"I am freed from all fetters, both heavenly and human; I am freed from the great bond, you are defeated, O End-maker."

[saṃ. ni. 1.151 mārasaṃyuttepi] ‘‘Antalikkhacaro pāso, yvāyaṃ carati mānaso;Tena taṃ bādhayissāmi, na me samaṇa mokkhasīti.

"The snare that travels in the sky, which moves in the mind; With that I will bind you, ascetic, you will not escape me."

[saṃ. ni. 1.1151 mārasaṃyuttepi] ‘‘Rūpā saddā rasā gandhā, phoṭṭhabbā ca manoramā;Ettha me vigato chando, nihato tvamasi antakā’’ti.

"Forms, sounds, tastes, scents, And pleasant tactile objects—all these; Here my desire is extinguished; You are defeated, O End-maker."

Atha kho māro pāpimā – jānāti maṃ bhagavā, jānāti maṃ sugatoti dukkhī dummano

Then Māra the Evil One, knowing, "The Blessed One knows me; the Sublime One knows me," sorrowful and disappointed,

Tatthevantaradhāyīti.

There he vanished.

Mārakathā niṭṭhitā.

The discourse on Māra is finished.

### 9. Pabbajjūpasampadākathā ^9

> [!TIP]- Links to [[mv1-brahmali-pali#^9|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch14|BMC Chapter 14]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-MV1.9" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


9.The Discussion on Going Forth and Admission to the Order

34. Tena kho pana samayena bhikkhū nānādisā nānājanapadā pabbajjāpekkhe ca upasampadāpekkhe ca ānenti – bhagavā ne pabbājessati upasampādessatīti. Tattha bhikkhū ceva kilamanti pabbajjāpekkhā ca upasampadāpekkhā ca. Atha kho bhagavato rahogatassa paṭisallīnassa evaṃ cetaso parivitakko udapādi – ‘‘etarahi kho bhikkhū nānādisā nānājanapadā pabbajjāpekkhe ca upasampadāpekkhe ca ānenti – bhagavā ne pabbājessati upasampādessatīti. Tattha bhikkhū ceva kilamanti pabbajjāpekkhā ca upasampadāpekkhā ca. Yaṃnūnāhaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ anujāneyyaṃ – tumheva dāni, bhikkhave, tāsu tāsu disāsu tesu tesu janapadesu pabbājetha upasampādethā’’ti. Atha kho bhagavā sāyanhasamayaṃ paṭisallānā vuṭṭhito etasmiṃ nidāne etasmiṃ pakaraṇe dhammiṃ kathaṃ katvā bhikkhū āmantesi – ‘‘idha mayhaṃ, bhikkhave, rahogatassa paṭisallīnassa evaṃ cetaso parivitakko udapādi – ‘etarahi kho bhikkhū nānādisā nānājanapadā pabbajjāpekkhe ca upasampadāpekkhe ca ānenti bhagavā ne pabbājessati upasampādessatīti, tattha bhikkhū ceva kilamanti pabbajjāpekkhā ca upasampadāpekkhā ca, yaṃnūnāhaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ anujāneyyaṃ tumheva dāni, bhikkhave, tāsu tāsu disāsu tesu tesu janapadesu pabbājetha upasampādethā’’’ti, anujānāmi, bhikkhave, tumheva dāni tāsu tāsu disāsu tesu tesu janapadesu pabbājetha upasampādetha. Evañca pana, bhikkhave, pabbājetabbo upasampādetabbo –

34.At that time, monks were bringing those seeking going-forth and full ordination from various regions and countries, thinking, “The Blessed One will give them going-forth, will give them full ordination.” There, both the monks and those seeking going-forth and full ordination grow weary. Then, while the Blessed One was alone in seclusion, this thought arose in his mind: “Now monks are bringing those seeking going-forth and full ordination from various regions and countries, thinking, ‘The Blessed One will give them going-forth, will give them full ordination.’ There, both the monks and those seeking going-forth and full ordination grow weary. Why do I not allow the monks: ‘Now, monks, you yourselves may give going-forth and full ordination in those various regions and countries.’” Then, in the evening, the Blessed One emerged from seclusion and, having given a Dhamma talk in connection with this reason and this matter, addressed the monks: “Here, monks, while I was alone in seclusion, this thought arose in my mind: ‘Now monks are bringing those seeking going-forth and full ordination from various regions and countries, thinking, “The Blessed One will give them going-forth, will give them full ordination.” There, both the monks and those seeking going-forth and full ordination grow weary. Why do I not allow the monks: “Now, monks, you yourselves may give going-forth and full ordination in those various regions and countries.”’” I allow, monks, that you yourselves may now give going-forth and full ordination in those various regions and countries. And, monks, one should be given going-forth and full ordination in this way:

Paṭhamaṃ kesamassuṃ ohārāpetvā [ohāretvā (ka.)], kāsāyāni vatthāni acchādāpetvā, ekaṃsaṃ uttarāsaṅgaṃ kārāpetvā, bhikkhūnaṃ pāde vandāpetvā, ukkuṭikaṃ nisīdāpetvā, añjaliṃ paggaṇhāpetvā, evaṃ vadehīti vattabbo – buddhaṃ saraṇaṃ gacchāmi, dhammaṃ saraṇaṃ gacchāmi, saṅghaṃ saraṇaṃ gacchāmi; dutiyampi buddhaṃ saraṇaṃ gacchāmi, dutiyampi dhammaṃ saraṇaṃ gacchāmi, dutiyampi saṅghaṃ saraṇaṃ gacchāmi; tatiyampi buddhaṃ saraṇaṃ gacchāmi, tatiyampi dhammaṃ saraṇaṃ gacchāmi, tatiyampi saṅghaṃ saraṇaṃ gacchāmī’’ti. ‘‘Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, imehi tīhi saraṇagamanehi pabbajjaṃ upasampada’’nti.

First, having the hair and beard shaved off, having saffron robes put on, having the upper robe arranged over one shoulder, having been made to bow at the monks’ feet, having been seated in the squatting position, having the hands raised in añjali, one should be instructed to say thus: ‘I take refuge in the Buddha, I take refuge in the Dhamma, I take refuge in the Sangha; for the second time I take refuge in the Buddha, for the second time I take refuge in the Dhamma, for the second time I take refuge in the Sangha; for the third time I take refuge in the Buddha, for the third time I take refuge in the Dhamma, for the third time I take refuge in the Sangha.’ ‘I allow, monks, the going forth and the higher ordination with these three refuges.’

Tīhi saraṇagamanehi upasampadākathā niṭṭhitā.

The discourse on the higher ordination by means of the three refuges is concluded.

### 10. Dutiyamārakathā ^10

> [!TIP]- Links to [[mv1-brahmali-pali#^10|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch14|BMC Chapter 14]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-MV1.10" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


10.The Second Discourse on Māra

35. Atha kho bhagavā vassaṃvuṭṭho [vassaṃvuttho (sī.)] bhikkhū āmantesi [saṃ. ni. 1.155] – ‘‘mayhaṃ kho, bhikkhave, yoniso manasikārā yoniso sammappadhānā anuttarā vimutti anuppattā, anuttarā vimutti sacchikatā. Tumhepi, bhikkhave, yoniso manasikārā yoniso sammappadhānā anuttaraṃ vimuttiṃ anupāpuṇātha, anuttaraṃ vimuttiṃ sacchikarothā’’ti. Atha kho māro pāpimā yena bhagavā tenupasaṅkami, upasaṅkamitvā bhagavantaṃ gāthāya ajjhabhāsi –

35.Then the Blessed One, having completed the rains retreat, addressed the bhikkhus: ‘Bhikkhus, through wise attention and right strivings, I have attained the unsurpassed liberation and realized the unsurpassed liberation. You too, bhikkhus, through wise attention and right strivings, should attain the unsurpassed liberation and realize the unsurpassed liberation.’ Then Māra the Evil One approached the Blessed One and addressed him with a verse:

‘‘Baddhosi mārapāsehi, ye dibbā ye ca mānusā;Mahābandhanabaddhosi [mārabandhanabaddhosi (sī. syā.)], na me samaṇa mokkhasī’’ti.

‘You are bound by Māra’s snares, both divine and human. You are bound by the great bondage, O ascetic; you will not be freed from me.’

‘‘Muttāhaṃ mārapāsehi, ye dibbā ye ca mānusā;Mahābandhanamuttomhi [mārabandhanamuttomhi (sī. syā.)], nihato tvamasi antakā’’ti.

‘I am freed from Māra’s snares, both divine and human. I am freed from the great bondage; you are defeated, O End-maker!’

Atha kho māro pāpimā – jānāti maṃ bhagavā, jānāti maṃ sugatoti dukkhī dummano

Then Māra the Evil One, thinking, ‘The Blessed One knows me, the Well-gone One knows me,’ sorrowful and disappointed,

Tatthevantaradhāyi.

Right there he vanished.

Dutiyamārakathā niṭṭhitā.

The Second Discourse on Māra is concluded.

### 11. Bhaddavaggiyavatthu ^11

> [!TIP]- Links to [[mv1-brahmali-pali#^11|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch14|BMC Chapter 14]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-MV1.11" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


11.The Story of the Bhaddavaggiyas

36. Atha kho bhagavā bārāṇasiyaṃ yathābhirantaṃ viharitvā yena uruvelā tena cārikaṃ pakkāmi. Atha kho bhagavā maggā okkamma yena aññataro vanasaṇḍo tenupasaṅkami, upasaṅkamitvā taṃ vanasaṇḍaṃ ajjhogāhetvā aññatarasmiṃ rukkhamūle nisīdi. Tena kho pana samayena tiṃsamattā bhaddavaggiyā sahāyakā sapajāpatikā tasmiṃ vanasaṇḍe paricārenti. Ekassa pajāpati nāhosi; tassa atthāya vesī ānītā ahosi. Atha kho sā vesī tesu pamattesu paricārentesu bhaṇḍaṃ ādāya palāyittha. Atha kho te sahāyakā sahāyakassa veyyāvaccaṃ karontā, taṃ itthiṃ gavesantā, taṃ vanasaṇḍaṃ āhiṇḍantā addasaṃsu bhagavantaṃ aññatarasmiṃ rukkhamūle nisinnaṃ. Disvāna yena bhagavā tenupasaṅkamiṃsu, upasaṅkamitvā bhagavantaṃ etadavocuṃ – ‘‘api, bhante, bhagavā ekaṃ itthiṃ passeyyā’’ti? ‘‘Kiṃ pana vo, kumārā, itthiyā’’ti? ‘‘Idha mayaṃ, bhante, tiṃsamattā bhaddavaggiyā sahāyakā sapajāpatikā imasmiṃ vanasaṇḍe paricārimhā. Ekassa pajāpati nāhosi; tassa atthāya vesī ānītā ahosi. Atha kho sā, bhante, vesī amhesu pamattesu paricārentesu bhaṇḍaṃ ādāya palāyittha. Te mayaṃ, bhante, sahāyakā sahāyakassa veyyāvaccaṃ karontā, taṃ itthiṃ gavesantā, imaṃ vanasaṇḍaṃ āhiṇḍāmā’’ti. ‘‘Taṃ kiṃ maññatha vo, kumārā, katamaṃ nu kho tumhākaṃ varaṃ – yaṃ vā tumhe itthiṃ gaveseyyātha, yaṃ vā attānaṃ gaveseyyāthā’’ti? ‘‘Etadeva, bhante, amhākaṃ varaṃ yaṃ mayaṃ attānaṃ gaveseyyāmā’’ti. ‘‘Tena hi vo, kumārā, nisīdatha, dhammaṃ vo desessāmī’’ti. ‘‘Evaṃ, bhante’’ti kho te bhaddavaggiyā sahāyakā bhagavantaṃ abhivādetvā ekamantaṃ nisīdiṃsu. Tesaṃ bhagavā anupubbiṃ kathaṃ kathesi, seyyathidaṃ – dānakathaṃ sīlakathaṃ saggakathaṃ kāmānaṃ ādīnavaṃ okāraṃ saṃkilesaṃ nekkhamme ānisaṃsaṃ pakāsesi, yadā te bhagavā aññāsi kallacitte muducitte vinīvaraṇacitte udaggacitte pasannacitte, atha yā buddhānaṃ sāmukkaṃsikā dhammadesanā, taṃ pakāsesi dukkhaṃ samudayaṃ nirodhaṃ maggaṃ, seyyathāpi nāma suddhaṃ vatthaṃ apagatakāḷakaṃ sammadeva rajanaṃ paṭiggaṇheyya, evameva tesaṃ tasmiṃyeva āsane virajaṃ vītamalaṃ dhammacakkhuṃ udapādi ‘‘yaṃ kiñci samudayadhammaṃ, sabbaṃ taṃ nirodhadhamma’’nti. Te diṭṭhadhammā pattadhammā viditadhammā pariyogāḷhadhammā tiṇṇavicikicchā vigatakathaṃkathā vesārajjappattā aparappaccayā satthusāsane bhagavantaṃ etadavocuṃ – ‘‘labheyyāma mayaṃ, bhante, bhagavato santike pabbajjaṃ, labheyyāma upasampada’’nti. ‘‘Etha bhikkhavo’’ti bhagavā avoca – ‘‘svākkhāto dhammo, caratha brahmacariyaṃ sammā dukkhassa antakiriyāyā’’ti. Sāva tesaṃ āyasmantānaṃ upasampadā ahosi.

36.Then the Blessed One, having stayed at Bārāṇasī as long as he wished, journeyed towards Uruvelā. Leaving the road, the Blessed One approached a certain grove and, entering that grove, sat down at the foot of a tree. At that time, about thirty Bhaddavaggiyas, companions each with his wife, were amusing themselves in that grove. One of them had no wife, so a courtesan had been brought for him. While they were heedlessly amusing themselves, that courtesan took their belongings and ran away. Then those companions, helping their friend, searching for that woman, wandering through the grove, saw the Blessed One seated at the foot of a tree. Seeing him, they approached and said, "Venerable sir, did the Blessed One see a woman?" "What is it to you, young men, about a woman?" "Here, venerable sir, we, about thirty Bhaddavaggiyas, companions each with his wife, were amusing ourselves in this grove. One of us had no wife, so a courtesan was brought for him. Then, venerable sir, while we were heedlessly amusing ourselves, that courtesan took our belongings and ran away. We, venerable sir, helping our friend, searching for that woman, are wandering through this grove." "What do you think, young men, which is better for you—that you should search for a woman or that you should search for yourselves?" "Indeed, venerable sir, it would be better for us to search for ourselves." "Well then, young men, sit down, I will teach you the Dhamma." "Yes, venerable sir," those Bhaddavaggiya companions replied, and having paid homage to the Blessed One, sat down to one side. The Blessed One gave them a progressive discourse: that is, a talk on generosity, on virtue, on heaven; he revealed the danger, degradation, and defilement of sensual pleasures and the benefits of renunciation. When the Blessed One knew that their minds were ready, pliable, free from hindrances, uplifted, and confident, he revealed the supreme teaching of the Buddhas: suffering, its origin, its cessation, and the path. Just as a clean cloth free from stains would properly absorb dye, so too in those very seats the dust-free, stainless Dhamma-eye arose in them: "Whatever is subject to arising is all subject to cessation." They, having seen the Dhamma, attained the Dhamma, known the Dhamma, plunged into the Dhamma, were free from doubt, rid of perplexity, attained to confidence, and were independent of others in the Teacher's dispensation. They said to the Blessed One, "May we receive the going forth, venerable sir, may we receive the higher ordination in the Blessed One's presence." "Come, bhikkhus!" the Blessed One said, "The Dhamma is well-proclaimed; lead the holy life for the complete ending of suffering." That was the higher ordination of those venerable ones.

Bhaddavaggiyasahāyakānaṃ vatthu niṭṭhitaṃ.

The account of the Bhaddavaggiya companions is concluded.

Dutiyabhāṇavāro.

The Second Recitation Section.

### 12. Uruvelapāṭihāriyakathā ^12

> [!TIP]- Links to [[mv1-brahmali-pali#^12|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch14|BMC Chapter 14]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-MV1.12" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


12.The Story of the Miracle at Uruvelā

37. Atha kho bhagavā anupubbena cārikaṃ caramāno yena uruvelā tadavasari. Tena kho pana samayena uruvelāyaṃ tayo jaṭilā paṭivasanti – uruvelakassapo, nadīkassapo, gayākassapoti. Tesu uruvelakassapo jaṭilo pañcannaṃ jaṭilasatānaṃ nāyako hoti, vināyako aggo pamukho pāmokkho. Nadīkassapo jaṭilo tiṇṇaṃ jaṭilasatānaṃ nāyako hoti, vināyako aggo pamukho pāmokkho. Gayākassapo jaṭilo dvinnaṃ jaṭilasatānaṃ nāyako hoti, vināyako aggo pamukho pāmokkho. Atha kho bhagavā yena uruvelakassapassa jaṭilassa assamo tenupasaṅkami, upasaṅkamitvā uruvelakassapaṃ jaṭilaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘sace te, kassapa, agaru, vaseyyāma ekarattaṃ agyāgāre’’ti? ‘‘Na kho me, mahāsamaṇa, garu, caṇḍettha nāgarājā iddhimā āsiviso ghoraviso, so taṃ mā viheṭhesī’’ti. Dutiyampi kho bhagavā uruvelakassapaṃ jaṭilaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘sace te, kassapa, agaru, vaseyyāma ekarattaṃ agyāgāre’’ti? ‘‘Na kho me, mahāsamaṇa, garu, caṇḍettha nāgarājā iddhimā āsiviso ghoraviso, so taṃ mā viheṭhesī’’ti. Tatiyampi kho bhagavā uruvelakassapaṃ jaṭilaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘sace te, kassapa, agaru, vaseyyāma ekarattaṃ agyāgāre’’ti? ‘‘Na kho me, mahāsamaṇa, garu, caṇḍettha nāgarājā iddhimā āsiviso ghoraviso, so taṃ mā viheṭhesī’’ti. ‘‘Appeva maṃ na viheṭheyya, iṅgha tvaṃ, kassapa, anujānāhi agyāgāra’’nti. ‘‘Vihara, mahāsamaṇa, yathāsukha’’nti. Atha kho bhagavā agyāgāraṃ pavisitvā tiṇasanthārakaṃ paññapetvā nisīdi pallaṅkaṃ ābhujitvā ujuṃ kāyaṃ paṇidhāya parimukhaṃ satiṃ upaṭṭhapetvā.

37.Then the Blessed One, wandering by stages, arrived at Uruvelā. At that time, three ascetics with matted hair were living in Uruvelā: Uruvelā Kassapa, Nadī Kassapa, and Gayā Kassapa. Among them, Uruvelā Kassapa was the leader, guide, chief, foremost, and supreme of five hundred ascetics with matted hair. Nadī Kassapa was the leader, guide, chief, foremost, and supreme of three hundred ascetics with matted hair. Gayā Kassapa was the leader, guide, chief, foremost, and supreme of two hundred ascetics with matted hair. Then the Blessed One approached the hermitage of Uruvelā Kassapa and said to Uruvelā Kassapa, the ascetic with matted hair: "If it is not troublesome to you, Kassapa, I would like to stay one night in the fire-hall." "It is not troublesome to me, great ascetic, but there is a fierce nāga-king there, powerful, venomous with dreadful poison. He might harm you." A second time, the Blessed One said to Uruvelā Kassapa, the ascetic with matted hair: "If it is not troublesome to you, Kassapa, I would like to stay one night in the fire-hall." "It is not troublesome to me, great ascetic, but there is a fierce nāga-king there, powerful, venomous with dreadful poison. He might harm you." A third time, the Blessed One said to Uruvelā Kassapa, the ascetic with matted hair: "If it is not troublesome to you, Kassapa, I would like to stay one night in the fire-hall." "It is not troublesome to me, great ascetic, but there is a fierce nāga-king there, powerful, venomous with dreadful poison. He might harm you." "Perhaps he will not harm me. Please, Kassapa, permit me the fire-hall." "Dwell, great ascetic, as you please." Then the Blessed One entered the fire-hall, spread out a grass mat, sat down cross-legged, straightened his body, and established mindfulness facing forward.

38. Addasā kho so nāgo bhagavantaṃ paviṭṭhaṃ, disvāna dummano [dukkhī dummano (sī. syā.)] padhūpāyi [pakhūpāsi (ka.)]. Atha kho bhagavato etadahosi – ‘‘yaṃnūnāhaṃ imassa nāgassa anupahacca chaviñca cammañca maṃsañca nhāruñca aṭṭhiñca aṭṭhimiñjañca tejasā tejaṃ pariyādiyeyya’’nti. Atha kho bhagavā tathārūpaṃ iddhābhisaṅkhāraṃ abhisaṅkharitvā padhūpāyi. Atha kho so nāgo makkhaṃ asahamāno pajjali. Bhagavāpi tejodhātuṃ samāpajjitvā pajjali. Ubhinnaṃ sajotibhūtānaṃ agyāgāraṃ ādittaṃ viya hoti sampajjalitaṃ sajotibhūtaṃ. Atha kho te jaṭilā agyāgāraṃ parivāretvā evamāhaṃsu – ‘‘abhirūpo vata bho mahāsamaṇo nāgena viheṭhiyatī’’ti. Atha kho bhagavā tassā rattiyā accayena tassa nāgassa anupahacca chaviñca cammañca maṃsañca nhāruñca aṭṭhiñca aṭṭhimiñjañca tejasā tejaṃ pariyādiyitvā patte pakkhipitvā uruvelakassapassa jaṭilassa dassesi – ‘‘ayaṃ te, kassapa, nāgo pariyādinno [pariyādiṇṇo (ka.)] assa tejasā tejo’’ti. Atha kho uruvelakassapassa jaṭilassa etadahosi – ‘‘mahiddhiko kho mahāsamaṇo mahānubhāvo, yatra hi nāma caṇḍassa nāgarājassa iddhimato āsivisassa ghoravisassa tejasā tejaṃ pariyādiyissati, natveva ca kho arahā yathā aha’’nti.

38.Then the nāga saw the Blessed One entering, and upon seeing him, it became distressed and emitted smoke. Then the Blessed One thought: 'Suppose I were to overcome this nāga’s fiery power with my own, without harming its skin, hide, flesh, sinews, bones, or bone marrow.' Then the Blessed One produced such a psychic formation that he too emitted smoke. Unable to bear the malice, the nāga burst into flames. The Blessed One, too, attained the fire element and blazed up. When both blazed forth radiantly, the fire-hall seemed ablaze and luminous. Then those ascetics, surrounding the fire-hall, said: 'How handsome the great ascetic is, yet he is being harassed by the nāga!' Then, when the night had passed, the Blessed One, without harming the nāga’s skin, hide, flesh, sinews, bones, or bone marrow, overcame its fiery power with his own. He placed it in his alms bowl and showed it to Uruvelā Kassapa the ascetic, saying: 'Here, Kassapa, this nāga has been overcome by my fiery power.' Then Uruvelā Kassapa thought: 'The great ascetic is indeed mighty and powerful, for he has overcome the fiery power of this fierce, venomous nāga-king. But he is not an arahant like me.'

39.

Nerañjarāyaṃ bhagavā, uruvelakassapaṃ jaṭilaṃ avoca;‘‘Sace te kassapa agaru, viharemu ajjaṇho aggisālamhī’’ti [aggisaraṇamhīti (sī. syā.)].

On the bank of the Nerañjarā River, the Blessed One said to Uruvelā Kassapa the ascetic: 'If it is not troublesome to you, Kassapa, let us stay tonight in the fire-hall.'

‘‘Na kho me mahāsamaṇa garu;Phāsukāmova taṃ nivāremi;Caṇḍettha nāgarājā;Iddhimā āsiviso ghoraviso;So taṃ mā viheṭhesī’’ti.

'It is not troublesome to me, Great Ascetic; I warn you for your own ease. For the nāga-king here is fierce, powerful, a venomous viper, deadly poisonous; may he not harm you.'

‘‘Appeva maṃ na viheṭheyya;Iṅgha tvaṃ kassapa anujānāhi agyāgāra’’nti;Dinnanti naṃ viditvā;Abhīto [asambhīto (sī.)] pāvisi bhayamatīto.

'Perhaps he will not harm me. Come now, Kassapa, permit me the fire-hall.' Knowing it was given, fearless and having overcome fear, he entered.

Disvā isiṃ paviṭṭhaṃ, ahināgo dummano padhūpāyi;Sumanamanaso adhimano [avimano (katthaci), navimano (syā.)], manussanāgopi tattha padhūpāyi.

Seeing the sage enter, the nāga, displeased, fumed; With a joyful mind and elated, the human nāga also fumed there.

Makkhañca asahamāno, ahināgo pāvakova pajjali;Tejodhātusu kusalo, manussanāgopi tattha pajjali.

Unable to bear the malice, the nāga blazed like fire; Skilled in the fire element, the human nāga also blazed there.

Ubhinnaṃ sajotibhūtānaṃ;Agyāgāraṃ ādittaṃ hoti sampajjalitaṃ sajotibhūtaṃ;Udicchare jaṭilā;‘‘Abhirūpo vata bho mahāsamaṇo;Nāgena viheṭhiyatī’’ti bhaṇanti.

The fire-hall of the two shining ones was ablaze, burning brightly. The ascetics with matted hair cried out: "Indeed, the Great Ascetic is beautiful! He is being harassed by a nāga!" they said.

Atha tassā rattiyā [atha rattiyā (sī. syā.)] accayena;Hatā nāgassa acciyo honti [ahināgassa acciyo na honti (sī. syā.)];Iddhimato pana ṭhitā [iddhimato panuṭṭhitā (sī.)];Anekavaṇṇā acciyo honti.

Then, with the passing of that night, the fires of the nāga were extinguished; but for the one possessed of psychic power, they remained; the fires were of various colors.

Nīlā atha lohitikā;Mañjiṭṭhā pītakā phalikavaṇṇāyo;Aṅgīrasassa kāye;Anekavaṇṇā acciyo honti.

Blue, then red; Madder, yellow, crystal-hued; In Angirasa's body flames of many colors there were.

Pattamhi odahitvā;Ahināgaṃ brāhmaṇassa dassesi;‘‘Ayaṃ te kassapa nāgo;Pariyādinno assa tejasā tejo’’ti.

Having placed it in the bowl, he showed the brahmin the nāga: "Here, Kassapa, is your nāga, overcome, its fiery power by my own."

Atha kho uruvelakassapo jaṭilo bhagavato iminā iddhipāṭihāriyena abhippasanno bhagavantaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘idheva, mahāsamaṇa, vihara, ahaṃ te [te upaṭṭhāmi (itipi)] dhuvabhattenā’’ti.

Then Uruvelā Kassapa, the matted-hair ascetic, being exceedingly pleased by this display of psychic power, said to the Blessed One: "Dwell right here, Great Ascetic, and I will provide you with regular meals."

Paṭhamaṃ pāṭihāriyaṃ.

The first wonder.

40. Atha kho bhagavā uruvelakassapassa jaṭilassa assamassa avidūre aññatarasmiṃ vanasaṇḍe vihāsi. Atha kho cattāro mahārājāno abhikkantāya rattiyā abhikkantavaṇṇā kevalakappaṃ vanasaṇḍaṃ obhāsetvā yena bhagavā tenupasaṅkamiṃsu, upasaṅkamitvā bhagavantaṃ abhivādetvā catuddisā aṭṭhaṃsu seyyathāpi mahantā aggikkhandhā. Atha kho uruvelakassapo jaṭilo tassā rattiyā accayena yena bhagavā tenupasaṅkami, upasaṅkamitvā bhagavantaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘kālo, mahāsamaṇa, niṭṭhitaṃ bhattaṃ. Ke nu kho te, mahāsamaṇa, abhikkantāya rattiyā abhikkantavaṇṇā kevalakappaṃ vanasaṇḍaṃ obhāsetvā yena tvaṃ tenupasaṅkamiṃsu, upasaṅkamitvā taṃ abhivādetvā catuddisā aṭṭhaṃsu ‘‘seyyathāpi mahantā aggikkhandhā’’ti. ‘‘Ete kho, kassapa, cattāro mahārājāno yenāhaṃ tenupasaṅkamiṃsu dhammassavanāyā’’ti. Atha kho uruvelakassapassa jaṭilassa etadahosi – ‘‘mahiddhiko kho mahāsamaṇo mahānubhāvo, yatra hi nāma cattāropi mahārājāno upasaṅkamissanti dhammassavanāya, na tveva ca kho arahā yathā aha’’nti. Atha kho bhagavā uruvelakassapassa jaṭilassa bhattaṃ bhuñjitvā tasmiṃyeva vanasaṇḍe vihāsi.

40.Then the Blessed One dwelt in a certain grove not far from the hermitage of Uruvelā Kassapa, the matted-hair ascetic. Then, as the night was far advanced, the Four Great Kings, with surpassing radiance, illuminating the entire grove, approached the Blessed One. Having approached, they paid homage to the Blessed One and stood on four sides, like great masses of fire. Then, when the night had passed, Uruvelā Kassapa the matted-hair ascetic approached the Blessed One and said: "It is time, Great Ascetic; the meal is ready. Who were those, Great Ascetic, who as the night was far advanced, with surpassing radiance, illuminating the entire grove, approached you, paid homage, and stood on four sides like great masses of fire?" "Those, Kassapa, were the Four Great Kings who came to me to hear the Dhamma." Then Uruvelā Kassapa thought: "The Great Ascetic is indeed of great power and might, since even the Four Great Kings approach him to hear the Dhamma, but he is not an arahant like me." Then the Blessed One, having eaten the meal, dwelt in that same grove.

Dutiyaṃ pāṭihāriyaṃ.

The second wonder.

41. Atha kho sakko devānamindo abhikkantāya rattiyā abhikkantavaṇṇo kevalakappaṃ vanasaṇḍaṃ obhāsetvā yena bhagavā tenupasaṅkami, upasaṅkamitvā bhagavantaṃ abhivādetvā ekamantaṃ aṭṭhāsi seyyathāpi mahāaggikkhandho, purimāhi vaṇṇanibhāhi abhikkantataro ca paṇītataro ca. Atha kho uruvelakassapo jaṭilo tassā rattiyā accayena yena bhagavā tenupasaṅkami, upasaṅkamitvā bhagavantaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘kālo, mahāsamaṇa, niṭṭhitaṃ bhattaṃ. Ko nu kho so, mahāsamaṇa, abhikkantāya rattiyā abhikkantavaṇṇo kevalakappaṃ vanasaṇḍaṃ obhāsetvā yena tvaṃ tenupasaṅkami, upasaṅkamitvā taṃ abhivādetvā ekamantaṃ aṭṭhāsi seyyathāpi mahāaggikkhandho, purimāhi vaṇṇanibhāhi abhikkantataro ca paṇītataro cā’’ti? ‘‘Eso kho, kassapa, sakko devānamindo yenāhaṃ tenupasaṅkami dhammassavanāyā’’ti. Atha kho uruvelakassapassa jaṭilassa etadahosi – ‘‘mahiddhiko kho mahāsamaṇo mahānubhāvo, yatra hi nāma sakkopi devānamindo upasaṅkamissati dhammassavanāya, na tveva ca kho arahā yathā aha’’nti. Atha kho bhagavā uruvelakassapassa jaṭilassa bhattaṃ bhuñjitvā tasmiṃyeva vanasaṇḍe vihāsi.

41.Then Sakka, lord of the devas, when the night was far advanced, with surpassing radiance, illuminating the entire grove, approached the Blessed One. Having approached, he paid homage to the Blessed One and stood to one side like a great mass of fire, more splendid and refined than before. Then, when the night had passed, Uruvelā Kassapa the matted-hair ascetic approached the Blessed One and said: "It is time, Great Ascetic, the meal is ready. Who was that, Great Ascetic, who when the night was far advanced, with surpassing radiance, illuminating the entire grove, approached you, paid homage, and stood to one side like a great mass of fire, more splendid and refined than before?" "That, Kassapa, was Sakka, lord of the devas, who came to me to hear the Dhamma." Then Uruvelā Kassapa thought: "The Great Ascetic is indeed of great power and might, since even Sakka, lord of the devas, comes to hear the Dhamma, but he is not an arahant like me." Then the Blessed One, having eaten the meal, remained in that same grove.

Tatiyaṃ pāṭihāriyaṃ.

The third wonder.

42. Atha kho brahmā sahampati abhikkantāya rattiyā abhikkantavaṇṇo kevalakappaṃ vanasaṇḍaṃ obhāsetvā yena bhagavā tenupasaṅkami, upasaṅkamitvā bhagavantaṃ abhivādetvā ekamantaṃ aṭṭhāsi seyyathāpi mahāaggikkhandho, purimāhi vaṇṇanibhāhi abhikkantataro ca paṇītataro ca. Atha kho uruvelakassapo jaṭilo tassā rattiyā accayena yena bhagavā tenupasaṅkami, upasaṅkamitvā bhagavantaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘kālo, mahāsamaṇa, niṭṭhitaṃ bhattaṃ. Ko nu kho so, mahāsamaṇa, abhikkantāya rattiyā abhikkantavaṇṇo kevalakappaṃ vanasaṇḍaṃ obhāsetvā yena tvaṃ tenupasaṅkami, upasaṅkamitvā taṃ abhivādetvā ekamantaṃ aṭṭhāsi seyyathāpi mahāaggikkhandho, purimāhi vaṇṇanibhāhi abhikkantataro ca paṇītataro cā’’ti? ‘‘Eso kho, kassapa, brahmā sahampati yenāhaṃ tenupasaṅkami dhammassavanāyā’’ti. Atha kho uruvelakassapassa jaṭilassa etadahosi – ‘‘mahiddhiko kho mahāsamaṇo mahānubhāvo, yatra hi nāma brahmāpi sahampati upasaṅkamissati dhammassavanāya, na tveva ca kho arahā yathā aha’’nti. Atha kho bhagavā uruvelakassapassa jaṭilassa bhattaṃ bhuñjitvā tasmiṃyeva vanasaṇḍe vihāsi.

42.Then Brahmā Sahampati, when the night was far advanced, illuminating the entire grove with his surpassing radiance, approached the Blessed One. Having approached, he paid homage to the Blessed One and stood to one side, shining like a great mass of fire, more surpassingly radiant and excellent than his former radiance. Then, when that night had passed, the ascetic Uruvelā Kassapa approached the Blessed One and said: “It is time, great ascetic, the meal is ready. Who was that, great ascetic, who, when the night was far advanced, illuminating the entire grove with his surpassing radiance, approached you, paid homage to you, and stood to one side, shining like a great mass of fire, more surpassingly radiant and excellent than his former radiance?” “That, Kassapa, was Brahmā Sahampati, who approached me to hear the Dhamma.” Then it occurred to the ascetic Uruvelā Kassapa: “The great ascetic is indeed of great power and might, since even Brahmā Sahampati comes to hear the Dhamma. Yet he is not an arahant like me.” Then the Blessed One, having eaten the meal, remained dwelling in that same grove.

Catutthaṃ pāṭihāriyaṃ.

The fourth wonder.

43. Tena kho pana samayena uruvelakassapassa jaṭilassa mahāyañño paccupaṭṭhito hoti, kevalakappā ca aṅgamagadhā pahūtaṃ khādanīyaṃ bhojanīyaṃ ādāya abhikkamitukāmā honti. Atha kho uruvelakassapassa jaṭilassa etadahosi – ‘‘etarahi kho me mahāyañño paccupaṭṭhito, kevalakappā ca aṅgamagadhā pahūtaṃ khādanīyaṃ bhojanīyaṃ ādāya abhikkamissanti. Sace mahāsamaṇo mahājanakāye iddhipāṭihāriyaṃ karissati, mahāsamaṇassa lābhasakkāro abhivaḍḍhissati, mama lābhasakkāro parihāyissati. Aho nūna mahāsamaṇo svātanāya nāgaccheyyā’’ti. Atha kho bhagavā uruvelakassapassa jaṭilassa cetasā cetoparivitakkamaññāya uttarakuruṃ gantvā tato piṇḍapātaṃ āharitvā anotattadahe paribhuñjitvā tattheva divāvihāraṃ akāsi. Atha kho uruvelakassapo jaṭilo tassā rattiyā accayena yena bhagavā tenupasaṅkami, upasaṅkamitvā bhagavantaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘kālo, mahāsamaṇa, niṭṭhitaṃ bhattaṃ. Kiṃ nu kho, mahāsamaṇa, hiyyo nāgamāsi? Api ca mayaṃ taṃ sarāma – kiṃ nu kho mahāsamaṇo nāgacchatīti? Khādanīyassa ca bhojanīyassa ca te paṭivīso [paṭiviṃso (sī.), paṭiviso (syā.)] ṭhapito’’ti. Nanu te, kassapa, etadahosi – ‘‘‘etarahi kho me mahāyañño paccupaṭṭhito, kevalakappā ca aṅgamagadhā pahūtaṃ khādanīyaṃ bhojanīyaṃ ādāya abhikkamissanti, sace mahāsamaṇo mahājanakāye iddhipāṭihāriyaṃ karissati, mahāsamaṇassa lābhasakkāro abhivaḍḍhissati, mama lābhasakkāro parihāyissati, aho nūna mahāsamaṇo svātanāya nāgaccheyyā’ti. So kho ahaṃ, kassapa, tava cetasā cetoparivitakkaṃ aññāya uttarakuruṃ gantvā tato piṇḍapātaṃ āharitvā anotattadahe paribhuñjitvā tattheva divāvihāraṃ akāsi’’nti. Atha kho uruvelakassapassa jaṭilassa etadahosi – ‘‘mahiddhiko kho mahāsamaṇo mahānubhāvo, yatra hi nāma cetasāpi cittaṃ pajānissati, na tveva ca kho arahā yathā aha’’nti. Atha kho bhagavā uruvelakassapassa jaṭilassa bhattaṃ bhuñjitvā tasmiṃyeva vanasaṇḍe vihāsi.

43.Now at that time, a great sacrificial ceremony was prepared for the ascetic Uruvelā Kassapa. And the entire populace of Aṅga and Magadha were intending to come, bringing abundant solid and soft food. Then it occurred to the ascetic Uruvelā Kassapa: “Now a great sacrificial ceremony is prepared for me, and the entire populace of Aṅga and Magadha will come, bringing abundant solid and soft food. If the great ascetic performs a miracle in the midst of the great assembly, the great ascetic’s gain and honor will increase, and my gain and honor will decline. Oh, if only the great ascetic would not come tomorrow!” Then the Blessed One, knowing with his mind the thought of the ascetic Uruvelā Kassapa, went to Uttarakuru, brought almsfood from there, ate it at Lake Anotatta, and spent the day there. Then, when the night had passed, the ascetic Uruvelā Kassapa approached the Blessed One and said to him: “It is time, great ascetic, the meal is ready. Why, great ascetic, did you not come yesterday? We were indeed remembering you, thinking: ‘Why does the great ascetic not come?’ A portion of solid and soft food was set aside for you.” “Did it not occur to you, Kassapa: ‘Now a great sacrificial ceremony is prepared for me, and the entire populace of Aṅga and Magadha will come, bringing abundant solid and soft food. If the great ascetic performs a miracle in the midst of the great assembly, the great ascetic’s gain and honor will increase, and my gain and honor will decline. Oh, if only the great ascetic would not come tomorrow!’? Knowing with my mind, Kassapa, your thought, I went to Uttarakuru, brought almsfood from there, ate it at Lake Anotatta, and spent the day there.” Then it occurred to the ascetic Uruvelā Kassapa: “The great ascetic is indeed of great power and might, for he can know the thoughts of others with his mind. Yet he is not an arahant like me.” Then the Blessed One, having eaten the meal, remained dwelling in that same grove.

Pañcamaṃ pāṭihāriyaṃ.

The fifth wonder.

44. Tena kho pana samayena bhagavato paṃsukūlaṃ uppannaṃ hoti. Atha kho bhagavato etadahosi – ‘‘kattha nu kho ahaṃ paṃsukūlaṃ dhoveyya’’nti? Atha kho sakko devānamindo bhagavato cetasā cetoparivitakkamaññāya pāṇinā pokkharaṇiṃ khaṇitvā bhagavantaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘idha, bhante, bhagavā paṃsukūlaṃ dhovatū’’ti. Atha kho bhagavato etadahosi – ‘‘kimhi nu kho ahaṃ paṃsukūlaṃ parimaddeyya’’nti? Atha kho sakko devānamindo bhagavato cetasā cetoparivitakkamaññāya mahatiṃ silaṃ upanikkhipi – idha, bhante, bhagavā paṃsukūlaṃ parimaddatūti. Atha kho bhagavato etadahosi – ‘‘kimhi nu kho ahaṃ [ahaṃ paṃsukūlaṃ (ka.)] ālambitvā uttareyya’’nti? Atha kho kakudhe adhivatthā devatā bhagavato cetasā cetoparivitakkamaññāya sākhaṃ onāmesi – idha, bhante, bhagavā ālambitvā uttaratūti. Atha kho bhagavato etadahosi – ‘‘kimhi nu kho ahaṃ paṃsukūlaṃ vissajjeyya’’nti? Atha kho sakko devānamindo bhagavato cetasā cetoparivitakkamaññāya mahatiṃ silaṃ upanikkhipi – idha, bhante, bhagavā paṃsukūlaṃ vissajjetūti. Atha kho uruvelakassapo jaṭilo tassā rattiyā accayena yena bhagavā tenupasaṅkami, upasaṅkamitvā bhagavantaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘kālo, mahāsamaṇa, niṭṭhitaṃ bhattaṃ. Kiṃ nu kho, mahāsamaṇa, nāyaṃ pubbe idha pokkharaṇī, sāyaṃ idha pokkharaṇī. Nayimā silā pubbe upanikkhittā. Kenimā silā upanikkhittā? Nayimassa kakudhassa pubbe sākhā onatā, sāyaṃ sākhā onatā’’ti. Idha me, kassapa, paṃsukūlaṃ uppannaṃ ahosi. Tassa mayhaṃ, kassapa, etadahosi – ‘‘kattha nu kho ahaṃ paṃsukūlaṃ dhoveyya’’nti? Atha kho, kassapa, sakko devānamindo mama cetasā cetoparivitakkamaññāya pāṇinā pokkharaṇiṃ khaṇitvā maṃ etadavoca – ‘‘idha, bhante, bhagavā paṃsukūlaṃ dhovatū’’ti. Sāyaṃ kassapa amanussena pāṇinā khaṇitā pokkharaṇī. Tassa mayhaṃ, kassapa, etadahosi – ‘‘kimhi nu kho ahaṃ paṃsukūlaṃ parimaddeyya’’nti? Atha kho, kassapa, sakko devānamindo mama cetasā cetoparivitakkamaññāya mahatiṃ silaṃ upanikkhipi – ‘‘idha, bhante, bhagavā paṃsukūlaṃ parimaddatū’’ti. Sāyaṃ kassapa amanussena upanikkhittā silā. Tassa mayhaṃ, kassapa, etadahosi – ‘‘kimhi nu kho ahaṃ ālambitvā uttareyya’’nti? Atha kho, kassapa, kakudhe adhivatthā devatā ja mama cetasā cetoparivitakkamaññāya sākhaṃ onāmesi – ‘‘idha, bhante, bhagavā ālambitvā uttaratū’’ti. Svāyaṃ āharahattho kakudho. Tassa mayhaṃ, kassapa, etadahosi – ‘‘kimhi nu kho ahaṃ paṃsukūlaṃ vissajjeyya’’nti? Atha kho, kassapa, sakko devānamindo mama cetasā cetoparivitakkamaññāya mahatiṃ silaṃ upanikkhipi – ‘‘idha, bhante, bhagavā paṃsukūlaṃ vissajjetū’’ti. Sāyaṃ kassapa amanussena upanikkhittā silāti. Atha kho uruvelakassapassa jaṭilassa etadahosi – ‘‘mahiddhiko kho mahāsamaṇo mahānubhāvo, yatra hi nāma sakkopi devānamindo veyyāvaccaṃ karissati, na tveva ca kho arahā yathā aha’’nti. Atha kho bhagavā uruvelakassapassa jaṭilassa bhattaṃ bhuñjitvā tasmiṃyeva vanasaṇḍe vihāsi.

44.At that time, a rag-robe had appeared for the Blessed One. Then it occurred to the Blessed One: “Where now shall I wash this rag-robe?” Then Sakka, lord of the devas, knowing with his mind the Blessed One’s thought, dug a pond with his hand and said to the Blessed One: “Here, venerable sir, let the Blessed One wash the rag-robe.” Then it occurred to the Blessed One: “On what now shall I rub this rag-robe?” Then Sakka, lord of the devas, knowing with his mind the Blessed One’s thought, placed a large stone: “Here, venerable sir, let the Blessed One rub the rag-robe.” Then it occurred to the Blessed One: “What now shall I hold onto to climb out?” Then the deity dwelling in the kakudha tree, knowing with his mind the Blessed One’s thought, bent down a branch: “Here, venerable sir, let the Blessed One hold on and climb out.” Then it occurred to the Blessed One: “Where now shall I spread out this rag-robe to dry?” Then Sakka, lord of the devas, knowing with his mind the Blessed One’s thought, placed a large stone: “Here, venerable sir, let the Blessed One spread out the rag-robe to dry.” Then, when the night had passed, the ascetic Uruvelā Kassapa approached the Blessed One and said: “It is time, great ascetic, the meal is ready. But, great ascetic, this pond was not here before; now it is here. These stones were not placed here before; by whom were these stones placed here? The branch of this kakudha tree was not bent down before; now it is bent down.” “Here, Kassapa, a rag-robe had appeared for me. Then it occurred to me: ‘Where now shall I wash this rag-robe?’ Then, Kassapa, Sakka, lord of the devas, knowing with his mind my thought, dug a pond with his hand and said to me: ‘Here, venerable sir, let the Blessed One wash the rag-robe.’ This pond, Kassapa, was dug by a non-human hand. Then it occurred to me: ‘On what now shall I rub this rag-robe?’ Then, Kassapa, Sakka, lord of the devas, knowing with his mind my thought, placed a large stone: ‘Here, venerable sir, let the Blessed One rub the rag-robe.’ This stone, Kassapa, was placed by a non-human. Then it occurred to me: ‘What now shall I hold onto to climb out?’ Then, Kassapa, the deity dwelling in the kakudha tree, knowing with his mind my thought, bent down a branch: ‘Here, venerable sir, let the Blessed One hold on and climb out.’ This kakudha tree, Kassapa, is one that offers its branch. Then it occurred to me: ‘Where now shall I spread out this rag-robe to dry?’ Then, Kassapa, Sakka, lord of the devas, knowing with his mind my thought, placed a large stone: ‘Here, venerable sir, let the Blessed One spread out the rag-robe to dry.’ This stone, Kassapa, was placed by a non-human.” Then it occurred to the ascetic Uruvelā Kassapa: “The great ascetic is indeed of great power and might, since even Sakka, lord of the devas, performs services for him. Yet he is not an arahant like me.” Then the Blessed One, having eaten the meal, remained dwelling in that same grove.

Atha kho uruvelakassapo jaṭilo tassā rattiyā accayena yena bhagavā tenupasaṅkami, upasaṅkamitvā bhagavato kālaṃ ārocesi – ‘‘kālo, mahāsamaṇa, niṭṭhitaṃ bhatta’’nti. ‘‘Gaccha tvaṃ, kassapa, āyāmaha’’nti uruvelakassapaṃ jaṭilaṃ uyyojetvā yāya jambuyā ‘jambudīpo’ paññāyati, tato phalaṃ gahetvā paṭhamataraṃ āgantvā agyāgāre nisīdi. Addasā kho uruvelakassapo jaṭilo bhagavantaṃ agyāgāre nisinnaṃ, disvāna bhagavantaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘katamena tvaṃ, mahāsamaṇa, maggena āgato? Ahaṃ tayā paṭhamataraṃ pakkanto, so tvaṃ paṭhamataraṃ āgantvā agyāgāre nisinno’’ti. ‘‘Idhāhaṃ, kassapa, taṃ uyyojetvā yāya jambuyā ‘jambudīpo’ paññāyati, tato phalaṃ gahetvā paṭhamataraṃ āgantvā agyāgāre nisinno. Idaṃ kho, kassapa, jambuphalaṃ vaṇṇasampannaṃ gandhasampannaṃ rasasampannaṃ. Sace ākaṅkhasi paribhuñjā’’ti. ‘‘Alaṃ, mahāsamaṇa, tvaṃyeva taṃ arahasi, tvaṃyeva taṃ [tvaṃyevetaṃ āharasi, tvaṃyevetaṃ (sī. syā.)] paribhuñjāhī’’ti. Atha kho uruvelakassapassa jaṭilassa etadahosi – ‘‘mahiddhiko kho mahāsamaṇo mahānubhāvo, yatra hi nāma maṃ paṭhamataraṃ uyyojetvā yāya jambuyā ‘jambudīpo’ paññāyati, tato phalaṃ gahetvā paṭhamataraṃ āgantvā agyāgāre nisīdissati, na tveva ca kho arahā yathā aha’’nti. Atha kho bhagavā uruvelakassapassa jaṭilassa bhattaṃ bhuñjitvā tasmiṃyeva vanasaṇḍe vihāsi.

Then, when that night had passed, Uruvelā Kassapa the matted-hair ascetic approached the Blessed One and, on arrival, announced the time to him: “It is time, Great Ascetic, the meal is ready.” “Go, Kassapa, I am coming.” Dismissing Uruvelā Kassapa the matted-hair ascetic, he went to the Jambu tree by which Jambudīpa is known, took a fruit from it, arrived back before him, and sat down in the fire-chamber. Uruvelā Kassapa saw the Blessed One seated in the fire-chamber and said to him: “By what path did you come, Great Ascetic? I left before you, but you arrived before me and are seated in the fire-chamber.” “Here, Kassapa, after dismissing you, I went to the Jambu tree by which Jambudīpa is known, took a fruit from it, arrived back before you, and sat down in the fire-chamber. This, Kassapa, is a rose-apple fruit endowed with color, fragrance, and taste. If you wish, partake of it.” “Enough, Great Ascetic, you yourself are worthy of it, you yourself partake of it.” Then it occurred to Uruvelā Kassapa: “The Great Ascetic is indeed of great power and might, since, after dismissing me first, he went to the Jambu tree by which Jambudīpa is known, took a fruit from it, arrived back before me, and sat down in the fire-chamber. But still, he is not an arahant like me.” Then the Blessed One, having eaten the meal of Uruvelā Kassapa, remained right there in that grove.

45. Atha kho uruvelakassapo jaṭilo tassā rattiyā accayena yena bhagavā tenupasaṅkami, upasaṅkamitvā bhagavato kālaṃ ārocesi – ‘‘kālo, mahāsamaṇa, niṭṭhitaṃ bhatta’’nti. Gaccha tvaṃ, kassapa, āyāmahanti uruvelakassapaṃ jaṭilaṃ uyyojetvā yāya jambuyā ‘jambudīpo’ paññāyati, tassā avidūre ambo…pe… tassā avidūre āmalakī…pe… tassā avidūre harītakī…pe… tāvatiṃsaṃ gantvā pāricchattakapupphaṃ gahetvā paṭhamataraṃ āgantvā agyāgāre nisīdi. Addasā kho uruvelakassapo jaṭilo bhagavantaṃ agyāgāre nisinnaṃ, disvāna bhagavantaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘katamena tvaṃ, mahāsamaṇa, maggena āgato? Ahaṃ tayā paṭhamataraṃ pakkanto, so tvaṃ paṭhamataraṃ āgantvā agyāgāre nisinno’’ti. ‘‘Idhāhaṃ, kassapa, taṃ uyyojetvā tāvatiṃsaṃ gantvā pāricchattakapupphaṃ gahetvā paṭhamataraṃ āgantvā agyāgāre nisinno. Idaṃ kho, kassapa, pāricchattakapupphaṃ vaṇṇasampannaṃ gandhasampannaṃ [sugandhikaṃ (ka.)]. (Sace ākaṅkhasi gaṇhā’’ti. ‘‘Alaṃ, mahāsamaṇa, tvaṃyeva taṃ arahasi, tvaṃyeva taṃ gaṇhā’’ti) [( ) sī. syā. potthakesu natthi]. Atha kho uruvelakassapassa jaṭilassa etadahosi – ‘‘mahiddhiko kho mahāsamaṇo mahānubhāvo, yatra hi nāma maṃ paṭhamataraṃ uyyojetvā tāvatiṃsaṃ gantvā pāricchattakapupphaṃ gahetvā paṭhamataraṃ āgantvā agyāgāre nisīdissati, na tveva ca kho arahā yathā aha’’nti.

45.Then, when the night had passed, the ascetic Uruvelā Kassapa approached the Blessed One, and having approached, announced the time to the Blessed One: “It is time, great ascetic, the meal is ready.” “Go, Kassapa, I shall come.” Having dismissed the ascetic Uruvelā Kassapa, he went to the jambu tree by which Jambudīpa is known as ‘Jambudīpa’; then to the mango tree near which… to the emblic myrobalan tree near which… to the yellow myrobalan tree near which… then to the Tāvatiṃsa realm, took a pāricchattaka flower, and arriving before him, sat down in the fire chamber. The ascetic Uruvelā Kassapa saw the Blessed One seated in the fire chamber, and upon seeing him, said: “By which path, great ascetic, did you come? I departed before you, yet you arrived before me and are seated in the fire chamber.” “Here, Kassapa, after dismissing you, I went to the Tāvatiṃsa realm, took a pāricchattaka flower, and arriving before you, sat down in the fire chamber. This, Kassapa, is a pāricchattaka flower, endowed with color and fragrance. (If you wish, take it.)” “Enough, great ascetic, you are the one worthy of it, you should take it.” Then it occurred to the ascetic Uruvelā Kassapa: “The great ascetic is indeed of great power and might, in that after dismissing me before, he could go to the Tāvatiṃsa realm, take a pāricchattaka flower, arrive before me, and sit down in the fire chamber. Yet he is not an arahant like me.”

46. Tena kho pana samayena te jaṭilā aggiṃ paricaritukāmā na sakkonti kaṭṭhāni phāletuṃ. Atha kho tesaṃ jaṭilānaṃ etadahosi – ‘‘nissaṃsayaṃ kho mahāsamaṇassa iddhānubhāvo, yathā mayaṃ na sakkoma kaṭṭhāni phāletu’’nti. Atha kho bhagavā uruvelakassapaṃ jaṭilaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘phāliyantu, kassapa, kaṭṭhānī’’ti. ‘‘Phāliyantu, mahāsamaṇā’’ti. Sakideva pañca kaṭṭhasatāni phāliyiṃsu. Atha kho uruvelakassapassa jaṭilassa etadahosi – ‘‘mahiddhiko kho mahāsamaṇo mahānubhāvo, yatra hi nāma kaṭṭhānipi phāliyissanti, na tveva ca kho arahā yathā aha’’nti.

46.At that time, those matted-hair ascetics, wishing to tend the fire, were unable to split the firewood. Then it occurred to those matted-hair ascetics: “Surely the great ascetic possesses psychic power, since we cannot split the firewood.” Then the Blessed One said to Uruvela Kassapa the matted-hair ascetic: “Let the firewood be split, Kassapa.” “Let it be split, great ascetic.” Instantly, five hundred pieces of firewood split. Then it occurred to Uruvela Kassapa the matted-hair ascetic: “The great ascetic possesses great psychic power and might, since even the firewood splits. But he is not an arahant as I am.”

47. Tena kho pana samayena te jaṭilā aggiṃ paricaritukāmā na sakkonti aggiṃ ujjaletuṃ [jāletuṃ (sī.), ujjalituṃ (ka.)]. Atha kho tesaṃ jaṭilānaṃ etadahosi – ‘‘nissaṃsayaṃ kho mahāsamaṇassa iddhānubhāvo, yathā mayaṃ na sakkoma aggiṃ ujjaletu’’nti. Atha kho bhagavā uruvelakassapaṃ jaṭilaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘ujjaliyantu, kassapa, aggī’’ti. ‘‘Ujjaliyantu, mahāsamaṇā’’ti. Sakideva pañca aggisatāni ujjaliyiṃsu. Atha kho uruvelakassapassa jaṭilassa etadahosi – ‘‘mahiddhiko kho mahāsamaṇo mahānubhāvo, yatra hi nāma aggīpi ujjaliyissanti, na tveva ca kho arahā yathā aha’’nti.

47.At that time, those matted-hair ascetics, wishing to tend the fire, were unable to kindle the fire. Then it occurred to those matted-hair ascetics: “Surely the great ascetic possesses psychic power, since we are unable to kindle the fire.” Then the Blessed One said to Uruvela Kassapa the matted-hair ascetic: “Let the fires be kindled, Kassapa.” “Let them be kindled, great ascetic.” Instantly, five hundred fires blazed up. Then it occurred to Uruvela Kassapa the matted-hair ascetic: “The great ascetic possesses great psychic power and might, since even the fires blaze up. But he is not an arahant as I am.”

48. Tena kho pana samayena te jaṭilā aggiṃ paricaritvā na sakkonti aggiṃ vijjhāpetuṃ. Atha kho tesaṃ jaṭilānaṃ etadahosi – ‘‘nissaṃsayaṃ kho mahāsamaṇassa iddhānubhāvo, yathā mayaṃ na sakkoma aggiṃ vijjhāpetu’’nti. Atha kho bhagavā uruvelakassapaṃ jaṭilaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘vijjhāyantu, kassapa, aggī’’ti. ‘‘Vijjhāyantu, mahāsamaṇā’’ti. Sakideva pañca aggisatāni vijjhāyiṃsu. Atha kho uruvelakassapassa jaṭilassa etadahosi – ‘‘mahiddhiko kho mahāsamaṇo mahānubhāvo, yatra hi nāma aggīpi vijjhāyissanti, na tveva ca kho arahā yathā aha’’nti.

48.At that time, those matted-hair ascetics, having tended the fire, were unable to extinguish the fire. Then it occurred to those matted-hair ascetics: “Surely the great ascetic possesses psychic power, since we cannot extinguish the fire.” Then the Blessed One said to Uruvela Kassapa the matted-hair ascetic: “Let the fires be extinguished, Kassapa.” “Let them be extinguished, great ascetic.” Instantly, five hundred fires were extinguished. Then it occurred to Uruvela Kassapa the matted-hair ascetic: “The great ascetic possesses great psychic power and might, since even the fires are extinguished. But he is not an arahant as I am.”

49. Tena kho pana samayena te jaṭilā sītāsu hemantikāsu rattīsu antaraṭṭhakāsu himapātasamaye najjā nerañjarāya ummujjantipi, nimujjantipi, ummujjananimujjanampi karonti. Atha kho bhagavā pañcamattāni mandāmukhisatāni abhinimmini, yattha te jaṭilā uttaritvā visibbesuṃ. Atha kho tesaṃ jaṭilānaṃ etadahosi – ‘‘nissaṃsayaṃ kho mahāsamaṇassa iddhānubhāvo, yathayimā mandāmukhiyo nimmitā’’ti. Atha kho uruvelakassapassa jaṭilassa etadahosi – ‘‘mahiddhiko kho mahāsamaṇo mahānubhāvo, yatra hi nāma tāva bahū mandāmukhiyopi abhinimminissati, na tveva ca kho arahā yathā aha’’nti.

49.At that time, during the cold winter nights, at the time of snowfall, those matted-hair ascetics would emerge from and plunge into the Nerañjarā River, performing immersions and submersions. Then the Blessed One manifested five hundred heated braziers where those matted-hair ascetics could dry themselves after coming out. Then it occurred to those matted-hair ascetics: “Surely the great ascetic possesses psychic power, since these heated braziers have been created.” Then it occurred to Uruvela Kassapa the matted-hair ascetic: “The great ascetic possesses great psychic power and might, since he can manifest so many heated braziers. But he is not an arahant as I am.”

50. Tena kho pana samayena mahā akālamegho pāvassi, mahā udakavāhako sañjāyi. Yasmiṃ padese bhagavā viharati, so padeso udakena na otthaṭo [udakena otthaṭo (sī. syā.)] hoti. Atha kho bhagavato etadahosi – ‘‘yaṃnūnāhaṃ samantā udakaṃ ussāretvā majjhe reṇuhatāya bhūmiyā caṅkameyya’’nti. Atha kho bhagavā samantā udakaṃ ussāretvā majjhe reṇuhatāya bhūmiyā caṅkami. Atha kho uruvelakassapo jaṭilo – māheva kho mahāsamaṇo udakena vūḷho ahosīti nāvāya sambahulehi jaṭilehi saddhiṃ yasmiṃ padese bhagavā viharati taṃ padesaṃ agamāsi. Addasā kho uruvelakassapo jaṭilo bhagavantaṃ samantā udakaṃ ussāretvā majjhe reṇuhatāya bhūmiyā caṅkamantaṃ, disvāna bhagavantaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘idaṃ nu tvaṃ, mahāsamaṇā’’ti? ‘‘Ayamahamasmi [āma ahamasmi (syā.)], kassapā’’ti bhagavā vehāsaṃ abbhuggantvā nāvāya paccuṭṭhāsi. Atha kho uruvelakassapassa jaṭilassa etadahosi – ‘‘mahiddhiko kho mahāsamaṇo mahānubhāvo, yatra hi nāma udakampi na pavāhissati [nappasahissati (sī.)], na tveva ca kho arahā yathā aha’’nti.

50.Now at that time, a great untimely rainstorm poured down, and a great flood arose. The place where the Blessed One was staying was not submerged by the water. Then it occurred to the Blessed One: “Why don’t I push back the water all around and walk in the middle on dry ground?” Then the Blessed One pushed back the water all around and walked in the middle on dry ground. Then Uruvela Kassapa the matted-hair ascetic thought: “Surely the great ascetic has been swept away by the water!” So he took a boat and went with several other matted-hair ascetics to the place where the Blessed One was staying. Uruvela Kassapa the matted-hair ascetic saw the Blessed One pushing back the water all around and walking in the middle on dry ground. Seeing this, he said to the Blessed One: “Is that you, great ascetic?” “It is I, Kassapa,” the Blessed One replied, rising into the air and appearing on the boat. Then it occurred to Uruvela Kassapa the matted-hair ascetic: “The great ascetic possesses great psychic power and might, since even the water does not sweep him away. But he is not an arahant as I am.”

51. Atha kho bhagavato etadahosi – ‘‘cirampi kho imassa moghapurisassa evaṃ bhavissati – ‘mahiddhiko kho mahāsamaṇo mahānubhāvo, na tveva ca kho arahā yathā aha’nti; yaṃnūnāhaṃ imaṃ jaṭilaṃ saṃvejeyya’’nti. Atha kho bhagavā uruvelakassapaṃ jaṭilaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘neva ca kho tvaṃ, kassapa, arahā, nāpi arahattamaggasamāpanno. Sāpi te paṭipadā natthi, yāya tvaṃ arahā vā assasi, arahattamaggaṃ vā samāpanno’’ti. Atha kho uruvelakassapo jaṭilo bhagavato pādesu sirasā nipatitvā bhagavantaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘labheyyāhaṃ, bhante, bhagavato santike pabbajjaṃ, labheyyaṃ upasampada’’nti. Tvaṃ khosi, kassapa, pañcannaṃ jaṭilasatānaṃ nāyako vināyako aggo pamukho pāmokkho. Tepi tāva apalokehi, yathā te maññissanti tathā te karissantīti. Atha kho uruvelakassapo jaṭilo yena te jaṭilā tenupasaṅkami, upasaṅkamitvā te jaṭile etadavoca – ‘‘icchāmahaṃ, bho, mahāsamaṇe brahmacariyaṃ carituṃ, yathā bhavanto maññanti tathā karontū’’ti. ‘‘Cirapaṭikā mayaṃ, bho, mahāsamaṇe abhippasannā, sace bhavaṃ, mahāsamaṇe brahmacariyaṃ carissati, sabbeva mayaṃ mahāsamaṇe brahmacariyaṃ carissāmā’’ti. Atha kho te jaṭilā kesamissaṃ jaṭāmissaṃ khārikājamissaṃ aggihutamissaṃ udake pavāhetvā yena bhagavā tenupasaṅkamiṃsu, upasaṅkamitvā bhagavato pādesu sirasā nipatitvā bhagavantaṃ etadavocuṃ – ‘‘labheyyāma mayaṃ, bhante, bhagavato santike pabbajjaṃ, labheyyāma upasampada’’nti. ‘‘Etha bhikkhavo’’ti bhagavā avoca – ‘‘svākkhāto dhammo, caratha brahmacariyaṃ sammā dukkhassa antakiriyāyā’’ti. Sāva tesaṃ āyasmantānaṃ upasampadā ahosi.

51.Then it occurred to the Blessed One: “For a long time this foolish man will be thinking, ‘The great ascetic possesses great psychic power and might, yet he is not an arahant as I am.’ Suppose I were to stir this matted-hair ascetic.” Then the Blessed One said to Uruvela Kassapa the matted-hair ascetic: “You, Kassapa, are not an arahant, nor have you attained the path to arahantship. And that practice of yours does not exist by which you might be an arahant or have attained the path to arahantship.” Then Uruvela Kassapa the matted-hair ascetic bowed his head at the Blessed One’s feet and said: “May I receive the going forth, Venerable Sir, in the presence of the Blessed One; may I receive full ordination.” “But you, Kassapa, are the leader, the guide, the chief, the foremost, the principal of five hundred matted-hair ascetics. Go and consult them first, so they may do as they think fit.” Then Uruvela Kassapa the matted-hair ascetic went to those matted-hair ascetics and said: “I wish, friends, to lead the holy life under the great ascetic. Let the venerable ones do as they think fit.” “For a long time, friend, we have been pleased with the great ascetic. If you lead the holy life under the great ascetic, we will all lead the holy life under the great ascetic.” Then those matted-hair ascetics cast their hair, matted locks, ash-implements, and fire-offering implements into the water and approached the Blessed One. Having approached, they bowed their heads at the Blessed One’s feet and said: “May we receive the going forth, Venerable Sir, in the presence of the Blessed One; may we receive full ordination.” “Come, monks,” the Blessed One said, “the Dhamma is well proclaimed. Live the holy life for the complete ending of suffering.” That itself was their ordination as venerable ones.”
