> "VIN-MV1.15" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


15.Account of Duties to the Preceptor

64. Tena kho pana samayena bhikkhū anupajjhāyakā anācariyakā [idaṃ padaṃ sī. syā. potthakesu natthi] anovadiyamānā ananusāsiyamānā dunnivatthā duppārutā anākappasampannā piṇḍāya caranti; manussānaṃ [te manussānaṃ (ka.)] bhuñjamānānaṃ uparibhojanepi uttiṭṭhapattaṃ upanāmenti, uparikhādanīyepi uttiṭṭhapattaṃ upanāmenti, uparisāyanīyepi uttiṭṭhapattaṃ upanāmenti, uparipānīyepi uttiṭṭhapattaṃ upanāmenti; sāmaṃ sūpampi odanampi viññāpetvā bhuñjanti; bhattaggepi uccāsaddā mahāsaddā viharanti. Manussā ujjhāyanti khiyyanti vipācenti – ‘‘kathañhi nāma samaṇā sakyaputtiyā dunnivatthā duppārutā anākappasampannā piṇḍāya carissanti; manussānaṃ bhuñjamānānaṃ, uparibhojanepi uttiṭṭhapattaṃ upanāmessanti, uparikhādanīyepi uttiṭṭhapattaṃ upanāmessanti, uparisāyanīyepi uttiṭṭhapattaṃ upanāmessanti, uparipānīyepi uttiṭṭhapattaṃ upanāmessanti; sāmaṃ sūpampi odanampi viññāpetvā bhuñjissanti; bhattaggepi uccāsaddā mahāsaddā viharissanti seyyathāpi brāhmaṇā brāhmaṇabhojane’’ti.

64.Now at that time monks without preceptors, without teachers, not being admonished or instructed, wandered for alms poorly dressed, improperly clad, lacking in proper conduct. While people were eating, they would hold out a bowl for food from which one has risen, for edibles from which one has risen, for delicacies from which one has risen, for drinks from which one has risen. They would ask for soup and rice and eat it. In the dining hall, they lived making loud and great noises. People complained, criticized, and grumbled: "How can these Sakyan ascetics wander for alms poorly dressed, improperly clad, lacking in proper conduct? While people are eating, they hold out a bowl for food from which one has risen, for edibles from which one has risen, for delicacies from which one has risen, for drinks from which one has risen. They ask for soup and rice and eat it. In the dining hall, they live making loud and great noises, just like brahmins at a brahmin feast!"

Assosuṃ kho bhikkhū tesaṃ manussānaṃ ujjhāyantānaṃ khiyyantānaṃ vipācentānaṃ. Ye te bhikkhū appicchā santuṭṭhā lajjino kukkuccakā sikkhākāmā, te ujjhāyanti khiyyanti vipācenti – ‘‘kathañhi nāma bhikkhū dunnivatthā duppārutā anākappasampannā piṇḍāya carissanti; manussānaṃ bhuñjamānānaṃ, uparibhojanepi uttiṭṭhapattaṃ upanāmessanti, uparikhādanīyepi uttiṭṭhapattaṃ upanāmessanti, uparisāyanīyepi uttiṭṭhapattaṃ upanāmessanti, uparipānīyepi uttiṭṭhapattaṃ upanāmessanti; sāmaṃ sūpampi odanampi viññāpetvā bhuñjissanti; bhattaggepi uccāsaddā mahāsaddā viharissantī’’ti. Atha kho te bhikkhū…pe… bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ.

The monks heard those people complaining, grumbling, and criticizing. Those monks who were modest, content, conscientious, scrupulous, and desirous of training complained, grumbled, and criticized, "How can monks go for alms poorly dressed, improperly covered, and lacking decorum? While people are eating, they hold out a bowl for food from which one has risen, for edibles from which one has risen, for delicacies from which one has risen, and for drinks from which one has risen. They even ask for soup and rice for themselves and then eat. And in the refectory, they live making loud noises and great noises." Then those monks… reported this matter to the Blessed One.

Atha kho bhagavā etasmiṃ nidāne etasmiṃ pakaraṇe bhikkhusaṅghaṃ sannipātāpetvā bhikkhū paṭipucchi – ‘‘saccaṃ kira, bhikkhave, bhikkhū dunnivatthā duppārutā anākappasampannā piṇḍāya caranti, manussānaṃ bhuñjamānānaṃ upari bhojanepi uttiṭṭhapattaṃ upanāmenti, uparikhādanīyepi uttiṭṭhapattaṃ upanāmenti, uparisāyanīyepi uttiṭṭhapattaṃ upanāmenti, uparipānīyepi uttiṭṭhapattaṃ upanāmenti, sāmaṃ sūpampi odanampi viññāpetvā bhuñjanti, bhattaggepi uccāsaddā mahāsaddā viharantī’’ti? ‘‘Saccaṃ bhagavā’’ti. Vigarahi buddho bhagavā – ‘‘ananucchavikaṃ, bhikkhave, tesaṃ moghapurisānaṃ ananulomikaṃ appatirūpaṃ assāmaṇakaṃ akappiyaṃ akaraṇīyaṃ. Kathañhi nāma te, bhikkhave, moghapurisā dunnivatthā duppārutā anākappasampannā piṇḍāya carissanti, manussānaṃ bhuñjamānānaṃ uparibhojanepi uttiṭṭhapattaṃ upanāmessanti, uparikhādanīyepi uttiṭṭhapattaṃ upanāmessanti, uparisāyanīyepi uttiṭṭhapattaṃ upanāmessanti, uparipānīyepi uttiṭṭhapattaṃ upanāmessanti, sāmaṃ sūpampi odanampi viññāpetvā bhuñjissanti, bhattaggepi uccāsaddā mahāsaddā viharissanti. Netaṃ, bhikkhave, appasannānaṃ vā pasādāya, pasannānaṃ vā bhiyyobhāvāya. Atha khvetaṃ, bhikkhave, appasannānañceva appasādāya, pasannānañca ekaccānaṃ aññathattāyā’’ti. Atha kho bhagavā te bhikkhū anekapariyāyena vigarahitvā dubbharatāya dupposatāya mahicchatāya asantuṭṭhitāya [asantuṭṭhiyā (sī.), asantuṭṭhatāya (syā)] saṅgaṇikāya kosajjassa avaṇṇaṃ bhāsitvā anekapariyāyena subharatāya suposatāya appicchassa santuṭṭhassa sallekhassa dhutassa pāsādikassa apacayassa vīriyārambhassa [viriyārambhassa (sī. syā.)] vaṇṇaṃ bhāsitvā bhikkhūnaṃ tadanucchavikaṃ tadanulomikaṃ dhammiṃ kathaṃ katvā bhikkhū āmantesi –

Then the Blessed One, regarding this incident, on this occasion, convened the Sangha of monks, questioned the monks: "Is it true, monks, that monks, poorly dressed, improperly clad, without proper deportment, go for alms, and while people are eating, hold out a bowl for food from which one has risen, for edibles from which one has risen, for delicacies from which one has risen, for drinks from which one has risen; that they themselves ask for and eat both soup and rice; and that they live with loud and excessive noise in the refectory?" "It is true, Blessed One." The Blessed One rebuked them: "It is unseemly, monks, unsuitable for these foolish men, inappropriate, unworthy of ascetics, unlawful, not to be done. How could these foolish men, monks, poorly dressed, improperly clad, without proper deportment, go for alms, and while people are eating, hold out a bowl for food from which one has risen, for edibles from which one has risen, for delicacies from which one has risen, for drinks from which one has risen; that they themselves ask for and eat both soup and rice; and that they live with loud and excessive noise in the refectory? This, monks, will not lead to confidence in the unconvinced, nor to increase in the convinced. Rather, monks, it will lead to lack of confidence in the unconvinced and to the changing of mind in some of the convinced." Then the Blessed One, having rebuked those monks in many ways, having spoken in dispraise of being difficult to support, difficult to nourish, very ambitious, discontented, fond of society, and indolent, having praised in many ways being easy to support, easy to nourish, having few wishes, being content, austere, refined, inspiring confidence, modest, energetic, gave a Dhamma talk appropriate and suitable for the monks, and then addressed them:

65. ‘‘Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, upajjhāyaṃ. Upajjhāyo, bhikkhave, saddhivihārikamhi puttacittaṃ upaṭṭhapessati, saddhivihāriko upajjhāyamhi pitucittaṃ upaṭṭhapessati. Evaṃ te aññamaññaṃ sagāravā sappatissā sabhāgavuttino viharantā imasmiṃ dhammavinaye vuḍḍhiṃ viruḷhiṃ vepullaṃ āpajjissanti. Evañca pana, bhikkhave, upajjhāyo gahetabbo – ekaṃsaṃ uttarāsaṅgaṃ karitvā pāde vanditvā ukkuṭikaṃ nisīditvā añjaliṃ paggahetvā evamassa vacanīyo – ‘upajjhāyo me, bhante, hohi; upajjhāyo me, bhante, hohi; upajjhāyo me, bhante, hohī’ti. Sāhūti vā lahūti vā opāyikanti vā patirūpanti vā pāsādikena sampādehīti vā kāyena viññāpeti, vācāya viññāpeti, kāyena vācāya [na vācāya (ka.)] viññāpeti, gahito hoti upajjhāyo; na kāyena viññāpeti, na vācāya viññāpeti, na kāyena vācāya viññāpeti, na gahito hoti upajjhāyo.

65."I allow, monks, a preceptor. The preceptor, monks, should establish a parental attitude toward the student, and the student should establish a filial attitude toward the preceptor. Thus, living with mutual respect, deference, and shared good conduct, they will attain growth, development, and abundance in this Dhamma and Discipline. And, monks, the preceptor should be accepted in this way: Having arranged the upper robe over one shoulder, bowing at the feet, sitting in a squatting position, raising joined palms, one should say: 'Venerable sir, be my preceptor; venerable sir, be my preceptor; venerable sir, be my preceptor.' If he indicates acceptance by body, speech, or both—whether by saying 'Good,' 'Very well,' 'It is possible,' 'Suitable,' or 'Accomplish it with confidence'—then the preceptor is accepted. If he does not indicate acceptance by body, speech, or both, then the preceptor is not accepted."

66. [cūḷava. 376 ādayo]‘‘Saddhivihārikena, bhikkhave, upajjhāyamhi sammā vattitabbaṃ. Tatrāyaṃ sammāvattanā –

66."Monks, a student should behave properly towards his preceptor. This is the proper conduct:

‘‘Kālasseva vuṭṭhāya upāhanā omuñcitvā ekaṃsaṃ uttarāsaṅgaṃ karitvā dantakaṭṭhaṃ dātabbaṃ, mukhodakaṃ dātabbaṃ, āsanaṃ paññapetabbaṃ. Sace yāgu hoti, bhājanaṃ dhovitvā yāgu upanāmetabbā. Yāguṃ pītassa udakaṃ datvā bhājanaṃ paṭiggahetvā nīcaṃ katvā sādhukaṃ appaṭighaṃsantena dhovitvā paṭisāmetabbaṃ. Upajjhāyamhi vuṭṭhite āsanaṃ uddharitabbaṃ. Sace so deso uklāpo hoti, so deso sammajjitabbo.

"Rising early in the morning, one should remove the sandals, arrange the upper robe over one shoulder, and offer a tooth-stick and water for washing the mouth. A seat should be arranged. If there is rice-gruel, the bowl should be washed and the rice-gruel offered. After the rice-gruel has been drunk, water should be given, the bowl received, lowered, and carefully washed without knocking it about, then put away. When the preceptor rises, the seat should be removed. If that place is untidy, that place should be swept."

‘‘Sace upajjhāyo gāmaṃ pavisitukāmo hoti, nivāsanaṃ dātabbaṃ, paṭinivāsanaṃ paṭiggahetabbaṃ, kāyabandhanaṃ dātabbaṃ, saguṇaṃ katvā saṅghāṭiyo dātabbā, dhovitvā patto sodako [saudako (ka.)] dātabbo. Sace upajjhāyo pacchāsamaṇaṃ ākaṅkhati, timaṇḍalaṃ paṭicchādentena parimaṇḍalaṃ nivāsetvā kāyabandhanaṃ bandhitvā saguṇaṃ katvā saṅghāṭiyo pārupitvā gaṇṭhikaṃ paṭimuñcitvā dhovitvā pattaṃ gahetvā upajjhāyassa pacchāsamaṇena hotabbaṃ. Nātidūre gantabbaṃ, nāccāsanne gantabbaṃ, pattapariyāpannaṃ paṭiggahetabbaṃ. Na upajjhāyassa bhaṇamānassa antarantarā kathā opātetabbā. Upajjhāyo āpattisāmantā bhaṇamāno nivāretabbo.

If the preceptor wishes to enter the village, the lower robe should be given, the outer robe received, the belt offered, and the outer robes should be made into one and given. The bowl should be washed and filled with water, and given. If the preceptor desires an attendant, covering the three circles (of the body), one should wear the lower robe evenly, fasten the belt, make the outer robes into one and put them on, untie the knot, take the washed bowl, and attend the preceptor as his follower. One should not walk too far behind, nor too close. The bowl should be received as required. One should not interrupt the preceptor while he is speaking. If the preceptor speaks within the vicinity of an offense, he should be restrained.

‘‘Nivattantena paṭhamataraṃ āgantvā āsanaṃ paññapetabbaṃ, pādodakaṃ pādapīṭhaṃ pādakathalikaṃ upanikkhipitabbaṃ, paccuggantvā pattacīvaraṃ paṭiggahetabbaṃ, paṭinivāsanaṃ dātabbaṃ, nivāsanaṃ paṭiggahetabbaṃ. Sace cīvaraṃ sinnaṃ hoti, muhuttaṃ uṇhe otāpetabbaṃ, na ca uṇhe cīvaraṃ nidahitabbaṃ; cīvaraṃ saṅgharitabbaṃ, cīvaraṃ saṅgharantena caturaṅgulaṃ kaṇṇaṃ ussāretvā cīvaraṃ saṅgharitabbaṃ – mā majjhe bhaṅgo ahosīti. Obhoge kāyabandhanaṃ kātabbaṃ.

Upon returning, one should arrive first and prepare a seat. Foot-water, a footstool, and a foot-wiper should be set out. Going to meet him, the bowl and robe should be received, the outer robe given, and the lower robe received. If the robe is damp, it should be briefly warmed in the sun, but the robe should not be left in the sun. The robe should be folded; when folding, the corner should be raised four finger-widths to prevent a crease in the middle. The belt should be arranged in the hem.

‘‘Sace piṇḍapāto hoti, upajjhāyo ca bhuñjitukāmo hoti, udakaṃ datvā piṇḍapāto upanāmetabbo. Upajjhāyo pānīyena pucchitabbo. Bhuttāvissa udakaṃ datvā pattaṃ paṭiggahetvā nīcaṃ katvā sādhukaṃ appaṭighaṃsantena dhovitvā vodakaṃ katvā muhuttaṃ uṇhe otāpetabbo, na ca uṇhe patto nidahitabbo. Pattacīvaraṃ nikkhipitabbaṃ. Pattaṃ nikkhipantena ekena hatthena pattaṃ gahetvā ekena hatthena heṭṭhāmañcaṃ vā heṭṭhāpīṭhaṃ vā parāmasitvā patto nikkhipitabbo. Na ca anantarahitāya bhūmiyā patto nikkhipitabbo. Cīvaraṃ nikkhipantena ekena hatthena cīvaraṃ gahetvā ekena hatthena cīvaravaṃsaṃ vā cīvararajjuṃ vā pamajjitvā pārato antaṃ orato bhogaṃ katvā cīvaraṃ nikkhipitabbaṃ. Upajjhāyamhi vuṭṭhite āsanaṃ uddharitabbaṃ, pādodakaṃ pādapīṭhaṃ pādakathalikaṃ paṭisāmetabbaṃ. Sace so deso uklāpo hoti, so deso sammajjitabbo.

If there is almsfood and the preceptor wishes to eat, water should be given and the almsfood presented to him. The preceptor should be asked if he needs drinking water. After he has eaten, water should be given, the bowl received, lowered, washed well without scraping, made waterless, and briefly exposed to the sun—but the bowl should not be left in the sun. The bowl and robe should be put away. When placing the bowl, one should hold the bowl with one hand and touch the lower cot or lower seat with the other hand before setting the bowl down. The bowl should not be placed directly on the bare ground. When putting away the robe, one should hold the robe with one hand, wipe the robe-rack or robe-cord with the other, fold the edge inward from the outer end, and put the robe away. When the preceptor rises, the seat should be removed, and the foot-water, footstool, and foot-wiper returned to their place. If the place is untidy, it should be swept.

‘‘Sace upajjhāyo nahāyitukāmo hoti, nahānaṃ paṭiyādetabbaṃ. Sace sītena attho hoti, sītaṃ paṭiyādetabbaṃ. Sace uṇhena attho hoti, uṇhaṃ paṭiyādetabbaṃ.

If the preceptor wishes to bathe, bathing arrangements should be made. If he needs cold water, cold water should be prepared; if he needs warm water, warm water should be prepared.

‘‘Sace upajjhāyo jantāgharaṃ pavisitukāmo hoti, cuṇṇaṃ sannetabbaṃ, mattikā temetabbā, jantāgharapīṭhaṃ ādāya upajjhāyassa piṭṭhito piṭṭhito gantvā jantāgharapīṭhaṃ datvā cīvaraṃ paṭiggahetvā ekamantaṃ nikkhipitabbaṃ, cuṇṇaṃ dātabbaṃ, mattikā dātabbā. Sace ussahati, jantāgharaṃ pavisitabbaṃ. Jantāgharaṃ pavisantena mattikāya mukhaṃ makkhetvā purato ca pacchato ca paṭicchādetvā jantāgharaṃ pavisitabbaṃ. Na there bhikkhū anupakhajja nisīditabbaṃ. Na navā bhikkhū āsanena paṭibāhitabbā. Jantāghare upajjhāyassa parikammaṃ kātabbaṃ. Jantāgharā nikkhamantena jantāgharapīṭhaṃ ādāya purato ca pacchato ca paṭicchādetvā jantāgharā nikkhamitabbaṃ.

If the preceptor wishes to enter the hot room, powder should be prepared, clay should be soaked, and, taking the hot room stool, one should follow behind the preceptor. After giving the hot room stool, the robe should be received and set aside. Powder should be given, clay should be given. If one is capable, one should enter the hot room. When entering the hot room, one should smear the face with clay, cover oneself in front and behind, and then enter the hot room. One should not sit crowding the senior monks. Junior monks should not be pushed away from their seats. In the hot room, one should attend to the preceptor’s needs. When leaving the hot room, one should take the hot room stool, cover oneself in front and behind, and then exit the hot room.

‘‘Udakepi upajjhāyassa parikammaṃ kātabbaṃ. Nahātena paṭhamataraṃ uttaritvā attano gattaṃ vodakaṃ katvā nivāsetvā upajjhāyassa gattato udakaṃ pamajjitabbaṃ, nivāsanaṃ dātabbaṃ, saṅghāṭi dātabbā, jantāgharapīṭhaṃ ādāya paṭhamataraṃ āgantvā āsanaṃ paññapetabbaṃ, pādodakaṃ pādapīṭhaṃ pādakathalikaṃ upanikkhipitabbaṃ, upajjhāyo pānīyena pucchitabbo. Sace uddisāpetukāmo hoti, uddisitabbo. Sace paripucchitukāmo hoti, paripucchitabbo.

One should also attend to the preceptor’s needs regarding water. After bathing, one should emerge first, dry one's body, put on the lower robe, and then wipe the water from the preceptor’s body. The lower robe should be given, the outer robe should be given. Taking the hot-bath stool, one should return first, prepare the seat, set out foot-washing water, a footstool, and a foot-wiping cloth. The preceptor should be asked if he desires drinking water. If he wishes to be taught, he should be taught. If he wishes to question, he should be questioned.

‘‘Yasmiṃ vihāre upajjhāyo viharati, sace so vihāro uklāpo hoti, sace ussahati, sodhetabbo. Vihāraṃ sodhentena paṭhamaṃ pattacīvaraṃ nīharitvā ekamantaṃ nikkhipitabbaṃ. Nisīdanapaccattharaṇaṃ nīharitvā ekamantaṃ nikkhipitabbaṃ. Bhisibibbohanaṃ [bhisibimbohanaṃ (sī. syā.)] nīharitvā ekamantaṃ nikkhipitabbaṃ. Mañco nīcaṃ katvā sādhukaṃ appaṭighaṃsantena, asaṅghaṭṭentena kavāṭapiṭṭhaṃ, nīharitvā ekamantaṃ nikkhipitabbo. Pīṭhaṃ nīcaṃ katvā sādhukaṃ appaṭighaṃsantena, asaṅghaṭṭentena kavāṭapiṭṭhaṃ, nīharitvā ekamantaṃ nikkhipitabbaṃ. Mañcapaṭipādakā nīharitvā ekamantaṃ nikkhipitabbā. Kheḷamallako nīharitvā ekamantaṃ nikkhipitabbo. Apassenaphalakaṃ nīharitvā ekamantaṃ nikkhipitabbaṃ. Bhūmattharaṇaṃ yathāpaññattaṃ sallakkhetvā nīharitvā ekamantaṃ nikkhipitabbaṃ. Sace vihāre santānakaṃ hoti, ullokā paṭhamaṃ ohāretabbaṃ, ālokasandhikaṇṇabhāgā pamajjitabbā. Sace gerukaparikammakatā bhitti kaṇṇakitā hoti, coḷakaṃ temetvā pīḷetvā pamajjitabbā. Sace kāḷavaṇṇakatā bhūmi kaṇṇakitā hoti, coḷakaṃ temetvā pīḷetvā pamajjitabbā. Sace akatā hoti bhūmi, udakena paripphositvā sammajjitabbā – mā vihāro rajena uhaññīti. Saṅkāraṃ vicinitvā ekamantaṃ chaḍḍetabbaṃ.

“In whichever dwelling the preceptor resides, if that dwelling is untidy, and if one is capable, it should be cleaned. When cleaning the dwelling, one should first remove the bowl and robe and set them aside. One should remove the sitting cloth and set it aside. One should remove the mattress and pillow and set them aside. Lowering the bed carefully, without scraping or bumping it against the doorposts, one should remove it and set it aside. Lowering the stool carefully, without scraping or bumping it against the doorposts, one should remove it and set it aside. One should remove the bed legs and set them aside. One should remove the spittoon and set it aside. One should remove the backrest and set it aside. Examining the floor covering as laid out, one should remove it and set it aside. If the dwelling has cobwebs, one should first take them down from above, and wipe the window sills and corners. If the walls, treated with red ochre, have become stained, one should moisten a cloth, wring it out, and wipe them. If the floor, treated with black coloring, has become stained, one should moisten a cloth, wring it out, and wipe it. If the floor is untreated, one should sprinkle it with water and sweep it—lest the dwelling be soiled with dust. One should gather the rubbish and discard it to one side.”

‘‘Bhūmattharaṇaṃ otāpetvā sodhetvā papphoṭetvā atiharitvā yathāpaññattaṃ paññapetabbaṃ. Mañcapaṭipādakā otāpetvā pamajjitvā atiharitvā yathāṭhāne ṭhapetabbā. Mañco otāpetvā sodhetvā papphoṭetvā nīcaṃ katvā sādhukaṃ appaṭighaṃsantena, asaṅghaṭṭentena kavāṭapiṭṭhaṃ, atiharitvā yathāpaññattaṃ paññapetabbo. Pīṭhaṃ otāpetvā sodhetvā papphoṭetvā nīcaṃ katvā sādhukaṃ appaṭighaṃsantena, asaṅghaṭṭentena kavāṭapiṭṭhaṃ, atiharitvā yathāpaññattaṃ paññapetabbaṃ. Bhisibibbohanaṃ otāpetvā sodhetvā papphoṭetvā atiharitvā yathāpaññattaṃ paññapetabbaṃ. Nisīdanapaccattharaṇaṃ otāpetvā sodhetvā papphoṭetvā atiharitvā yathāpaññattaṃ paññapetabbaṃ. Kheḷamallako otāpetvā pamajjitvā atiharitvā yathāṭhāne ṭhapetabbo. Apassenaphalakaṃ otāpetvā pamajjitvā atiharitvā yathāṭhāne ṭhapetabbaṃ. Pattacīvaraṃ nikkhipitabbaṃ. Pattaṃ nikkhipantena ekena hatthena pattaṃ gahetvā ekena hatthena heṭṭhāmañcaṃ vā heṭṭhāpīṭhaṃ vā parāmasitvā patto nikkhipitabbo. Na ca anantarahitāya bhūmiyā patto nikkhipitabbo. Cīvaraṃ nikkhipantena ekena hatthena cīvaraṃ gahetvā ekena hatthena cīvaravaṃsaṃ vā cīvararajjuṃ vā pamajjitvā pārato antaṃ orato bhogaṃ katvā cīvaraṃ nikkhipitabbaṃ.

Having aired the floor covering, one should clean it, shake it out, bring it in, and arrange it as prescribed. One should wipe the bed legs, bring them in, and set them in their proper places. Having cleaned the bed and shaken it out, one should lower it carefully, without scraping or bumping it against the doorposts, bring it in, and arrange it as prescribed. Having cleaned the stool and shaken it out, one should lower it carefully, without scraping or bumping it against the doorposts, bring it in, and arrange it as prescribed. Having cleaned the mattress and pillow and shaken them out, one should bring them in and arrange them as prescribed. Having cleaned the sitting cloth and shaken it out, one should bring it in and arrange it as prescribed. One should wipe the spittoon, bring it in, and set it in its proper place. One should wipe the backrest, bring it in, and set it in its proper place. The bowl and robe should be put away. When putting away the bowl, one should hold it with one hand and touch underneath the bed or stool with the other before setting the bowl down. The bowl should not be set directly on the bare ground. When putting away the robe, one should hold it with one hand and wipe the robe-rack or clothesline with the other, then fold the robe inwards from the edge and put it away.

‘‘Sace puratthimā sarajā vātā vāyanti, puratthimā vātapānā thaketabbā. Sace pacchimā sarajā vātā vāyanti, pacchimā vātapānā thaketabbā. Sace uttarā sarajā vātā vāyanti, uttarā vātapānā thaketabbā. Sace dakkhiṇā sarajā vātā vāyanti, dakkhiṇā vātapānā thaketabbā. Sace sītakālo hoti, divā vātapānā vivaritabbā, rattiṃ thaketabbā. Sace uṇhakālo hoti, divā vātapānā thaketabbā, rattiṃ vivaritabbā.

If dusty winds blow from the east, the eastern windows should be closed. If dusty winds blow from the west, the western windows should be closed. If dusty winds blow from the north, the northern windows should be closed. If dusty winds blow from the south, the southern windows should be closed. If it is the cold season, the windows should be opened during the day and closed at night. If it is the hot season, the windows should be closed during the day and opened at night.

‘‘Sace pariveṇaṃ uklāpaṃ hoti, pariveṇaṃ sammajjitabbaṃ. Sace koṭṭhako uklāpo hoti, koṭṭhako sammajjitabbo. Sace upaṭṭhānasālā uklāpā hoti, upaṭṭhānasālā sammajjitabbā. Sace aggisālā uklāpā hoti, aggisālā sammajjitabbā. Sace vaccakuṭi uklāpā hoti, vaccakuṭi sammajjitabbā. Sace pānīyaṃ na hoti, pānīyaṃ upaṭṭhāpetabbaṃ. Sace paribhojanīyaṃ na hoti, paribhojanīyaṃ upaṭṭhāpetabbaṃ. Sace ācamanakumbhiyā udakaṃ na hoti, ācamanakumbhiyā udakaṃ āsiñcitabbaṃ.

If the monastery courtyard is untidy, it should be swept. If the storeroom is untidy, it should be swept. If the service hall is untidy, it should be swept. If the fire hall is untidy, it should be swept. If the toilet is untidy, it should be swept. If there is no drinking water, drinking water should be provided. If there is no water for use, water for use should be provided. If there is no water in the washing pot, water should be poured into the washing pot.

‘‘Sace upajjhāyassa anabhirati uppannā hoti, saddhivihārikena vūpakāsetabbo, vūpakāsāpetabbo, dhammakathā vāssa kātabbā. Sace upajjhāyassa kukkuccaṃ uppannaṃ hoti, saddhivihārikena vinodetabbaṃ, vinodāpetabbaṃ, dhammakathā vāssa kātabbā. Sace upajjhāyassa diṭṭhigataṃ uppannaṃ hoti, saddhivihārikena vivecetabbaṃ, vivecāpetabbaṃ, dhammakathā vāssa kātabbā. Sace upajjhāyo garudhammaṃ ajjhāpanno hoti parivāsāraho, saddhivihārikena ussukkaṃ kātabbaṃ – kinti nu kho saṅgho upajjhāyassa parivāsaṃ dadeyyāti. Sace upajjhāyo mūlāya paṭikassanāraho hoti, saddhivihārikena ussukkaṃ kātabbaṃ – kinti nu kho saṅgho upajjhāyaṃ mūlāya paṭikasseyyāti. Sace upajjhāyo mānattāraho hoti, saddhivihārikena ussukkaṃ kātabbaṃ – kinti nu kho saṅgho upajjhāyassa mānattaṃ dadeyyāti. Sace upajjhāyo abbhānāraho hoti, saddhivihārikena ussukkaṃ kātabbaṃ – kinti nu kho saṅgho upajjhāyaṃ abbheyyāti. Sace saṅgho upajjhāyassa kammaṃ kattukāmo hoti tajjanīyaṃ vā niyassaṃ [niyasaṃ (ka.)] vā pabbājanīyaṃ vā paṭisāraṇīyaṃ vā ukkhepanīyaṃ vā, saddhivihārikena ussukkaṃ kātabbaṃ – kinti nu kho saṅgho upajjhāyassa kammaṃ na kareyya lahukāya vā pariṇāmeyyāti. Kataṃ vā panassa hoti saṅghena kammaṃ tajjanīyaṃ vā niyassaṃ vā pabbājanīyaṃ vā paṭisāraṇīyaṃ vā ukkhepanīyaṃ vā, saddhivihārikena ussukkaṃ kātabbaṃ – kinti nu kho upajjhāyo sammā vatteyya, lomaṃ pāteyya, netthāraṃ vatteyya, saṅgho taṃ kammaṃ paṭippassambheyyāti.

If dissatisfaction arises in the preceptor, the pupil should remove it, have it removed, or give him a Dhamma talk. If remorse arises in the preceptor, the pupil should dispel it, have it dispelled, or give him a Dhamma talk. If a wrong view arises in the preceptor, the pupil should correct it, have it corrected, or give him a Dhamma talk. If the preceptor has committed a grave offense deserving probation, the pupil should make an effort: “How might the Saṅgha grant probation to the preceptor?” If the preceptor deserves to be sent back to the beginning, the pupil should make an effort: “How might the Saṅgha send the preceptor back to the beginning?” If the preceptor deserves a penalty, the pupil should make an effort: “How might the Saṅgha impose a penalty on the preceptor?” If the preceptor deserves reinstatement, the pupil should make an effort: “How might the Saṅgha reinstate the preceptor?” If the Saṅgha desires to take a formal act against the preceptor—whether censure, suspension, probation, reconciliation, or expulsion—the pupil should make an effort: “How might the Saṅgha not take a formal act against the preceptor, or change it to a lighter penalty?” If the Saṅgha has already taken a formal act—whether censure, suspension, probation, reconciliation, or expulsion—the pupil should make an effort: “How might the preceptor behave properly, humble himself, mend his ways, so that the Saṅgha may revoke that formal act?”

‘‘Sace upajjhāyassa cīvaraṃ dhovitabbaṃ hoti, saddhivihārikena dhovitabbaṃ, ussukkaṃ vā kātabbaṃ – kinti nu kho upajjhāyassa cīvaraṃ dhoviyethāti. Sace upajjhāyassa cīvaraṃ kātabbaṃ hoti, saddhivihārikena kātabbaṃ, ussukkaṃ vā kātabbaṃ – kinti nu kho upajjhāyassa cīvaraṃ kariyethāti. Sace upajjhāyassa rajanaṃ pacitabbaṃ hoti, saddhivihārikena pacitabbaṃ, ussukkaṃ vā kātabbaṃ – kinti nu kho upajjhāyassa rajanaṃ paciyethāti. Sace upajjhāyassa cīvaraṃ rajitabbaṃ [rajetabbaṃ (sī. syā.)] hoti, saddhivihārikena rajitabbaṃ, ussukkaṃ vā kātabbaṃ – kinti nu kho upajjhāyassa cīvaraṃ rajiyethāti. Cīvaraṃ rajantena [rajentena (sī. syā.)] sādhukaṃ samparivattakaṃ samparivattakaṃ rajitabbaṃ, na ca acchinne theve pakkamitabbaṃ.

If the preceptor’s robe needs washing, the student should wash it or make an effort, thinking: 'How can the preceptor’s robe be washed?' If the preceptor’s robe needs making, the student should make it or make an effort, thinking: 'How can the preceptor’s robe be made?' If dye needs to be cooked for the preceptor, the student should cook it or make an effort, thinking: 'How can dye be cooked for the preceptor?' If the preceptor’s robe needs dyeing, the student should dye it or make an effort, thinking: 'How can the preceptor’s robe be dyed?' When dyeing the robe, one should dye it well, turning it over and over, and not leave before the process is complete.

‘‘Na upajjhāyaṃ anāpucchā ekaccassa patto dātabbo, na ekaccassa patto paṭiggahetabbo; na ekaccassa cīvaraṃ dātabbaṃ, na ekaccassa cīvaraṃ paṭiggahetabbaṃ; na ekaccassa parikkhāro dātabbo, na ekaccassa parikkhāro paṭiggahetabbo; na ekaccassa kesā chedetabbā [chettabbā (sī.), cheditabbā (ka.)], na ekaccena kesā chedāpetabbā; na ekaccassa parikammaṃ kātabbaṃ, na ekaccena parikammaṃ kārāpetabbaṃ; na ekaccassa veyyāvacco [veyyāvaccaṃ (katthaci)] kātabbo, na ekaccena veyyāvacco kārāpetabbo; na ekaccassa pacchāsamaṇena hotabbaṃ, na ekacco pacchāsamaṇo ādātabbo; na ekaccassa piṇḍapāto nīharitabbo, na ekaccena piṇḍapāto nīharāpetabbo; na upajjhāyaṃ anāpucchā gāmo pavisitabbo; na susānaṃ gantabbaṃ; na disā pakkamitabbā. Sace upajjhāyo gilāno hoti, yāvajīvaṃ upaṭṭhātabbo; vuṭṭhānamassa āgametabba’’nti.

Without asking the preceptor, a bowl should not be given to a particular person, nor should a bowl be received from a particular person; a robe should not be given to a particular person, nor should a robe be received from a particular person; requisites should not be given to a particular person, nor should requisites be received from a particular person; hair should not be cut for a particular person, nor should hair be caused to be cut by a particular person; personal services should not be performed for a particular person, nor should personal services be caused to be performed by a particular person; assistance should not be rendered to a particular person, nor should assistance be caused to be rendered by a particular person; one should not be an attendant for a particular person, nor should a particular person be taken as an attendant; alms-food should not be taken out for a particular person, nor should alms-food be caused to be taken out by a particular person; without asking the preceptor, one should not enter a village; one should not go to a charnel ground; one should not depart to another direction. If the preceptor is sick, he should be attended to for life; his recovery should be awaited.

Upajjhāyavattaṃ niṭṭhitaṃ.

The chapter on duties toward the preceptor is concluded.

### 16. Saddhivihārikavattakathā ^16

> [!TIP]- Links to [[mv1-brahmali-pali#^16|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch14|BMC Chapter 14]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-MV1.16" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


16.The Discourse on the Duties of a Pupil

67. [cūḷava. 378 ādayo] ‘‘Upajjhāyena, bhikkhave, saddhivihārikamhi sammā vattitabbaṃ. Tatrāyaṃ sammāvattanā –

67."Monks, a preceptor should conduct himself properly towards his pupil. This is the proper conduct:

‘‘Upajjhāyena, bhikkhave, saddhivihāriko saṅgahetabbo anuggahetabbo uddesena paripucchāya ovādena anusāsaniyā. Sace upajjhāyassa patto hoti, saddhivihārikassa patto na hoti, upajjhāyena saddhivihārikassa patto dātabbo, ussukkaṃ vā kātabbaṃ – kinti nu kho saddhivihārikassa patto uppajjiyethāti. Sace upajjhāyassa cīvaraṃ hoti, saddhivihārikassa cīvaraṃ na hoti, upajjhāyena saddhivihārikassa cīvaraṃ dātabbaṃ, ussukkaṃ vā kātabbaṃ – kinti nu kho saddhivihārikassa cīvaraṃ uppajjiyethāti. Sace upajjhāyassa parikkhāro hoti, saddhivihārikassa parikkhāro na hoti, upajjhāyena saddhivihārikassa parikkhāro dātabbo, ussukkaṃ vā kātabbaṃ – kinti nu kho saddhivihārikassa parikkhāro uppajjiyethāti.

"A preceptor, monks, should embrace and support his pupil by means of teaching, questioning, exhortation, and instruction. If the preceptor has an extra bowl, but the pupil does not have a bowl, a bowl should be given to the pupil by the preceptor, or an effort should be made: 'How might a bowl arise for the pupil?' If the preceptor has an extra robe, but the pupil does not have a robe, a robe should be given to the pupil by the preceptor, or an effort should be made: 'How might a robe arise for the pupil?' If the preceptor has extra requisites, but the pupil does not have requisites, requisites should be given to the pupil by the preceptor, or an effort should be made: 'How might requisites arise for the pupil?'

‘‘Sace saddhivihāriko gilāno hoti, kālasseva uṭṭhāya dantakaṭṭhaṃ dātabbaṃ, mukhodakaṃ dātabbaṃ, āsanaṃ paññapetabbaṃ. Sace yāgu hoti, bhājanaṃ dhovitvā yāgu upanāmetabbā. Yāguṃ pītassa udakaṃ datvā bhājanaṃ paṭiggahetvā nīcaṃ katvā sādhukaṃ appaṭighaṃsantena dhovitvā paṭisāmetabbaṃ. Saddhivihārikamhi vuṭṭhite āsanaṃ uddharitabbaṃ. Sace so deso uklāpo hoti, so deso sammajjitabbo.

"If the pupil is sick, having risen early, a tooth-stick should be given, water for the mouth should be given, and a seat should be prepared. If there is rice-gruel, the vessel should be washed and the rice-gruel offered. After he has drunk the rice-gruel, water should be given, the vessel should be received, lowered, and carefully washed without scraping it noisily, then put away. When the pupil has risen, the seat should be removed. If that place is untidy, that place should be swept."

‘‘Sace saddhivihāriko gāmaṃ pavisitukāmo hoti, nivāsanaṃ dātabbaṃ, paṭinivāsanaṃ paṭiggahetabbaṃ, kāyabandhanaṃ dātabbaṃ, saguṇaṃ katvā saṅghāṭiyo dātabbā, dhovitvā patto sodako dātabbo. Ettāvatā nivattissatīti āsanaṃ paññapetabbaṃ, pādodakaṃ pādapīṭhaṃ pādakathalikaṃ upanikkhipitabbaṃ, paccuggantvā pattacīvaraṃ paṭiggahetabbaṃ, paṭinivāsanaṃ dātabbaṃ, nivāsanaṃ paṭiggahetabbaṃ. Sace cīvaraṃ sinnaṃ hoti, muhuttaṃ uṇhe otāpetabbaṃ, na ca uṇhe cīvaraṃ nidahitabbaṃ; cīvaraṃ saṅgharitabbaṃ, cīvaraṃ saṅgharantena caturaṅgulaṃ kaṇṇaṃ ussāretvā cīvaraṃ saṅgharitabbaṃ – mā majjhe bhaṅgo ahosīti. Obhoge kāyabandhanaṃ kātabbaṃ.

"If the pupil wishes to enter the village, the lower robe should be given, the upper robe should be received, the belt should be given, the outer robes should be given after being properly folded, the bowl should be washed and given with water. Thinking, 'He will return soon,' a seat should be prepared, foot-water, a footstool, and a foot-scraper should be placed nearby. Having gone out to meet him, the bowl and robes should be received, the upper robe should be given, the lower robe should be received. If the robe is damp, it should be aired in the sun for a moment, but the robe should not be left in the sun; the robe should be folded. When folding the robe, raising the edge four finger-widths, the robe should be folded—lest there be a crease in the middle. The belt should be placed in the fold."

‘‘Sace piṇḍapāto hoti, saddhivihāriko ca bhuñjitukāmo hoti, udakaṃ datvā piṇḍapāto upanāmetabbo. Saddhivihāriko pānīyena pucchitabbo. Bhuttāvissa udakaṃ datvā pattaṃ paṭiggahetvā nīcaṃ katvā sādhukaṃ appaṭighaṃsantena dhovitvā vodakaṃ katvā muhuttaṃ uṇhe otāpetabbo, na ca uṇhe patto nidahitabbo. Pattacīvaraṃ nikkhipitabbaṃ. Pattaṃ nikkhipantena ekena hatthena pattaṃ gahetvā ekena hatthena heṭṭhāmañcaṃ vā heṭṭhāpīṭhaṃ vā parāmasitvā patto nikkhipitabbo. Na ca anantarahitāya bhūmiyā patto nikkhipitabbo. Cīvaraṃ nikkhipantena ekena hatthena cīvaraṃ gahetvā ekena hatthena cīvaravaṃsaṃ vā cīvararajjuṃ vā pamajjitvā pārato antaṃ orato bhogaṃ katvā cīvaraṃ nikkhipitabbaṃ. Saddhivihārikamhi vuṭṭhite āsanaṃ uddharitabbaṃ, pādodakaṃ pādapīṭhaṃ pādakathalikaṃ paṭisāmetabbaṃ. Sace so deso uklāpo hoti, so deso sammajjitabbo.

"If there is almsfood and the pupil wishes to eat, water should be given, and then the almsfood should be offered. The pupil should be asked about drinking water. After he has eaten, water should be given, the bowl should be received, lowered, and carefully washed without scraping it noisily, made free of water, and aired in the sun for a moment, but the bowl should not be left in the sun. The bowl and robes should be put away. When putting away the bowl, one should hold the bowl with one hand and feel for the lower bed or lower stool with the other hand before putting the bowl down. The bowl should not be put directly on the bare ground. When putting away the robe, one should hold the robe with one hand and wipe the robe pole or robe cord with the other hand, then fold the robe from the far end to the near end and put it away. When the pupil has risen, the seat should be removed, the foot-water, footstool, and foot-scraper should be put away. If that place is untidy, that place should be swept."

‘‘Sace saddhivihāriko nahāyitukāmo hoti, nahānaṃ paṭiyādetabbaṃ. Sace sītena attho hoti, sītaṃ paṭiyādetabbaṃ. Sace uṇhena attho hoti, uṇhaṃ paṭiyādetabbaṃ.

"If the pupil wishes to bathe, bathing water should be prepared. If cold water is desired, cold water should be prepared. If hot water is desired, hot water should be prepared."

‘‘Sace saddhivihāriko jantāgharaṃ pavisitukāmo hoti, cuṇṇaṃ sannetabbaṃ, mattikā temetabbā, jantāgharapīṭhaṃ ādāya gantvā jantāgharapīṭhaṃ datvā cīvaraṃ paṭiggahetvā ekamantaṃ nikkhipitabbaṃ, cuṇṇaṃ dātabbaṃ, mattikā dātabbā. Sace ussahati, jantāgharaṃ pavisitabbaṃ. Jantāgharaṃ pavisantena mattikāya mukhaṃ makkhetvā purato ca pacchato ca paṭicchādetvā jantāgharaṃ pavisitabbaṃ. Na there bhikkhū anupakhajja nisīditabbaṃ. Na navā bhikkhū āsanena paṭibāhitabbā. Jantāghare saddhivihārikassa parikammaṃ kātabbaṃ. Jantāgharā nikkhamantena jantāgharapīṭhaṃ ādāya purato ca pacchato ca paṭicchādetvā jantāgharā nikkhamitabbaṃ.

"If the pupil wishes to enter the bathhouse, powder should be prepared, clay should be moistened. Having taken the bathhouse stool and gone, the bathhouse stool should be given, the robe should be received and set aside. Powder should be given, clay should be given. If one is able, the bathhouse should be entered. When entering the bathhouse, having smeared the face with clay and covered oneself both front and back, the bathhouse should be entered. Senior monks should not be sat too close to. New monks should not be pushed off their seats. In the bathhouse, service should be performed for the pupil. When leaving the bathhouse, having taken the bathhouse stool and covered oneself both front and back, the bathhouse should be left."

‘‘Udakepi saddhivihārikassa parikammaṃ kātabbaṃ. Nahātena paṭhamataraṃ uttaritvā attano gattaṃ vodakaṃ katvā nivāsetvā saddhivihārikassa gattato udakaṃ pamajjitabbaṃ, nivāsanaṃ dātabbaṃ, saṅghāṭi dātabbā. Jantāgharapīṭhaṃ ādāya paṭhamataraṃ āgantvā āsanaṃ paññapetabbaṃ, pādodakaṃ pādapīṭhaṃ pādakathalikaṃ upanikkhipitabbaṃ. Saddhivihāriko pānīyena pucchitabbo.

"Even in water, service should be performed for the pupil. Having bathed, one should first come out, dry one's own body, put on the lower robe, then the water should be wiped from the pupil's body, the lower robe should be given, and the outer robe should be given. Having taken the bathhouse stool and arrived first, a seat should be prepared, foot-water, a footstool, and a foot-scraper should be placed nearby. The pupil should be asked about drinking water."

‘‘Yasmiṃ vihāre saddhivihāriko viharati, sace so vihāro uklāpo hoti, sace ussahati, sodhetabbo. Vihāraṃ sodhentena paṭhamaṃ pattacīvaraṃ nīharitvā ekamantaṃ nikkhipitabbaṃ; nisīdanapaccattharaṇaṃ nīharitvā ekamantaṃ nikkhipitabbaṃ; bhisibibbohanaṃ nīharitvā ekamantaṃ nikkhipitabbaṃ; mañco nīcaṃ katvā sādhukaṃ appaṭighaṃsantena, asaṅghaṭṭentena kavāṭapiṭṭhaṃ, nīharitvā ekamantaṃ nikkhipitabbo; pīṭhaṃ nīcaṃ katvā sādhukaṃ appaṭighaṃsantena asaṅghaṭṭentena kavāṭapiṭṭhaṃ nīharitvā ekamantaṃ nikkhipitabbaṃ; mañcapaṭipādakā nīharitvā ekamantaṃ nikkhipitabbā; kheḷamallako nīharitvā ekamantaṃ nikkhipitabbo; apassenaphalakaṃ nīharitvā ekamantaṃ nikkhipitabbaṃ; bhūmattharaṇaṃ yathāpaññattaṃ sallakkhetvā nīharitvā ekamantaṃ nikkhipitabbaṃ. Sace vihāre santānakaṃ hoti, ullokā paṭhamaṃ ohāretabbaṃ, ālokasandhikaṇṇabhāgā pamajjitabbā. Sace gerukaparikammakatā bhitti kaṇṇakitā hoti, coḷakaṃ temetvā pīḷetvā pamajjitabbā. Sace kāḷavaṇṇakatā bhūmi kaṇṇakitā hoti, coḷakaṃ temetvā pīḷetvā pamajjitabbā. Sace akatā hoti bhūmi, udakena paripphositvā sammajjitabbā – mā vihāro rajena uhaññīti. Saṅkāraṃ vicinitvā ekamantaṃ chaḍḍetabbaṃ.

"In whatever dwelling the pupil dwells, if that dwelling is untidy, and one is able, it should be cleaned. When cleaning the dwelling, first the bowl and robes should be taken out and set aside; the sitting mat and cover should be taken out and set aside; the mattress and pillow should be taken out and set aside; the bed should be lowered carefully, without scraping or bumping against the door frame, taken out, and set aside; the stool should be lowered carefully, without scraping or bumping against the door frame, taken out, and set aside; the bed supports should be taken out and set aside; the spittoon should be taken out and set aside; the leaning board should be taken out and set aside; after inspecting the floor covering as it was laid out, it should be taken out and set aside. If there are cobwebs in the dwelling, they should first be removed from the ceiling, and the window recesses and corners should be wiped. If the walls treated with red ochre are stained, a cloth should be dampened, wrung out, and used to wipe them. If the floor treated with black dye is stained, a cloth should be dampened, wrung out, and used to wipe it. If the floor is untreated, it should be sprinkled with water and swept—lest the dwelling be covered with dust. The rubbish should be collected and thrown away to one side."

‘‘Bhūmattharaṇaṃ otāpetvā sodhetvā papphoṭetvā atiharitvā yathāpaññattaṃ paññapetabbaṃ. Mañcapaṭipādakā otāpetvā pamajjitvā atiharitvā yathāṭhāne ṭhapetabbā. Mañco otāpetvā sodhetvā papphoṭetvā nīcaṃ katvā sādhukaṃ appaṭighaṃsantena, asaṅghaṭṭentena kavāṭapiṭṭhaṃ, atiharitvā yathāpaññattaṃ paññapetabbo. Pīṭhaṃ otāpetvā sodhetvā papphoṭetvā nīcaṃ katvā sādhukaṃ appaṭighaṃsantena, asaṅghaṭṭentena kavāṭapiṭṭhaṃ, atiharitvā yathāpaññattaṃ paññapetabbaṃ. Bhisibibbohanaṃ otāpetvā sodhetvā papphoṭetvā atiharitvā yathāpaññattaṃ paññapetabbaṃ. Nisīdanapaccattharaṇaṃ otāpetvā sodhetvā papphoṭetvā atiharitvā yathāpaññattaṃ paññapetabbaṃ. Kheḷamallako otāpetvā pamajjitvā atiharitvā yathāṭhāne ṭhapetabbo. Apassenaphalakaṃ otāpetvā pamajjitvā atiharitvā yathāṭhāne ṭhapetabbaṃ. Pattacīvaraṃ nikkhipitabbaṃ. Pattaṃ nikkhipantena ekena hatthena pattaṃ gahetvā ekena hatthena heṭṭhāmañcaṃ vā heṭṭhāpīṭhaṃ vā parāmasitvā patto nikkhipitabbo. Na ca anantarahitāya bhūmiyā patto nikkhipitabbo. Cīvaraṃ nikkhipantena ekena hatthena cīvaraṃ gahetvā ekena hatthena cīvaravaṃsaṃ vā cīvararajjuṃ vā pamajjitvā pārato antaṃ orato bhogaṃ katvā cīvaraṃ nikkhipitabbaṃ.

"After airing the floor covering, cleaning it, shaking it out, and bringing it back, it should be laid out as arranged. The bed supports should be aired, wiped, brought back, and placed in their proper positions. The bed should be aired, cleaned, shaken out, lowered carefully without scraping or bumping against the door frame, brought back, and set up as arranged. The stool should be aired, cleaned, shaken out, lowered carefully without scraping or bumping against the door frame, brought back, and set up as arranged. The mattress and pillow should be aired, cleaned, shaken out, brought back, and set up as arranged. The sitting mat and cover should be aired, cleaned, shaken out, brought back, and set up as arranged. The spittoon should be aired, wiped, brought back, and placed in its proper position. The leaning board should be aired, wiped, brought back, and placed in its proper position. The bowl and robes should be put away. When putting away the bowl, one should hold the bowl with one hand and feel for the lower bed or lower stool with the other hand before putting the bowl down. The bowl should not be put directly on the bare ground. When putting away the robe, one should hold the robe with one hand and wipe the robe pole or robe cord with the other hand, then fold the robe from the far end to the near end and put it away."

‘‘Sace puratthimā sarajā vātā vāyanti, puratthimā vātapānā thaketabbā. Sace pacchimā sarajā vātā vāyanti, pacchimā vātapānā thaketabbā. Sace uttarā sarajā vātā vāyanti, uttarā vātapānā thaketabbā. Sace dakkhiṇā sarajā vātā vāyanti, dakkhiṇā vātapānā thaketabbā. Sace sītakālo hoti, divā vātapānā vivaritabbā, rattiṃ thaketabbā. Sace uṇhakālo hoti, divā vātapānā thaketabbā, rattiṃ vivaritabbā.

"If dusty winds blow from the east, the eastern windows should be closed. If dusty winds blow from the west, the western windows should be closed. If dusty winds blow from the north, the northern windows should be closed. If dusty winds blow from the south, the southern windows should be closed. If it is the cold season, the windows should be opened during the day and closed at night. If it is the hot season, the windows should be closed during the day and opened at night."

‘‘Sace pariveṇaṃ uklāpaṃ hoti, pariveṇaṃ sammajjitabbaṃ. Sace koṭṭhako uklāpo hoti, koṭṭhako sammajjitabbo. Sace upaṭṭhānasālā uklāpā hoti, upaṭṭhānasālā sammajjitabbā. Sace aggisālā uklāpā hoti, aggisālā sammajjitabbā. Sace vaccakuṭi uklāpā hoti, vaccakuṭi sammajjitabbā. Sace pānīyaṃ na hoti, pānīyaṃ upaṭṭhāpetabbaṃ. Sace paribhojanīyaṃ na hoti, paribhojanīyaṃ upaṭṭhāpetabbaṃ. Sace ācamanakumbhiyā udakaṃ na hoti, ācamanakumbhiyā udakaṃ āsiñcitabbaṃ.

"If the monastery is dirty, the monastery should be swept. If the storeroom is dirty, the storeroom should be swept. If the service hall is dirty, the service hall should be swept. If the fire-hall is dirty, the fire-hall should be swept. If the toilet is dirty, the toilet should be swept. If there is no drinking water, drinking water should be provided. If there is no water for use, water for use should be provided. If there is no water in the rinsing pot, water should be poured into the rinsing pot."

‘‘Sace saddhivihārikassa anabhirati uppannā hoti, upajjhāyena vūpakāsetabbo, vūpakāsāpetabbo, dhammakathā vāssa kātabbā. Sace saddhivihārikassa kukkuccaṃ uppannaṃ hoti, upajjhāyena vinodetabbaṃ, vinodāpetabbaṃ, dhammakathā vāssa kātabbā. Sace saddhivihārikassa diṭṭhigataṃ uppannaṃ hoti, upajjhāyena vivecetabbaṃ, vivecāpetabbaṃ, dhammakathā vāssa kātabbā. Sace saddhivihāriko garudhammaṃ ajjhāpanno hoti parivāsāraho, upajjhāyena ussukkaṃ kātabbaṃ – kinti nu kho saṅgho saddhivihārikassa parivāsaṃ dadeyyāti. Sace saddhivihāriko mūlāya paṭikassanāraho hoti, upajjhāyena ussukkaṃ kātabbaṃ – kinti nu kho saṅgho saddhivihārikaṃ mūlāya paṭikasseyyāti. Sace saddhivihāriko mānattāraho hoti, upajjhāyena ussukkaṃ kātabbaṃ – kinti nu kho saṅgho saddhivihārikassa mānattaṃ dadeyyāti. Sace saddhivihāriko abbhānāraho hoti, upajjhāyena ussukkaṃ kātabbaṃ – kinti nu kho saṅgho saddhivihārikaṃ abbheyyāti. Sace saṅgho saddhivihārikassa kammaṃ kattukāmo hoti, tajjanīyaṃ vā niyassaṃ vā pabbājanīyaṃ vā paṭisāraṇīyaṃ vā ukkhepanīyaṃ vā, upajjhāyena ussukkaṃ kātabbaṃ – kinti nu kho saṅgho saddhivihārikassa kammaṃ na kareyya, lahukāya vā pariṇāmeyyāti. Kataṃ vā panassa hoti saṅghena kammaṃ, tajjanīyaṃ vā niyassaṃ vā pabbājanīyaṃ vā paṭisāraṇīyaṃ vā ukkhepanīyaṃ vā, upajjhāyena ussukkaṃ kātabbaṃ – kinti nu kho saddhivihāriko sammā vatteyya, lomaṃ pāteyya, netthāraṃ vatteyya, saṅgho taṃ kammaṃ paṭippassambheyyāti.

"If dissatisfaction arises in the pupil, the preceptor should address it, or have someone else address it, or give him a Dhamma talk. If anxiety arises in the pupil, the preceptor should dispel it, or have someone else dispel it, or give him a Dhamma talk. If wrong view arises in the pupil, the preceptor should help him abandon it, or have someone else help him abandon it, or give him a Dhamma talk. If the pupil has committed a serious offense warranting parivāsa, the preceptor should make an effort: 'How might the Saṅgha grant parivāsa to the pupil?' If the pupil deserves to be sent back to the origin, the preceptor should make an effort: 'How might the Saṅgha send the pupil back to the origin?' If the pupil deserves mānatta, the preceptor should make an effort: 'How might the Saṅgha grant mānatta to the pupil?' If the pupil deserves reinstatement, the preceptor should make an effort: 'How might the Saṅgha reinstate the pupil?' If the Saṅgha intends to carry out an action against the pupil—whether tajjanīya, niyassa, pabbājanīya, paṭisāraṇīya, or ukkhepanīya—the preceptor should make an effort: 'How might the Saṅgha not carry out the action against the pupil, or modify it to be a lighter one?' If the Saṅgha has already carried out an action against him—whether tajjanīya, niyassa, pabbājanīya, paṭisāraṇīya, or ukkhepanīya—the preceptor should make an effort: 'How might the pupil behave properly, lower his pride, mend his ways, so that the Saṅgha might revoke the action?'"

‘‘Sace saddhivihārikassa cīvaraṃ dhovitabbaṃ hoti, upajjhāyena ācikkhitabbaṃ evaṃ dhoveyyāsīti, ussukkaṃ vā kātabbaṃ – kinti nu kho saddhivihārikassa cīvaraṃ dhoviyethāti. Sace saddhivihārikassa cīvaraṃ kātabbaṃ hoti, upajjhāyena ācikkhitabbaṃ evaṃ kareyyāsīti, ussukkaṃ vā kātabbaṃ – kinti nu kho saddhivihārikassa cīvaraṃ kariyethāti. Sace saddhivihārikassa rajanaṃ pacitabbaṃ hoti, upajjhāyena ācikkhitabbaṃ evaṃ paceyyāsīti, ussukkaṃ vā kātabbaṃ – kinti nu kho saddhivihārikassa rajanaṃ paciyethāti. Sace saddhivihārikassa cīvaraṃ rajitabbaṃ hoti, upajjhāyena ācikkhitabbaṃ, evaṃ rajeyyāsīti, ussukkaṃ vā kātabbaṃ – kinti nu kho saddhivihārikassa cīvaraṃ rajiyethāti. Cīvaraṃ rajantena sādhukaṃ samparivattakaṃ samparivattakaṃ rajitabbaṃ. Na ca acchinne theve pakkamitabbaṃ. Sace saddhivihāriko gilāno hoti, yāvajīvaṃ upaṭṭhātabbo, vuṭṭhānamassa āgametabba’’nti.

"If the pupil’s robe needs washing, the preceptor should instruct him, saying, ‘Wash it in this way,’ or make an effort: ‘How might the pupil’s robe be washed?’ If the pupil’s robe needs making, the preceptor should instruct him, saying, ‘Make it in this way,’ or make an effort: ‘How might the pupil’s robe be made?’ If dye needs to be prepared for the pupil, the preceptor should instruct him, saying, ‘Prepare it in this way,’ or make an effort: ‘How might dye be prepared for the pupil?’ If the pupil’s robe needs dyeing, the preceptor should instruct him, saying, ‘Dye it in this way,’ or make an effort: ‘How might the pupil’s robe be dyed?’ When dyeing the robe, one should carefully turn it over and over. One should not leave while the dye is incomplete. If the pupil is sick, he should be attended to as long as life lasts; his recovery should be awaited."

Saddhivihārikavattaṃ niṭṭhitaṃ.

The chapter on the conduct toward a co-resident is finished.

### 17. Paṇāmitakathā ^17

> [!TIP]- Links to [[mv1-brahmali-pali#^17|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch14|BMC Chapter 14]] and the following cites:
