> "VIN-MV1.17" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


17.Talk on Dismissal

68. Tena kho pana samayena saddhivihārikā upajjhāyesu na sammā vattanti. Ye te bhikkhū appicchā…pe… te ujjhāyanti khiyyanti vipācenti – ‘‘kathañhi nāma saddhivihārikā upajjhāyesu na sammā vattissantī’’ti. Atha kho te bhikkhū bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ…pe… saccaṃ kira, bhikkhave, saddhivihārikā upajjhāyesu na sammā vattantīti? Saccaṃ bhagavāti. Vigarahi buddho bhagavā…pe… kathañhi nāma, bhikkhave, saddhivihārikā upajjhāyesu na sammā vattissantīti…pe… vigarahitvā…pe… dhammiṃ kathaṃ katvā bhikkhū āmantesi – ‘‘na, bhikkhave, saddhivihārikena upajjhāyamhi na sammā vattitabbaṃ. Yo na sammā vatteyya, āpatti dukkaṭassā’’ti. Neva sammā vattanti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, asammāvattantaṃ paṇāmetuṃ. Evañca pana, bhikkhave, paṇāmetabbo – ‘‘paṇāmemi ta’’nti vā, ‘‘māyidha paṭikkamī’’ti vā, ‘‘nīhara te pattacīvara’’nti vā, ‘‘nāhaṃ tayā upaṭṭhātabbo’’ti vā, kāyena viññāpeti, vācāya viññāpeti, kāyena vācāya viññāpeti, paṇāmito hoti saddhivihāriko; na kāyena viññāpeti, na vācāya viññāpeti, na kāyena vācāya viññāpeti, na paṇāmito hoti saddhivihārikoti.

68.Now at that time, the resident pupils did not behave properly toward their preceptors. Those monks who were modest … complained and criticized them, saying, “How indeed can resident pupils not behave properly toward their preceptors?” Then those monks reported this matter to the Blessed One … “Is it true, monks, that the resident pupils do not behave properly toward their preceptors?” “It is true, Blessed One.” The Buddha rebuked them … “How indeed, monks, can resident pupils not behave properly toward their preceptors?” … Having rebuked them … he gave a Dhamma talk and addressed the monks: “Monks, a resident pupil should not behave improperly toward his preceptor. Whoever does not behave properly incurs an offense of wrong conduct.” They still did not behave properly. They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “I allow, monks, to dismiss one who does not behave properly. And this is how, monks, he should be dismissed: by saying, ‘I dismiss you,’ or ‘Do not come back here,’ or ‘Take your bowl and robe away,’ or ‘I will not be attended to by you.’ If he makes it known by body, by speech, or by both body and speech, the resident pupil is dismissed; if he does not make it known by body, by speech, or by both body and speech, the resident pupil is not dismissed.

Tena kho pana samayena saddhivihārikā paṇāmitā na khamāpenti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, khamāpetunti. Neva khamāpenti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Na, bhikkhave, paṇāmitena na khamāpetabbo. Yo na khamāpeyya, āpatti dukkaṭassāti.

At that time, the dismissed resident pupils did not ask for forgiveness. They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “I allow, monks, that they ask for forgiveness.” Still, they did not ask for forgiveness. They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, one who has been dismissed should not fail to ask for forgiveness. Whoever does not ask for forgiveness incurs an offense of wrong conduct.”

Tena kho pana samayena upajjhāyā khamāpiyamānā na khamanti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, khamitunti. Neva khamanti. Saddhivihārikā pakkamantipi vibbhamantipi titthiyesupi saṅkamanti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Na, bhikkhave, khamāpiyamānena na khamitabbaṃ. Yo na khameyya, āpatti dukkaṭassāti.

At that time, preceptors, when asked for forgiveness, would not forgive. They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “I allow, monks, that they forgive.” Still, they would not forgive. The resident pupils departed, or disrobed, and some even went over to other sects. They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, one who is asked for forgiveness should not fail to forgive. Whoever does not forgive incurs an offense of wrong conduct.”

Tena kho pana samayena upajjhāyā sammāvattantaṃ paṇāmenti, asammāvattantaṃ na paṇāmenti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Na, bhikkhave, sammāvattanto paṇāmetabbo. Yo paṇāmeyya, āpatti dukkaṭassa. Na ca, bhikkhave, asammāvattanto na paṇāmetabbo. Yo na paṇāmeyya, āpatti dukkaṭassāti.

At that time, preceptors dismissed those who behaved properly, but did not dismiss those who behaved improperly. They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, one who behaves properly should not be dismissed. Whoever dismisses such a one incurs an offense of wrong conduct. And monks, one who behaves improperly should not fail to be dismissed. Whoever does not dismiss such a one incurs an offense of wrong conduct.”

‘‘Pañcahi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgato saddhivihāriko paṇāmetabbo. Upajjhāyamhi nādhimattaṃ pemaṃ hoti, nādhimatto pasādo hoti, nādhimattā hirī hoti, nādhimatto gāravo hoti, nādhimattā bhāvanā hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgato saddhivihāriko paṇāmetabbo.

“Monks, a resident pupil endowed with five qualities should be dismissed. He has no excessive affection for his preceptor, no excessive confidence in his preceptor, no excessive shame toward his preceptor, no excessive respect for his preceptor, and no excessive cultivation. Monks, a resident pupil endowed with these five qualities should be dismissed.”

‘‘Pañcahi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgato saddhivihāriko na paṇāmetabbo. Upajjhāyamhi adhimattaṃ pemaṃ hoti, adhimatto pasādo hoti, adhimattā hirī hoti, adhimatto gāravo hoti, adhimattā bhāvanā hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgato saddhivihāriko na paṇāmetabbo.

“Monks, a resident pupil endowed with five qualities should not be dismissed. He has excessive affection for his preceptor, excessive confidence in his preceptor, excessive shame toward his preceptor, excessive respect for his preceptor, and excessive cultivation. Monks, a resident pupil endowed with these five qualities should not be dismissed.”

‘‘Pañcahi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgato saddhivihāriko alaṃ paṇāmetuṃ. Upajjhāyamhi nādhimattaṃ pemaṃ hoti, nādhimatto pasādo hoti, nādhimattā hirī hoti, nādhimattā gāravo hoti, nādhimattā bhāvanā hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgato saddhivihāriko alaṃ paṇāmetuṃ.

“Monks, a resident pupil endowed with five qualities is fit to be dismissed. He has no excessive affection for his preceptor, no excessive confidence in his preceptor, no excessive shame toward his preceptor, no excessive respect for his preceptor, and no excessive cultivation. Monks, a resident pupil endowed with these five qualities is fit to be dismissed.”

‘‘Pañcahi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgato saddhivihāriko nālaṃ paṇāmetuṃ. Upajjhāyamhi adhimattaṃ pemaṃ hoti, adhimatto pasādo hoti, adhimattā hirī hoti, adhimatto gāravo hoti, adhimattā bhāvanā hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgato saddhivihāriko nālaṃ paṇāmetuṃ.

“Monks, a resident pupil endowed with five qualities is not fit to be dismissed. He has excessive affection for his preceptor, excessive confidence in his preceptor, excessive shame toward his preceptor, excessive respect for his preceptor, and excessive cultivation. Monks, a resident pupil endowed with these five qualities is not fit to be dismissed.”

‘‘Pañcahi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgataṃ saddhivihārikaṃ appaṇāmento upajjhāyo sātisāro hoti, paṇāmento anatisāro hoti. Upajjhāyamhi nādhimattaṃ pemaṃ hoti, nādhimatto pasādo hoti, nādhimattā hirī hoti, nādhimatto gāravo hoti, nādhimattā bhāvanā hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgataṃ saddhivihārikaṃ appaṇāmento upajjhāyo sātisāro hoti, paṇāmento anatisāro hoti.

“Monks, a preceptor who does not dismiss a resident pupil endowed with five qualities is blameworthy, but one who dismisses him is not blameworthy. The resident pupil does not have excessive affection for the preceptor, excessive confidence in him, excessive shame toward him, excessive respect for him, or excessive cultivation. A preceptor who does not dismiss a resident pupil endowed with these five qualities is blameworthy, but one who dismisses him is not blameworthy.”

‘‘Pañcahi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgataṃ saddhivihārikaṃ paṇāmento upajjhāyo sātisāro hoti, appaṇāmento anatisāro hoti. Upajjhāyamhi adhimattaṃ pemaṃ hoti, adhimatto pasādo hoti, adhimattā hirī hoti, adhimatto gāravo hoti, adhimattā bhāvanā hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgataṃ saddhivihārikaṃ paṇāmento upajjhāyo sātisāro hoti, appaṇāmento anatisāro hotī’’ti.

“Monks, a preceptor who dismisses a resident pupil endowed with five qualities is blameworthy, but one who does not dismiss him is not blameworthy. The resident pupil has excessive affection for his preceptor, excessive confidence in him, excessive shame toward him, excessive respect for him, and excessive cultivation. A preceptor who dismisses a resident pupil with these five qualities is blameworthy, but one who does not dismiss him is not blameworthy.”

69. Tena kho pana samayena aññataro brāhmaṇo bhikkhū upasaṅkamitvā pabbajjaṃ yāci. Taṃ bhikkhū na icchiṃsu pabbājetuṃ. So bhikkhūsu pabbajjaṃ alabhamāno kiso ahosi lūkho dubbaṇṇo uppaṇḍuppaṇḍukajāto dhamanisanthatagatto. Addasā kho bhagavā taṃ brāhmaṇaṃ kisaṃ lūkhaṃ dubbaṇṇaṃ uppaṇḍuppaṇḍukajātaṃ dhamanisanthatagattaṃ, disvāna bhikkhū āmantesi – ‘‘kiṃ nu kho so, bhikkhave, brāhmaṇo kiso lūkho dubbaṇṇo uppaṇḍuppaṇḍukajāto dhamanisanthatagatto’’ti? Eso, bhante, brāhmaṇo bhikkhū upasaṅkamitvā pabbajjaṃ yāci. Taṃ bhikkhū na icchiṃsu pabbājetuṃ. So bhikkhūsu pabbajjaṃ alabhamāno kiso lūkho dubbaṇṇo uppaṇḍuppaṇḍukajāto dhamanisanthatagattoti. Atha kho bhagavā bhikkhū āmantesi – ‘‘ko nu kho, bhikkhave, tassa brāhmaṇassa adhikāraṃ sarasī’’ti? Evaṃ vutte āyasmā sāriputto bhagavantaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘ahaṃ kho, bhante, tassa brāhmaṇassa adhikāraṃ sarāmī’’ti. ‘‘Kiṃ pana tvaṃ, sāriputta, tassa brāhmaṇassa adhikāraṃ sarasī’’ti? ‘‘Idha me, bhante, so brāhmaṇo rājagahe piṇḍāya carantassa kaṭacchubhikkhaṃ dāpesi. Imaṃ kho ahaṃ, bhante, tassa brāhmaṇassa adhikāraṃ sarāmī’’ti. ‘‘Sādhu sādhu, sāriputta, kataññuno hi, sāriputta, sappurisā katavedino. Tena hi tvaṃ, sāriputta, taṃ brāhmaṇaṃ pabbājehi upasampādehī’’ti. ‘‘Kathāhaṃ, bhante, taṃ brāhmaṇaṃ pabbājemi upasampādemī’’ti? Atha kho bhagavā etasmiṃ nidāne etasmiṃ pakaraṇe dhammiṃ kathaṃ katvā bhikkhū āmantesi – yā sā, bhikkhave, mayā tīhi saraṇagamanehi upasampadā anuññātā, taṃ ajjatagge paṭikkhipāmi. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, ñatticatutthena kammena upasampādetuṃ [upasampadaṃ (sī. syā.)]. Evañca pana, bhikkhave, upasampādetabbo. Byattena bhikkhunā paṭibalena saṅgho ñāpetabbo –

69.At that time, a certain brahmin approached the monks and requested ordination. The monks were unwilling to ordain him. Unable to obtain ordination from the monks, he became thin, haggard, ugly, pale, with veins spread over his body. The Blessed One saw that brahmin—thin, haggard, ugly, pale, with veins spread over his body—and having seen him, he addressed the monks: “Why, monks, is that brahmin so thin, haggard, ugly, pale, with veins spread over his body?” “Venerable sir, this brahmin approached the monks and requested ordination. The monks were unwilling to ordain him. Unable to obtain ordination from the monks, he has become thin, haggard, ugly, pale, with veins spread over his body.” Then the Blessed One addressed the monks: “Monks, who among you remembers a kindness done by that brahmin?” When this was said, Venerable Sāriputta said to the Blessed One: “Venerable sir, I remember a kindness done by that brahmin.” “But what kindness do you remember, Sāriputta?” “Venerable sir, while I was wandering for alms in Rājagaha, this brahmin gave me a ladleful of food. This, venerable sir, is the kindness I remember from that brahmin.” “Good, good, Sāriputta. For good people, Sāriputta, are grateful and acknowledge what has been done for them. Well then, Sāriputta, you should ordain that brahmin and confer the higher ordination on him.” “But how, venerable sir, should I ordain him and confer the higher ordination on him?” Then the Blessed One, on this occasion and in this connection, having given a Dhamma talk, addressed the monks: “Monks, the higher ordination that I allowed through the three refuges—from today onwards, I revoke that. I allow, monks, to confer the higher ordination by means of a formal act consisting of a motion and three announcements. And monks, this is how one should be conferred the higher ordination. A competent and capable monk should inform the Sangha:

70. ‘‘Suṇātu me, bhante, saṅgho. Ayaṃ itthannāmo itthannāmassa āyasmato upasampadāpekkho. Yadi saṅghassa pattakallaṃ, saṅgho itthannāmaṃ upasampādeyya itthannāmena upajjhāyena. Esā ñatti.

70.“May the Sangha, venerable sirs, hear me. This person named so-and-so is a candidate for higher ordination under the Venerable so-and-so. If it is agreeable to the Sangha, the Sangha should confer higher ordination on so-and-so with the Venerable so-and-so as his preceptor. This is the motion.”

‘‘Suṇātu me, bhante, saṅgho. Ayaṃ itthannāmo itthannāmassa āyasmato upasampadāpekkho. Saṅgho itthannāmaṃ upasampādeti itthannāmena upajjhāyena. Yassāyasmato khamati itthannāmassa upasampadā itthannāmena upajjhāyena, so tuṇhassa; yassa nakkhamati, so bhāseyya.

“May the Sangha, venerable sirs, hear me. This person named so-and-so is a candidate for higher ordination under the Venerable so-and-so. The Sangha confers higher ordination on so-and-so with the Venerable so-and-so as his preceptor. Any venerable one who approves of the higher ordination of so-and-so with the Venerable so-and-so as preceptor should remain silent; any who disapproves should speak.”

‘‘Dutiyampi etamatthaṃ vadāmi – suṇātu me, bhante, saṅgho. Ayaṃ itthannāmo itthannāmassa āyasmato upasampadāpekkho. Saṅgho itthannāmaṃ upasampādeti itthannāmena upajjhāyena. Yassāyasmato khamati itthannāmassa upasampadā itthannāmena upajjhāyena, so tuṇhassa; yassa nakkhamati, so bhāseyya.

For a second time I speak on this matter: Venerable sirs, may the Sangha listen to me. This person named so-and-so is a candidate for higher ordination under the venerable so-and-so. The Sangha confers higher ordination on this person named so-and-so, with the venerable so-and-so as preceptor. Any venerable one who approves of the higher ordination of this person named so-and-so, with the venerable so-and-so as preceptor, should remain silent; any who does not approve should speak.

‘‘Tatiyampi etamatthaṃ vadāmi – suṇātu me, bhante, saṅgho. Ayaṃ itthannāmo itthannāmassa āyasmato upasampadāpekkho. Saṅgho itthannāmaṃ upasampādeti itthannāmena upajjhāyena. Yassāyasmato khamati itthannāmassa upasampadā itthannāmena upajjhāyena, so tuṇhassa; yassa nakkhamati, so bhāseyya.

For a third time I speak on this matter: Venerable sirs, may the Sangha listen to me. This person named so-and-so is a candidate for higher ordination under the venerable so-and-so. The Sangha confers higher ordination on this person named so-and-so, with the venerable so-and-so as preceptor. Any venerable one who approves of the higher ordination of this person named so-and-so, with the venerable so-and-so as preceptor, should remain silent; any who does not approve should speak.

‘‘Upasampanno saṅghena itthannāmo itthannāmena upajjhāyena. Khamati saṅghassa, tasmā tuṇhī, evametaṃ dhārayāmī’’ti.

This person named so-and-so has been conferred higher ordination by the Sangha, with the venerable so-and-so as preceptor. The Sangha approves, therefore it is silent. Thus I hold it.

71. Tena kho pana samayena aññataro bhikkhu upasampannasamanantarā anācāraṃ ācarati. Bhikkhū evamāhaṃsu – ‘‘māvuso, evarūpaṃ akāsi, netaṃ kappatī’’ti. So evamāha – ‘‘nevāhaṃ āyasmante yāciṃ upasampādetha manti. Kissa maṃ tumhe ayācitā upasampāditthā’’ti? Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Na, bhikkhave, ayācitena upasampādetabbo. Yo upasampādeyya, āpatti dukkaṭassa. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, yācitena upasampādetuṃ. Evañca pana, bhikkhave, yācitabbo. Tena upasampadāpekkhena saṅghaṃ upasaṅkamitvā ekaṃsaṃ uttarāsaṅgaṃ karitvā bhikkhūnaṃ pāde vanditvā ukkuṭikaṃ nisīditvā añjaliṃ paggahetvā evamassa vacanīyo – ‘‘saṅghaṃ, bhante, upasampadaṃ yācāmi, ullumpatu maṃ, bhante, saṅgho anukampaṃ upādāyā’’ti. Dutiyampi yācitabbo. Tatiyampi yācitabbo. Byattena bhikkhunā paṭibalena saṅgho ñāpetabbo –

71.Now at that time a certain monk, immediately after receiving higher ordination, behaved improperly. The monks said to him, "Friend, do not act like this; it is not allowable." He replied, "Venerable sirs, I did not ask you to confer higher ordination on me. Why did you confer higher ordination on me without my asking?" They reported this matter to the Blessed One. "Monks, one should not confer higher ordination on someone who has not asked. Whoever confers higher ordination on someone who has not asked commits an offense of wrong-doing. I allow, monks, that one should confer higher ordination only on those who have asked. And this is how one should be asked: The candidate for higher ordination should approach the Sangha, arrange his upper robe over one shoulder, pay homage at the feet of the monks, squat on his heels, raise his joined palms, and say: 'Venerable sirs, I ask the Sangha for higher ordination. Venerable sirs, may the Sangha lift me up out of compassion.' He should be asked a second time. He should be asked a third time. A competent and capable monk should then inform the Sangha:

72. ‘‘Suṇātu me, bhante, saṅgho. Ayaṃ itthannāmo itthannāmassa āyasmato upasampadāpekkho. Itthannāmo saṅghaṃ upasampadaṃ yācati itthannāmena upajjhāyena. Yadi saṅghassa pattakallaṃ, saṅgho itthannāmaṃ upasampādeyya itthannāmena upajjhāyena. Esā ñatti.

72.Venerable sirs, may the Sangha listen to me. This person named so-and-so is a candidate for higher ordination under the venerable so-and-so. This person named so-and-so asks the Sangha for higher ordination with the venerable so-and-so as preceptor. If it is agreeable to the Sangha, the Sangha should confer higher ordination on this person named so-and-so with the venerable so-and-so as preceptor. This is the motion.

‘‘Suṇātu me, bhante, saṅgho. Ayaṃ itthannāmo itthannāmassa āyasmato upasampadāpekkho. Itthannāmo saṅghaṃ upasampadaṃ yācati itthannāmena upajjhāyena. Saṅgho itthannāmaṃ upasampādeti itthannāmena upajjhāyena. Yassāyasmato khamati itthannāmassa upasampadā itthannāmena upajjhāyena, so tuṇhassa; yassa nakkhamati, so bhāseyya.

Venerable sirs, may the Sangha listen to me. This person named so-and-so is a candidate for higher ordination under the venerable so-and-so. This person named so-and-so asks the Sangha for higher ordination with the venerable so-and-so as preceptor. The Sangha confers higher ordination on this person named so-and-so with the venerable so-and-so as preceptor. Any venerable one who approves of the higher ordination of this person named so-and-so with the venerable so-and-so as preceptor should remain silent; any who does not approve should speak.

‘‘Dutiyampi etamatthaṃ vadāmi…pe… tatiyampi etamatthaṃ vadāmi…pe….

For a second time I speak on this matter… For a third time I speak on this matter….

‘‘Upasampanno saṅghena itthannāmo itthannāmena upajjhāyena. Khamati saṅghassa, tasmā tuṇhī, evametaṃ dhārayāmī’’ti.

This person named so-and-so has been conferred higher ordination by the Sangha, with the venerable so-and-so as preceptor. The Sangha approves, therefore it is silent. Thus I hold it.

73. Tena kho pana samayena rājagahe paṇītānaṃ bhattānaṃ bhattapaṭipāṭi aṭṭhitā [adhiṭṭhitā (ka.)] hoti. Atha kho aññatarassa brāhmaṇassa etadahosi – ‘‘ime kho samaṇā sakyaputtiyā sukhasīlā sukhasamācārā, subhojanāni bhuñjitvā nivātesu sayanesu sayanti. Yaṃnūnāhaṃ samaṇesu sakyaputtiyesu pabbajeyya’’nti. Atha kho so brāhmaṇo bhikkhū upasaṅkamitvā pabbajjaṃ yāci. Taṃ bhikkhū pabbājesuṃ upasampādesuṃ. Tasmiṃ pabbajite bhattapaṭipāṭi khīyittha. Bhikkhū evamāhaṃsu – ‘‘ehi dāni, āvuso, piṇḍāya carissāmā’’ti. So evamāha – ‘‘nāhaṃ, āvuso, etaṃkāraṇā pabbajito piṇḍāya carissāmīti. Sace me dassatha bhuñjissāmi, no ce me dassatha vibbhamissāmī’’ti. ‘‘Kiṃ pana tvaṃ, āvuso, udarassa kāraṇā pabbajito’’ti? ‘‘Evamāvuso’’ti. Ye te bhikkhū appicchā…pe… te ujjhāyanti khiyyanti vipācenti – kathañhi nāma bhikkhu evaṃ svākkhāte dhammavinaye udarassa kāraṇā pabbajissatīti. Te bhikkhū bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ…pe… saccaṃ kira tvaṃ, bhikkhu, udarassa kāraṇā pabbajitoti? Saccaṃ bhagavāti. Vigarahi buddho bhagavā…pe… ‘‘kathañhi nāma tvaṃ, moghapurisa, evaṃ svākkhāte dhammavinaye udarassa kāraṇā pabbajissasi. Netaṃ, moghapurisa, appasannānaṃ vā pasādāya pasannānaṃ vā bhiyyobhāvāya’’…pe… vigarahitvā…pe… dhammiṃ kathaṃ katvā bhikkhū āmantesi – ‘‘anujānāmi, bhikkhave, upasampādentena cattāro nissaye ācikkhituṃ – piṇḍiyālopabhojanaṃ nissāya pabbajjā, tattha te yāvajīvaṃ ussāho karaṇīyo; atirekalābho – saṅghabhattaṃ, uddesabhattaṃ, nimantanaṃ, salākabhattaṃ, pakkhikaṃ, uposathikaṃ, pāṭipadikaṃ. Paṃsukūlacīvaraṃ nissāya pabbajjā, tattha te yāvajīvaṃ ussāho karaṇīyo; atirekalābho – khomaṃ, kappāsikaṃ, koseyyaṃ, kambalaṃ, sāṇaṃ, bhaṅgaṃ. Rukkhamūlasenāsanaṃ nissāya pabbajjā, tattha te yāvajīvaṃ ussāho karaṇīyo; atirekalābho – vihāro, aḍḍhayogo, pāsādo, hammiyaṃ, guhā. Pūtimuttabhesajjaṃ nissāya pabbajjā, tattha te yāvajīvaṃ ussāho karaṇīyo; atirekalābho – sappi, navanītaṃ, telaṃ, madhu, phāṇita’’nti.

73.Now at that time in Rājagaha, a regular distribution of choice food was established. Then a certain brahmin thought: "These ascetics, the Sakyan sons, are of comfortable habits and comfortable conduct; they eat choice food and sleep in sheltered beds. Why don't I go forth among the ascetics, the Sakyan sons?" Then that brahmin approached the monks and requested going forth. The monks gave him going forth and conferred higher ordination. After he had gone forth, the distribution of food dwindled. The monks said to him: "Come now, friend, we will go for almsfood." He replied: "Friends, I did not go forth for this reason, to go for almsfood. If you give me food, I will eat; if not, I will disrobe." "But did you go forth, friend, for the sake of your belly?" "Yes, friend." Those monks who were modest … complained, criticized, and spread it about, saying: "How could a monk go forth in this well-proclaimed Dhamma and Discipline for the sake of his belly?" Those monks reported this matter to the Blessed One. … "Is it true, monk, that you went forth for the sake of your belly?" "It is true, Blessed One." The Buddha, the Blessed One, rebuked him: … "Foolish man, how could you go forth in this well-proclaimed Dhamma and Discipline for the sake of your belly? This, foolish man, is not for the confidence of those who are without it, nor for the increase of confidence in those who have it." … Having rebuked him, … having given a Dhamma talk, he addressed the monks: "Monks, I allow that when conferring higher ordination, one should explain the four supports: Going forth relies on almsfood obtained by morsels; you should strive at it for life. Any extra allowance: a communal meal, a designated meal, an invitation, a ticket meal, a fortnightly meal, an Uposatha meal, a day-after-Uposatha meal. Going forth relies on rag-robes; you should strive at it for life. Any extra allowance: linen, cotton, silk, wool, hemp, hempen cloth. Going forth relies on lodging at the root of a tree; you should strive at it for life. Any extra allowance: a monastery, a lean-to, a mansion, a dwelling, a cave. Going forth relies on fermented urine as medicine; you should strive at it for life. Any extra allowance: ghee, fresh butter, oil, honey, molasses."

Paṇāmitakathā niṭṭhitā.

The topic on expulsion is concluded.

Upajjhāyavattabhāṇavāro niṭṭhito pañcamo.

The fifth recitation section on the duties to one's preceptor is concluded.

Pañcamabhāṇavāro

The fifth recitation section.

### 18. Ācariyavattakathā ^18

> [!TIP]- Links to [[mv1-brahmali-pali#^18|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch14|BMC Chapter 14]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-MV1.18" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


18.The Discourse on the Teacher's Duties

74. Tena kho pana samayena aññataro māṇavako bhikkhū upasaṅkamitvā pabbajjaṃ yāci. Tassa bhikkhū paṭikacceva nissaye ācikkhiṃsu. So evamāha – ‘‘sace me, bhante, pabbajite nissaye ācikkheyyātha, abhirameyyāmahaṃ [abhirameyyañcāhaṃ (sī.), abhirameyyaṃ svāhaṃ (ka.)]. Na dānāhaṃ, bhante, pabbajissāmi; jegucchā me nissayā paṭikūlā’’ti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Na, bhikkhave, paṭikacceva nissayā ācikkhitabbā. Yo ācikkheyya, āpatti dukkaṭassa. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, upasampannasamanantarā nissaye ācikkhitunti.

74.Now at that time a certain young man approached the monks and requested ordination. The monks told him about the supports beforehand. He said: "Venerable sirs, if you would tell me about the supports after I have gone forth, I would be pleased. But now, venerable sirs, I will not go forth; I find the supports disgusting and repulsive." They reported this matter to the Blessed One. "Monks, one should not tell about the supports beforehand. Whoever does so commits an offense of wrong-doing. I allow that the supports be told immediately after the full ordination."

Tena kho pana samayena bhikkhū duvaggenapi tivaggenapi gaṇena upasampādenti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Na, bhikkhave, ūnadasavaggena gaṇena upasampādetabbo. Yo upasampādeyya, āpatti dukkaṭassa. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, dasavaggena vā atirekadasavaggena vā gaṇena upasampādetunti.

At that time, monks were giving full ordination with groups of two or three. They reported this matter to the Blessed One. "Monks, full ordination should not be given with a group of fewer than ten. Whoever ordains (someone thus) incurs an offense of wrong-doing. I allow, monks, full ordination to be given by a group of ten or more than ten."

75. Tena kho pana samayena bhikkhū ekavassāpi duvassāpi saddhivihārikaṃ upasampādenti. Āyasmāpi upaseno vaṅgantaputto ekavasso saddhivihārikaṃ upasampādesi. So vassaṃvuṭṭho duvasso ekavassaṃ saddhivihārikaṃ ādāya yena bhagavā tenupasaṅkami, upasaṅkamitvā bhagavantaṃ abhivādetvā ekamantaṃ nisīdi. Āciṇṇaṃ kho panetaṃ buddhānaṃ bhagavantānaṃ āgantukehi bhikkhūhi saddhiṃ paṭisammodituṃ. Atha kho bhagavā āyasmantaṃ upasenaṃ vaṅgantaputtaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘kacci, bhikkhu, khamanīyaṃ, kacci yāpanīyaṃ, kacci tvaṃ appakilamathena addhānaṃ āgato’’ti? ‘‘Khamanīyaṃ, bhagavā, yāpanīyaṃ, bhagavā. Appakilamathena mayaṃ, bhante, addhānaṃ āgatā’’ti. Jānantāpi tathāgatā pucchanti, jānantāpi na pucchanti, kālaṃ viditvā pucchanti, kālaṃ viditvā na pucchanti; atthasaṃhitaṃ tathāgatā pucchanti; no anatthasaṃhitaṃ. Anatthasaṃhite setughāto tathāgatānaṃ. Dvīhi ākārehi buddhā bhagavanto bhikkhū paṭipucchanti – dhammaṃ vā desessāma, sāvakānaṃ vā sikkhāpadaṃ paññapessāmāti. Atha kho bhagavā āyasmantaṃ upasenaṃ vaṅgantaputtaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘kativassosi tvaṃ, bhikkhū’’ti? ‘‘Duvassohaṃ, bhagavā’’ti. ‘‘Ayaṃ pana bhikkhu kativasso’’ti? ‘‘Ekavasso, bhagavā’’ti. ‘‘Kiṃ tāyaṃ bhikkhu hotī’’ti? ‘‘Saddhivihāriko me, bhagavā’’ti. Vigarahi buddho bhagavā – ‘‘ananucchavikaṃ, moghapurisa, ananulomikaṃ appatirūpaṃ assāmaṇakaṃ akappiyaṃ akaraṇīyaṃ. Kathañhi nāma tvaṃ, moghapurisa, aññehi ovadiyo anusāsiyo aññaṃ ovadituṃ anusāsituṃ maññissasi. Atilahuṃ kho tvaṃ, moghapurisa, bāhullāya āvatto, yadidaṃ gaṇabandhikaṃ. Netaṃ, moghapurisa, appasannānaṃ vā pasādāya pasannānaṃ vā bhiyyobhāvāya’’…pe… vigarahitvā…pe… dhammiṃ kathaṃ katvā bhikkhū āmantesi – ‘‘na, bhikkhave, ūnadasavassena upasampādetabbo. Yo upasampādeyya, āpatti dukkaṭassa. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, dasavassena vā atirekadasavassena vā upasampādetu’’nti.

75.At that time, monks were giving the full ordination to pupils who were one or two years in the rains. Venerable Upasena, the son of Vaṅganta, though one year in the rains, gave the full ordination to a pupil. Having completed the rains, though he was two years in the rains, he took his one-year pupil and went to the Blessed One. Having approached, he paid homage to the Blessed One and sat down to one side. Now, it is the custom of the Buddhas, the Blessed Ones, to exchange friendly greetings with incoming monks. Then the Blessed One said to Venerable Upasena, the son of Vaṅganta: "I hope, monk, you are well, I hope you are comfortable, I hope you have not come fatigued from the journey?" "I am well, Blessed One, I am comfortable, Blessed One. We, venerable sir, have not come fatigued from the journey." The Tathāgatas ask knowing, and they ask not knowing. They ask at the right time, and they ask not at the wrong time. The Tathāgatas ask about what is connected with the goal, not about what is unconnected. For the Tathāgatas, there is a breaking of the bridge to what is unconnected. The Buddhas, the Blessed Ones, question monks in two ways: either they will teach the Dhamma or they will lay down a training rule for the disciples. Then the Blessed One said to Venerable Upasena, the son of Vaṅganta: "How many years in the rains are you, monk?" "I am two years in the rains, Blessed One." "And how many years in the rains is this monk?" "He is one year in the rains, Blessed One." "What relation is this monk to you?" "He is my pupil, Blessed One." The Buddha, the Blessed One, rebuked him: "It is unsuitable, foolish man, improper, unseemly, unworthy of a renunciate, not allowable, not to be done. How could you, foolish man, think to instruct and admonish another, when you yourself need instruction and admonishment? You have quickly turned to indulgence, foolish man, namely, group-formation. This will not, foolish man, lead to confidence in the unconfident, or to increase of confidence in the confident..." Having rebuked him... he gave a Dhamma talk and addressed the monks: "Monks, one should not give the full ordination to one with less than ten years in the rains. Whoever gives the full ordination, there is an offense of wrong-doing. I allow, monks, to give the full ordination to one with ten or more years in the rains."

76. Tena kho pana samayena bhikkhū – dasavassamhā dasavassamhāti – bālā abyattā upasampādenti. Dissanti upajjhāyā bālā, saddhivihārikā paṇḍitā. Dissanti upajjhāyā abyattā, saddhivihārikā byattā. Dissanti upajjhāyā appassutā, saddhivihārikā bahussutā. Dissanti upajjhāyā duppaññā, saddhivihārikā paññavanto. Aññataropi aññatitthiyapubbo upajjhāyena sahadhammikaṃ vuccamāno upajjhāyassa vādaṃ āropetvā taṃyeva titthāyatanaṃ saṅkami. Ye te bhikkhū appicchā…pe… te ujjhāyanti khiyyanti vipācenti – kathañhi nāma bhikkhū – dasavassamhā dasavassamhāti – bālā abyattā upasampādessanti. Dissanti upajjhāyā bālā saddhivihārikā paṇḍitā, dissanti upajjhāyā abyattā saddhivihārikā byattā, dissanti upajjhāyā appassutā saddhivihārikā bahussutā, dissanti upajjhāyā duppaññā, saddhivihārikā paññavantoti. Atha kho te bhikkhū bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. ‘‘Saccaṃ kira, bhikkhave, bhikkhū – dasavassamhā dasavassamhāti – bālā abyattā upasampādenti. Dissanti upajjhāyā bālā, saddhivihārikā paṇḍitā, dissanti upajjhāyā abyattā saddhivihārikā byattā, dissanti upajjhāyā appassutā, saddhivihārikā bahussutā, dissanti upajjhāyā duppaññā, saddhivihārikā paññavanto’’ti? ‘‘Saccaṃ, bhagavā’’ti. Vigarahi buddho bhagavā…pe… kathañhi nāma te, bhikkhave, moghapurisā – dasavassamhā dasavassamhāti – bālā abyattā upasampādessanti. Dissanti upajjhāyā bālā, saddhivihārikā paṇḍitā, dissanti upajjhāyā abyattā saddhivihārikā byattā, dissanti upajjhāyā appassutā, saddhivihārikā bahussutā, dissanti upajjhāyā duppaññā, saddhivihārikā paññavanto. Netaṃ, bhikkhave, appasannānaṃ vā pasādāya…pe… vigarahitvā…pe… dhammiṃ kathaṃ katvā bhikkhū āmantesi – ‘‘na, bhikkhave, bālena abyattena upasampādetabbo. Yo upasampādeyya, āpatti dukkaṭassa. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, byattena bhikkhunā paṭibalena dasavassena vā atirekadasavassena vā upasampādetu’’nti.

76.Now at that time monks—thinking, 'We have ten years' seniority, we have ten years' seniority'—were giving the full ordination to the foolish and incompetent. There were preceptors who were foolish, while their pupils were wise. There were preceptors who were incompetent, while their pupils were competent. There were preceptors who were of little learning, while their pupils were very learned. There were preceptors who were of poor wisdom, while their pupils were wise. Even one who had formerly belonged to another sect, when being legitimately corrected by his preceptor, would refute his preceptor’s statement and return to that very sectarian refuge. The monks who were modest … complained and criticized them: "How can monks—thinking, 'We have ten years' seniority, we have ten years' seniority'—give the full ordination to the foolish and incompetent? There are preceptors who are foolish, while their pupils are wise; preceptors who are incompetent, while their pupils are competent; preceptors who are of little learning, while their pupils are very learned; preceptors who are of poor wisdom, while their pupils are wise." Then those monks informed the Buddha of this matter. "Is it true, monks, that monks—thinking, 'We have ten years' seniority, we have ten years' seniority'—are giving the full ordination to the foolish and incompetent? There are preceptors who are foolish, while their pupils are wise; preceptors who are incompetent, while their pupils are competent; preceptors who are of little learning, while their pupils are very learned; preceptors who are of poor wisdom, while their pupils are wise?" "It is true, Blessed One." The Buddha rebuked them: "How can these foolish men—thinking, 'We have ten years' seniority, we have ten years' seniority'—give the full ordination to the foolish and incompetent? There are preceptors who are foolish, while their pupils are wise; preceptors who are incompetent, while their pupils are competent; preceptors who are of little learning, while their pupils are very learned; preceptors who are of poor wisdom, while their pupils are wise. This will not inspire confidence in those without it …" After rebuking them … he gave a Dhamma talk and addressed the monks: "Monks, full ordination should not be given by a foolish and incompetent monk. Whoever gives the full ordination incurs an offense of wrong conduct. I allow, monks, that a competent and capable monk of ten years’ standing or more may give the full ordination."

77. Tena kho pana samayena bhikkhū upajjhāyesu pakkantesupi vibbhantesupi kālaṅkatesupi pakkhasaṅkantesupi anācariyakā anovadiyamānā ananusāsiyamānā dunnivatthā duppārutā anākappasampannā piṇḍāya caranti, manussānaṃ bhuñjamānānaṃ uparibhojanepi uttiṭṭhapattaṃ upanāmenti, uparikhādanīyepi – uparisāyanīyepi – uparipānīyepi uttiṭṭhapattaṃ upanāmenti; sāmaṃ sūpampi odanampi viññāpetvā bhuñjanti; bhattaggepi uccāsaddā mahāsaddā viharanti. Manussā ujjhāyanti khiyyanti vipācenti – ‘‘kathañhi nāma samaṇā sakyaputtiyā dunnivatthā duppārutā anākappasampannā piṇḍāya carissanti; manussānaṃ bhuñjamānānaṃ uparibhojanepi uttiṭṭhapattaṃ upanāmessanti, uparikhādanīyepi – uparisāyanīyepi – uparipānīyepi uttiṭṭhapattaṃ upanāmessanti; sāmaṃ sūpampi odanampi viññāpetvā bhuñjissanti; bhattaggepi uccāsaddā mahāsaddā viharissanti, seyyathāpi brāhmaṇā brāhmaṇabhojane’’ti. Assosuṃ kho bhikkhū tesaṃ manussānaṃ ujjhāyantānaṃ khiyyantānaṃ vipācentānaṃ …pe… atha kho te bhikkhū bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Saccaṃ kira, bhikkhave…pe… saccaṃ, bhagavāti…pe… vigarahitvā dhammiṃ kathaṃ katvā bhikkhū āmantesi –

77.Now at that time monks, when their preceptors had left, had disrobed, had passed away, or had gone over to another faction, being without a teacher, unadmonished, uninstructed, poorly dressed, improperly robed, lacking in decorum, went for alms. While people were eating, they held out their bowls for leftover food, for leftover snacks, for leftover delicacies, and for leftover drinks. They themselves asked for curries and rice and ate them. In the refectory, they lived making loud and great noises. People complained and criticized them, saying, "How can these Sakyan ascetics go for alms poorly dressed, improperly robed, lacking in decorum? While people are eating, they hold out their bowls for leftover food, for leftover snacks, for leftover delicacies, and for leftover drinks. They themselves ask for curries and rice and eat them. In the refectory, they live making loud and great noises, just like brahmins at a brahmin feast!" The monks heard the complaints of those people... and they reported the matter to the Blessed One. "Is it true, monks...?" "It is true, Blessed One." ...Having rebuked them, given a Dhamma talk, the Blessed One addressed the monks:

‘‘Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, ācariyaṃ. Ācariyo, bhikkhave, antevāsikamhi puttacittaṃ upaṭṭhāpessati, antevāsiko ācariyamhi pitucittaṃ upaṭṭhāpessati. Evaṃ te aññamaññaṃ sagāravā sappatissā sabhāgavuttino viharantā imasmiṃ dhammavinaye vuddhiṃ viruḷhiṃ vepullaṃ āpajjissanti. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, dasavassaṃ nissāya vatthuṃ, dasavassena nissayaṃ dātuṃ. Evañca pana, bhikkhave, ācariyo gahetabbo. Ekaṃsaṃ uttarāsaṅgaṃ karitvā pāde vanditvā ukkuṭikaṃ nisīditvā añjaliṃ paggahetvā evamassa vacanīyo – ‘ācariyo me, bhante, hohi, āyasmato nissāya vacchāmi; ācariyo me, bhante, hohi, āyasmato nissāya vacchāmi; ācariyo me, bhante, hohi, āyasmato nissāya vacchāmī’ti. ‘Sāhūti’ vā ‘lahūti’ vā ‘opāyika’nti vā ‘patirūpa’nti vā ‘pāsādikena sampādehī’ti vā kāyena viññāpeti, vācāya viññāpeti, kāyena vācāya viññāpeti, gahito hoti ācariyo; na kāyena viññāpeti, na vācāya viññāpeti, na kāyena vācāya viññāpeti, na gahito hoti ācariyo.

"Monks, I allow a teacher. Monks, the teacher should establish a parental attitude towards the disciple, and the disciple should establish a filial attitude towards the teacher. Thus, living with mutual respect, deference, and concord, they will attain growth, increase, and abundance in this Dhamma and Discipline. Monks, I allow dependence for ten years, and the giving of dependence to one who has ten years. And, monks, a teacher should be accepted in this way: having arranged the upper robe over one shoulder, bowed at the feet, sat in a squatting position, and raised joined palms, one should say: ‘Venerable sir, be my teacher; I will live in dependence on the venerable one. Venerable sir, be my teacher; I will live in dependence on the venerable one. Venerable sir, be my teacher; I will live in dependence on the venerable one.’ If he indicates with the body, or with speech, or with both body and speech, ‘Good,’ or ‘Very well,’ or ‘It is allowable,’ or ‘It is suitable,’ or ‘Carry it out confidently,’ then the teacher is accepted. If he does not indicate with the body, nor with speech, nor with both body and speech, then the teacher is not accepted."

78. [cūḷava. 380 ādayo] ‘‘Antevāsikena, bhikkhave, ācariyamhi sammā vattitabbaṃ. Tatrāyaṃ sammāvattanā –

78."Monks, a disciple should behave properly towards the teacher. This is the proper conduct:"

‘‘Kālasseva uṭṭhāya upāhanaṃ omuñcitvā ekaṃsaṃ uttarāsaṅgaṃ karitvā dantakaṭṭhaṃ dātabbaṃ, mukhodakaṃ dātabbaṃ, āsanaṃ paññapetabbaṃ. Sace yāgu hoti, bhājanaṃ dhovitvā yāgu upanāmetabbā. Yāguṃ pītassa udakaṃ datvā bhājanaṃ paṭiggahetvā nīcaṃ katvā sādhukaṃ appaṭighaṃsantena dhovitvā paṭisāmetabbaṃ. Ācariyamhi vuṭṭhite āsanaṃ uddharitabbaṃ. Sace so deso uklāpo hoti, so deso sammajjitabbo.

"Rising early, one should take off the sandals, arrange the upper robe over one shoulder, and offer a tooth-cleaning stick. Water for rinsing the mouth should be provided, and a seat should be arranged. If there is rice gruel, the bowl should be washed and the rice gruel offered. After the rice gruel has been drunk, water should be given, and the bowl should be received back. Holding it low, one should wash it thoroughly without scraping it and put it away. When the teacher has risen, the seat should be removed. If that place is untidy, it should be swept."

‘‘Sace ācariyo gāmaṃ pavisitukāmo hoti, nivāsanaṃ dātabbaṃ, paṭinivāsanaṃ paṭiggahetabbaṃ, kāyabandhanaṃ dātabbaṃ, saguṇaṃ katvā saṅghāṭiyo dātabbā, dhovitvā patto sodako dātabbo. Sace ācariyo pacchāsamaṇaṃ ākaṅkhati, timaṇḍalaṃ paṭicchādentena parimaṇḍalaṃ nivāsetvā kāyabandhanaṃ bandhitvā saguṇaṃ katvā saṅghāṭiyo pārupitvā gaṇṭhikaṃ paṭimuñcitvā dhovitvā pattaṃ gahetvā ācariyassa pacchāsamaṇena hotabbaṃ. Nātidūre gantabbaṃ, nāccāsanne gantabbaṃ, pattapariyāpannaṃ paṭiggahetabbaṃ. Na ācariyassa bhaṇamānassa antarantarā kathā opātetabbā. Ācariyo āpattisāmantā bhaṇamāno nivāretabbo.

"If the teacher wishes to enter the village, a lower robe should be given, the returned lower robe should be received, a belt should be given, the outer robes should be given folded, and a bowl should be given, washed and with water. If the teacher desires an attendant, one should dress in a well-arranged lower robe covering the three circles, fasten the belt, fold the outer robes, put them on, loosen the knot, take the washed bowl, and attend the teacher. One should not walk too far behind, nor too close. The bowl, once full, should be received. One should not interrupt the teacher while he is speaking. If the teacher is speaking about something near an offense, he should be restrained."

‘‘Nivattantena paṭhamataraṃ āgantvā āsanaṃ paññapetabbaṃ, pādodakaṃ pādapīṭhaṃ pādakathalikaṃ upanikkhipitabbaṃ, paccuggantvā pattacīvaraṃ paṭiggahetabbaṃ, paṭinivāsanaṃ dātabbaṃ, nivāsanaṃ paṭiggahetabbaṃ. Sace cīvaraṃ sinnaṃ hoti, muhuttaṃ uṇhe otāpetabbaṃ, na ca uṇhe cīvaraṃ nidahitabbaṃ. Cīvaraṃ saṅgharitabbaṃ. Cīvaraṃ saṅgharantena caturaṅgulaṃ kaṇṇaṃ ussāretvā cīvaraṃ saṅgharitabbaṃ – mā majjhe bhaṅgo ahosīti. Obhoge kāyabandhanaṃ kātabbaṃ.

"On returning, one should first prepare a seat, provide foot water, a footstool, and a foot-wiping cloth, go forward to receive the bowl and robe, offer an under-robe, and accept the outer robe. If the robe is damp, it should be warmed for a short while, but the robe should not be placed directly in the sun. The robe should be folded. When folding the robe, one should lift the edge by four finger-widths and then fold it—so that no crease forms in the middle. A waistband should be placed on the fold."

‘‘Sace piṇḍapāto hoti, ācariyo ca bhuñjitukāmo hoti, udakaṃ datvā piṇḍapāto upanāmetabbo. Ācariyo pānīyena pucchitabbo. Bhuttāvissa udakaṃ datvā pattaṃ paṭiggahetvā nīcaṃ katvā sādhukaṃ appaṭighaṃsantena dhovitvā vodakaṃ katvā muhuttaṃ uṇhe otāpetabbo, na ca uṇhe patto nidahitabbo. Pattacīvaraṃ nikkhipitabbaṃ. Pattaṃ nikkhipantena ekena hatthena pattaṃ gahetvā ekena hatthena heṭṭhāmañcaṃ vā heṭṭhāpīṭhaṃ vā parāmasitvā patto nikkhipitabbo. Na ca anantarahitāya bhūmiyā patto nikkhipitabbo. Cīvaraṃ nikkhipantena ekena hatthena cīvaraṃ gahetvā ekena hatthena cīvaravaṃsaṃ vā cīvararajjuṃ vā pamajjitvā pārato antaṃ orato bhogaṃ katvā cīvaraṃ nikkhipitabbaṃ. Ācariyamhi vuṭṭhite āsanaṃ uddharitabbaṃ, pādodakaṃ pādapīṭhaṃ pādakathalikaṃ paṭisāmetabbaṃ. Sace so deso uklāpo hoti, so deso sammajjitabbo.

"If there is almsfood and the teacher wishes to eat, after giving water, the almsfood should be presented. The teacher should be asked for drinking water. After he has eaten, water should be given, the bowl received, lowered, and carefully washed without scraping it. After making it free of water, it should be exposed to warmth for a short while, but the bowl should not be placed directly in the sun. The bowl and robe should be put away. When putting away the bowl, one should take the bowl with one hand and touch the lower bench or lower seat with the other hand before placing the bowl down. The bowl should not be placed on the bare ground without an intervening layer. When putting away the robe, one should take the robe with one hand and smooth out the robe rack or robe cord with the other hand, then fold the robe edge to edge and put it away. When the teacher has risen, the seat should be removed, and the foot-water, footstool, and foot-wiping cloth should be put away. If the place is untidy, it should be swept."

‘‘Sace ācariyo nahāyitukāmo hoti, nahānaṃ paṭiyādetabbaṃ. Sace sītena attho hoti, sītaṃ paṭiyādetabbaṃ. Sace uṇhena attho hoti, uṇhaṃ paṭiyādetabbaṃ.

"If the teacher wishes to bathe, bathing facilities should be prepared. If cool water is needed, cool water should be provided. If warm water is needed, warm water should be provided."

‘‘Sace ācariyo jantāgharaṃ pavisitukāmo hoti, cuṇṇaṃ sannetabbaṃ, mattikā temetabbā, jantāgharapīṭhaṃ ādāya ācariyassa piṭṭhito piṭṭhito gantvā jantāgharapīṭhaṃ datvā cīvaraṃ paṭiggahetvā ekamantaṃ nikkhipitabbaṃ, cuṇṇaṃ dātabbaṃ, mattikā dātabbā. Sace ussahati, jantāgharaṃ pavisitabbaṃ. Jantāgharaṃ pavisantena mattikāya mukhaṃ makkhetvā purato ca pacchato ca paṭicchādetvā jantāgharaṃ pavisitabbaṃ. Na there bhikkhū anupakhajja nisīditabbaṃ. Na navā bhikkhū āsanena paṭibāhitabbā. Jantāghare ācariyassa parikammaṃ kātabbaṃ. Jantāgharā nikkhamantena jantāgharapīṭhaṃ ādāya purato ca pacchato ca paṭicchādetvā jantāgharā nikkhamitabbaṃ.

"If the teacher wishes to enter the hot room, powder should be prepared, and clay moistened. Taking the hot room stool, one should follow right behind the teacher and give him the stool. After receiving his robe, it should be set aside. Powder should be given, and clay should be given. If capable, one should enter the hot room. When entering the hot room, one should smear the face with clay, cover oneself front and back, and then enter the hot room. One should not sit crowding the senior monks. Junior monks should not be pushed aside from the seats. In the hot room, one should attend to the teacher’s needs. When leaving the hot room, one should take the hot room stool, cover oneself front and back, and then leave the hot room."

‘‘Udakepi ācariyassa parikammaṃ kātabbaṃ. Nahātena paṭhamataraṃ uttaritvā attano gattaṃ vodakaṃ katvā nivāsetvā ācariyassa gattato udakaṃ pamajjitabbaṃ, nivāsanaṃ dātabbaṃ, saṅghāṭi dātabbā, jantāgharapīṭhaṃ ādāya paṭhamataraṃ āgantvā āsanaṃ paññapetabbaṃ, pādodakaṃ pādapīṭhaṃ pādakathalikaṃ upanikkhipitabbaṃ. Ācariyo pānīyena pucchitabbo. Sace uddisāpetukāmo hoti, uddisāpetabbo. Sace paripucchitukāmo hoti, paripucchitabbo.

"One should also attend to the teacher’s needs regarding water. After bathing, one should emerge first, dry one's body, put on the lower robe, and then wipe the water from the teacher’s body. The lower robe should be given, and the outer robe should be given. Taking the hot room stool, one should return first, prepare the seat, and set out foot-washing water, a footstool, and a foot-wiping cloth. The teacher should be asked about drinking water. If he wishes to recite, he should be allowed to recite. If he wishes to question, he should be allowed to question."

‘‘Yasmiṃ vihāre ācariyo viharati, sace so vihāro uklāpo hoti, sace ussahati, sodhetabbo. Vihāraṃ sodhentena paṭhamaṃ pattacīvaraṃ nīharitvā ekamantaṃ nikkhipitabbaṃ; nisīdanapaccattharaṇaṃ nīharitvā ekamantaṃ nikkhipitabbaṃ; bhisibibbohanaṃ nīharitvā ekamantaṃ nikkhipitabbaṃ; mañco nīcaṃ katvā sādhukaṃ appaṭighaṃsantena, asaṅghaṭṭentena kavāṭapiṭṭhaṃ, nīharitvā ekamantaṃ nikkhipitabbo; pīṭhaṃ nīcaṃ katvā sādhukaṃ appaṭighaṃsantena, asaṅghaṭṭentena kavāṭapiṭṭhaṃ, nīharitvā ekamantaṃ nikkhipitabbaṃ; mañcapaṭipādakā nīharitvā ekamantaṃ nikkhipitabbā; kheḷamallako nīharitvā ekamantaṃ nikkhipitabbo; apassenaphalakaṃ nīharitvā ekamantaṃ nikkhipitabbaṃ; bhūmattharaṇaṃ yathāpaññattaṃ sallakkhetvā nīharitvā ekamantaṃ nikkhipitabbaṃ. Sace vihāre santānakaṃ hoti, ullokā paṭhamaṃ ohāretabbaṃ, ālokasandhikaṇṇabhāgā pamajjitabbā. Sace gerukaparikammakatā bhitti kaṇṇakitā hoti, coḷakaṃ temetvā pīḷetvā pamajjitabbā. Sace kāḷavaṇṇakatā bhūmi kaṇṇakitā hoti, coḷakaṃ temetvā pīḷetvā pamajjitabbā. Sace akatā hoti bhūmi, udakena paripphositvā sammajjitabbā – mā vihāro rajena uhaññīti. Saṅkāraṃ vicinitvā ekamantaṃ chaḍḍetabbaṃ.

"In the dwelling where the teacher resides, if the dwelling is untidy, and one is capable, it should be cleaned. When cleaning the dwelling, first the bowl and robe should be taken out and set aside. The sitting mat and spread should be taken out and set aside. The mattress and bolster should be taken out and set aside. The bed should be lowered carefully, without scraping or knocking against the doorposts, taken out, and set aside. The stool should be lowered carefully, without scraping or knocking against the doorposts, taken out, and set aside. The bed legs should be taken out and set aside. The spittoon should be taken out and set aside. The backrest should be taken out and set aside. The floor covering should be inspected according to the arrangement, taken up, and set aside. If the dwelling has cobwebs, they should first be removed from above. The corners of the window openings should be wiped. If the walls, treated with red ochre, are stained, a cloth should be moistened and wrung out to wipe them. If the floor, treated with black color, is stained, a cloth should be moistened and wrung out to wipe it. If the floor is untreated, it should be sprinkled with water and swept—lest the dwelling be soiled with dust. Rubbish should be collected and discarded to one side."

‘‘Bhūmattharaṇaṃ otāpetvā sodhetvā papphoṭetvā atiharitvā yathāpaññattaṃ paññapetabbaṃ. Mañcapaṭipādakā otāpetvā pamajjitvā atiharitvā yathāṭhāne ṭhapetabbā. Mañco otāpetvā sodhetvā papphoṭetvā nīcaṃ katvā sādhukaṃ appaṭighaṃsantena, asaṅghaṭṭentena kavāṭapiṭṭhaṃ, atiharitvā yathāpaññattaṃ paññapetabbo. Pīṭhaṃ otāpetvā sodhetvā papphoṭetvā nīcaṃ katvā sādhukaṃ appaṭighaṃsantena, asaṅghaṭṭentena kavāṭapiṭṭhaṃ, atiharitvā yathāpaññattaṃ paññapetabbaṃ. Bhisibibbohanaṃ otāpetvā sodhetvā papphoṭetvā atiharitvā yathāpaññattaṃ paññapetabbaṃ. Nisīdanapaccattharaṇaṃ otāpetvā sodhetvā papphoṭetvā atiharitvā yathāpaññattaṃ paññapetabbaṃ. Kheḷamallako otāpetvā pamajjitvā atiharitvā yathāṭhāne ṭhapetabbo. Apassenaphalakaṃ otāpetvā pamajjitvā atiharitvā yathāṭhāne ṭhapetabbaṃ. Pattacīvaraṃ nikkhipitabbaṃ. Pattaṃ nikkhipantena ekena hatthena pattaṃ gahetvā ekena hatthena heṭṭhāmañcaṃ vā heṭṭhāpīṭhaṃ vā parāmasitvā patto nikkhipitabbo. Na ca anantarahitāya bhūmiyā patto nikkhipitabbo. Cīvaraṃ nikkhipantena ekena hatthena cīvaraṃ gahetvā ekena hatthena cīvaravaṃsaṃ vā cīvararajjuṃ vā pamajjitvā pārato antaṃ orato bhogaṃ katvā cīvaraṃ nikkhipitabbaṃ.

Having taken up the floor covering, cleaned it, beaten it, and put it aside, it should be laid out as prescribed. The bed legs should be taken up, wiped, put aside, and placed in their proper positions. The bed should be taken up, cleaned, beaten, lowered carefully without scraping or bumping against the doorposts, put aside, and laid out as prescribed. The bench should be taken up, cleaned, beaten, lowered carefully without scraping or bumping against the doorposts, put aside, and laid out as prescribed. The mattress and pillow should be taken up, cleaned, beaten, put aside, and laid out as prescribed. The sitting mat and covering should be taken up, cleaned, beaten, put aside, and laid out as prescribed. The spittoon should be taken up, wiped, put aside, and placed in its proper position. The leaning board should be taken up, wiped, put aside, and placed in its proper position. The bowl and robe should be put away. When putting away the bowl, one should hold the bowl with one hand and touch underneath the bed or bench with the other hand before placing the bowl down. The bowl should not be placed directly on the bare ground. When putting away the robe, one should hold the robe with one hand, wipe the robe rack or robe cord with the other hand, fold the robe edge over edge from the near end to the far end, and then place it away.

‘‘Sace puratthimā sarajā vātā vāyanti, puratthimā vātapānā thaketabbā. Sace pacchimā sarajā vātā vāyanti, pacchimā vātapānā thaketabbā. Sace uttarā sarajā vātā vāyanti, uttarā vātapānā thaketabbā. Sace dakkhiṇā sarajā vātā vāyanti, dakkhiṇā vātapānā thaketabbā. Sace sītakālo hoti, divā vātapānā vivaritabbā, rattiṃ thaketabbā. Sace uṇhakālo hoti, divā vātapānā thaketabbā, rattiṃ vivaritabbā.

If dusty winds blow from the east, eastern windows should be closed. If dusty winds blow from the west, western windows should be closed. If dusty winds blow from the north, northern windows should be closed. If dusty winds blow from the south, southern windows should be closed. If it is the cold season, windows should be opened during the day and closed at night. If it is the hot season, windows should be closed during the day and opened at night.

‘‘Sace pariveṇaṃ uklāpaṃ hoti, pariveṇaṃ sammajjitabbaṃ. Sace koṭṭhako uklāpo hoti, koṭṭhako sammajjitabbo. Sace upaṭṭhānasālā uklāpā hoti, upaṭṭhānasālā sammajjitabbā. Sace aggisālā uklāpā hoti, aggisālā sammajjitabbā. Sace vaccakuṭi uklāpā hoti, vaccakuṭi sammajjitabbā. Sace pānīyaṃ na hoti, pānīyaṃ upaṭṭhāpetabbaṃ. Sace paribhojanīyaṃ na hoti, paribhojanīyaṃ upaṭṭhāpetabbaṃ. Sace ācamanakumbhiyaṃ udakaṃ na hoti, ācamanakumbhiyā udakaṃ āsiñcitabbaṃ.

If the enclosure is dirty, the enclosure should be swept. If the storeroom is dirty, the storeroom should be swept. If the service hall is dirty, the service hall should be swept. If the fire room is dirty, the fire room should be swept. If the toilet is dirty, the toilet should be swept. If there is no drinking water, drinking water should be provided. If there is no water for use, water for use should be provided. If there is no water in the washing bowl, water should be poured into the washing bowl.

‘‘Sace ācariyassa anabhirati uppannā hoti, antevāsikena vūpakāsetabbo, vūpakāsāpetabbo, dhammakathā vāssa kātabbā. Sace ācariyassa kukkuccaṃ uppannaṃ hoti, antevāsikena vinodetabbaṃ, vinodāpetabbaṃ, dhammakathā vāssa kātabbā. Sace ācariyassa diṭṭhigataṃ uppannaṃ hoti, antevāsikena vivecetabbaṃ, vivecāpetabbaṃ, dhammakathā vāssa kātabbā. Sace ācariyo garudhammaṃ ajjhāpanno hoti parivāsāraho, antevāsikena ussukkaṃ kātabbaṃ – kinti nu kho saṅgho ācariyassa parivāsaṃ dadeyyāti. Sace ācariyo mūlāya paṭikassanāraho hoti, antevāsikena ussukkaṃ kātabbaṃ – kinti nu kho saṅgho ācariyaṃ mūlāya paṭikasseyyāti. Sace ācariyo mānattāraho hoti, antevāsikena ussukkaṃ kātabbaṃ – kinti nu kho saṅgho ācariyassa mānattaṃ dadeyyāti. Sace ācariyo abbhānāraho hoti, antevāsikena ussukkaṃ kātabbaṃ – kinti nu kho saṅgho ācariyaṃ abbheyyāti. Sace saṅgho ācariyassa kammaṃ kattukāmo hoti, tajjanīyaṃ vā niyassaṃ vā pabbājanīyaṃ vā paṭisāraṇīyaṃ vā ukkhepanīyaṃ vā, antevāsikena ussukkaṃ kātabbaṃ – kinti nu kho saṅgho ācariyassa kammaṃ na kareyya, lahukāya vā pariṇāmeyyāti. Kataṃ vā panassa hoti saṅghena kammaṃ, tajjanīyaṃ vā niyassaṃ vā pabbājanīyaṃ vā paṭisāraṇīyaṃ vā ukkhepanīyaṃ vā, antevāsikena ussukkaṃ kātabbaṃ – kinti nu kho ācariyo sammā vatteyya, lomaṃ pāteyya, netthāraṃ vatteyya, saṅgho taṃ kammaṃ paṭippassambheyyāti.

If dissatisfaction arises in the teacher, the student should pacify it, or have it pacified, or give him a Dhamma talk. If remorse arises in the teacher, the student should dispel it, or arrange for others to dispel it, or give him a Dhamma talk. If a wrong view arises in the teacher, the student should help him abandon it, or arrange for others to do so, or give him a Dhamma talk. If the teacher has committed a heavy offense deserving parivāsa, the student should make an effort: ‘How can the Saṅgha grant the teacher parivāsa?’ If the teacher deserves to be sent back to the beginning (mūlāya paṭikassanāraho), the student should make an effort: ‘How can the Saṅgha send the teacher back to the beginning?’ If the teacher deserves mānatta, the student should make an effort: ‘How can the Saṅgha grant the teacher mānatta?’ If the teacher deserves rehabilitation (abbhāna), the student should make an effort: ‘How can the Saṅgha rehabilitate the teacher?’ If the Saṅgha wants to take disciplinary action against the teacher—whether censure (tajjanīya), demotion (niyassa), banishment (pabbājanīya), reconciliation (paṭisāraṇīya), or suspension (ukkhepanīya)—the student should make an effort: ‘How can the Saṅgha not take action against the teacher, or impose a lighter penalty?’ And if the Saṅgha has already taken disciplinary action—whether censure (tajjanīya), demotion (niyassa), banishment (pabbājanīya), reconciliation (paṭisāraṇīya), or suspension (ukkhepanīya)—the student should make an effort: ‘How can the teacher behave properly, lower his crest, mend his ways, so that the Saṅgha might rescind that action?’

‘‘Sace ācariyassa cīvaraṃ dhovitabbaṃ hoti, antevāsikena dhovitabbaṃ, ussukkaṃ vā kātabbaṃ – kinti nu kho ācariyassa cīvaraṃ dhoviyethāti. Sace ācariyassa cīvaraṃ kātabbaṃ hoti, antevāsikena kātabbaṃ, ussukkaṃ vā kātabbaṃ – kinti nu kho ācariyassa cīvaraṃ kariyethāti. Sace ācariyassa rajanaṃ pacitabbaṃ hoti, antevāsikena pacitabbaṃ, ussukkaṃ vā kātabbaṃ – kinti nu kho ācariyassa rajanaṃ paciyethāti. Sace ācariyassa cīvaraṃ rajitabbaṃ hoti, antevāsikena rajitabbaṃ, ussukkaṃ vā kātabbaṃ – kinti nu kho ācariyassa cīvaraṃ rajiyethāti. Cīvaraṃ rajantena sādhukaṃ samparivattakaṃ samparivattakaṃ rajitabbaṃ, na ca acchinne theve pakkamitabbaṃ.

If the teacher’s robe needs washing, the student should wash it, or make an effort, thinking: ‘How can the teacher’s robe be washed?’ If the teacher’s robe needs making, the student should make it, or make an effort, thinking: ‘How can the teacher’s robe be made?’ If the teacher’s dye needs boiling, the student should boil it, or make an effort, thinking: ‘How can the teacher’s dye be boiled?’ If the teacher’s robe needs dyeing, the student should dye it, or make an effort, thinking: ‘How can the teacher’s robe be dyed?’ When dyeing the robe, the student should carefully turn it over and over, and he should not leave without the dye taking properly.

‘‘Na ācariyaṃ anāpucchā ekaccassa patto dātabbo, na ekaccassa patto paṭiggahetabbo; na ekaccassa cīvaraṃ dātabbaṃ; na ekaccassa cīvaraṃ paṭiggahetabbaṃ; na ekaccassa parikkhāro dātabbo; na ekaccassa parikkhāro paṭiggahetabbo; na ekaccassa kesā chedetabbā; na ekaccena kesā chedāpetabbā; na ekaccassa parikammaṃ kātabbaṃ; na ekaccena parikammaṃ kārāpetabbaṃ; na ekaccassa veyyāvacco kātabbo; na ekaccena veyyāvacco kārāpetabbo; na ekaccassa pacchāsamaṇena hotabbaṃ; na ekacco pacchāsamaṇo ādātabbo; na ekaccassa piṇḍapāto nīharitabbo; na ekaccena piṇḍapāto nīharāpetabbo. Na ācariyaṃ anāpucchā gāmo pavisitabbo, na susānaṃ gantabbaṃ, na disā pakkamitabbā. Sace ācariyo gilāno hoti, yāvajīvaṃ upaṭṭhātabbo, vuṭṭhānamassa āgametabba’’nti.

Without asking the teacher, a bowl should not be given to certain individuals, nor should a bowl be received from certain individuals; a robe should not be given to certain individuals; a robe should not be received from certain individuals; requisites should not be given to certain individuals; requisites should not be received from certain individuals; the hair of certain individuals should not be cut; one’s hair should not be cut by certain individuals; services should not be performed for certain individuals; services should not be caused to be performed by certain individuals; one should not be an attendant for certain individuals; certain individuals should not be taken as attendants; almsfood should not be taken out for certain individuals; almsfood should not be caused to be taken out by certain individuals. Without asking the teacher, a village should not be entered, a charnel ground should not be visited, or another direction should not be departed to. If the teacher is sick, he should be attended to for life, awaiting his recovery.

Ācariyavattaṃ niṭṭhitaṃ.

The chapter on the Teacher's Duties is concluded.

### 19. Antevāsikavattakathā ^19

> [!TIP]- Links to [[mv1-brahmali-pali#^19|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch14|BMC Chapter 14]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-MV1.19" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


19.The Discourse on the Duties of a Resident Pupil

79. [cūḷava. 381-382] ‘‘Ācariyena, bhikkhave, antevāsikamhi sammā vattitabbaṃ. Tatrāyaṃ sammāvattanā –

79.Monks, a teacher should behave properly towards his pupil. Here is the proper conduct:

‘‘Ācariyena, bhikkhave, antevāsiko saṅgahetabbo anuggahetabbo uddesena paripucchāya ovādena anusāsaniyā. Sace ācariyassa patto hoti, antevāsikassa patto na hoti, ācariyena antevāsikassa patto dātabbo, ussukkaṃ vā kātabbaṃ – kinti nu kho antevāsikassa patto uppajjiyethāti. Sace ācariyassa cīvaraṃ hoti, antevāsikassa cīvaraṃ na hoti, ācariyena antevāsikassa cīvaraṃ dātabbaṃ, ussukkaṃ vā kātabbaṃ – kinti nu kho antevāsikassa cīvaraṃ uppajjiyethāti. Sace ācariyassa parikkhāro hoti, antevāsikassa parikkhāro na hoti, ācariyena antevāsikassa parikkhāro dātabbo, ussukkaṃ vā kātabbaṃ – kinti nu kho antevāsikassa parikkhāro uppajjiyethāti.

A teacher, monks, should embrace his pupil and support him with instruction, questioning, advice, and admonition. If the teacher has a bowl but the pupil does not, the teacher should give a bowl to the pupil, or make an effort, thinking, ‘How might a bowl come to the pupil?’ If the teacher has a robe but the pupil does not, the teacher should give a robe to the pupil, or make an effort, thinking, ‘How might a robe come to the pupil?’ If the teacher has requisites but the pupil does not, the teacher should give requisites to the pupil, or make an effort, thinking, ‘How might requisites come to the pupil?’

‘‘Sace antevāsiko gilāno hoti, kālasseva uṭṭhāya dantakaṭṭhaṃ dātabbaṃ, mukhodakaṃ dātabbaṃ, āsanaṃ paññapetabbaṃ. Sace yāgu hoti, bhājanaṃ dhovitvā yāgu upanāmetabbā. Yāguṃ pītassa udakaṃ datvā bhājanaṃ paṭiggahetvā nīcaṃ katvā sādhukaṃ appaṭighaṃsantena dhovitvā paṭisāmetabbaṃ. Antevāsikamhi vuṭṭhite āsanaṃ uddharitabbaṃ. Sace so deso uklāpo hoti, so deso sammajjitabbo.

If the pupil is sick, one should rise early and give him a tooth-stick and water for washing the mouth, and prepare a seat. If there is rice-gruel, one should wash the bowl and offer the rice-gruel. After he has drunk the rice-gruel, one should give him water, receive the bowl, lower it gently, wash it carefully without scraping, drain it of water, and put it away. When the pupil has risen, one should remove the seat. If the place is unswept, one should sweep it.

‘‘Sace antevāsiko gāmaṃ pavisitukāmo hoti, nivāsanaṃ dātabbaṃ, paṭinivāsanaṃ paṭiggahetabbaṃ, kāyabandhanaṃ dātabbaṃ, saguṇaṃ katvā saṅghāṭiyo dātabbā, dhovitvā patto sodako dātabbo.

If the pupil wishes to enter the village, one should give him a lower robe, receive the lower robe (he was wearing), give him a belt, give him his outer robes after folding them properly, and give him a washed bowl with water.

‘‘Ettāvatā nivattissatīti āsanaṃ paññapetabbaṃ, pādodakaṃ pādapīṭhaṃ pādakathalikaṃ upanikkhipitabbaṃ, paccuggantvā pattacīvaraṃ paṭiggahetabbaṃ, paṭinivāsanaṃ dātabbaṃ, nivāsanaṃ paṭiggahetabbaṃ. Sace cīvaraṃ sinnaṃ hoti, muhuttaṃ uṇhe otāpetabbaṃ, na ca uṇhe cīvaraṃ nidahitabbaṃ. Cīvaraṃ saṅgharitabbaṃ. Cīvaraṃ saṅgharantena caturaṅgulaṃ kaṇṇaṃ ussāretvā cīvaraṃ saṅgharitabbaṃ – mā majjhe bhaṅgo ahosīti. Obhoge kāyabandhanaṃ kātabbaṃ.

Thinking, 'He will return by this time,' a seat should be prepared. Foot water, a footstool, and a foot wiper should be placed nearby. One should go to meet him and receive his bowl and robe. A fresh lower robe should be given (to him), and the (worn) lower robe should be received (from him). If the robe is damp, it should be aired in the sun for a short while, but the robe should not be left in the sun. The robe should be folded. While folding the robe, one should lift the edge four finger-widths and fold it carefully, thinking, 'Lest it crease in the middle.' A waistband should be made at the hem.

‘‘Sace piṇḍapāto hoti, antevāsiko ca bhuñjitukāmo hoti, udakaṃ datvā piṇḍapāto upanāmetabbo. Antevāsiko pānīyena pucchitabbo. Bhuttāvissa udakaṃ datvā pattaṃ paṭiggahetvā nīcaṃ katvā sādhukaṃ appaṭighaṃsantena dhovitvā vodakaṃ katvā muhuttaṃ uṇhe otāpetabbo, na ca uṇhe patto nidahitabbo. Pattacīvaraṃ nikkhipitabbaṃ. Pattaṃ nikkhipantena ekena hatthena pattaṃ gahetvā ekena hatthena heṭṭhāmañcaṃ vā heṭṭhāpīṭhaṃ vā parāmasitvā patto nikkhipitabbo. Na ca anantarahitāya bhūmiyā patto nikkhipitabbo. Cīvaraṃ nikkhipantena ekena hatthena cīvaraṃ gahetvā ekena hatthena cīvaravaṃsaṃ vā cīvararajjuṃ vā pamajjitvā pārato antaṃ orato bhogaṃ katvā cīvaraṃ nikkhipitabbaṃ. Antevāsikamhi vuṭṭhite āsanaṃ uddharitabbaṃ, pādodakaṃ pādapīṭhaṃ pādakathalikaṃ paṭisāmetabbaṃ. Sace so deso uklāpo hoti, so deso sammajjitabbo.

If there is almsfood, and the pupil wishes to eat, water should be given, and the almsfood should be offered. The pupil should be asked about drinking water. After he has eaten, water should be given, and the bowl should be received. Holding it low, it should be washed thoroughly without scraping, drained of water, and aired in the sun for a short while—but the bowl should not be left in the sun. The bowl and robe should be put away. When putting away the bowl, one should hold the bowl with one hand and touch the lower bench or seat with the other hand before placing it down. The bowl should not be placed directly on the bare ground. When putting away the robe, one should hold the robe with one hand and smooth the robe rack or robe cord with the other. Then, folding the robe lengthwise, edge to edge, it should be put away. When the pupil has risen, the seat should be removed, and the foot water, footstool, and foot wiper should be put away. If the place is unswept, it should be swept.

‘‘Sace antevāsiko nahāyitukāmo hoti, nahānaṃ paṭiyādetabbaṃ. Sace sītena attho hoti, sītaṃ paṭiyādetabbaṃ. Sace uṇhena attho hoti, uṇhaṃ paṭiyādetabbaṃ.

If the pupil wishes to bathe, bathing should be arranged. If he needs cool water, cool water should be arranged. If he needs warm water, warm water should be arranged.

‘‘Sace antevāsiko jantāgharaṃ pavisitukāmo hoti, cuṇṇaṃ sannetabbaṃ, mattikā temetabbā, jantāgharapīṭhaṃ ādāya gantvā jantāgharapīṭhaṃ datvā cīvaraṃ paṭiggahetvā ekamantaṃ nikkhipitabbaṃ, cuṇṇaṃ dātabbaṃ, mattikā dātabbā. Sace ussahati, jantāgharaṃ pavisitabbaṃ. Jantāgharaṃ pavisantena mattikāya mukhaṃ makkhetvā purato ca pacchato ca paṭicchādetvā jantāgharaṃ pavisitabbaṃ. Na ca there bhikkhū anupakhajja nisīditabbaṃ, na navā bhikkhū āsanena paṭibāhitabbā. Jantāghare antevāsikassa parikammaṃ kātabbaṃ. Jantāgharā nikkhamantena jantāgharapīṭhaṃ ādāya purato ca pacchato ca paṭicchādetvā jantāgharā nikkhamitabbaṃ.

If the pupil wishes to enter the bathhouse, bath powder should be prepared, clay should be moistened, and the bathhouse stool should be taken along. Upon arriving, the bathhouse stool should be given, and the robe should be received and set aside on one side. Bath powder should be given, and clay should be given. If he is able, he should enter the bathhouse. When entering the bathhouse, one should smear the face with clay, and covering oneself in front and back, one should enter the bathhouse. One should not sit crowding senior monks, nor should junior monks be pushed aside from their seats. In the bathhouse, the pupil should be attended to. When leaving the bathhouse, one should take the bathhouse stool, covering oneself in front and back, and then exit the bathhouse.

‘‘Udakepi antevāsikassa parikammaṃ kātabbaṃ. Nahātena paṭhamataraṃ uttaritvā attano gattaṃ vodakaṃ katvā nivāsetvā antevāsikassa gattato udakaṃ pamajjitabbaṃ, nivāsanaṃ dātabbaṃ, saṅghāṭi dātabbā, jantāgharapīṭhaṃ ādāya paṭhamataraṃ āgantvā āsanaṃ paññapetabbaṃ, pādodakaṃ pādapīṭhaṃ pādakathalikaṃ upanikkhipitabbaṃ. Antevāsiko pānīyena pucchitabbo.

In the water, too, attendance for the pupil should be done. After bathing, one should emerge first, having made one’s own body free from water, dress, and then wipe the water from the pupil’s body. A lower robe should be given, and an outer robe should be given. Taking the bathhouse stool, one should return first, prepare a seat, and set out foot water, a footstool, and a foot-wiper. The pupil should be asked about drinking water.

‘‘Yasmiṃ vihāre antevāsiko viharati, sace so vihāro uklāpo hoti, sace ussahati, sodhetabbo. Vihāraṃ sodhentena paṭhamaṃ pattacīvaraṃ nīharitvā ekamantaṃ nikkhipitabbaṃ; nisīdanapaccattharaṇaṃ nīharitvā ekamantaṃ nikkhipitabbaṃ; bhisibibbohanaṃ nīharitvā ekamantaṃ nikkhipitabbaṃ; mañco nīcaṃ katvā sādhukaṃ appaṭighaṃsantena, asaṅghaṭṭentena kavāṭapiṭṭhaṃ, nīharitvā ekamantaṃ nikkhipitabbo; pīṭhaṃ nīcaṃ katvā sādhukaṃ appaṭighaṃsantena, asaṅghaṭṭentena kavāṭapiṭṭhaṃ, nīharitvā ekamantaṃ nikkhipitabbaṃ; mañcapaṭipādakā nīharitvā ekamantaṃ nikkhipitabbā; kheḷamallako nīharitvā ekamantaṃ nikkhipitabbo; apassenaphalakaṃ nīharitvā ekamantaṃ nikkhipitabbaṃ; bhūmattharaṇaṃ yathāpaññattaṃ sallakkhetvā nīharitvā ekamantaṃ nikkhipitabbaṃ. Sace vihāre santānakaṃ hoti, ullokā paṭhamaṃ otāretabbaṃ, ālokasandhikaṇṇabhāgā pamajjitabbā. Sace gerukaparikammakatā bhitti kaṇṇakitā hoti, coḷakaṃ temetvā pīḷetvā pamajjitabbā. Sace kāḷavaṇṇakatā bhūmi kaṇṇakitā hoti, coḷakaṃ temetvā pīḷetvā pamajjitabbā. Sace akatā hoti bhūmi, udakena paripphositvā sammajjitabbā – mā vihāro rajena uhaññīti. Saṅkāraṃ vicinitvā ekamantaṃ chaḍḍetabbaṃ.

In the dwelling where a pupil resides, if that dwelling is dirty, and if he is able, he should clean it. When cleaning the dwelling, first take out the bowl and robe and set them aside to one side. Take out the sitting mat and covering and set them aside to one side. Take out the cushion and pillow and set them aside to one side. Lower the bed carefully, without scraping or knocking it against the doorposts, and take it out to set it aside to one side. Lower the stool carefully, without scraping or knocking it against the doorposts, and take it out to set it aside to one side. Take out the bed legs and set them aside to one side. Take out the spittoon and set it aside to one side. Take out the leaning board and set it aside to one side. Examine the floor covering as arranged, take it out, and set it aside to one side. If the dwelling has cobwebs, first remove them from the ceiling, and wipe the corners and window joints. If the walls, treated with red ochre, have become moldy, moisten a cloth, wring it out, and wipe them. If the floor, treated with black color, has become moldy, moisten a cloth, wring it out, and wipe it. If the floor is untreated, sprinkle it with water and sweep it—lest the dwelling be covered by dust. Gather the rubbish and discard it in one place.

‘‘Bhūmattharaṇaṃ otāpetvā sodhetvā papphoṭetvā atiharitvā yathāpaññattaṃ paññapetabbaṃ. Mañcapaṭipādakā otāpetvā pamajjitvā atiharitvā yathāṭhāne ṭhapetabbā. Mañco otāpetvā sodhetvā papphoṭetvā nīcaṃ katvā sādhukaṃ appaṭighaṃsantena, asaṅghaṭṭentena kavāṭapiṭṭhaṃ, atiharitvā yathāpaññattaṃ paññapetabbo. Pīṭhaṃ otāpetvā sodhetvā papphoṭetvā nīcaṃ katvā sādhukaṃ appaṭighaṃsantena, asaṅghaṭṭentena kavāṭapiṭṭhaṃ, atiharitvā yathāpaññattaṃ paññapetabbaṃ. Bhisibibbohanaṃ otāpetvā sodhetvā papphoṭetvā atiharitvā yathāpaññattaṃ paññapetabbaṃ. Nisīdanapaccattharaṇaṃ otāpetvā sodhetvā papphoṭetvā atiharitvā yathāpaññattaṃ paññapetabbaṃ. Kheḷamallako otāpetvā pamajjitvā atiharitvā yathāṭhāne ṭhapetabbo. Apassenaphalakaṃ otāpetvā pamajjitvā atiharitvā yathāṭhāne ṭhapetabbaṃ. Pattacīvaraṃ nikkhipitabbaṃ. Pattaṃ nikkhipantena ekena hatthena pattaṃ gahetvā ekena hatthena heṭṭhāmañcaṃ vā heṭṭhāpīṭhaṃ vā parāmasitvā patto nikkhipitabbo. Na ca anantarahitāya bhūmiyā patto nikkhipitabbo. Cīvaraṃ nikkhipantena ekena hatthena cīvaraṃ gahetvā ekena hatthena cīvaravaṃsaṃ vā cīvararajjuṃ vā pamajjitvā pārato antaṃ orato bhogaṃ katvā cīvaraṃ nikkhipitabbaṃ.

The floor covering should be aired, cleaned, beaten, and returned to its place and arranged as it was. The bed legs should be aired, wiped, and returned to their proper positions. The bed should be aired, cleaned, beaten, lowered carefully, without scraping or knocking it against the doorposts, and returned to its place and arranged as it was. The stool should be aired, cleaned, beaten, lowered carefully, without scraping or knocking it against the doorposts, and returned to its place and arranged as it was. The cushion and pillow should be aired, cleaned, beaten, and returned to their place and arranged as they were. The sitting mat and covering should be aired, cleaned, beaten, and returned to their place and arranged as they were. The spittoon should be aired, wiped, and returned to its proper position. The leaning board should be aired, wiped, and returned to its proper position. The bowl and robe should be put away. When putting away the bowl, one should hold the bowl with one hand and touch the lower bed or stool with the other hand before placing it down. The bowl should not be placed directly on the bare ground. When putting away the robe, one should hold the robe with one hand and smooth the robe rack or robe cord with the other. Then, folding the robe lengthwise, edge to edge, it should be put away.

‘‘Sace puratthimā sarajā vātā vāyanti, puratthimā vātapānā thaketabbā. Sace pacchimā sarajā vātā vāyanti, pacchimā vātapānā thaketabbā. Sace uttarā sarajā vātā vāyanti, uttarā vātapānā thaketabbā. Sace dakkhiṇā sarajā vātā vāyanti, dakkhiṇā vātapānā thaketabbā. Sace sītakālo hoti, divā vātapānā vivaritabbā, rattiṃ thaketabbā. Sace uṇhakālo hoti, divā vātapānā thaketabbā, rattiṃ vivaritabbā.

If dusty winds blow from the east, the eastern windows should be closed. If dusty winds blow from the west, the western windows should be closed. If dusty winds blow from the north, the northern windows should be closed. If dusty winds blow from the south, the southern windows should be closed. If it is the cold season, the windows should be opened during the day and closed at night. If it is the hot season, the windows should be closed during the day and opened at night.

‘‘Sace pariveṇaṃ uklāpaṃ hoti, pariveṇaṃ sammajjitabbaṃ. Sace koṭṭhako uklāpo hoti, koṭṭhako sammajjitabbo. Sace upaṭṭhānasālā uklāpā hoti, upaṭṭhānasālā sammajjitabbā. Sace aggisālā uklāpā hoti, aggisālā sammajjitabbā. Sace vaccakuṭi uklāpā hoti, vaccakuṭi sammajjitabbā. Sace pānīyaṃ na hoti, pānīyaṃ upaṭṭhāpetabbaṃ. Sace paribhojanīyaṃ na hoti, paribhojanīyaṃ upaṭṭhāpetabbaṃ. Sace ācamanakumbhiyā udakaṃ na hoti, ācamanakumbhiyā udakaṃ āsiñcitabbaṃ.

“If the monastery enclosure is dirty, the monastery enclosure should be swept. If the storeroom is dirty, the storeroom should be swept. If the service hall is dirty, the service hall should be swept. If the fire hall is dirty, the fire hall should be swept. If the toilet is dirty, the toilet should be swept. If there is no drinking water, drinking water should be provided. If there is no water for use, water for use should be provided. If there is no water in the washing bowl, water should be poured into the washing bowl.”

‘‘Sace antevāsikassa anabhirati uppannā hoti, ācariyena vūpakāsetabbo, vūpakāsāpetabbo, dhammakathā vāssa kātabbā. Sace antevāsikassa kukkuccaṃ uppannaṃ hoti, ācariyena vinodetabbaṃ, vinodāpetabbaṃ, dhammakathā vāssa kātabbā. Sace antevāsikassa diṭṭhigataṃ uppannaṃ hoti, ācariyena vivecetabbaṃ, vivecāpetabbaṃ, dhammakathā vāssa kātabbā. Sace antevāsiko garudhammaṃ ajjhāpanno hoti parivāsāraho, ācariyena ussukkaṃ kātabbaṃ – kinti nu kho saṅgho, antevāsikassa parivāsaṃ dadeyyāti. Sace antevāsiko mūlāya paṭikassanāraho hoti, ācariyena ussukkaṃ kātabbaṃ – kinti nu kho saṅgho antevāsikaṃ mūlāya paṭikasseyyāti. Sace antevāsiko mānattāraho hoti, ācariyena ussukkaṃ kātabbaṃ – kinti nu kho saṅgho antevāsikassa mānattaṃ dadeyyāti. Sace antevāsiko abbhānāraho hoti, ācariyena ussukkaṃ kātabbaṃ – kinti nu kho saṅgho antevāsikaṃ abbheyyāti. Sace saṅgho antevāsikassa kammaṃ kattukāmo hoti, tajjanīyaṃ vā niyassaṃ vā pabbājanīyaṃ vā paṭisāraṇīyaṃ vā ukkhepanīyaṃ vā, ācariyena ussukkaṃ kātabbaṃ – kinti nu kho saṅgho antevāsikassa kammaṃ na kareyya, lahukāya vā pariṇāmeyyāti. Kataṃ vā panassa hoti saṅghena kammaṃ, tajjanīyaṃ vā niyassaṃ vā pabbājanīyaṃ vā paṭisāraṇīyaṃ vā ukkhepanīyaṃ vā, ācariyena ussukkaṃ kātabbaṃ – kinti nu kho antevāsiko sammā vatteyya, lomaṃ pāteyya, netthāraṃ vatteyya, saṅgho taṃ kammaṃ paṭippassambheyyāti.

“If dissatisfaction arises in a pupil, the teacher should dispel it, have it dispelled, or give them a Dhamma talk. If remorse arises in a pupil, the teacher should dispel it, have it dispelled, or give them a Dhamma talk. If wrong view arises in a pupil, the teacher should eliminate it, have it eliminated, or give them a Dhamma talk. If a pupil has committed a grave offense warranting probation, the teacher should make an effort: ‘How might the Saṅgha grant the pupil probation?’ If a pupil deserves to be sent back to the beginning, the teacher should make an effort: ‘How might the Saṅgha send the pupil back to the beginning?’ If a pupil deserves penance, the teacher should make an effort: ‘How might the Saṅgha grant the pupil penance?’ If a pupil deserves reinstatement, the teacher should make an effort: ‘How might the Saṅgha reinstate the pupil?’ If the Saṅgha intends to carry out an action against a pupil—whether censure, degradation, banishment, requiring reconciliation, or suspension—the teacher should make an effort: ‘How might the Saṅgha not carry out the action against the pupil, or mitigate it?’ But if the Saṅgha has already carried out an action against them—whether censure, degradation, banishment, requiring reconciliation, or suspension—the teacher should make an effort: ‘How might the pupil behave rightly, lower their pride, find a way out, so that the Saṅgha might rescind that action?’

‘‘Sace antevāsikassa cīvaraṃ dhovitabbaṃ hoti, ācariyena ācikkhitabbaṃ – ‘evaṃ dhoveyyāsī’ti, ussukkaṃ vā kātabbaṃ – kinti nu kho antevāsikassa cīvaraṃ dhoviyethāti. Sace antevāsikassa cīvaraṃ kātabbaṃ hoti, ācariyena ācikkhitabbaṃ – ‘evaṃ kareyyāsī’ti, ussukkaṃ vā kātabbaṃ – kinti nu kho antevāsikassa cīvaraṃ kariyethāti. Sace antevāsikassa rajanaṃ pacitabbaṃ hoti, ācariyena ācikkhitabbaṃ – ‘evaṃ paceyyāsī’ti, ussukkaṃ vā kātabbaṃ – kinti nu kho antevāsikassa rajanaṃ paciyethāti. Sace antevāsikassa cīvaraṃ rajitabbaṃ hoti, ācariyena ācikkhitabbaṃ – ‘evaṃ rajeyyāsī’ti, ussukkaṃ vā kātabbaṃ – kinti nu kho antevāsikassa cīvaraṃ rajiyethāti. Cīvaraṃ rajantena sādhukaṃ samparivattakaṃ samparivattakaṃ rajitabbaṃ, na ca acchinne theve pakkamitabbaṃ. Sace antevāsiko gilāno hoti, yāvajīvaṃ upaṭṭhātabbo, vuṭṭhānamassa āgametabba’’nti.

“If the pupil’s robe needs washing, the teacher should instruct: ‘Wash it like this,’ or make an effort: ‘How might the pupil’s robe be washed?’ If the pupil’s robe needs making, the teacher should instruct: ‘Make it like this,’ or make an effort: ‘How might the pupil’s robe be made?’ If dye needs to be cooked for the pupil, the teacher should instruct: ‘Cook it like this,’ or make an effort: ‘How might dye be cooked for the pupil?’ If the pupil’s robe needs dyeing, the teacher should instruct: ‘Dye it like this,’ or make an effort: ‘How might the pupil’s robe be dyed?’ When dyeing a robe, it should be dyed carefully, turning it over and over, and one should not leave the dye-vat with the dye still dripping. If the pupil is sick, he should be cared for as long as he lives, and his recovery should be awaited.”

Antevāsikavattaṃ niṭṭhitaṃ.

The chapter on the duties of a resident pupil is concluded.

Chaṭṭhabhāṇavāro.

The sixth chapter of recitations.

### 20. Paṇāmanā khamāpanā ^20

> [[bmc2#^ch14|BMC Chapter 14]] and the following cites:

> "VIN-MV1.20" file:bmc2 -queryblock
