20.Dismissal and Forgiveness

80. Tena kho pana samayena antevāsikā ācariyesu na sammā vattanti…pe… bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ…pe… na, bhikkhave, antevāsikena ācariyamhi na sammā vattitabbaṃ. Yo na sammā vatteyya, āpatti dukkaṭassāti. Neva sammā vattanti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ…pe… anujānāmi, bhikkhave, asammāvattantaṃ paṇāmetuṃ. Evañca pana, bhikkhave, paṇāmetabbo – paṇāmemi tanti vā, māyidha paṭikkamīti vā, nīhara te pattacīvaranti vā, nāhaṃ tayā upaṭṭhātabboti vā. Kāyena viññāpeti, vācāya viññāpeti, kāyena vācāya viññāpeti, paṇāmito hoti antevāsiko; na kāyena viññāpeti, na vācāya viññāpeti, na kāyena vācāya viññāpeti, na paṇāmito hoti antevāsikoti.

80.Now at that time the pupils did not behave properly towards their teachers… they reported this matter to the Blessed One… “Monks, a pupil should not behave improperly towards his teacher. Whoever behaves improperly commits an offense of wrong-doing.” They still did not behave properly. They reported this matter to the Blessed One… “I allow, monks, to dismiss one who behaves improperly. And monks, he should be dismissed in this way: ‘I dismiss you,’ or ‘Do not come back here,’ or ‘Take away your bowl and robe,’ or ‘You are not to attend to me.’ He makes it known by body, he makes it known by speech, he makes it known by body and speech—the pupil is dismissed. He does not make it known by body, he does not make it known by speech, he does not make it known by body and not by speech—the pupil is not dismissed.”

Tena kho pana samayena antevāsikā paṇāmitā na khamāpenti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, khamāpetunti. Neva khamāpenti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Na, bhikkhave, paṇāmitena na khamāpetabbo. Yo na khamāpeyya, āpatti dukkaṭassāti.

At that time, dismissed pupils did not ask for forgiveness. They reported the matter to the Blessed One. “I allow, monks, that forgiveness should be asked.” Still, they did not ask for forgiveness. They reported the matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, one who has been dismissed must not fail to ask for forgiveness. Whoever does not ask for forgiveness incurs an offense of wrong conduct.”

Tena kho pana samayena ācariyā khamāpiyamānā na khamanti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, khamitunti. Neva khamanti. Antevāsikā pakkamantipi vibbhamantipi titthiyesupi saṅkamanti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Na, bhikkhave, khamāpiyamānena na khamitabbaṃ. Yo na khameyya, āpatti dukkaṭassāti.

At that time, teachers did not accept apologies. They reported the matter to the Blessed One. “I allow, monks, acceptance of apologies.” Still, they did not accept. Pupils departed, wandered off, or even went over to other sects. They reported the matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, one who is asked for forgiveness should not refuse. Whoever does not forgive incurs an offense of wrong conduct.”

Tena kho pana samayena ācariyā sammāvattantaṃ paṇāmenti, asammāvattantaṃ na paṇāmenti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Na, bhikkhave, sammāvattanto paṇāmetabbo. Yo paṇāmeyya, āpatti dukkaṭassa. Na ca, bhikkhave, asammāvattanto na paṇāmetabbo. Yo na paṇāmeyya, āpatti dukkaṭassa.

At that time, teachers dismissed those who behaved correctly and did not dismiss those who behaved incorrectly. They reported the matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, one who behaves correctly should not be dismissed. Whoever dismisses them incurs an offense of wrong conduct. And one who behaves incorrectly should not be left undismissed. Whoever does not dismiss them incurs an offense of wrong conduct.”

81. ‘‘Pañcahi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgato antevāsiko paṇāmetabbo. Ācariyamhi nādhimattaṃ pemaṃ hoti, nādhimatto pasādo hoti, nādhimattā hirī hoti, nādhimatto gāravo hoti, nādhimattā bhāvanā hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgato antevāsiko paṇāmetabbo.

81.“Monks, a pupil endowed with five qualities should be dismissed. He has no excessive affection for the teacher, no excessive confidence in the teacher, no excessive shame toward the teacher, no excessive reverence for the teacher, and no excessive development [of virtue] toward the teacher. Monks, a pupil endowed with these five qualities should be dismissed.”

‘‘Pañcahi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgato antevāsiko na paṇāmetabbo. Ācariyamhi adhimattaṃ pemaṃ hoti, adhimatto pasādo hoti, adhimattā hirī hoti, adhimatto gāravo hoti, adhimattā bhāvanā hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgato antevāsiko na paṇāmetabbo.

“Monks, a pupil endowed with five qualities should not be dismissed. He has excessive affection for the teacher, excessive confidence in the teacher, excessive shame toward the teacher, excessive reverence for the teacher, and excessive cultivation (of the teachings). Monks, a pupil endowed with these five qualities should not be dismissed.”

‘‘Pañcahi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgato antevāsiko alaṃ paṇāmetuṃ. Ācariyamhi nādhimattaṃ pemaṃ hoti, nādhimatto pasādo hoti, nādhimattā hirī hoti, nādhimatto gāravo hoti, nādhimattā bhāvanā hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgato antevāsiko alaṃ paṇāmetuṃ.

“Monks, a pupil endowed with five qualities is fit for dismissal. He has no excessive affection for the teacher, no excessive confidence in the teacher, no excessive shame toward the teacher, no excessive reverence for the teacher, and no excessive devotion to the teacher. Monks, a pupil endowed with these five qualities is fit for dismissal.”

‘‘Pañcahi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgato antevāsiko nālaṃ paṇāmetuṃ. Ācariyamhi adhimattaṃ pemaṃ hoti, adhimatto pasādo hoti, adhimattā hirī hoti, adhimatto gāravo hoti, adhimattā bhāvanā hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgato antevāsiko nālaṃ paṇāmetuṃ.

“Monks, a pupil endowed with five qualities is not fit for dismissal. He has excessive affection for the teacher, excessive confidence in the teacher, excessive shame toward the teacher, excessive reverence toward the teacher, and excessive devotion toward the teacher. Monks, a pupil endowed with these five qualities is not fit for dismissal.”

‘‘Pañcahi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgataṃ antevāsikaṃ appaṇāmento ācariyo sātisāro hoti, paṇāmento anatisāro hoti. Ācariyamhi nādhimattaṃ pemaṃ hoti, nādhimatto pasādo hoti, nādhimattā hirī hoti, nādhimatto gāravo hoti, nādhimattā bhāvanā hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgataṃ antevāsikaṃ appaṇāmento ācariyo sātisāro hoti, paṇāmento anatisāro hoti.

“Monks, a teacher who does not dismiss a pupil endowed with five qualities is blameworthy, but one who dismisses such a pupil is not blameworthy. The pupil has no excessive affection for the teacher, no excessive confidence in the teacher, no excessive shame toward the teacher, no excessive reverence for the teacher, and no excessive cultivation (of virtue) towards the teacher. Monks, a teacher who does not dismiss a pupil endowed with these five qualities is blameworthy, but one who dismisses such a pupil is not blameworthy.”

‘‘Pañcahi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgataṃ antevāsikaṃ paṇāmento ācariyo sātisāro hoti, appaṇāmento anatisāro hoti. Ācariyamhi adhimattaṃ pemaṃ hoti, adhimatto pasādo hoti, adhimattā hirī hoti, adhimatto gāravo hoti, adhimattā bhāvanā hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgataṃ antevāsikaṃ paṇāmento ācariyo sātisāro hoti, appaṇāmento anatisāro hotī’’ti.

“Monks, a teacher who dismisses a pupil endowed with five qualities incurs blame, but one who does not dismiss such a pupil does not incur blame. The pupil has excessive affection for the teacher, excessive confidence in the teacher, excessive shame toward the teacher, excessive reverence for the teacher, and excessive cultivation (of virtue) toward the teacher. Monks, a teacher who dismisses a pupil endowed with these five qualities incurs blame, but one who does not dismiss such a pupil does not incur blame.”

Paṇāmanā khamāpanā niṭṭhitā.

Dismissal and Forgiveness are concluded.

### 21. Bālaabyattavatthu ^21

> [!TIP]- Links to [[mv1-brahmali-pali#^21|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch14|BMC Chapter 14]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-MV1.21" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


21.The Topic of the Foolish and the Incompetent

82. Tena kho pana samayena bhikkhū, dasavassamhā dasavassamhāti, bālā abyattā nissayaṃ denti. Dissanti ācariyā bālā, antevāsikā paṇḍitā. Dissanti ācariyā abyattā, antevāsikā byattā. Dissanti ācariyā appassutā, antevāsikā bahussutā. Dissanti ācariyā duppaññā, antevāsikā paññavanto. Ye te bhikkhū appicchā…pe… te ujjhāyanti khiyyanti vipācenti – ‘‘kathañhi nāma bhikkhū, dasavassamhā dasavassamhāti, bālā abyattā nissayaṃ dassanti. Dissanti ācariyā bālā antevāsikā paṇḍitā, dissanti ācariyā abyattā antevāsikā byattā, dissanti ācariyā appassutā antevāsikā bahussutā, dissanti ācariyā duppaññā antevāsikā paññavanto’’ti. Atha kho te bhikkhū bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ…pe… saccaṃ kira, bhikkhave, bhikkhū, dasavassamhā dasavassamhāti, bālā abyattā nissayaṃ denti…pe… saccaṃ, bhagavāti. Vigarahi buddho bhagavā…pe… vigarahitvā…pe… dhammiṃ kathaṃ katvā bhikkhū āmantesi – ‘‘na, bhikkhave, bālena abyattena nissayo dātabbo. Yo dadeyya, āpatti dukkaṭassa. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, byattena bhikkhunā paṭibalena dasavassena vā atirekadasavassena vā nissayaṃ dātu’’nti.

82.Now at that time monks, saying, "We have been ordained for ten years, we have been ordained for ten years," gave dependence to foolish and incompetent ones. Foolish teachers were seen with wise pupils. Incompetent teachers were seen with competent pupils. Teachers of little learning were seen with pupils of great learning. Unwise teachers were seen with wise pupils. Those monks who were modest… complained and criticized them: "How can monks, saying, 'We have been ordained for ten years, we have been ordained for ten years,' give dependence to foolish and incompetent ones? Foolish teachers are seen with wise pupils; incompetent teachers are seen with competent pupils; teachers of little learning are seen with pupils of great learning; unwise teachers are seen with wise pupils." Then those monks reported this matter to the Blessed One… "Is it true, monks, that monks, saying, 'We have been ordained for ten years, we have been ordained for ten years,' give dependence to foolish and incompetent ones?" … "It is true, Blessed One." The Blessed One rebuked them… Having rebuked them… after delivering a Dhamma talk, he addressed the monks: "Monks, dependence should not be given by a foolish and incompetent one. Whoever gives it, there is an offense of wrong-doing. I allow, monks, that a competent and capable monk of ten years or more than ten years may give dependence."

Bālaabyattavatthu niṭṭhitaṃ.

The Topic of the Foolish and the Incompetent is concluded.

### 22. Nissayapaṭippassaddhikathā ^22

> [!TIP]- Links to [[mv1-brahmali-pali#^22|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch14|BMC Chapter 14]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-MV1.22" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


22.The Discussion on the Cessation of Dependence

83. Tena kho pana samayena bhikkhū ācariyupajjhāyesu pakkantesupi vibbhantesupi kālaṅkatesupi pakkhasaṅkantesupi nissayapaṭippassaddhiyo na jānanti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ.

83.At that time, monks did not know how to withdraw dependence even after their teachers or preceptors had departed, become deranged, passed away, or gone over to another group. They reported this matter to the Blessed One.

‘‘Pañcimā, bhikkhave, nissayapaṭippassaddhiyo upajjhāyamhā – upajjhāyo pakkanto vā hoti, vibbhanto vā, kālaṅkato vā, pakkhasaṅkanto vā, āṇattiyeva pañcamī. Imā kho, bhikkhave, pañca nissayapaṭippassaddhiyo upajjhāyamhā.

“Monks, there are these five cessations of dependence on a preceptor: the preceptor has departed, become deranged, passed away, gone over to another community, or a formal declaration is made—this is the fifth. These, monks, are the five cessations of dependence on a preceptor.”

‘‘Chayimā, bhikkhave, nissayapaṭippassaddhiyo ācariyamhā – ācariyo pakkanto vā hoti, vibbhanto vā, kālaṅkato vā, pakkhasaṅkanto vā, āṇattiyeva pañcamī, upajjhāyena vā samodhānagato hoti. Imā kho, bhikkhave, cha nissayapaṭippassaddhiyo ācariyamhā’’.

“Monks, there are these six cessations of dependence on a teacher: the teacher has departed, become deranged, passed away, gone over to another group, or a formal declaration is made—this is the fifth—or he has come into contact with the preceptor. These, monks, are the six cessations of dependence on a teacher.”

Nissapaṭippassaddhikathā niṭṭhitā.

The Discussion on the Cessation of Dependence is concluded.

### 23. Upasampādetabbapañcakaṃ ^23

> [!TIP]- Links to [[mv1-brahmali-pali#^23|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch14|BMC Chapter 14]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-MV1.23" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


23.The Quintet on Conferring Higher Ordination

84. ‘‘Pañcahi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā na upasampādetabbaṃ, na nissayo dātabbo, na sāmaṇero upaṭṭhāpetabbo. Na asekkhena [na asekhena (ka.)] sīlakkhandhena samannāgato hoti, na asekkhena samādhikkhandhena samannāgato hoti, na asekkhena paññākkhandhena samannāgato hoti, na asekkhena vimuttikkhandhena samannāgato hoti, na asekkhena vimuttiñāṇadassanakkhandhena samannāgato hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā na upasampādetabbaṃ, na nissayo dātabbo, na sāmaṇero upaṭṭhāpetabbo.

84.“Monks, a monk endowed with five factors should not confer higher ordination, should not give dependence, and should not have a novice attend on him. He is not endowed with the consummate aggregate of moral discipline, not endowed with the consummate aggregate of concentration, not endowed with the consummate aggregate of wisdom, not endowed with the consummate aggregate of liberation, not endowed with the consummate aggregate of the knowledge and vision of liberation. Monks, a monk endowed with these five factors should not confer higher ordination, should not give dependence, and should not have a novice attend on him.”

‘‘Pañcahi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā upasampādetabbaṃ, nissayo dātabbo, sāmaṇero upaṭṭhāpetabbo. Asekkhena sīlakkhandhena samannāgato hoti, asekkhena samādhikkhandhena samannāgato hoti, asekkhena paññākkhandhena samannāgato hoti, asekkhena vimuttikkhandhena samannāgato hoti, asekkhena vimuttiñāṇadassanakkhandhena samannāgato hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā upasampādetabbaṃ, nissayo dātabbo, sāmaṇero upaṭṭhāpetabbo.

“Monks, a monk endowed with five factors should confer higher ordination, should give dependence, and should have a novice attend on him. He is endowed with the consummate aggregate of moral discipline, the consummate aggregate of concentration, the consummate aggregate of wisdom, the consummate aggregate of liberation, and the consummate aggregate of the knowledge and vision of liberation. Monks, a monk endowed with these five factors should confer higher ordination, should give dependence, and should have a novice attend on him.”

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā na upasampādetabbaṃ, na nissayo dātabbo, na sāmaṇero upaṭṭhāpetabbo. Attanā na asekkhena sīlakkhandhena samannāgato hoti, na paraṃ asekkhe sīlakkhandhe samādapetā; attanā na asekkhena samādhikkhandhena samannāgato hoti, na paraṃ asekkhe samādhikkhandhe samādapetā; attanā na asekkhena paññākkhandhena samannāgato hoti, na paraṃ asekkhe paññākkhandhe samādapetā; attanā na asekkhena vimuttikkhandhena samannāgato hoti, na paraṃ asekkhe vimuttikkhandhe samādapetā; attanā na asekkhena vimuttiñāṇadassanakkhandhena samannāgato hoti, na paraṃ asekkhe vimuttiñāṇadassanakkhandhe samādapetā – imehi kho, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā na upasampādetabbaṃ, na nissayo dātabbo, na sāmaṇero upaṭṭhāpetabbo.

“Monks, a monk endowed with another five factors should not confer higher ordination, should not give dependence, and should not have a novice attend on him. He himself is not endowed with the consummate aggregate of moral discipline, nor does he establish others in the consummate aggregate of moral discipline; he himself is not endowed with the consummate aggregate of concentration, nor does he establish others in the consummate aggregate of concentration; he himself is not endowed with the consummate aggregate of wisdom, nor does he establish others in the consummate aggregate of wisdom; he himself is not endowed with the consummate aggregate of liberation, nor does he establish others in the consummate aggregate of liberation; he himself is not endowed with the consummate aggregate of the knowledge and vision of liberation, nor does he establish others in the consummate aggregate of the knowledge and vision of liberation. Monks, a monk endowed with these five factors should not confer higher ordination, should not give dependence, and should not have a novice attend on him.”

‘‘Pañcahi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā upasampādetabbaṃ, nissayo dātabbo, sāmaṇero upaṭṭhāpetabbo. Attanā asekkhena sīlakkhandhena samannāgato hoti, paraṃ asekkhe sīlakkhandhe samādapetā; attanā asekkhena samādhikkhandhena samannāgato hoti, paraṃ asekkhe samādhikkhandhe samādapetā; attanā asekkhena paññākkhandhena samannāgato hoti, paraṃ asekkhe paññākkhandhe samādapetā; attanā asekkhena vimuttikkhandhena samannāgato hoti, paraṃ asekkhe vimuttikkhandhe samādapetā; attanā asekkhena vimuttiñāṇadassanakkhandhena samannāgato hoti, paraṃ asekkhe vimuttiñāṇadassanakkhandhe samādapetā – imehi kho, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā upasampādetabbaṃ, nissayo dātabbo, sāmaṇero upaṭṭhāpetabbo.

“Monks, a monk endowed with five factors should confer higher ordination, should give dependence, and should have a novice attend on him. He himself is endowed with the consummate aggregate of moral discipline and establishes others in the consummate aggregate of moral discipline; he himself is endowed with the consummate aggregate of concentration and establishes others in the consummate aggregate of concentration; he himself is endowed with the consummate aggregate of wisdom and establishes others in the consummate aggregate of wisdom; he himself is endowed with the consummate aggregate of liberation and establishes others in the consummate aggregate of liberation; he himself is endowed with the consummate aggregate of the knowledge and vision of liberation and establishes others in the consummate aggregate of the knowledge and vision of liberation. Monks, a monk endowed with these five factors should confer higher ordination, should give dependence, and should have a novice attend on him.”

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā na upasampādetabbaṃ, na nissayo dātabbo, na sāmaṇero upaṭṭhāpetabbo. Assaddho hoti, ahiriko hoti, anottappī hoti, kusīto hoti, muṭṭhassati hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā na upasampādetabbaṃ, na nissayo dātabbo, na sāmaṇero upaṭṭhāpetabbo.

“Monks, a monk endowed with another five factors should not confer higher ordination, should not give dependence, and should not have a novice attend on him. He is faithless, shameless, without moral dread, indolent, and lacking mindfulness. Monks, a monk endowed with these five factors should not confer higher ordination, should not give dependence, and should not have a novice attend on him.”

‘‘Pañcahi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā upasampādetabbaṃ, nissayo dātabbo, sāmaṇero upaṭṭhāpetabbo. Saddho hoti, hirimā hoti, ottappī hoti, āraddhavīriyo hoti, upaṭṭhitassati hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā upasampādetabbaṃ, nissayo dātabbo, sāmaṇero upaṭṭhāpetabbo.

“Monks, a monk endowed with five factors should confer higher ordination, should give dependence, and should have a novice attend on him. He is faithful, has a sense of shame, has moral dread, is energetic, and is mindful. Monks, a monk endowed with these five factors should confer higher ordination, should give dependence, and should have a novice attend on him.”

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā na upasampādetabbaṃ, na nissayo dātabbo, na sāmaṇero upaṭṭhāpetabbo. Adhisīle sīlavipanno hoti, ajjhācāre ācāravipanno hoti, atidiṭṭhiyā diṭṭhivipanno hoti, appassuto hoti, duppañño hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā na upasampādetabbaṃ, na nissayo dātabbo, na sāmaṇero upaṭṭhāpetabbo.

“Monks, a monk endowed with another five factors should not confer higher ordination, should not give dependence, and should not have a novice attend on him. He is morally corrupt in higher virtue, corrupt in conduct, corrupt in view, has little learning, and is unwise. Monks, a monk endowed with these five factors should not confer higher ordination, should not give dependence, and should not have a novice attend on him.”

‘‘Pañcahi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā upasampādetabbaṃ, nissayo dātabbo, sāmaṇero upaṭṭhāpetabbo. Na adhisīle sīlavipanno hoti, na ajjhācāre ācāravipanno hoti, na atidiṭṭhiyā diṭṭhivipanno hoti, bahussuto hoti, paññavā hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā upasampādetabbaṃ, nissayo dātabbo, sāmaṇero upaṭṭhāpetabbo.

“Monks, a monk endowed with five factors should confer higher ordination, should give dependence, and should have a novice attend on him. He is not morally corrupt in higher virtue, not corrupt in conduct, not corrupt in view, is very learned, and is wise. Monks, a monk endowed with these five factors should confer higher ordination, should give dependence, and should have a novice attend on him.”

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā na upasampādetabbaṃ, na nissayo dātabbo, na sāmaṇero upaṭṭhāpetabbo. Na paṭibalo hoti antevāsiṃ vā saddhivihāriṃ vā gilānaṃ upaṭṭhātuṃ vā upaṭṭhāpetuṃ vā, anabhirataṃ [anabhiratiṃ (syā.), uppannaṃ anabhiratiṃ (ka.)] vūpakāsetuṃ vā vūpakāsāpetuṃ vā, uppannaṃ kukkuccaṃ dhammato vinodetuṃ [vinodetuṃ vā vinodāpetuṃ vā (sabbattha, vimativinodanī ṭīkā oloketabbā)] āpattiṃ na jānāti, āpattiyā vuṭṭhānaṃ na jānāti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā na upasampādetabbaṃ, na nissayo dātabbo, na sāmaṇero upaṭṭhāpetabbo.

"Monks, a monk endowed with another five factors should not give ordination, should not give dependence, and should not take a novice into his charge. He is not capable of attending to or arranging for attendance for a sick pupil or co-resident; he is not capable of settling a discontented one or having him settled; he is not capable of dispelling remorse that has arisen in accordance with the Dhamma; he does not know an offense; and he does not know the emergence from an offense. Monks, a monk endowed with these five factors should not give ordination, should not give dependence, and should not take a novice into his charge."

‘‘Pañcahi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā upasampādetabbaṃ, nissayo dātabbo, sāmaṇero upaṭṭhāpetabbo. Paṭibalo hoti antevāsiṃ vā saddhivihāriṃ vā gilānaṃ upaṭṭhātuṃ vā upaṭṭhāpetuṃ vā, anabhirataṃ vūpakāsetuṃ vā vūpakāsāpetuṃ vā, uppannaṃ kukkuccaṃ dhammato vinodetuṃ āpattiṃ jānāti, āpattiyā vuṭṭhānaṃ jānāti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā upasampādetabbaṃ, nissayo dātabbo, sāmaṇero upaṭṭhāpetabbo.

"Monks, a monk endowed with five factors is fit to give ordination, to give dependence, and to take a novice into his charge. He is capable of attending to or arranging for attendance for a sick pupil or co-resident; he is capable of settling a discontented one or having him settled; he is capable of dispelling remorse that has arisen in accordance with the Dhamma; he knows an offense; and he knows the emergence from an offense. Monks, a monk endowed with these five factors is fit to give ordination, to give dependence, and to take a novice into his charge."

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā na upasampādetabbaṃ, na nissayo dātabbo, na sāmaṇero upaṭṭhāpetabbo. Na paṭibalo hoti antevāsiṃ vā saddhivihāriṃ vā abhisamācārikāya sikkhāya sikkhāpetuṃ, ādibrahmacariyakāya sikkhāya vinetuṃ, abhidhamme vinetuṃ, abhivinaye vinetuṃ, uppannaṃ diṭṭhigataṃ dhammato vivecetuṃ – imehi kho, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā na upasampādetabbaṃ, na nissayo dātabbo, na sāmaṇero upaṭṭhāpetabbo.

"Monks, a monk endowed with another five factors should not give ordination, should not give dependence, and should not take a novice into his charge. He is not capable of training a pupil or co-resident in the training in higher conduct; of guiding them in the fundamental holy life; of guiding them in the Abhidhamma; of guiding them in the Vinaya; or of dispelling an arisen wrong view in accordance with the Dhamma. Monks, a monk endowed with these five factors should not give ordination, should not give dependence, and should not take a novice into his charge."

‘‘Pañcahi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā upasampādetabbaṃ, nissayo dātabbo, sāmaṇero upaṭṭhāpetabbo. Paṭibalo hoti antevāsiṃ vā saddhivihāriṃ vā abhisamācārikāya sikkhāya sikkhāpetuṃ, ādibrahmacariyakāya sikkhāya vinetuṃ, abhidhamme vinetuṃ, abhivinaye vinetuṃ, uppannaṃ diṭṭhigataṃ dhammato vivecetuṃ – imehi kho, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā upasampādetabbaṃ, nissayo dātabbo, sāmaṇero upaṭṭhāpetabbo.

"Monks, a monk endowed with five factors is fit to give ordination, to give dependence, and to take a novice into his charge. He is capable of training a pupil or co-resident in the training in higher conduct; of guiding them in the fundamental holy life; of guiding them in the Abhidhamma; of guiding them in the Vinaya; and of dispelling an arisen wrong view in accordance with the Dhamma. Monks, a monk endowed with these five factors is fit to give ordination, to give dependence, and to take a novice into his charge."

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā na upasampādetabbaṃ, na nissayo dātabbo, na sāmaṇero upaṭṭhāpetabbo. Āpattiṃ na jānāti, anāpattiṃ na jānāti, lahukaṃ āpattiṃ na jānāti, garukaṃ āpattiṃ na jānāti, ubhayāni kho panassa pātimokkhāni vitthārena na svāgatāni honti na suvibhattāni na suppavattīni na suvinicchitāni suttaso anubyañjanaso – imehi kho, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā na upasampādetabbaṃ, na nissayo dātabbo, na sāmaṇero upaṭṭhāpetabbo.

"Monks, a monk endowed with another five factors should not give ordination, should not give dependence, and should not take a novice into his charge. He does not know an offense; does not know a non-offense; does not know a light offense; does not know a heavy offense; and both Pātimokkhas are not well learned by him in detail, not well analyzed, not well recited, not well determined according to the letter and the spirit. Monks, a monk endowed with these five factors should not give ordination, should not give dependence, and should not take a novice into his charge."

‘‘Pañcahi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā upasampādetabbaṃ, nissayo dātabbo, sāmaṇero upaṭṭhāpetabbo. Āpattiṃ jānāti, anāpattiṃ jānāti, lahukaṃ āpattiṃ jānāti, garukaṃ āpattiṃ jānāti, ubhayāni kho panassa pātimokkhāni vitthārena svāgatāni honti suvibhattāni suppavattīni suvinicchitāni suttaso anubyañjanaso – imehi kho, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā upasampādetabbaṃ, nissayo dātabbo, sāmaṇero upaṭṭhāpetabbo.

"Monks, a monk endowed with five factors is fit to give ordination, to give dependence, and to take a novice into his charge. He knows an offense; knows a non-offense; knows a light offense; knows a heavy offense; and both Pātimokkhas are well learned by him in detail, well analyzed, well recited, well determined according to the letter and the spirit. Monks, a monk endowed with these five factors is fit to give ordination, to give dependence, and to take a novice into his charge."

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā na upasampādetabbaṃ, na nissayo dātabbo, na sāmaṇero upaṭṭhāpetabbo. Āpattiṃ na jānāti, anāpattiṃ na jānāti, lahukaṃ āpattiṃ na jānāti, garukaṃ āpattiṃ na jānāti, ūnadasavasso hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā na upasampādetabbaṃ, na nissayo dātabbo, na sāmaṇero upaṭṭhāpetabbo.

"Monks, a monk endowed with another five factors should not give ordination, should not give dependence, and should not take a novice into his charge. He does not know an offense; does not know a non-offense; does not know a light offense; does not know a heavy offense; and he is less than ten years in seniority. Monks, a monk endowed with these five factors should not give ordination, should not give dependence, and should not take a novice into his charge."

‘‘Pañcahi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā upasampādetabbaṃ, nissayo dātabbo, sāmaṇero upaṭṭhāpetabbo. Āpattiṃ jānāti, anāpattiṃ jānāti, lahukaṃ āpattiṃ jānāti, garukaṃ āpattiṃ jānāti, dasavasso vā hoti atirekadasavasso vā – imehi kho, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā upasampādetabbaṃ, nissayo dātabbo, sāmaṇero upaṭṭhāpetabbo’’ti.

"Monks, a monk endowed with five factors is fit to give ordination, to give dependence, and to take a novice into his charge. He knows an offense; knows a non-offense; knows a light offense; knows a heavy offense; and he is ten years or more in seniority. Monks, a monk endowed with these five factors is fit to give ordination, to give dependence, and to take a novice into his charge."

Upasampādetabbapañcakaṃ niṭṭhitaṃ.

The Section on the Five Factors for Giving Ordination is Concluded.

### 24. Upasampādetabbachakkaṃ ^24

> [!TIP]- Links to [[mv1-brahmali-pali#^24|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch14|BMC Chapter 14]] and the following cites:

24.The Six Qualities for Ordination

85. ‘‘Chahi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā na upasampādetabbaṃ, na nissayo dātabbo, na sāmaṇero upaṭṭhāpetabbo. Na asekkhena sīlakkhandhena samannāgato hoti, na asekkhena samādhikkhandhena samannāgato hoti, na asekkhena paññākkhandhena samannāgato hoti, na asekkhena vimuttikkhandhena samannāgato hoti, na asekkhena vimuttiñāṇadassanakkhandhena samannāgato hoti, ūnadasavasso hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, chahaṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā na upasampādetabbaṃ, na nissayo dātabbo, na sāmaṇero upaṭṭhāpetabbo.

85.“Monks, a monk endowed with six qualities should not give higher ordination, should not give dependence, and should not keep a novice. He is not endowed with the aggregate of virtue of one beyond training, not endowed with the aggregate of concentration of one beyond training, not endowed with the aggregate of wisdom of one beyond training, not endowed with the aggregate of liberation of one beyond training, not endowed with the aggregate of the knowledge and vision of liberation of one beyond training, and he is less than ten years old. Monks, a monk endowed with these six qualities should not give higher ordination, should not give dependence, and should not keep a novice.”

‘‘Chahi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā upasampādetabbaṃ, nissayo dātabbo, sāmaṇero upaṭṭhāpetabbo. Asekkhena sīlakkhandhena samannāgato hoti, asekkhena samādhikkhandhena samannāgato hoti, asekkhena paññākkhandhena samannāgato hoti, asekkhena vimuttikkhandhena samannāgato hoti, asekkhena vimuttiñāṇadassanakkhandhena samannāgato hoti, dasavasso vā hoti atirekadasavasso vā – imehi kho, bhikkhave, chahaṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā upasampādetabbaṃ, nissayo dātabbo, sāmaṇero upaṭṭhāpetabbo.

“Monks, a monk endowed with six qualities may give higher ordination, may give dependence, and may keep a novice. He is endowed with the aggregate of virtue of one beyond training, endowed with the aggregate of concentration of one beyond training, endowed with the aggregate of wisdom of one beyond training, endowed with the aggregate of liberation of one beyond training, endowed with the aggregate of the knowledge and vision of liberation of one beyond training, and is of ten years’ standing or more. Monks, a monk endowed with these six qualities may give higher ordination, may give dependence, and may keep a novice.”

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, chahaṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā na upasampādetabbaṃ, na nissayo dātabbo, na sāmaṇero upaṭṭhāpetabbo. Attanā na asekkhena sīlakkhandhena samannāgato hoti, na paraṃ asekkhe sīlakkhandhe samādapetā; attanā na asekkhena samādhikkhandhena samannāgato hoti, na paraṃ asekkhe samādhikkhandhe samādapetā; attanā na asekkhena paññākkhandhena samannāgato hoti, na paraṃ asekkhe paññākkhandhe samādapetā; attanā na asekkhena vimuttikkhandhena samannāgato hoti, na paraṃ asekkhe vimuttikkhandhe samādapetā; attanā na asekkhena vimuttiñāṇadassanakkhandhena samannāgato hoti, na paraṃ asekkhe vimuttiñāṇadassanakkhandhe samādapetā; ūnadasavasso hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, chahaṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā na upasampādetabbaṃ, na nissayo dātabbo, na sāmaṇero upaṭṭhāpetabbo.

“Furthermore, monks, a monk endowed with another six qualities should not give higher ordination, should not give dependence, and should not keep a novice. He himself is not endowed with the aggregate of virtue of one beyond training, nor does he encourage others in the aggregate of virtue of one beyond training; he himself is not endowed with the aggregate of concentration of one beyond training, nor does he encourage others in the aggregate of concentration of one beyond training; he himself is not endowed with the aggregate of wisdom of one beyond training, nor does he encourage others in the aggregate of wisdom of one beyond training; he himself is not endowed with the aggregate of liberation of one beyond training, nor does he encourage others in the aggregate of liberation of one beyond training; he himself is not endowed with the aggregate of the knowledge and vision of liberation of one beyond training, nor does he encourage others in the aggregate of the knowledge and vision of liberation of one beyond training; and he is less than ten years old. Monks, a monk endowed with these six qualities should not give higher ordination, should not give dependence, and should not keep a novice.”

‘‘Chahi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā upasampādetabbaṃ, nissayo dātabbo, sāmaṇero upaṭṭhāpetabbo. Attanā asekkhena sīlakkhandhena samannāgato hoti, paraṃ asekkhe sīlakkhandhe samādapetā attanā asekkhena samādhikkhandhena samannāgato hoti, paraṃ asekkhe samādhikkhandhe samādapetā. Attanā asekkhena paññākkhandhena samannāgato hoti, paraṃ asekkhe paññākkhandhe samādapetā. Attanā asekkhena vimuttikkhandhena samannāgato hoti, paraṃ asekkhe vimuttikkhandhe samādapetā. Attanā asekkhena vimuttiñāṇadassanakkhandhena samannāgato hoti, paraṃ asekkhe vimuttiñāṇadassanakkhandhe samādapetā; dasavasso vā hoti atirekadasavasso vā – imehi kho, bhikkhave, chahaṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā upasampādetabbaṃ, nissayo dātabbo, sāmaṇero upaṭṭhāpetabbo.

“Monks, a monk endowed with six qualities may give higher ordination, may give dependence, and may keep a novice. He himself is endowed with the aggregate of virtue of one beyond training, and he encourages others in the aggregate of virtue of one beyond training. He himself is endowed with the aggregate of concentration of one beyond training, and he encourages others in the aggregate of concentration of one beyond training. He himself is endowed with the aggregate of wisdom of one beyond training, and he encourages others in the aggregate of wisdom of one beyond training. He himself is endowed with the aggregate of liberation of one beyond training, and he encourages others in the aggregate of liberation of one beyond training. He himself is endowed with the aggregate of the knowledge and vision of liberation of one beyond training, and he encourages others in the aggregate of the knowledge and vision of liberation of one beyond training. He is of ten years’ standing or more. Monks, a monk endowed with these six qualities may give higher ordination, may give dependence, and may keep a novice.”

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, chahaṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā na upasampādetabbaṃ, na nissayo dātabbo, na sāmaṇero upaṭṭhāpetabbo. Assaddho hoti, ahiriko hoti, anottappī hoti, kusīto hoti, muṭṭhassati hoti, ūnadasavasso hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, chahaṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā na upasampādetabbaṃ, na nissayo dātabbo, na sāmaṇero upaṭṭhāpetabbo.

“Furthermore, monks, a monk endowed with another six qualities should not give higher ordination, should not give dependence, and should not keep a novice. He is faithless, shameless, without moral dread, lazy, unmindful, and is less than ten years old. Monks, a monk endowed with these six qualities should not give higher ordination, should not give dependence, and should not keep a novice.”

‘‘Chahi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā upasampādetabbaṃ, nissayo dātabbo, sāmaṇero upaṭṭhāpetabbo. Saddho hoti, hirimā hoti, ottappī hoti, āraddhavīriyo hoti, upaṭṭhitassati hoti, dasavasso vā hoti atirekadasavasso vā – imehi kho, bhikkhave, chahaṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā upasampādetabbaṃ, nissayo dātabbo, sāmaṇero upaṭṭhāpetabbo.

“Monks, a monk endowed with six qualities may give higher ordination, may give dependence, and may keep a novice. He is faithful, conscientious, has moral dread, has aroused energy, has mindfulness established, and is of ten years’ standing or more. Monks, a monk endowed with these six qualities may give higher ordination, may give dependence, and may keep a novice.”

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, chahaṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā na upasampādetabbaṃ, na nissayo dātabbo, na sāmaṇero upaṭṭhāpetabbo. Adhisīle sīlavipanno hoti, ajjhācāre ācāravipanno hoti, atidiṭṭhiyā diṭṭhivipanno hoti, appassuto hoti, duppañño hoti, ūnadasavasso hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, chahaṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā na upasampādetabbaṃ, na nissayo dātabbo, na sāmaṇero upaṭṭhāpetabbo.

“Furthermore, monks, a monk endowed with another six qualities should not give higher ordination, should not give dependence, and should not keep a novice. He is deficient in higher virtue, is corrupt in conduct, has wrong view, is of little learning, is unwise, and is less than ten years old. Monks, a monk endowed with these six qualities should not give higher ordination, should not give dependence, and should not keep a novice.”

‘‘Chahi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā upasampādetabbaṃ, nissayo dātabbo, sāmaṇero upaṭṭhāpetabbo. Na adhisīle sīlavipanno hoti, na ajjhācāre ācāravipanno hoti, na atidiṭṭhiyā diṭṭhivipanno hoti, bahussuto hoti, paññavā hoti, dasavasso vā hoti atirekadasavasso vā – imehi kho, bhikkhave, chahaṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā upasampādetabbaṃ, nissayo dātabbo, sāmaṇero upaṭṭhāpetabbo.

“Monks, a monk endowed with six qualities may give higher ordination, may give dependence, and may keep a novice. He is not deficient in higher virtue, is not corrupt in conduct, does not have wrong view, is learned, is wise, and is of ten years’ standing or more. Monks, a monk endowed with these six qualities may give higher ordination, may give dependence, and may keep a novice.”

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, chahaṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā na upasampādetabbaṃ, na nissayo dātabbo, na sāmaṇero upaṭṭhāpetabbo. Na paṭibalo hoti antevāsiṃ vā saddhivihāriṃ vā gilānaṃ upaṭṭhātuṃ vā upaṭṭhāpetuṃ vā, anabhirataṃ vūpakāsetuṃ vā vūpakāsāpetuṃ vā, uppannaṃ kukkuccaṃ dhammato vinodetuṃ, āpattiṃ na jānāti, āpattiyā vuṭṭhānaṃ na jānāti, ūnadasavasso hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, chahaṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā na upasampādetabbaṃ, na nissayo dātabbo, na sāmaṇero upaṭṭhāpetabbo.

“Furthermore, monks, a monk endowed with another six qualities should not give higher ordination, should not give dependence, and should not keep a novice. He is not capable of attending to a sick pupil or co-resident, or of having one attended to; he is not capable of pacifying one who is discontented, or of having one pacified; he is not capable of dispelling arisen remorse in accordance with the Dhamma; he does not know an offense; he does not know the emergence from an offense; and he is less than ten years old. Monks, a monk endowed with these six qualities should not give higher ordination, should not give dependence, and should not keep a novice.”

‘‘Chahi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā upasampādetabbaṃ, nissayo dātabbo, sāmaṇero upaṭṭhāpetabbo. Paṭibalo hoti antevāsiṃ vā saddhivihāriṃ vā gilānaṃ upaṭṭhātuṃ vā upaṭṭhāpetuṃ vā, anabhirataṃ vūpakāsetuṃ vā vūpakāsāpetuṃ vā, uppannaṃ kukkuccaṃ dhammato vinodetuṃ, āpattiṃ jānāti, āpattiyā vuṭṭhānaṃ jānāti, dasavasso vā hoti atirekadasavasso vā – imehi kho, bhikkhave, chahaṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā upasampādetabbaṃ, nissayo dātabbo, sāmaṇero upaṭṭhāpetabbo.

“Monks, a monk endowed with six qualities may give higher ordination, may give dependence, and may keep a novice. He is capable of attending to a sick pupil or co-resident, or of having one attended to; he is capable of pacifying one who is discontented, or of having one pacified; he is capable of dispelling arisen remorse in accordance with the Dhamma; he knows an offense; he knows the emergence from an offense; and he is of ten years’ standing or more. Monks, a monk endowed with these six qualities may give higher ordination, may give dependence, and may keep a novice.”

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, chahaṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā na upasampādetabbaṃ, na nissayo dātabbo, na sāmaṇero upaṭṭhāpetabbo. Na paṭibalo hoti antevāsiṃ vā saddhivihāriṃ vā abhisamācārikāya sikkhāya sikkhāpetuṃ, ādibrahmacariyakāya sikkhāya vinetuṃ, abhidhamme vinetuṃ, abhivinaye vinetuṃ, uppannaṃ diṭṭhigataṃ dhammato vivecetuṃ, ūnadasavasso hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, chahaṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā na upasampādetabbaṃ, na nissayo dātabbo, na sāmaṇero upaṭṭhāpetabbo.

“Furthermore, monks, a monk endowed with another six qualities should not give higher ordination, should not give dependence, and should not keep a novice. He is not capable of training a pupil or co-resident in the training of proper conduct; he is not capable of guiding them in the preliminary training of the holy life; he is not capable of guiding them in the Abhidhamma; he is not capable of guiding them in the higher discipline; he is not capable of resolving an arisen wrong view in accordance with the Dhamma; and he is less than ten years old. Monks, a monk endowed with these six qualities should not give higher ordination, should not give dependence, and should not keep a novice.”

‘‘Chahi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā upasampādetabbaṃ, nissayo dātabbo, sāmaṇero upaṭṭhāpetabbo. Paṭibalo hoti antevāsiṃ vā saddhivihāriṃ vā abhisamācārikāya sikkhāya sikkhāpetuṃ ādibrahmacariyakāya sikkhāya vinetuṃ, abhidhamme vinetuṃ, abhivinaye vinetuṃ, uppannaṃ diṭṭhigataṃ dhammato vivecetuṃ, dasavasso vā hoti atirekadasavasso vā – imehi kho, bhikkhave, chahaṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā upasampādetabbaṃ, nissayo dātabbo, sāmaṇero upaṭṭhāpetabbo.

Monks, a monk endowed with six qualities is fit to give higher ordination, give dependence, and have a novice attend on him. He is capable of training a pupil or co-resident in the training concerning proper conduct; he is capable of guiding them in the initial training of the spiritual life; he is capable of instructing them in the Abhidhamma; he is capable of instructing them in the Abhivinaya; he is capable of dispelling a wrong view that has arisen, in accordance with the Dhamma; he is ten years old or more. Monks, a monk endowed with these six qualities is fit to give higher ordination, give dependence, and have a novice attend on him.

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, chahaṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā na upasampādetabbaṃ, na nissayo dātabbo, na sāmaṇero upaṭṭhāpetabbo. Āpattiṃ na jānāti, anāpattiṃ na jānāti, lahukaṃ āpattiṃ na jānāti, garukaṃ āpattiṃ na jānāti, ubhayāni kho panassa pātimokkhāni vitthārena na svāgatāni honti na suvibhattāni na suppavattīni na suvinicchitāni suttaso anubyañjanaso, ūnadasavasso hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, chahaṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā na upasampādetabbaṃ, na nissayo dātabbo, na sāmaṇero upaṭṭhāpetabbo.

Furthermore, monks, a monk endowed with six qualities should not give ordination, should not give dependence, and should not have a novice attend on him. He does not know an offense; he does not know a non-offense; he does not know a light offense; he does not know a grave offense; furthermore, both Pātimokkhas have not been properly learned by him in detail, well analyzed, well recited, well determined in terms of the suttas and their detailed explanations; he is less than ten years old. Monks, a monk endowed with these six qualities should not give ordination, should not give dependence, and should not have a novice attend on him.

‘‘Chahi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā upasampādetabbaṃ, nissayo dātabbo, sāmaṇero upaṭṭhāpetabbo. Āpattiṃ jānāti, anāpattiṃ jānāti, lahukaṃ āpattiṃ jānāti, garukaṃ āpattiṃ jānāti, ubhayāni kho panassa pātimokkhāni vitthārena svāgatāni honti suvibhattāni suppavattīni suvinicchitāni suttaso anubyañjanaso, dasavasso vā hoti atirekadasavasso vā – imehi kho, bhikkhave, chahaṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā upasampādetabbaṃ, nissayo dātabbo, sāmaṇero upaṭṭhāpetabbo’’ti.

Monks, a monk endowed with six qualities is fit to give the higher ordination, give dependence, and have a novice attend on him. He knows what is an offense, knows what is not an offense, knows what is a light offense, knows what is a grave offense. Both Pātimokkhas have been well-learned by him in detail, well analyzed, well recited, well-determined in terms of the wording and its underlying meaning. He is ten years old or more. Monks, a monk endowed with these six qualities is fit to give the higher ordination, give dependence, and have a novice attend on him.

Upasampādetabbachakkaṃ niṭṭhitaṃ.

The section on six things concerning conferring the Higher Ordination is finished.

### 25. Aññatitthiyapubbakathā ^25

> [!TIP]- Links to [[mv1-brahmali-pali#^25|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch14|BMC Chapter 14]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-MV1.25" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


25.Discourse on a Former Adherent of Another Sect

86. Tena kho pana samayena yo so aññatitthiyapubbo [yo so pasuraparibbājako aññatitthiyapubbo (ka.)] pajjhāyena sahadhammikaṃ vuccamāno upajjhāyassa vādaṃ āropetvā taṃyeva titthāyatanaṃ saṅkami. So puna paccāgantvā bhikkhū upasampadaṃ yāci. Bhikkhū bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Yo so, bhikkhave, aññatitthiyapubbo upajjhāyena sahadhammikaṃ vuccamāno upajjhāyassa vādaṃ āropetvā taṃyeva titthāyatanaṃ saṅkanto, so āgato na upasampādetabbo. Yo so, bhikkhave, aññopi aññatitthiyapubbo imasmiṃ dhammavinaye ākaṅkhati pabbajjaṃ, ākaṅkhati upasampadaṃ, tassa cattāro māse parivāso dātabbo. Evañca pana, bhikkhave, dātabbo – paṭhamaṃ kesamassuṃ ohārāpetvā kāsāyāni vatthāni acchādāpetvā ekaṃsaṃ uttarāsaṅgaṃ kārāpetvā bhikkhūnaṃ pāde vandāpetvā ukkuṭikaṃ nisīdāpetvā añjaliṃ paggaṇhāpetvā evaṃ vadehīti vattabbo – ‘‘buddhaṃ saraṇaṃ gacchāmi, dhammaṃ saraṇaṃ gacchāmi, saṅghaṃ saraṇaṃ gacchāmi; dutiyampi buddhaṃ saraṇaṃ gacchāmi, dutiyampi dhammaṃ saraṇaṃ gacchāmi, dutiyampi saṅghaṃ saraṇaṃ gacchāmi; tatiyampi buddhaṃ saraṇaṃ gacchāmi, tatiyampi dhammaṃ saraṇaṃ gacchāmi, tatiyampi saṅghaṃ saraṇaṃ gacchāmī’’ti.

86.At that time, a certain former adherent of another sect, when being legitimately addressed by his preceptor in accordance with the Dhamma, accused his preceptor and returned to that same sectarian establishment. Later, he came back and asked the monks for the higher ordination. The monks reported the matter to the Blessed One. "Monks, that former adherent of another sect who, when being legitimately addressed by his preceptor in accordance with the Dhamma, accused his preceptor and returned to that same sectarian establishment—he has come back and should not be given the higher ordination. Monks, any other former adherent of another sect who desires the going forth, desires the higher ordination in this Dhamma and Discipline, should be given probation for four months. And this is how it should be given: First, he should have his hair and beard shaved off, be dressed in ochre robes, arrange his upper robe over one shoulder, pay homage at the feet of the monks, sit in a squatting position, raise his joined palms, and be told to say: ‘I go for refuge to the Buddha, I go for refuge to the Dhamma, I go for refuge to the Sangha; for the second time I go for refuge to the Buddha, for the second time I go for refuge to the Dhamma, for the second time I go for refuge to the Sangha; for the third time I go for refuge to the Buddha, for the third time I go for refuge to the Dhamma, for the third time I go for refuge to the Sangha.’"

Tena, bhikkhave, aññatitthiyapubbena saṅghaṃ upasaṅkamitvā ekaṃsaṃ uttarāsaṅgaṃ karitvā bhikkhūnaṃ pāde vanditvā ukkuṭikaṃ nisīditvā añjaliṃ paggahetvā evamassa vacanīyo – ‘‘ahaṃ, bhante, aññatitthiyapubbo imasmiṃ dhammavinaye ākaṅkhāmi upasampadaṃ. Sohaṃ, bhante, saṅghaṃ cattāro māse parivāsaṃ yācāmī’’ti. Dutiyampi yācitabbo. Tatiyampi yācitabbo. Byattena bhikkhunā paṭibalena saṅgho ñāpetabbo –

Monks, that former member of another sect should approach the Saṅgha, arrange his upper robe over one shoulder, pay homage at the feet of the monks, sit in the squatting position, raise his joined palms, and say: ‘Venerable sirs, I, a former member of another sect, desire ordination in this Dhamma and Discipline. I ask the Saṅgha for four months’ probation.’ He should be asked a second time. He should be asked a third time. A competent and capable monk should inform the Saṅgha:

‘‘Suṇātu me, bhante, saṅgho. Ayaṃ itthannāmo aññatitthiyapubbo imasmiṃ dhammavinaye ākaṅkhati upasampadaṃ. So saṅghaṃ cattāro māse parivāsaṃ yācati. Yadi saṅghassa pattakallaṃ saṅgho itthannāmassa aññatitthiyapubbassa cattāro māse parivāsaṃ dadeyya. Esā ñatti.

Venerable sir, let the Sangha hear me. This person, so-and-so by name, formerly belonging to another sect, desires the higher ordination in this Dhamma and Discipline. He asks the Sangha for four months' probation. If it seems appropriate to the Sangha, the Sangha should grant four months' probation to this person, so-and-so by name, formerly belonging to another sect. This is the motion.

‘‘Suṇātu me, bhante, saṅgho. Ayaṃ itthannāmo aññatitthiyapubbo imasmiṃ dhammavinaye ākaṅkhati upasampadaṃ. So saṅghaṃ cattāro māse parivāsaṃ yācati. Saṅgho itthannāmassa aññatitthiyapubbassa cattāro māse parivāsaṃ deti. Yassāyasmato khamati itthannāmassa aññatitthiyapubbassa cattāro māse parivāsassa dānaṃ, so tuṇhassa; yassa nakkhamati, so bhāseyya.

Venerable sir, may the Sangha hear me. This person named so-and-so, formerly of another sect, desires the higher ordination in this Dhamma and Discipline. He requests from the Sangha a four-month probationary period. The Sangha grants to so-and-so, formerly of another sect, a four-month probationary period. If it seems fit to any venerable one that the four-month probationary period should be granted to so-and-so, formerly of another sect, let him be silent; if it does not seem fit to anyone, let him speak.

‘‘Dinno saṅghena itthannāmassa aññatitthiyapubbassa cattāro māse parivāso. Khamati saṅghassa, tasmā tuṇhī, evametaṃ dhārayāmī’’ti.

The Saṅgha has granted a four-month probationary period to the one named so-and-so, formerly of another sect. It is pleasing to the Saṅgha, therefore it is silent; thus I hold it.

87. ‘‘Evaṃ kho, bhikkhave, aññatitthiyapubbo ārādhako hoti, evaṃ anārādhako. Kathañca, bhikkhave, aññatitthiyapubbo anārādhako hoti? Idha, bhikkhave, aññatitthiyapubbo atikālena gāmaṃ pavisati, atidivā paṭikkamati. Evampi, bhikkhave, aññatitthiyapubbo anārādhako hoti.

87.Thus, monks, one formerly of another sect can be compliant or non-compliant. And how, monks, is one formerly of another sect non-compliant? Here, monks, one formerly of another sect enters the village at an improper time and returns too late in the day. In this way, monks, one formerly of another sect is non-compliant.

‘‘Puna caparaṃ, bhikkhave, aññatitthiyapubbo vesiyāgocaro vā hoti, vidhavāgocaro vā hoti, thullakumārikāgocaro vā hoti, paṇḍakagocaro vā hoti, bhikkhunigocaro vā hoti. Evampi, bhikkhave, aññatitthiyapubbo anārādhako hoti.

Furthermore, monks, one formerly of another sect consorts with prostitutes, or with widows, or with mature maidens, or with eunuchs, or with bhikkhunīs. In this way, monks, one formerly of another sect is non-compliant.

‘‘Puna caparaṃ, bhikkhave, aññatitthiyapubbo yāni tāni sabrahmacārīnaṃ uccāvacāni karaṇīyāni, tattha na dakkho hoti, na analaso, na tatrupāyāya vīmaṃsāya samannāgato, na alaṃ kātuṃ, na alaṃ saṃvidhātuṃ. Evampi, bhikkhave, aññatitthiyapubbo anārādhako hoti.

Furthermore, monks, one formerly of another sect is not skilled, nor is he energetic in the various duties to be done for his fellow brahmacārins; he is not endowed with practical discernment, and he is not capable of doing or arranging. In this way, monks, one formerly of another sect is non-compliant.

‘‘Puna caparaṃ, bhikkhave, aññatitthiyapubbo na tibbacchando hoti uddese, paripucchāya, adhisīle, adhicitte, adhipaññāya. Evampi, bhikkhave, aññatitthiyapubbo anārādhako hoti.

Furthermore, monks, one formerly of another sect does not have intense enthusiasm for study, inquiry, higher virtue, higher mind, or higher wisdom. In this way, monks, one formerly of another sect is non-compliant.

‘‘Puna caparaṃ, bhikkhave, aññatitthiyapubbo yassa titthāyatanā saṅkanto hoti, tassa satthuno tassa diṭṭhiyā tassa khantiyā tassa ruciyā tassa ādāyassa avaṇṇe bhaññamāne kupito hoti anattamano anabhiraddho, buddhassa vā dhammassa vā saṅghassa vā avaṇṇe bhaññamāne attamano hoti udaggo abhiraddho. Yassa vā pana titthāyatanā saṅkanto hoti, tassa satthuno tassa diṭṭhiyā tassa khantiyā tassa ruciyā tassa ādāyassa vaṇṇe bhaññamāne attamano hoti udaggo abhiraddho, buddhassa vā dhammassa vā saṅghassa vā vaṇṇe bhaññamāne kupito hoti anattamano anabhiraddho. Idaṃ, bhikkhave, saṅghātanikaṃ aññatitthiyapubbassa anārādhanīyasmiṃ. Evampi kho, bhikkhave, aññatitthiyapubbo anārādhako hoti. Evaṃ anārādhako kho, bhikkhave, aññatitthiyapubbo āgato na upasampādetabbo.

Furthermore, monks, one formerly of another sect, having come over to this Teaching, becomes angry, displeased, and dissatisfied when the teacher, the view, the preference, the conviction, or the adherence of the sect he left is criticized, but becomes pleased, elated, and satisfied when the Buddha, the Dhamma, or the Sangha is criticized. Or he becomes pleased, elated, and satisfied when the teacher, the view, the preference, the conviction, or the adherence of the sect he left is praised, but becomes angry, displeased, and dissatisfied when the Buddha, the Dhamma, or the Sangha is praised. This, monks, is a factor for non-compliance in one formerly of another sect. In this way, monks, one formerly of another sect is not compliant. Being thus non-compliant, monks, one formerly of another sect should not be given higher ordination.

‘‘Kathañca, bhikkhave, aññatitthiyapubbo ārādhako hoti? Idha, bhikkhave, aññatitthiyapubbo nātikālena gāmaṃ pavisati nātidivā paṭikkamati. Evampi, bhikkhave, aññatitthiyapubbo ārādhako hoti.

And how, monks, is one formerly of another sect compliant? Here, monks, one formerly of another sect does not enter the village at an improper time nor return too late in the day. In this way, monks, one formerly of another sect is compliant.

‘‘Puna caparaṃ, bhikkhave, aññatitthiyapubbo na vesiyāgocaro hoti, na vidhavāgocaro hoti, na thullakumārikāgocaro hoti, na paṇḍakagocaro hoti, na bhikkhunigocaro hoti. Evampi, bhikkhave, aññatitthiyapubbo ārādhako hoti.

Furthermore, monks, one formerly of another sect does not associate with prostitutes, does not associate with widows, does not associate with mature maidens, does not associate with eunuchs, and does not associate with nuns. In this way too, monks, one formerly of another sect is worthy of approval.

‘‘Puna caparaṃ, bhikkhave, aññatitthiyapubbo yāni tāni sabrahmacārīnaṃ uccāvacāni karaṇīyāni, tattha dakkho hoti, analaso, tatrupāyāya vīmaṃsāya samannāgato, alaṃ kātuṃ, alaṃ saṃvidhātuṃ. Evampi, bhikkhave, aññatitthiyapubbo ārādhako hoti.

Furthermore, monks, one formerly of another sect is skilled and unlazy in the various duties to be done for his fellow practitioners, endowed with the discerning wisdom for them, capable of doing them, and capable of arranging them. In this way too, monks, one formerly of another sect is worthy of approval.

‘‘Puna caparaṃ, bhikkhave, aññatitthiyapubbo tibbacchando hoti uddese, paripucchāya, adhisīle, adhicitte, adhipaññāya. Evampi, bhikkhave, aññatitthiyapubbo ārādhako hoti.

Furthermore, monks, one formerly of another sect has intense enthusiasm for study, inquiry, higher virtue, higher mind, and higher wisdom. In this way too, monks, one formerly of another sect is worthy of approval.

‘‘Puna caparaṃ, bhikkhave, aññatitthiyapubbo yassa titthāyatanā saṅkanto hoti, tassa satthuno tassa diṭṭhiyā tassa khantiyā tassa ruciyā tassa ādāyassa avaṇṇe bhaññamāne attamano hoti udaggo abhiraddho, buddhassa vā dhammassa vā saṅghassa vā avaṇṇe bhaññamāne kupito hoti anattamano anabhiraddho. Yassa vā pana titthāyatanā saṅkanto hoti, tassa satthuno tassa diṭṭhiyā tassa khantiyā tassa ruciyā tassa ādāyassa vaṇṇe bhaññamāne kupito hoti anattamano anabhiraddho, buddhassa vā dhammassa vā saṅghassa vā vaṇṇe bhaññamāne attamano hoti udaggo abhiraddho. Idaṃ, bhikkhave, saṅghātanikaṃ aññatitthiyapubbassa ārādhanīyasmiṃ. Evampi kho, bhikkhave, aññatitthiyapubbo ārādhako hoti. Evaṃ ārādhako kho, bhikkhave, aññatitthiyapubbo āgato upasampādetabbo.

Furthermore, monks, when one formerly of another sect has come over to this Dispensation, if criticism is spoken of the teacher, the view, the tolerance, the inclination, or the commitment of the sect he has left, he is pleased, uplifted, and delighted. But when criticism is spoken of the Buddha, the Dhamma, or the Saṅgha, he becomes angry, displeased, and discontent. Or if praise is spoken of the teacher, the view, the tolerance, the inclination, or the commitment of the sect he has left, he becomes angry, displeased, and discontent. But when praise is spoken of the Buddha, the Dhamma, or the Saṅgha, he is pleased, uplifted, and delighted. This, monks, is what constitutes acceptability in one formerly of another sect. In this way too, monks, one formerly of another sect is worthy of approval. Being thus worthy of approval, monks, one formerly of another sect who comes should be given full ordination.

‘‘Sace, bhikkhave, aññatitthiyapubbo naggo āgacchati, upajjhāyamūlakaṃ cīvaraṃ pariyesitabbaṃ. Sace acchinnakeso āgacchati, saṅgho apaloketabbo bhaṇḍukammāya. Ye te, bhikkhave, aggikā jaṭilakā, te āgatā upasampādetabbā, na tesaṃ parivāso dātabbo. Taṃ kissa hetu? Kammavādino ete, bhikkhave, kiriyavādino. Sace, bhikkhave, jātiyā sākiyo aññatitthiyapubbo āgacchati, so āgato upasampādetabbo, na tassa parivāso dātabbo. Imāhaṃ, bhikkhave, ñātīnaṃ āveṇikaṃ parihāraṃ dammī’’ti.

If, monks, a former member of another sect comes naked, robes should be sought on the basis of the preceptor. If he comes with uncut hair, the Saṅgha should be informed for the tonsure ceremony. Those fire-worshipping ascetics with matted hair, monks, who come should be given full ordination; no period of probation should be given to them. Why is that? These, monks, are advocates of kamma, advocates of action. If, monks, a former member of another sect comes who is a Sakyan by birth, he should be given full ordination; no period of probation should be given to him. This, monks, is a special privilege I grant to relatives.

Aññatitthiyapubbakathā niṭṭhitā.

The discourse on those formerly of other sects is concluded.

Sattamabhāṇavāro.

The Seventh Recitation Section.

### 26. Pañcābādhavatthu ^26

26.The Chapter on the Five Diseases

88. Tena kho pana samayena magadhesu pañca ābādhā ussannā honti – kuṭṭhaṃ, gaṇḍo, kilāso, soso, apamāro. Manussā pañcahi ābādhehi phuṭṭhā jīvakaṃ komārabhaccaṃ upasaṅkamitvā evaṃ vadanti – ‘‘sādhu no, ācariya, tikicchāhī’’ti. ‘‘Ahaṃ khvayyo, bahukicco bahukaraṇīyo; rājā ca me māgadho seniyo bimbisāro upaṭṭhātabbo itthāgārañca buddhappamukho ca bhikkhusaṅgho; nāhaṃ sakkomi tikicchitu’’nti. ‘‘Sabbaṃ sāpateyyañca te, ācariya, hotu; mayañca te dāsā; sādhu, no, ācariya, tikicchāhī’’ti. ‘‘Ahaṃ khvayyo, bahukicco bahukaraṇīyo rājā ca me māgadho seniyo bimbisāro upaṭṭhātabbo itthāgārañca buddhappamukho ca bhikkhusaṅgho; nāhaṃ sakkomi tikicchitu’’nti. Atha kho tesaṃ manussānaṃ etadahosi – ‘‘ime kho samaṇā sakyaputtiyā sukhasīlā sukhasamācārā, subhojanāni bhuñjitvā nivātesu sayanesu sayanti. Yaṃnūna mayaṃ samaṇesu sakyaputtiyesu pabbajeyyāma. Tattha bhikkhū ceva upaṭṭhahissanti, jīvako ca komārabhacco tikicchissatī’’ti. Atha kho te manussā bhikkhū upasaṅkamitvā pabbajjaṃ yāciṃsu. Te bhikkhū pabbājesuṃ, upasampādesuṃ. Te bhikkhū ceva upaṭṭhahiṃsu jīvako ca komārabhacco tikicchi. Tena kho pana samayena bhikkhū bahū gilāne bhikkhū upaṭṭhahantā yācanabahulā viññattibahulā viharanti – gilānabhattaṃ detha, gilānupaṭṭhākabhattaṃ detha, gilānabhesajjaṃ dethāti. Jīvakopi komārabhacco bahū gilāne bhikkhū tikicchanto aññataraṃ rājakiccaṃ parihāpesi.

88.At that time, five diseases were prevalent in Magadha—leprosy, boils, leucoderma, consumption, and epilepsy. People afflicted by these five diseases approached Jīvaka Komārabhacca and said, “Please, teacher, treat us.” “I am busy, sirs, with much to do. I must attend to King Seniya Bimbisāra of Magadha, the women’s quarters, and the community of monks with the Buddha at their head. I cannot treat you.” “All our property will be yours, teacher, and we will be your slaves. Please, teacher, treat us.” “I am busy, sirs, with much to do. I must attend to King Seniya Bimbisāra of Magadha, the women’s quarters, and the community of monks with the Buddha at their head. I cannot treat you.” Then those people thought, “These Sakyan ascetics live easily, behave easily, eat good food, and sleep in sheltered beds. Why don’t we go forth among the Sakyan ascetics? There, the monks will care for us, and Jīvaka Komārabhacca will treat us.” So they approached the monks and requested ordination. The monks gave them ordination and full admission. The monks cared for them, and Jīvaka Komārabhacca treated them. At that time, monks who were caring for many sick monks lived demanding and importunate lives, constantly asking, “Give food for the sick, give food for those attending the sick, give medicine for the sick.” Jīvaka Komārabhacca, while treating many sick monks, neglected a certain royal duty.

89. Aññataropi puriso pañcahi ābādhehi phuṭṭho jīvakaṃ komārabhaccaṃ upasaṅkamitvā etadavoca – ‘‘sādhu maṃ, ācariya, tikicchāhī’’ti. ‘‘Ahaṃ khvayyo, bahukicco, bahukaraṇīyo, rājā ca me māgadho seniyo bimbisāro upaṭṭhātabbo itthāgārañca buddhappamukho ca bhikkhusaṅgho; nāhaṃ sakkomi tikicchitu’’nti. ‘‘Sabbaṃ sāpateyyañca te, ācariya, hotu, ahañca te dāso; sādhu maṃ, ācariya, tikicchāhī’’ti. ‘‘Ahaṃ khvayyo, bahukicco bahukaraṇīyo, rājā ca me māgadho seniyo bimbisāro upaṭṭhātabbo itthāgārañca buddhappamukho ca bhikkhusaṅgho, nāhaṃ sakkomi tikicchitu’’nti. Atha kho tassa purisassa etadahosi – ‘‘ime kho samaṇā sakyaputtiyā sukhasīlā sukhasamācārā, subhojanāni bhuñjitvā nivātesu sayanesu sayanti. Yaṃnūnāhaṃ samaṇesu sakyaputtiyesu pabbajeyyaṃ. Tattha bhikkhū ceva upaṭṭhahissanti, jīvako ca komārabhacco tikicchissati. Somhi [sohaṃ (bahūsu, vimativinodanīṭīkā oloketabbā)] arogo vibbhamissāmī’’ti. Atha kho so puriso bhikkhu upasaṅkamitvā pabbajjaṃ yāci. Taṃ bhikkhū pabbājesuṃ, upasampādesuṃ. Taṃ bhikkhū ceva upaṭṭhahiṃsu, jīvako ca komārabhacco tikicchi. So arogo vibbhami. Addasā kho jīvako komārabhacco taṃ purisaṃ vibbhantaṃ, disvāna taṃ purisaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘nanu tvaṃ, ayyo, bhikkhūsu pabbajito ahosī’’ti? ‘‘Evaṃ, ācariyā’’ti. ‘‘Kissa pana tvaṃ, ayyo, evarūpamakāsī’’ti? Atha kho so puriso jīvakassa komārabhaccassa etamatthaṃ ārocesi. Jīvako komārabhacco ujjhāyati khiyyati vipāceti – ‘‘kathañhi nāma bhadantā [bhaddantā (ka.)] pañcahi ābādhehi phuṭṭhaṃ pabbājessantī’’ti. Atha kho jīvako komārabhacco yena bhagavā tenupasaṅkami, upasaṅkamitvā bhagavantaṃ abhivādetvā ekamantaṃ nisīdi. Ekamantaṃ nisinno kho jīvako komārabhacco bhagavantaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘sādhu, bhante, ayyā pañcahi ābādhehi phuṭṭhaṃ na pabbājeyyu’’nti. Atha kho bhagavā jīvakaṃ komārabhaccaṃ dhammiyā kathāya sandassesi samādapesi samuttejesi sampahaṃsesi. Atha kho jīvako komārabhacco bhagavatā dhammiyā kathāya sandassito samādapito samuttejito sampahaṃsito uṭṭhāyāsanā bhagavantaṃ abhivādetvā padakkhiṇaṃ katvā pakkāmi. Atha kho bhagavā etasmiṃ nidāne etasmiṃ pakaraṇe dhammiṃ kathaṃ katvā bhikkhū āmantesi – ‘‘na, bhikkhave, pañcahi ābādhehi phuṭṭho pabbājetabbo. Yo pabbājeyya, āpatti dukkaṭassā’’ti.

89.A certain man afflicted with five diseases approached Jīvaka Komārabhacca and said, “Good Master, please treat me.” “Sir, I am very busy with many duties. I must attend to King Seniya Bimbisāra of Magadha, the women’s quarters, and the community of monks led by the Buddha. I cannot treat you.” “Master, let all my possessions be yours, and I will be your slave. Please, Master, treat me.” “Sir, I am very busy with many duties. I must attend to King Seniya Bimbisāra of Magadha, the women’s quarters, and the community of monks led by the Buddha. I cannot treat you.” Then that man thought, “These Sakyan ascetics live comfortably, behave comfortably, eat good food, and sleep in sheltered beds. What if I were to go forth among the Sakyan ascetics? There, the monks will attend to me, and Jīvaka Komārabhacca will treat me. Then I will recover and leave the Order.” So that man approached the monks and requested ordination. The monks ordained him and gave him full ordination. The monks attended to him, and Jīvaka Komārabhacca treated him. He recovered and left the Order. Jīvaka Komārabhacca saw that man after he had left the Order and said to him, “Sir, weren’t you ordained among the monks?” “Yes, Master.” “Then why, sir, did you act in such a way?” Then that man explained the matter to Jīvaka Komārabhacca. Jīvaka Komārabhacca complained, criticized, and protested, “How could the venerable ones ordain someone afflicted with five diseases?” Then Jīvaka Komārabhacca approached the Blessed One, paid homage, and sat down to one side. Seated there, he said, “Bhante, it would be good if the venerable ones did not ordain someone afflicted with five diseases.” Then the Blessed One instructed, encouraged, and gladdened Jīvaka Komārabhacca with a Dhamma talk. Having been instructed, encouraged, and gladdened by the Blessed One with a Dhamma talk, Jīvaka Komārabhacca rose from his seat, paid homage, circumambulated the Blessed One, and departed. Then, on this occasion, the Blessed One gave a Dhamma talk and addressed the monks: “Monks, one afflicted with five diseases should not be ordained. Whoever ordains such a person commits an offense of wrong-doing.”

Pañcābādhavatthu niṭṭhitaṃ.

The Chapter on the Five Diseases is concluded.

### 27. Rājabhaṭavatthu ^27

> [!TIP]- Links to [[mv1-brahmali-pali#^27|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch14|BMC Chapter 14]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-MV1.27" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


27.The Story of the Royal Soldier

90. Tena kho pana samayena rañño māgadhassa seniyassa bimbisārassa paccanto kupito hoti. Atha kho rājā māgadho seniyo bimbisāro senānāyake mahāmatte āṇāpesi – ‘‘gacchatha, bhaṇe, paccantaṃ uccinathā’’ti. ‘‘Evaṃ, devā’’ti kho senānāyakā mahāmattā rañño māgadhassa seniyassa bimbisārassa paccassosuṃ. Atha kho abhiññātānaṃ abhiññātānaṃ yodhānaṃ etadahosi – ‘‘mayaṃ kho yuddhābhinandino gacchantā pāpañca karoma, bahuñca apuññaṃ pasavāma. Kena nu kho mayaṃ upāyena pāpā ca virameyyāma kalyāṇañca kareyyāmā’’ti? Atha kho tesaṃ yodhānaṃ etadahosi – ‘‘ime kho samaṇā sakyaputtiyā dhammacārino samacārino brahmacārino saccavādino sīlavanto kalyāṇadhammā. Sace kho mayaṃ samaṇesu sakyaputtiyesu pabbajeyyāma, evaṃ mayaṃ pāpā ca virameyyāma kalyāṇañca kareyyāmā’’ti. Atha kho te yodhā bhikkhū upasaṅkamitvā pabbajjaṃ yāciṃsu. Te bhikkhū pabbājesuṃ, upasampādesuṃ. Senānāyakā mahāmattā rājabhaṭe pucchiṃsu – ‘‘kiṃ nu kho, bhaṇe, itthannāmo ca itthannāmo ca yodhā na dissantī’’ti? ‘‘Itthannāmo ca itthannāmo ca, sāmi, yodhā bhikkhūsu pabbajitā’’ti. Senānāyakā mahāmattā ujjhāyanti khiyyanti vipācenti – ‘‘kathañhi nāma samaṇā sakyaputtiyā rājabhaṭaṃ pabbājessantī’’ti. Senānāyakā mahāmattā rañño māgadhassa seniyassa bimbisārassa etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Atha kho rājā māgadho seniyo bimbisāro vohārike mahāmatte pucchi – ‘‘yo, bhaṇe, rājabhaṭaṃ pabbājeti, kiṃ so pasavatī’’ti? ‘‘Upajjhāyassa, deva, sīsaṃ chetabbaṃ, anussāvakassa [anusāvakassa (ka.)] jivhā uddharitabbā, gaṇassa upaḍḍhaphāsukā bhañjitabbā’’ti. Atha kho rājā māgadho seniyo bimbisāro yena bhagavā tenupasaṅkami, upasaṅkamitvā bhagavantaṃ abhivādetvā ekamantaṃ nisīdi. Ekamantaṃ nisinno kho rājā māgadho seniyo bimbisāro bhagavantaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘santi, bhante, rājāno assaddhā appasannā. Te appamattakenapi bhikkhū viheṭheyyuṃ. Sādhu, bhante, ayyā rājabhaṭaṃ na pabbājeyyu’’nti. Atha kho bhagavā rājānaṃ māgadhaṃ seniyaṃ bimbisāraṃ dhammiyā kathāya sandassesi samādapesi samuttejesi sampahaṃsesi. Atha kho rājā māgadho seniyo bimbisāro bhagavatā dhammiyā kathāya sandassito samādapito samuttejito sampahaṃsito uṭṭhāyāsanā bhagavantaṃ abhivādetvā padakkhiṇaṃ katvā pakkāmi. Atha kho bhagavā etasmiṃ nidāne etasmiṃ pakaraṇe dhammiṃ kathaṃ katvā bhikkhū āmantesi – ‘‘na, bhikkhave, rājabhaṭo pabbājetabbo. Yo pabbājeyya, āpatti dukkaṭassā’’ti.

90.Now at that time the border region of King Seniya Bimbisāra of Magadha was in revolt. Then King Bimbisāra of Magadha ordered his generals and ministers: "Go, sirs, and quell the border region." "Yes, Your Majesty," replied the generals and ministers to King Bimbisāra of Magadha. Then some well-known warriors thought: "We delight in war, but by going we will do evil and accumulate much demerit. By what means could we refrain from evil and do good?" Then those warriors thought: "These ascetics, the Sakyan sons, are Dhamma practitioners, righteous, celibate, truthful, virtuous, and of good character. If we were to go forth among the ascetics, the Sakyan sons, thus we would refrain from evil and do good." Then those warriors approached the monks and asked for ordination. The monks gave them ordination and full admission to the Saṅgha. The generals and ministers asked the royal soldiers: "Why, sirs, are so-and-so and so-and-so warriors not seen?" "So-and-so and so-and-so, sirs, have gone forth as monks." The generals and ministers complained, criticized, and expressed their displeasure: "How can the Sakyan ascetics ordain royal soldiers?" The generals and ministers informed King Bimbisāra of Magadha of this matter. Then King Bimbisāra of Magadha asked his judicial ministers: "Sirs, what does one who ordains a royal soldier incur?" "The preceptor, Your Majesty, should be beheaded, the announcer should have his tongue pulled out, and half the ribs of the Saṅgha should be broken." Then King Bimbisāra of Magadha approached the Blessed One, paid homage to him, and sat down to one side. Sitting to one side, King Bimbisāra of Magadha said to the Blessed One: "Venerable sir, there are kings who are faithless and unconfident. They might harass the monks even for trivial reasons. It would be good, venerable sir, if the venerable ones did not ordain royal soldiers." Then the Blessed One instructed, encouraged, aroused, and gladdened King Bimbisāra of Magadha with a Dhamma talk. Having been instructed, encouraged, aroused, and gladdened by the Blessed One with a Dhamma talk, King Bimbisāra of Magadha rose from his seat, paid homage to the Blessed One, circumambulated him, and departed. Then, on this occasion, having given a Dhamma talk, the Blessed One addressed the monks: "Monks, a royal soldier should not be ordained. Whoever ordains one commits an offense of wrong-doing."

Rājabhaṭavatthu niṭṭhitaṃ.

The story of the royal soldier is concluded.

### 28. Aṅgulimālacoravatthu ^28

> [!TIP]- Links to [[mv1-brahmali-pali#^28|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch14|BMC Chapter 14]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-MV1.28" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


28.The Story of the Robber Aṅgulimāla

91. Tena kho pana samayena coro aṅgulimālo bhikkhūsu pabbajito hoti. Manussā passitvā ubbijjantipi, uttasantipi, palāyantipi, aññenapi gacchanti, aññenapi mukhaṃ karonti, dvārampi thakenti. Manussā ujjhāyanti khiyyanti vipācenti – ‘‘kathañhi nāma samaṇā sakyaputtiyā dhajabandhaṃ coraṃ pabbājessantī’’ti. Assosuṃ kho bhikkhū tesaṃ manussānaṃ ujjhāyantānaṃ khiyyantānaṃ vipācentānaṃ. Atha kho te bhikkhū bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ…pe… na, bhikkhave, dhajabandho coro pabbājetabbo. Yo pabbājeyya, āpatti dukkaṭassāti.

91.At that time, the robber Aṅgulimāla had gone forth among the monks. People, upon seeing him, were repulsed, terrified, fled, took another route, turned their faces away, and even bolted their doors. People complained, criticized, and denounced: "How can the Sakyan ascetics ordain a notorious robber?" The monks heard these people complaining, criticizing, and denouncing. Then those monks reported the matter to the Blessed One… "Monks, a notorious robber should not be ordained. Whoever ordains him commits an offense of wrong-doing."

Aṅgulimālacoravatthu niṭṭhitaṃ.

The story of the robber Aṅgulimāla is concluded.

### 29. Kārabhedakacoravatthu ^29

> [!TIP]- Links to [[mv1-brahmali-pali#^29|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch14|BMC Chapter 14]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-MV1.29" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


29.The Story of the Prison-Breaking Thief

92. Tena kho pana samayena raññā māgadhena seniyena bimbisārena anuññātaṃ hoti – ‘‘ye samaṇesu sakyaputtiyesu pabbajanti, na te labbhā kiñci kātuṃ; svākkhāto dhammo, carantu brahmacariyaṃ sammā dukkhassa antakiriyāyā’’ti. Tena kho pana samayena aññataro puriso corikaṃ katvā kārāya baddho hoti. So kāraṃ bhinditvā palāyitvā bhikkhūsu pabbajito hoti. Manussā passitvā evamāhaṃsu – ‘‘ayaṃ so kārabhedako coro. Handa, naṃ nemā’’ti. Ekacce evamāhaṃsu – ‘‘māyyo, evaṃ avacuttha. Anuññātaṃ raññā māgadhena seniyena bimbisārena – ‘‘ye samaṇesu sakyaputtiyesu pabbajanti, na te labbhā kiñci kātuṃ; svākkhāto dhammo, carantu brahmacariyaṃ sammā dukkhassa antakiriyāyā’’ti. Manussā ujjhāyanti khiyyanti vipācenti – ‘‘abhayūvarā ime samaṇā sakyaputtiyā, nayime labbhā kiñci kātuṃ. Kathañhi nāma samaṇā sakyaputtiyā kārabhedakaṃ coraṃ pabbājessantī’’ti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Na, bhikkhave, kārabhedako coro pabbājetabbo. Yo pabbājeyya, āpatti dukkaṭassāti.

92.Now at that time, King Seniya Bimbisāra of Magadha had granted permission: “Nothing may be done to those who go forth among the Sakyan ascetics; the Dhamma is well-proclaimed, let them practice the holy life rightly for the cessation of suffering.” At that time, a certain man, having committed theft, was imprisoned. He broke out of prison, escaped, and went forth among the monks. People, upon seeing him, said: “This is that prison-breaking thief. Come, let us seize him.” Some said: “Sirs, do not speak thus. King Seniya Bimbisāra of Magadha had granted permission: ‘Nothing may be done to those who go forth among the Sakyan ascetics; the Dhamma is well-proclaimed, let them practice the holy life rightly for the cessation of suffering.’” People complained, criticized, and protested: “These Sakyan ascetics are immune; nothing can be done to them. How can the Sakyan ascetics ordain a prison-breaking thief?” They reported the matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, a prison-breaking thief should not be ordained. Whoever ordains him commits an offense of wrong-doing.”

Kārabhedakacoravatthu niṭṭhitaṃ.

The Story of the Prison-Breaking Thief is concluded.

### 30. Likhitakacoravatthu ^30

> [!TIP]- Links to [[mv1-brahmali-pali#^30|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch14|BMC Chapter 14]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-MV1.30" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


30.The Story of the Proscribed Thief

93. Tena kho pana samayena aññataro puriso corikaṃ katvā palāyitvā bhikkhūsu pabbajito hoti. So ca rañño antepure likhito hoti – yattha passati, tattha hantabboti. Manussā passitvā evamāhaṃsu – ‘‘ayaṃ so likhitako coro. Handa, naṃ hanāmā’’ti. Ekacce evamāhaṃsu – ‘‘māyyo, evaṃ avacuttha. Anuññātaṃ raññā māgadhena seniyena bimbisārena ‘‘ye samaṇesu sakyaputtiyesu pabbajanti, na te labbhā kiñci kātuṃ, svākkhāto dhammo, carantu brahmacariyaṃ sammā dukkhassa antakiriyāyā’’ti. Manussā ujjhāyanti khiyyanti vipācenti – ‘‘abhayūvarā ime samaṇā sakyaputtiyā, nayime labbhā kiñci kātuṃ. Kathañhi nāma samaṇā sakyaputtiyā likhitakaṃ coraṃ pabbājessantī’’ti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Na, bhikkhave, likhitako coro pabbājetabbo. Yo pabbājeyya, āpatti dukkaṭassāti.

93.Now at that time, a certain man, having committed theft, fled and went forth among the monks. He had been proscribed by the king’s inner court: “Wherever he is seen, he should be killed.” People, upon seeing him, said: “This is that proscribed thief. Come, let us kill him.” Some said: “Sirs, do not speak thus. King Seniya Bimbisāra of Magadha had granted permission: ‘Nothing may be done to those who go forth among the Sakyan ascetics; the Dhamma is well-proclaimed, let them practice the holy life rightly for the cessation of suffering.’” People complained, criticized, and protested: “These Sakyan ascetics are immune; nothing can be done to them. How can the Sakyan ascetics ordain a proscribed thief?” They reported the matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, a proscribed thief should not be ordained. Whoever ordains him commits an offense of wrong-doing.”

Likhitakacoravatthu niṭṭhitaṃ.

The Story of the Proscribed Thief is concluded.

### 31. Kasāhatavatthu ^31

> [!TIP]- Links to [[mv1-brahmali-pali#^31|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch14|BMC Chapter 14]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query

> ```


31.The Story of the Flogged Man

94. Tena kho pana samayena aññataro puriso kasāhato katadaṇḍakammo bhikkhūsu pabbajito hoti. Manussā ujjhāyanti khiyyanti vipācenti – ‘‘kathañhi nāma samaṇā sakyaputtiyā kasāhataṃ katadaṇḍakammaṃ pabbājessantī’’ti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Na, bhikkhave, kasāhato katadaṇḍakammo pabbājetabbo. Yo pabbājeyya, āpatti dukkaṭassāti.

94.Now at that time a certain man, flogged and subjected to a penal beating, had gone forth among the monks. People complained and criticized, saying: “How can these Sakyan ascetics ordain one who has been flogged and subjected to a penal beating?” They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, one who has been flogged and subjected to a penal beating should not be ordained. Whoever ordains such a person incurs an offense of wrong-doing.”

Kasāhatavatthu niṭṭhitaṃ.

The Story of the Flogged Man is concluded.

### 32. Lakkhaṇāhatavatthu ^32

> [!TIP]- Links to [[mv1-brahmali-pali#^32|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch14|BMC Chapter 14]] and the following cites:
