32.The Story of the Branded Man

95. Tena kho pana samayena aññataro puriso lakkhaṇāhato katadaṇḍakammo bhikkhūsu pabbajito hoti. Manussā ujjhāyanti khiyyanti vipācenti – ‘‘kathañhi nāma samaṇā sakyaputtiyā lakkhaṇāhataṃ katadaṇḍakammaṃ pabbājessantī’’ti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Na, bhikkhave, lakkhaṇāhato katadaṇḍakammo pabbājetabbo. Yo pabbājeyya, āpatti dukkaṭassāti.

95.Now at that time a certain man, branded and who had undergone a punishment involving beating, went forth among the monks. People complained and criticized, saying: “How can these Sakyan ascetics ordain a man who is branded and who has undergone a punishment involving beating?” They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, one who is branded and who has undergone a punishment involving beating should not be ordained. Whoever ordains such a person incurs an offense of wrong-doing.”

Lakkhaṇāhatavatthu niṭṭhitaṃ.

The Story of the Branded Man is concluded.

### 33. Iṇāyikavatthu ^33

> [!TIP]- Links to [[mv1-brahmali-pali#^33|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch14|BMC Chapter 14]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-MV1.33" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


33.The Story of the Creditor

96. Tena kho pana samayena aññataro puriso iṇāyiko palāyitvā bhikkhūsu pabbajito hoti. Dhaniyā passitvā evamāhaṃsu – ‘‘ayaṃ so amhākaṃ iṇāyiko. Handa, naṃ nemā’’ti. Ekacce evamāhaṃsu – ‘‘māyyo, evaṃ avacuttha. Anuññātaṃ raññā māgadhena seniyena bimbisārena – ‘‘ye samaṇesu sakyaputtiyesu pabbajanti, na te labbhā kiñci kātuṃ; svākkhāto dhammo, carantu brahmacariyaṃ sammā dukkhassa antakiriyāyā’’ti. Manussā ujjhāyanti khiyyanti vipācenti – ‘‘abhayūvarā ime samaṇā sakyaputtiyā. Nayime labbhā kiñci kātuṃ. Kathañhi nāma samaṇā sakyaputtiyā iṇāyikaṃ pabbājessantī’’ti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Na, bhikkhave, iṇāyiko pabbājetabbo. Yo pabbājeyya, āpatti dukkaṭassāti.

96.Now at that time a certain man, being in debt, fled and went forth among the monks. His creditors saw him and said, “This is our debtor. Come, let us seize him.” Some said, “Do not say so, sirs. It has been permitted by King Seniya Bimbisāra of Magadha: ‘Those who go forth among the Sakyan ascetics cannot be made to do anything. The Dhamma is well-proclaimed; let them live the holy life for the complete ending of suffering.’” People complained, criticized, and spread it about, saying, “These Sakyan ascetics are immune. They cannot be made to do anything. How can the Sakyan ascetics ordain a debtor?” They told this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, a debtor should not be ordained. Whoever ordains one commits an offense of wrong-doing.”

Iṇāyikavatthu niṭṭhitaṃ.

The Story of the Creditor is concluded.

### 34. Dāsavatthu ^34

> [!TIP]- Links to [[mv1-brahmali-pali#^34|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch14|BMC Chapter 14]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-MV1.34" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


34.The Story of a Slave

97. Tena kho pana samayena aññataro dāso palāyitvā bhikkhūsu pabbajito hoti. Ayyakā [ayyikā (ka.), ayirakā (sī.)] passitvā evamāhaṃsu – ‘‘ayaṃ so amhākaṃ dāso. Handa, naṃ nemā’’ti. Ekacce evamāhaṃsu – ‘‘māyyo, evaṃ avacuttha, anuññātaṃ raññā māgadhena seniyena bimbisārena ‘‘ye samaṇesu sakyaputtiyesu pabbajanti, na te labbhā kiñci kātuṃ, svākkhāto dhammo, carantu brahmacariyaṃ sammā dukkhassa antakiriyāyā’’ti. Manussā ujjhāyanti khiyyanti vipācenti – ‘‘abhayūvarā ime samaṇā sakyaputtiyā, nayime labbhā kiñci kātuṃ. Kathañhi nāma samaṇā sakyaputtiyā dāsaṃ pabbājessantī’’ti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Na, bhikkhave, dāso pabbājetabbo. Yo pabbājeyya, āpatti dukkaṭassāti.

97.Now on that occasion, a certain slave, having run away, went forth among the monks. His owners saw him and said, “This is our slave. Come, let us take him back.” Some said, “No, sirs, do not say that. It has been permitted by King Seniya Bimbisāra of Magadha: ‘Those who go forth among the Sakyan ascetics are not to be made to do anything. The Dhamma is well-proclaimed; let them live the holy life for the complete ending of suffering.’” People complained, murmured, and criticized: “These Sakyan ascetics are immune; nothing can be done to them. How can the Sakyan ascetics ordain a slave?” They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, a slave should not be ordained. Whoever ordains one commits an offense of wrong-doing.”

Dāsavatthu niṭṭhitaṃ.

The Story of a Slave is concluded.

### 35. Kammārabhaṇḍuvatthu ^35

> [!TIP]- Links to [[mv1-brahmali-pali#^35|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch14|BMC Chapter 14]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-MV1.35" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


35.The Story of the Blacksmith's Apprentice

98. Tena kho pana samayena aññataro kammārabhaṇḍu mātāpitūhi saddhiṃ bhaṇḍitvā ārāmaṃ gantvā bhikkhūsu pabbajito hoti. Atha kho tassa kammārabhaṇḍussa mātāpitaro taṃ kammārabhaṇḍuṃ vicinantā ārāmaṃ gantvā bhikkhū pucchiṃsu – ‘‘api, bhante, evarūpaṃ dārakaṃ passeyyāthā’’ti? Bhikkhū ajānaṃyeva āhaṃsu – ‘‘na jānāmā’’ti, apassaṃyeva āhaṃsu – ‘‘na passāmā’’ti. Atha kho tassa kammārabhaṇḍussa mātāpitaro taṃ kammārabhaṇḍuṃ vicinantā bhikkhūsu pabbajitaṃ disvā ujjhāyanti khiyyanti vipācenti – ‘‘alajjino ime samaṇā sakyaputtiyā, dussīlā musāvādino. Jānaṃyeva āhaṃsu – ‘na jānāmā’ti, passaṃyeva āhaṃsu – ‘na passāmā’ti. Ayaṃ dārako bhikkhūsu pabbajito’’ti. Assosuṃ kho bhikkhū tassa kammārabhaṇḍussa mātāpitūnaṃ ujjhāyantānaṃ khiyyantānaṃ vipācentānaṃ. Atha kho te bhikkhū bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, saṅghaṃ apaloketuṃ bhaṇḍukammāyāti.

98.Now at that time a certain blacksmith’s apprentice, having quarreled with his parents, went to the monastery and was ordained among the monks. Then that blacksmith’s apprentice’s parents, searching for him, went to the monastery and asked the monks: “Venerable sirs, have you seen a boy like this?” The monks, not knowing, said: “We do not know.” Not seeing, they said: “We do not see.” Then that blacksmith’s apprentice’s parents, searching for him, saw him ordained among the monks and complained, grumbled, and protested: “These shameless Sakyan ascetics are immoral and liars. Though they knew, they said, ‘We do not know’; though they saw, they said, ‘We do not see.’ This boy has been ordained among the monks!” The monks heard the complaints, grumblings, and protests of that blacksmith’s apprentice's parents. Then those monks informed the Blessed One of this matter. “I allow, monks, to consult the Sangha regarding the tonsure.”

Kammārabhaṇḍuvatthu niṭṭhitaṃ.

The Story of the Blacksmith's Apprentice is concluded.

### 36. Upālidārakavatthu ^36

> [!TIP]- Links to [[mv1-brahmali-pali#^36|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch14|BMC Chapter 14]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-MV1.36" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


36.The Story of Upāli the Boy

99. [idaṃ vatthu pāci. 402 ādayo] Tena kho pana samayena rājagahe sattarasavaggiyā dārakā sahāyakā honti. Upālidārako tesaṃ pāmokkho hoti. Atha kho upālissa mātāpitūnaṃ etadahosi – ‘‘kena nu kho upāyena upāli amhākaṃ accayena sukhañca jīveyya, na ca kilameyyā’’ti? Atha kho upālissa mātāpitūnaṃ etadahosi – ‘‘sace kho upāli lekhaṃ sikkheyya, evaṃ kho upāli amhākaṃ accayena sukhañca jīveyya, na ca kilameyyā’’ti. Atha kho upālissa mātāpitūnaṃ etadahosi – ‘‘sace kho upāli lekhaṃ sikkhissati, aṅguliyo dukkhā bhavissanti. Sace kho upāli gaṇanaṃ sikkheyya, evaṃ kho upāli amhākaṃ accayena sukhañca jīveyya, na ca kilameyyā’’ti. Atha kho upālissa mātāpitūnaṃ etadahosi – ‘‘sace kho upāli gaṇanaṃ sikkhissati, urassa dukkho bhavissati. Sace kho upāli rūpaṃ sikkheyya, evaṃ kho upāli amhākaṃ accayena sukhañca jīveyya, na ca kilameyyā’’ti. Atha kho upālissa mātāpitūnaṃ etadahosi – ‘‘sace kho upāli rūpaṃ sikkhissati, akkhīni dukkhā bhavissanti. Ime kho samaṇā sakyaputtiyā sukhasīlā sukhasamācārā, subhojanāni bhuñjitvā nivātesu sayanesu sayanti. Sace kho upāli samaṇesu sakyaputtiyesu pabbajeyya, evaṃ kho upāli amhākaṃ accayena sukhañca jīveyya, na ca kilameyyā’’ti.

99.Now at that time in Rājagaha, there was a group of seventeen boys who were friends. Among them, the boy Upāli was the foremost. Then Upāli’s parents thought: “By what means could Upāli live happily after our passing, without toiling?” Then Upāli’s parents thought: “If Upāli were to learn writing, then after our passing, he could live happily and without toiling.” Then Upāli’s parents thought: “But if Upāli learns writing, his fingers will ache. If Upāli were to learn arithmetic, then after our passing, he could live happily and without toiling.” Then Upāli’s parents thought: “But if Upāli learns arithmetic, his chest will ache. If Upāli were to learn painting, then after our passing, he could live happily and without toiling.” Then Upāli’s parents thought: “But if Upāli learns painting, his eyes will ache. These Sakyan ascetics are of pleasant habits and conduct; they eat good food and sleep in sheltered beds. If Upāli were to go forth among the Sakyan ascetics, then after our passing, he could live happily and without toiling.”

Assosi kho upālidārako mātāpitūnaṃ imaṃ kathāsallāpaṃ. Atha kho upālidārako yena te dārakā tenupasaṅkami, upasaṅkamitvā te dārake etadavoca – ‘‘etha mayaṃ, ayyā, samaṇesu sakyaputtiyesu pabbajissāmā’’ti. ‘‘Sace kho tvaṃ, ayya, pabbajissasi, evaṃ mayampi pabbajissāmā’’ti. Atha kho te dārakā ekamekassa mātāpitaro upasaṅkamitvā etadavocuṃ – ‘‘anujānātha maṃ agārasmā anāgāriyaṃ pabbajjāyā’’ti. Atha kho tesaṃ dārakānaṃ mātāpitaro – ‘‘sabbepime dārakā samānacchandā kalyāṇādhippāyā’’ti – anujāniṃsu. Te bhikkhū upasaṅkamitvā pabbajjaṃ yāciṃsu. Te bhikkhū pabbājesuṃ upasampādesuṃ. Te rattiyā paccūsasamayaṃ paccuṭṭhāya rodanti – ‘‘yāguṃ detha, bhattaṃ detha, khādanīyaṃ dethā’’ti. Bhikkhū evamāhaṃsu – ‘‘āgametha, āvuso, yāva ratti vibhāyati. Sace yāgu bhavissati pivissatha, sace bhattaṃ bhavissati bhuñjissatha, sace khādanīyaṃ bhavissati khādissatha; no ce bhavissati yāgu vā bhattaṃ vā khādanīyaṃ vā, piṇḍāya caritvā bhuñjissathā’’ti. Evampi kho te bhikkhū bhikkhūhi vuccamānā rodantiyeva ‘‘yāguṃ detha, bhattaṃ detha, khādanīyaṃ dethā’’ti; senāsanaṃ uhadantipi ummihantipi.

Young Upāli overheard his parents' conversation. Then young Upāli approached those boys and said to them, “Come, sirs, let us go forth among the Sakyan ascetics.” “If you, sir, go forth, then we too will go forth,” they replied. Then those boys each approached their own parents and said, “Permit me to go forth from the household life into homelessness.” Then the parents of those boys, thinking, “All these boys have the same desire and noble intentions,” gave their permission. They approached the monks and requested ordination. The monks ordained them and conferred full ordination. But at dawn, they would rise early and cry, “Give us gruel! Give us rice! Give us snacks!” The monks said to them, “Wait, friends, until daybreak. If there is gruel, you may drink it; if there is rice, you may eat it; if there are snacks, you may consume them. If there is no gruel, rice, or snacks, you may go for alms and eat.” Even when told this by the monks, they kept crying, “Give us gruel! Give us rice! Give us snacks!” They even overturned and dirtied the bedding.

Assosi kho bhagavā rattiyā paccūsasamayaṃ paccuṭṭhāya dārakasaddaṃ. Sutvāna āyasmantaṃ ānandaṃ āmantesi – ‘‘kiṃ nu kho so, ānanda, dārakasaddo’’ti? Atha kho āyasmā ānando bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesi…pe… ‘‘saccaṃ kira, bhikkhave, bhikkhū jānaṃ ūnavīsativassaṃ puggalaṃ upasampādentī’’ti? ‘‘Saccaṃ, bhagavā’’ti. Vigarahi buddho bhagavā…pe… ‘‘kathañhi nāma te, bhikkhave, moghapurisā jānaṃ ūnavīsativassaṃ puggalaṃ upasampādessanti. Ūnavīsativasso, bhikkhave, puggalo akkhamo hoti sītassa uṇhassa jighacchāya pipāsāya ḍaṃsamakasavātātapasarīsapasamphassānaṃ duruttānaṃ durāgatānaṃ vacanapathānaṃ uppannānaṃ sārīrikānaṃ vedanānaṃ dukkhānaṃ tibbānaṃ kharānaṃ kaṭukānaṃ asātānaṃ amanāpānaṃ pāṇaharānaṃ anadhivāsakajātiko hoti. Vīsativassova kho, bhikkhave, puggalo khamo hoti sītassa uṇhassa jighacchāya pipāsāya ḍaṃsamakasavātātapasarīsapasamphassānaṃ duruttānaṃ durāgatānaṃ vacanapathānaṃ, uppannānaṃ sārīrikānaṃ vedanānaṃ dukkhānaṃ tibbānaṃ kharānaṃ kaṭukānaṃ asātānaṃ amanāpānaṃ pāṇaharānaṃ adhivāsakajātiko hoti. Netaṃ, bhikkhave, appasannānaṃ vā pasādāya, pasannānaṃ vā bhiyyobhāvāya…pe… vigarahitvā…pe… dhammiṃ kathaṃ katvā bhikkhū āmantesi – ‘‘na, bhikkhave, jānaṃ ūnavīsativasso puggalo upasampādetabbo. Yo upasampādeyya, yathādhammo kāretabbo’’ti.

The Blessed One, having woken up in the early morning, heard the sound of children. Having heard it, he addressed Venerable Ānanda, “Ānanda, what is that sound of children?” Then Venerable Ānanda informed the Blessed One of this matter… “Is it true, monks, that monks knowingly give the full ordination to a person under twenty years of age?” “It is true, Blessed One.” The Buddha rebuked them… “How can you, monks, foolish men that you are, knowingly give the full ordination to a person under twenty years of age? A person under twenty years of age, monks, is incapable of enduring cold, heat, hunger, thirst, the touch of flies, mosquitoes, wind, sun, and creeping things, harsh and unwelcome speech, and bodily feelings that are painful, sharp, severe, acute, unpleasant, disagreeable, and life-threatening. But a person of twenty years of age, monks, is capable of enduring cold, heat, hunger, thirst, the touch of flies, mosquitoes, wind, sun, and creeping things, harsh and unwelcome speech, and bodily feelings that are painful, sharp, severe, acute, unpleasant, disagreeable, and life-threatening. This, monks, will not lead to confidence in those who are without it, nor to the increase of confidence in those who have it…” Having rebuked them… he gave a Dhamma talk and addressed the monks: “Monks, a person known to be under twenty years of age should not be given the full ordination. Whoever gives the full ordination to such a person should be dealt with according to the Dhamma.”

Upālidārakavatthu niṭṭhitaṃ.

The Story of Upāli the Boy is concluded.

### 37. Ahivātakarogavatthu ^37

> [!TIP]- Links to [[mv1-brahmali-pali#^37|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch14|BMC Chapter 14]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-MV1.37" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


37.The Story of the Plague

100. Tena kho pana samayena aññataraṃ kulaṃ ahivātakarogena kālaṅkataṃ hoti. Tassa pitāputtakā sesā honti. Te bhikkhūsu pabbajitvā ekatova piṇḍāya caranti. Atha kho so dārako pituno bhikkhāya dinnāya upadhāvitvā etadavoca – ‘‘mayhampi, tāta, dehi; mayhampi, tāta, dehī’’ti. Manussā ujjhāyanti khiyyanti vipācenti – ‘‘abrahmacārino ime samaṇā sakyaputtiyā. Ayampi dārako bhikkhuniyā jāto’’ti. Assosuṃ kho bhikkhū tesaṃ manussānaṃ ujjhāyantānaṃ khiyyantānaṃ vipācentānaṃ. Atha kho te bhikkhū bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Na, bhikkhave, ūnapannarasavasso dārako pabbājetabbo. Yo pabbājeyya, āpatti dukkaṭassāti.

100.At that time, a certain family had died from the plague. Only the father and son were left. They went forth among the bhikkhus and went on almsround together. Then that boy, seeing his father receiving alms, ran up and said, 'Give to me too, father! Give to me too, father!' People complained, grumbled, and criticized: 'These Sakyan ascetics are not celibate! This boy must have been born from a bhikkhunī!' The bhikkhus heard those people complaining, grumbling, and criticizing. Then those bhikkhus reported the matter to the Blessed One. 'Bhikkhus, a boy under fifteen years old should not be given the going forth. Whoever gives the going forth to such a boy commits an offense of wrong-doing.'

Tena kho pana samayena āyasmato ānandassa upaṭṭhākakulaṃ saddhaṃ pasannaṃ ahivātakarogena kālaṅkataṃ hoti, dve ca dārakā sesā honti. Te porāṇakena āciṇṇakappena bhikkhū passitvā upadhāvanti. Bhikkhū apasādenti. Te bhikkhūhi apasādiyamānā rodanti. Atha kho āyasmato ānandassa etadahosi – ‘‘bhagavatā paññattaṃ ‘na ūnapannarasavasso dārako pabbājetabbo’ti. Ime ca dārakā ūnapannarasavassā. Kena nu kho upāyena ime dārakā na vinasseyyu’’nti? Atha kho āyasmā ānando bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesi. Ussahanti pana te, ānanda, dārakā kāke uḍḍāpetunti? Ussahanti, bhagavāti. Atha kho bhagavā etasmiṃ nidāne etasmiṃ pakaraṇe dhammiṃ kathaṃ katvā bhikkhū āmantesi – ‘‘anujānāmi, bhikkhave, ūnapannarasavassaṃ dārakaṃ kākuḍḍepakaṃ pabbājetu’’nti.

At that time, the family supporting Venerable Ānanda, who were faithful and devoted, had died from the plague, leaving only two boys. Following an old custom, they ran up to the bhikkhus when they saw them. The bhikkhus rejected them. Being rejected by the bhikkhus, they cried. Then Venerable Ānanda thought, 'The Blessed One has laid down that a boy under fifteen should not be given the going forth. But these boys are under fifteen. By what means, then, would these boys not be ruined?' Then Venerable Ānanda reported the matter to the Blessed One. 'Ānanda, are those boys able to scare away crows?' 'They are able, Blessed One.' Then the Blessed One, on this occasion and in this connection, gave a Dhamma talk and addressed the bhikkhus: 'Bhikkhus, I allow a boy under fifteen who can scare away crows to be given the going forth.'

Ahivātakarogavatthu niṭṭhitaṃ.

The account of the plague is finished.

### 38. Kaṇṭakavatthu ^38

> [!TIP]- Links to [[mv1-brahmali-pali#^38|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch14|BMC Chapter 14]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-MV1.38" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


38.The Story of Kaṇṭaka

101. Tena kho pana samayena āyasmato upanandassa sakyaputtassa dve sāmaṇerā honti – kaṇṭako ca mahako ca. Te aññamaññaṃ dūsesuṃ. Bhikkhū ujjhāyanti khiyyanti vipācenti – ‘‘kathañhi nāma sāmaṇerā evarūpaṃ anācāraṃ ācarissantī’’ti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Na, bhikkhave, ekena dve sāmaṇerā upaṭṭhāpetabbā. Yo upaṭṭhāpeyya, āpatti dukkaṭassāti.

101.At that time, Venerable Upananda the Sakyan had two sāmaṇeras—Kaṇṭaka and Mahaka. They corrupted each other. The bhikkhus complained, grumbled, and criticized: 'How can these sāmaṇeras engage in such improper conduct?' They reported the matter to the Blessed One. 'Bhikkhus, one should not have two sāmaṇeras attend upon a single bhikkhu. Whoever does so commits an offense of wrong-doing.'

Kaṇṭakavatthu niṭṭhitaṃ.

The Story of Kaṇṭaka is finished.

### 39. Āhundarikavatthu ^39

> [!TIP]- Links to [[mv1-brahmali-pali#^39|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch14|BMC Chapter 14]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-MV1.39" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


39.The Story of Āhundarika

102. Tena kho pana samayena bhagavā tattheva rājagahe vassaṃ vasi, tattha hemantaṃ, tattha gimhaṃ. Manussā ujjhāyanti khiyyanti vipācenti – ‘‘āhundarikā samaṇānaṃ sakyaputtiyānaṃ disā andhakārā, na imesaṃ disā pakkhāyantī’’ti. Assosuṃ kho bhikkhū tesaṃ manussānaṃ ujjhāyantānaṃ khiyyantānaṃ vipācentānaṃ. Atha kho te bhikkhū bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Atha kho bhagavā āyasmantaṃ ānandaṃ āmantesi – ‘‘gacchānanda, avāpuraṇaṃ [apāpuraṇaṃ (ka.)] ādāya anupariveṇiyaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ ārocehi – ‘‘icchatāvuso bhagavā dakkhiṇāgiriṃ cārikaṃ pakkamituṃ. Yassāyasmato attho, so āgacchatū’’ti. Evaṃ, bhante, ti kho āyasmā ānando bhagavato paṭissuṇitvā avāpuraṇaṃ ādāya anupariveṇiyaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ ārocesi – ‘icchatāvuso bhagavā dakkhiṇāgiriṃ cārikaṃ pakkamituṃ. Yassāyasmato attho, so āgacchatū’’’ti. Bhikkhū evamāhaṃsu – ‘‘bhagavatā, āvuso ānanda, paññattaṃ dasavassāni nissāya vatthuṃ, dasavassena nissayaṃ dātuṃ. Tattha ca no gantabbaṃ bhavissati, nissayo ca gahetabbo bhavissati, ittaro ca vāso bhavissati, puna ca paccāgantabbaṃ bhavissati, puna ca nissayo gahetabbo bhavissati. Sace amhākaṃ ācariyupajjhāyā gamissanti, mayampi gamissāma; no ce amhākaṃ ācariyupajjhāyā gamissanti, mayampi na gamissāma. Lahucittakatā no, āvuso ānanda, paññāyissatī’’ti. Atha kho bhagavā ogaṇena bhikkhusaṅghena dakkhiṇāgiriṃ cārikaṃ pakkāmi.

102.At that time, the Blessed One was dwelling right there in Rājagaha for the rains, the winter, and the summer. People complained, grumbled, and criticized: 'These Sakyan ascetics are too domesticated; their horizons are dark, they do not go forth to new places.' The bhikkhus heard those people complaining, grumbling, and criticizing. Then those bhikkhus reported the matter to the Blessed One. Then the Blessed One addressed Venerable Ānanda: 'Go, Ānanda, take the key and announce to the bhikkhus in the surrounding residences: "Friends, the Blessed One wishes to set out on tour to Dakkhiṇāgiri. Whoever wishes may come."' 'Yes, Venerable Sir,' replied Venerable Ānanda to the Blessed One. Taking the key, he announced to the bhikkhus in the surrounding residences: 'Friends, the Blessed One wishes to set out on tour to Dakkhiṇāgiri. Whoever wishes may come.' The bhikkhus said: 'Friend Ānanda, the Blessed One has laid down that one must live in dependence for ten years, and one may grant dependence after ten years. There, we would have to go, take dependence, stay for a brief period, then return, and take dependence again. If our teachers and preceptors go, we will go too; if our teachers and preceptors do not go, we will not go. Friend Ānanda, our fickleness will become apparent.' Then the Blessed One set out on tour to Dakkhiṇāgiri with a depleted Saṅgha of bhikkhus.

Āhundarikavatthu niṭṭhitaṃ.

The Story of Āhundarika is finished.

### 40. Nissayamuccanakakathā ^40

> [!TIP]- Links to [[mv1-brahmali-pali#^40|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch14|BMC Chapter 14]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-MV1.40" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


40.The Discourse on Release from Dependence

103. Atha kho bhagavā dakkhiṇāgirismiṃ yathābhirantaṃ viharitvā punadeva rājagahaṃ paccāgacchi. Atha kho bhagavā āyasmantaṃ ānandaṃ āmantesi – ‘‘kiṃ nu kho, ānanda, tathāgato ogaṇena bhikkhusaṅghena dakkhiṇāgiriṃ cārikaṃ pakkanto’’ti? Atha kho āyasmā ānando bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesi. Atha kho bhagavā etasmiṃ nidāne etasmiṃ pakaraṇe dhammiṃ kathaṃ katvā bhikkhū āmantesi – ‘‘anujānāmi, bhikkhave, byattena bhikkhunā paṭibalena pañcavassāni nissāya vatthuṃ, abyattena yāvajīvaṃ.

103.Then the Blessed One, having stayed in Dakkhiṇāgiri as long as he pleased, returned to Rājagaha. Then the Blessed One addressed Venerable Ānanda: “Ānanda, did the Tathāgata set out on tour to Dakkhiṇāgiri with a depleted community of monks?” Then Venerable Ānanda informed the Blessed One of the matter. Then the Blessed One, on this occasion, in connection with this incident, gave a Dhamma talk and addressed the monks: “Monks, I allow that a monk who is articulate and able may live in dependence for five years; an inarticulate one, for life.

‘‘Pañcahi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā na anissitena vatthabbaṃ. Na asekkhena sīlakkhandhena samannāgato hoti na asekkhena samādhikkhandhena, na asekkhena paññākkhandhena na asekkhena vimuttikkhandhena na asekkhena vimuttiñāṇadassanakkhandhena samannāgato hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā na anissitena vatthabbaṃ.

“Monks, a monk endowed with five qualities should not live without dependence. He is not endowed with the consummate aggregate of virtue, nor the consummate aggregate of concentration, nor the consummate aggregate of wisdom, nor the consummate aggregate of liberation, nor the consummate aggregate of the knowledge and vision of liberation. Monks, a monk endowed with these five qualities should not live without dependence.”

‘‘Pañcahi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā anissitena vatthabbaṃ. Asekkhena sīlakkhandhena samannāgato hoti asekkhena samādhikkhandhena. Asekkhena paññākkhandhena… asekkhena vimuttikkhandhena… asekkhena vimuttiñāṇadassanakkhandhena samannāgato hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā anissitena vatthabbaṃ.

“Monks, a monk endowed with five qualities should live without dependence. He is endowed with the consummate aggregate of virtue, the consummate aggregate of concentration, the consummate aggregate of wisdom, the consummate aggregate of liberation, and the consummate aggregate of the knowledge and vision of liberation. Monks, a monk endowed with these five qualities should live without dependence.”

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā na anissitena vatthabbaṃ. Assaddho hoti, ahiriko hoti, anottappī hoti, kusīto hoti, muṭṭhassati hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā na anissitena vatthabbaṃ.

“Monks, a monk endowed with another five qualities should not live without dependence. He is faithless, shameless, without scruples, lazy, and unmindful. Monks, a monk endowed with these five qualities should not live without dependence.”

‘‘Pañcahi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā anissitena vatthabbaṃ. Saddho hoti, hirimā hoti, ottappī hoti, āraddhavīriyo hoti, upaṭṭhitassati hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā anissitena vatthabbaṃ.

“Monks, a monk endowed with five qualities should live without dependence. He is faithful, conscientious, scrupulous, energetic, and established in mindfulness. Monks, a monk endowed with these five qualities should live without dependence.”

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā na anissitena vatthabbaṃ. Adhisīle sīlavipanno hoti, ajjhācāre ācāravipanno hoti, atidiṭṭhiyā diṭṭhivipanno hoti, appassuto hoti, duppañño hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā na anissitena vatthabbaṃ.

“Monks, a monk endowed with another five qualities should not live without dependence. He is deficient in higher virtue, deficient in conduct, deficient in view, has little learning, and is unwise. Monks, a monk endowed with these five qualities should not live without dependence.”

‘‘Pañcahi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā anissitena vatthabbaṃ. Na adhisīle sīlavipanno hoti, na ajjhācāre ācāravipanno hoti, na atidiṭṭhiyā diṭṭhivipanno hoti, bahussuto hoti, paññavā hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā anissitena vatthabbaṃ.

“Monks, a monk endowed with five qualities should live without dependence. He is not deficient in higher virtue, not deficient in conduct, not deficient in view, is well-learned, and is wise. Monks, a monk endowed with these five qualities should live without dependence.”

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā na anissitena vatthabbaṃ. Āpattiṃ na jānāti, anāpattiṃ na jānāti, lahukaṃ āpattiṃ na jānāti, garukaṃ āpattiṃ na jānāti, ubhayāni kho panassa pātimokkhāni vitthārena na svāgatāni honti na suvibhattāni na suppavattīni na suvinicchitāni suttaso anubyañjanaso – imehi kho, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā na anissitena vatthabbaṃ.

“Monks, a monk endowed with these further five qualities should not live without dependence. He does not know an offense, does not know what is not an offense, does not know a minor offense, does not know a grave offense, and both Pātimokkhas are not well-learned by him in detail, not well analyzed, not well recited, not well determined by their clauses and by their meanings. Monks, a monk endowed with these five qualities should not live without dependence.”

‘‘Pañcahi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā anissitena vatthabbaṃ. Āpattiṃ jānāti, anāpattiṃ jānāti, lahukaṃ āpattiṃ jānāti, garukaṃ āpattiṃ jānāti, ubhayāni kho panassa pātimokkhāni vitthārena svāgatāni honti suvibhattāni suppavattīni suvinicchitāni suttaso anubyañjanaso – imehi kho, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā anissitena vatthabbaṃ.

“Monks, a monk endowed with five qualities should live without dependence. He knows what is an offense, knows what is not an offense, knows what is a minor offense, knows what is a grave offense, and both Pātimokkhas are thoroughly learned by him in detail, well analyzed, well recited, well determined by their clauses and by their meanings. Monks, a monk endowed with these five qualities should live without dependence.”

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā na anissitena vatthabbaṃ. Āpattiṃ na jānāti, anāpattiṃ na jānāti, lahukaṃ āpattiṃ na jānāti, garukaṃ āpattiṃ na jānāti, ūnapañcavasso hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā na anissitena vatthabbaṃ.

“Monks, a monk endowed with another five qualities should not live without dependence. He does not know what is an offense, does not know what is not an offense, does not know what is a minor offense, does not know what is a grave offense, and he is less than five years’ standing. Monks, a monk endowed with these five qualities should not live without dependence.”

‘‘Pañcahi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā anissitena vatthabbaṃ. Āpattiṃ jānāti, anāpattiṃ jānāti, lahukaṃ āpattiṃ jānāti, garukaṃ āpattiṃ jānāti, pañcavasso vā hoti atireka pañcavasso vā – imehi kho, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā anissitena vatthabbaṃ.

“Monks, a monk endowed with five qualities should live without dependence. He knows what is an offense, he knows what is not an offense, he knows what is a minor offense, he knows what is a grave offense, and he is five years’ standing or more. Monks, a monk endowed with these five qualities should live without dependence.”

Nissayamuccanakakathā niṭṭhitā.

The discourse on release from dependence is concluded.

Pañcakadasavāro niṭṭhito.

The fifteenth recitation is concluded.

104. ‘‘Chahi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā na anissitena vatthabbaṃ. Na asekkhena sīlakkhandhena samannāgato hoti, na asekkhena samādhikkhandhena, na asekkhena paññākkhandhena, na asekkhena vimuttikkhandhena, na asekkhena vimuttiñāṇadassanakkhandhena samannāgato hoti, ūnapañcavasso hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, chahaṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā na anissitena vatthabbaṃ.

104.“Monks, a monk endowed with six qualities should not live without dependence. He is not endowed with the consummate aggregate of virtue, nor the consummate aggregate of concentration, nor the consummate aggregate of wisdom, nor the consummate aggregate of liberation, nor the consummate aggregate of the knowledge and vision of liberation, and he is less than five years’ standing. Monks, a monk endowed with these six qualities should not live without dependence.”

‘‘Chahi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā anissitena vatthabbaṃ. Asekkhena sīlakkhandhena samannāgato hoti, asekkhena samādhikkhandhena, asekkhena paññākkhandhena, asekkhena vimuttikkhandhena, asekkhena vimuttiñāṇadassanakkhandhena samannāgato hoti, pañcavasso vā hoti atirekapañcavasso vā – imehi kho, bhikkhave, chahaṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā anissitena vatthabbaṃ.

“Monks, a monk endowed with six qualities should live without dependence. He is endowed with the consummate aggregate of virtue, the consummate aggregate of concentration, the consummate aggregate of wisdom, the consummate aggregate of liberation, the consummate aggregate of the knowledge and vision of liberation, and he is five years’ standing or more. Monks, a monk endowed with these six qualities should live without dependence.”

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, chahaṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā na anissitena vatthabbaṃ. Assaddho hoti, ahiriko hoti, anottappī hoti, kusīto hoti, muṭṭhassati hoti, ūnapañcavasso hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, chahaṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā na anissitena vatthabbaṃ.

“Monks, a monk endowed with another six qualities should not live without dependence. He is faithless, shameless, without scruples, lazy, unmindful, and is less than five years’ standing. Monks, a monk endowed with these six qualities should not live without dependence.”

‘‘Chahi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā anissitena vatthabbaṃ. Saddho hoti, hirimā hoti, ottappī hoti, āraddhavīriyo hoti, upaṭṭhitassati hoti, pañcavasso vā hoti atirekapañcavasso vā – imehi kho, bhikkhave, chahaṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā anissitena vatthabbaṃ.

“Monks, a monk endowed with six qualities should live without dependence. He is faithful, conscientious, scrupulous, energetic, mindful, and is five years’ standing or more. Monks, a monk endowed with these six qualities should live without dependence.”

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, chahaṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā na anissitena vatthabbaṃ. Adhisīle sīlavipanno hoti, ajjhācāre ācāravipanno hoti, atidiṭṭhiyā diṭṭhivipanno hoti, appassuto hoti, duppañño hoti, ūnapañcavasso hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, chahaṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā na anissitena vatthabbaṃ.

“Monks, a monk endowed with another six qualities should not live without dependence. He is deficient in higher virtue, deficient in conduct, deficient in view, has little learning, is unwise, and is less than five years’ standing. Monks, a monk endowed with these six qualities should not live without dependence.”

‘‘Chahi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā anissitena vatthabbaṃ. Na adhisīle sīlavipanno hoti, na ajjhācāre ācāravipanno hoti, na atidiṭṭhiyā diṭṭhivipanno hoti, bahussuto hoti, paññavā hoti, pañcavasso vā hoti atirekapañcavasso vā – imehi kho, bhikkhave, chahaṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā anissitena vatthabbaṃ.

“Monks, a monk endowed with six qualities should live without dependence. He is not deficient in higher virtue, not deficient in conduct, not deficient in view, is well-learned, is wise, and is five years’ standing or more. Monks, a monk endowed with these six qualities should live without dependence.”

‘‘Aparehipi, bhikkhave, chahaṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā na anissitena vatthabbaṃ. Āpattiṃ na jānāti, anāpattiṃ na jānāti, lahukaṃ āpattiṃ na jānāti, garukaṃ āpattiṃ na jānāti, ubhayāni kho panassa pātimokkhāni vitthārena na svāgatāni honti na suvibhattāni na suppavattīni na suvinicchitāni suttaso anubyañjanaso, ūnapañcavasso hoti – imehi kho, bhikkhave, chahaṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā na anissitena vatthabbaṃ.

“Monks, a monk endowed with six qualities should not live without dependence. He does not know an offense, he does not know a non-offense, he does not know a minor offense, he does not know a grave offense, and both Pātimokkhas are not well-learned by him in detail, not well analyzed, not well recited, not well determined by their clauses and by their meanings, and he is less than five years’ standing. Monks, a monk endowed with these six qualities should not live without dependence.”

‘‘Chahi, bhikkhave, aṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā anissitena vatthabbaṃ. Āpattiṃ jānāti, anāpattiṃ jānāti, lahukaṃ āpattiṃ jānāti, garukaṃ āpattiṃ jānāti, ubhayāni kho panassa pātimokkhāni vitthārena svāgatāni honti suvibhattāni suppavattīni suvinicchitāni suttaso anubyañjanaso, pañcavasso vā hoti atirekapañcavasso vā – imehi kho, bhikkhave, chahaṅgehi samannāgatena bhikkhunā anissitena vatthabba’’nti.

“Monks, a monk endowed with six qualities should live without dependence. He knows what is an offense, he knows what is not an offense, he knows what is a minor offense, he knows what is a grave offense, both Pātimokkhas are well-learned by him in detail, well analyzed, well recited, well determined by their clauses and by their meanings; and he is five years’ standing or more. Monks, a monk endowed with these six qualities should live without dependence.”

Abhayūvarabhāṇavāro niṭṭhito aṭṭhamo.

The eighth chapter, “The Story of Abhaya,” is finished.

Aṭṭhamabhāṇavāro.

The eighth chapter of recitations.

### 41. Rāhulavatthu ^41

> [!TIP]- Links to [[mv1-brahmali-pali#^41|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch14|BMC Chapter 14]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-MV1.41" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


41.The Story of Rāhula

105. Atha kho bhagavā rājagahe yathābhirantaṃ viharitvā yena kapilavatthu tena cārikaṃ pakkāmi. Anupubbena cārikaṃ caramāno yena kapilavatthu tadavasari. Tatra sudaṃ bhagavā sakkesu viharati kapilavatthusmiṃ nigrodhārāme. Atha kho bhagavā pubbaṇhasamayaṃ nivāsetvā pattacīvaramādāya yena suddhodanassa sakkassa nivesanaṃ tenupasaṅkami, upasaṅkamitvā paññatte āsane nisīdi. Atha kho rāhulamātā devī rāhulaṃ kumāraṃ etadavoca – ‘‘eso te, rāhula, pitā. Gacchassu [gacchassa (syā.)], dāyajjaṃ yācāhī’’ti. Atha kho rāhulo kumāro yena bhagavā tenupasaṅkami, upasaṅkamitvā bhagavato purato, aṭṭhāsi – ‘‘sukhā te, samaṇa, chāyā’’ti. Atha kho bhagavā uṭṭhāyāsanā pakkāmi. Atha kho rāhulo kumāro bhagavantaṃ piṭṭhito piṭṭhito anubandhi – ‘‘dāyajjaṃ me, samaṇa, dehi; dāyajjaṃ me, samaṇa, dehī’’ti. Atha kho bhagavā āyasmantaṃ sāriputtaṃ āmantesi – ‘‘tena hi tvaṃ, sāriputta, rāhulaṃ kumāraṃ pabbājehī’’ti. ‘‘Kathāhaṃ, bhante, rāhulaṃ kumāraṃ pabbājemī’’ti? Atha kho bhagavā etasmiṃ nidāne etasmiṃ pakaraṇe dhammiṃ kathaṃ katvā bhikkhū āmantesi – ‘‘anujānāmi, bhikkhave, tīhi saraṇagamanehi sāmaṇerapabbajjaṃ. Evañca pana, bhikkhave, pabbājetabbo – paṭhamaṃ kesamassuṃ ohārāpetvā kāsāyāni vatthāni acchādāpetvā ekaṃsaṃ uttarāsaṅgaṃ kārāpetvā bhikkhūnaṃ pāde vandāpetvā ukkuṭikaṃ nisīdāpetvā añjaliṃ paggaṇhāpetvā evaṃ vadehīti vattabbo – buddhaṃ saraṇaṃ gacchāmi, dhammaṃ saraṇaṃ gacchāmi, saṅghaṃ saraṇaṃ gacchāmi; dutiyampi buddhaṃ saraṇaṃ gacchāmi, dutiyampi dhammaṃ saraṇaṃ gacchāmi, dutiyampi saṅghaṃ saraṇaṃ gacchāmi; tatiyampi buddhaṃ saraṇaṃ gacchāmi, tatiyampi dhammaṃ saraṇaṃ gacchāmi, tatiyampi saṅghaṃ saraṇaṃ gacchāmīti. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, imehi tīhi saraṇagamanehi sāmaṇerapabbajja’’nti. Atha kho āyasmā sāriputto rāhulaṃ kumāraṃ pabbājesi.

105.Then the Blessed One, having stayed in Rājagaha as long as he pleased, set out on a journey toward Kapilavatthu. Traveling stage by stage, he arrived at Kapilavatthu. There the Blessed One stayed among the Sakyans in the Nigrodha Park. Then the Blessed One, having dressed in the morning, took his bowl and robe and went to the residence of the Sakyan Suddhodana. Having approached, he sat down on the prepared seat. Then Rāhula’s mother, the queen, said to the young Rāhula: "That, Rāhula, is your father. Go and ask for your inheritance." Then the young Rāhula approached the Blessed One. Having approached, he stood in front of the Blessed One and said: "Pleasant is your shade, ascetic." Then the Blessed One rose from his seat and departed. The young Rāhula followed closely behind the Blessed One, saying: "Give me my inheritance, ascetic; give me my inheritance, ascetic." Then the Blessed One addressed the Venerable Sāriputta: "Well then, Sāriputta, ordain the young Rāhula." "How, Venerable Sir, am I to ordain the young Rāhula?" Then the Blessed One, on this occasion, having given a Dhamma talk, addressed the monks: "I allow, monks, the going forth as a novice with the three refuges. And this is how, monks, he should be ordained: First, having had the hair and beard shaved off, having put on the ochre robes, having arranged the upper robe over one shoulder, having paid homage at the feet of the monks, having sat in the squatting position, having raised the joined palms, he should be told to say thus: 'I go to the Buddha for refuge. I go to the Dhamma for refuge. I go to the Saṅgha for refuge. For the second time, I go to the Buddha for refuge. For the second time, I go to the Dhamma for refuge. For the second time, I go to the Saṅgha for refuge. For the third time, I go to the Buddha for refuge. For the third time, I go to the Dhamma for refuge. For the third time, I go to the Saṅgha for refuge.' I allow, monks, the going forth as a novice with these three refuges." Then the Venerable Sāriputta ordained the young Rāhula.

Atha kho suddhodano sakko yena bhagavā tenupasaṅkami, upasaṅkamitvā bhagavantaṃ abhivādetvā ekamantaṃ nisīdi. Ekamantaṃ nisinno kho suddhodano sakko bhagavantaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘ekāhaṃ, bhante, bhagavantaṃ varaṃ yācāmī’’ti. ‘‘Atikkantavarā kho, gotama, tathāgatā’’ti. ‘‘Yañca, bhante, kappati, yañca anavajja’’nti. ‘‘Vadehi, gotamā’’ti. ‘‘Bhagavati me, bhante, pabbajite anappakaṃ dukkhaṃ ahosi, tathā nande, adhimattaṃ rāhule. Puttapemaṃ, bhante, chaviṃ chindati, chaviṃ chetvā cammaṃ chindati, cammaṃ chetvā maṃsaṃ chindati, maṃsaṃ chetvā nhāruṃ chindati, nhāruṃ chetvā aṭṭhiṃ chindati, aṭṭhiṃ chetvā aṭṭhimiñjaṃ āhacca tiṭṭhati. Sādhu, bhante, ayyā ananuññātaṃ mātāpitūhi puttaṃ na pabbājeyyu’’nti. Atha kho bhagavā suddhodanaṃ sakkaṃ dhammiyā kathāya sandassesi samādapesi samuttejesi sampahaṃsesi. Atha kho suddhodano sakko bhagavatā dhammiyā kathāya sandassito samādapito samuttejito sampahaṃsito uṭṭhāyāsanā bhagavantaṃ abhivādetvā padakkhiṇaṃ katvā pakkāmi. Atha kho bhagavā etasmiṃ nidāne etasmiṃ pakaraṇe dhammiṃ kathaṃ katvā bhikkhū āmantesi – ‘‘na, bhikkhave, ananuññāto mātāpitūhi putto pabbājetabbo. Yo pabbājeyya, āpatti dukkaṭassā’’ti.

Then King Suddhodana approached the Blessed One, paid homage to him, and sat down to one side. Seated to one side, King Suddhodana said to the Blessed One: "Venerable sir, I ask for one boon from the Blessed One." "The Tathāgatas, Gotama, have gone beyond granting boons." "Venerable sir, something that is permissible and blameless." "Speak, Gotama." "Venerable sir, when the Blessed One went forth, I suffered greatly, and so did Nanda, and Rāhula even more. The love for a son, venerable sir, cuts through the skin; having cut through the skin, it cuts through the hide; having cut through the hide, it cuts through the flesh; having cut through the flesh, it cuts through the sinews; having cut through the sinews, it cuts through the bones; having cut through the bones, it reaches the marrow and stays there. It would be good, venerable sir, if the noble ones would not ordain a son without the permission of his parents." Then the Blessed One instructed, inspired, and gladdened King Suddhodana with a Dhamma talk. Having been instructed, inspired, and gladdened by the Blessed One with a Dhamma talk, King Suddhodana rose from his seat, paid homage to the Blessed One, circumambulated him, and departed. Then the Blessed One, on this occasion, having given a Dhamma talk, addressed the monks: "Monks, a son should not be ordained without the permission of his parents. Whoever ordains one, commits an offense of wrongdoing."

Atha kho bhagavā kapilavatthusmiṃ yathābhirantaṃ viharitvā yena sāvatthi tena cārikaṃ pakkāmi. Anupubbena cārikaṃ caramāno yena sāvatthi tadavasari. Tatra sudaṃ bhagavā sāvatthiyaṃ viharati jetavane anāthapiṇḍikassa ārāme. Tena kho pana samayena āyasmato sāriputtassa upaṭṭhākakulaṃ āyasmato sāriputtassa santike dārakaṃ pāhesi – ‘‘imaṃ dārakaṃ thero pabbājetū’’ti. Atha kho āyasmato sāriputtassa etadahosi – ‘‘bhagavatā paññattaṃ ‘na ekena dve sāmaṇerā upaṭṭhāpetabbā’ti. Ayañca me rāhulo sāmaṇero. Kathaṃ nu kho mayā paṭipajjitabba’’nti? Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesi. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, byattena bhikkhunā paṭibalena ekena dve sāmaṇere upaṭṭhāpetuṃ, yāvatake vā pana ussahati ovadituṃ anusāsituṃ tāvatake upaṭṭhāpetunti.

Then the Blessed One, having stayed at Kapilavatthu as long as he pleased, set out on tour toward Sāvatthī. Traveling stage by stage, he arrived at Sāvatthī. There the Blessed One stayed in Jeta's Grove, Anāthapiṇḍika's monastery. Now at that time, the family supporting Venerable Sāriputta sent a boy to Venerable Sāriputta, saying, "Let the venerable one ordain this boy." Then Venerable Sāriputta thought: "The Blessed One has laid down a rule that 'two novices should not be supported by one monk.' And this Rāhula is my novice. How should I proceed?" He reported the matter to the Blessed One. "I allow, monks, a competent monk to support two novices, or as many as he is able to instruct and advise."

Rāhulavatthu niṭṭhitaṃ.

The story of Rāhula is finished.

### 42. Sikkhāpadakathā ^42

> [!TIP]- Links to [[mv1-brahmali-pali#^42|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch14|BMC Chapter 14]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-MV1.42" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


42.The Exposition on the Training Rules

106. Atha kho sāmaṇerānaṃ etadahosi – ‘‘kati nu kho amhākaṃ sikkhāpadāni, kattha ca amhehi sikkhitabba’’nti? Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ…pe… anujānāmi, bhikkhave, sāmaṇerānaṃ dasa sikkhāpadāni, tesu ca sāmaṇerehi sikkhituṃ – pāṇātipātā veramaṇī [veramaṇi, veramaṇiṃ (ka.)], adinnādānā veramaṇī, abrahmacariyā veramaṇī, musāvādā veramaṇī, surāmerayamajjapamādaṭṭhānā veramaṇī, vikālabhojanā veramaṇī, naccagītavāditavisūkadassanā veramaṇī, mālāgandhavilepanadhāraṇamaṇḍanavibhūsanaṭṭhānā veramaṇī, uccāsayanamahāsayanā veramaṇī, jātarūparajatapaṭiggahaṇā veramaṇī. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, sāmaṇerānaṃ imāni dasa sikkhāpadāni, imesu ca sāmaṇerehi sikkhitunti.

106.Then it occurred to the novices: “How many training rules do we have, and in what should we train?” They reported this matter to the Blessed One. … “I allow, bhikkhus, ten training rules for novices, and in these the novices should train: abstaining from the destruction of life, abstaining from taking what is not given, abstaining from unchastity, abstaining from false speech, abstaining from distilled and fermented liquors that are the basis for heedlessness, abstaining from untimely meals, abstaining from dancing, singing, music, and unseemly shows, abstaining from wearing garlands, using perfumes, and beautifying oneself with adornments, abstaining from high and luxurious beds and seats, abstaining from accepting gold and silver. I allow, bhikkhus, these ten training rules for novices, and in these the novices should train.”

Sikkhāpadakathā niṭṭhitā.

The Exposition of the Training Rules is concluded.

### 43. Daṇḍakammavatthu ^43

> [!TIP]- Links to [[mv1-brahmali-pali#^43|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch14|BMC Chapter 14]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-MV1.43" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


43.The Case of Disciplinary Action

107. Tena kho pana samayena sāmaṇerā bhikkhūsu agāravā appatissā asabhāgavuttikā viharanti. Bhikkhū ujjhāyanti khiyyanti vipācenti – ‘‘kathañhi nāma sāmaṇerā bhikkhūsu agāravā appatissā asabhāgavuttikā viharissantī’’ti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ…pe… anujānāmi, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatassa sāmaṇerassa daṇḍakammaṃ kātuṃ. Bhikkhūnaṃ alābhāya parisakkati, bhikkhūnaṃ anatthāya parisakkati, bhikkhūnaṃ avāsāya parisakkati, bhikkhū akkosati paribhāsati, bhikkhū bhikkhūhi bhedeti – anujānāmi, bhikkhave, imehi pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatassa sāmaṇerassa daṇḍakammaṃ kātunti.

107.Now at that time, the novices were living without respect or deference toward the bhikkhus, behaving in a way that was not harmonious. The bhikkhus complained, murmured, and became indignant: “How can these novices live without respect or deference toward the bhikkhus, behaving in a way that is not harmonious?” They reported this matter to the Blessed One… “I allow, bhikkhus, to impose disciplinary action on a novice endowed with five qualities: he strives for the bhikkhus' disadvantage, he strives for the bhikkhus' harm, he strives for the bhikkhus' expulsion, he insults and abuses the bhikkhus, he creates dissension among the bhikkhus. I allow, bhikkhus, to impose disciplinary action on a novice endowed with these five qualities.”

Atha kho bhikkhūnaṃ etadahosi – ‘‘kiṃ nu kho daṇḍakammaṃ kātabba’’nti? Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, āvaraṇaṃ kātunti.

Then it occurred to the bhikkhus: “What kind of disciplinary action should be imposed?” They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “I allow, bhikkhus, to impose a restriction.”

Tena kho pana samayena bhikkhū sāmaṇerānaṃ sabbaṃ saṅghārāmaṃ āvaraṇaṃ karonti. Sāmaṇerā ārāmaṃ pavisituṃ alabhamānā pakkamantipi, vibbhamantipi, titthiyesupi saṅkamanti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Na, bhikkhave, sabbo saṅghārāmo āvaraṇaṃ kātabbo. Yo kareyya, āpatti dukkaṭassa. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, yattha vā vasati, yattha vā paṭikkamati, tattha āvaraṇaṃ kātunti.

Now at that time, the bhikkhus were making the entire monastery off-limits to the novices. The novices, being unable to enter the monastery, either departed, wandered away, or even went over to other sects. They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Bhikkhus, the entire monastery should not be made off-limits. Whoever should do so, there is an offense of wrong-doing. I allow, bhikkhus, to make off-limits the place where he dwells or where he frequents.”

Tena kho pana samayena bhikkhū sāmaṇerānaṃ mukhadvārikaṃ āhāraṃ āvaraṇaṃ karonti. Manussā yāgupānampi saṅghabhattampi karontā sāmaṇere evaṃ vadenti – ‘‘etha, bhante, yāguṃ pivatha; etha, bhante, bhattaṃ bhuñjathā’’ti. Sāmaṇerā evaṃ vadenti – ‘‘nāvuso, labbhā. Bhikkhūhi āvaraṇaṃ kata’’nti. Manussā ujjhāyanti khiyyanti vipācenti – ‘‘kathañhi nāma bhadantā sāmaṇerānaṃ mukhadvārikaṃ āhāraṃ āvaraṇaṃ karissantī’’ti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Na, bhikkhave, mukhadvāriko āhāro āvaraṇaṃ kātabbo. Yo kareyya, āpatti dukkaṭassāti.

Now at that time, the bhikkhus were imposing a restriction on the novices' mouth-door food. People, when preparing rice-gruel or a Sangha-meal, would say to the novices: “Come, venerable ones, drink rice-gruel; come, venerable ones, eat the meal.” The novices would say: “Friends, it is not allowed. A restriction has been imposed by the bhikkhus.” People complained, murmured, and became indignant: “How can these venerable ones impose a restriction on the novices' mouth-door food?” They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Bhikkhus, mouth-door food should not be restricted. Whoever should do so, there is an offense of wrong-doing.”

Daṇḍakammavatthu niṭṭhitaṃ.

The Account of Disciplinary Action is concluded.

### 44. Anāpucchāvaraṇavatthu ^44

> [!TIP]- Links to [[mv1-brahmali-pali#^44|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch14|BMC Chapter 14]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-MV1.44" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


44.The Account of Restriction Without Asking

108. Tena kho pana samayena chabbaggiyā bhikkhū upajjhāye anāpucchā sāmaṇerānaṃ āvaraṇaṃ karonti. Upajjhāyā gavesanti – kathaṃ [kahaṃ (ka.)] nu kho amhākaṃ sāmaṇerā na dissantīti. Bhikkhū evamāhaṃsu – ‘‘chabbaggiyehi, āvuso, bhikkhūhi āvaraṇaṃ kata’’nti. Upajjhāyā ujjhāyanti khiyyanti vipācenti – ‘‘kathañhi nāma chabbaggiyā bhikkhū amhe anāpucchā amhākaṃ sāmaṇerānaṃ āvaraṇaṃ karissantī’’ti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Na, bhikkhave, upajjhāye anāpucchā āvaraṇaṃ kātabbaṃ. Yo kareyya, āpatti dukkaṭassāti.

108.Now at that time, the bhikkhus of the group of six, without asking their preceptors, were imposing restrictions on the novices. The preceptors searched, wondering, “Why are our novices not to be seen?” The bhikkhus said, “Friends, the bhikkhus of the group of six have imposed a restriction.” The preceptors complained, murmured, and became indignant: “How can the bhikkhus of the group of six, without asking us, impose restrictions on our novices?” They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Bhikkhus, a restriction should not be imposed without asking the preceptor. Whoever should do so, there is an offense of wrong-doing.”

Anāpucchāvaraṇavatthu niṭṭhitaṃ.

The Account of Restriction Without Asking is concluded.

### 45. Apalāḷanavatthu ^45

> [!TIP]- Links to [[mv1-brahmali-pali#^45|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch14|BMC Chapter 14]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-MV1.45" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


45.The Case of Coaxing

Tena kho pana samayena chabbaggiyā bhikkhū therānaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ sāmaṇere apalāḷenti. Therā sāmaṃ dantakaṭṭhampi mukhodakampi gaṇhantā kilamanti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Na, bhikkhave, aññassa parisā apalāḷetabbā. Yo apalāḷeyya, āpatti dukkaṭassā ti.

Now at that time the group-of-six monks enticed away the novices of the elder monks. The elders, fetching tooth sticks and mouthwash themselves, grew tired. They reported the matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, another’s following should not be enticed away. Whoever does so incurs an offense of wrong-doing.”

Apalāḷanavatthu niṭṭhitaṃ.

The Case of Coaxing is concluded.

### 46. Kaṇṭakasāmaṇeravatthu ^46

> [!TIP]- Links to [[mv1-brahmali-pali#^46|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch14|BMC Chapter 14]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-MV1.46" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


46.The Case of the Novice Kaṇṭaka

Tena kho pana samayena āyasmato upanandassa sakyaputtassa kaṇṭako nāma sāmaṇero kaṇṭakiṃ nāma bhikkhuniṃ dūsesi. Bhikkhū ujjhāyanti khiyyanti vipācenti – ‘‘kathañhi nāma sāmaṇero evarūpaṃ anācāraṃ ācarissatī’’ti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, dasahaṅgehi samannāgataṃ sāmaṇeraṃ nāsetuṃ. Pāṇātipātī hoti, adinnādāyī hoti, abrahmacārī hoti, musāvādī hoti, majjapāyī hoti, buddhassa avaṇṇaṃ bhāsati, dhammassa avaṇṇaṃ bhāsati, saṅghassa avaṇṇaṃ bhāsati, micchādiṭṭhiko hoti, bhikkhunidūsako hoti – anujānāmi, bhikkhave, imehi dasahaṅgehi samannāgataṃ sāmaṇeraṃ nāsetunti.

Now at that time a novice named Kaṇṭaka, belonging to Venerable Upananda the Sakyan, defiled a nun named Kaṇṭakī. The monks complained, criticized, and protested, “How can a novice engage in such improper conduct?” They reported the matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, I allow the expulsion of a novice possessing ten qualities: he takes life, he takes what is not given, he is unchaste, he is a liar, he drinks alcohol, he speaks dispraise of the Buddha, the Dhamma, and the Saṅgha, he holds wrong view, and he defiles nuns. Monks, I allow the expulsion of a novice possessing these ten qualities.”

### 47. Paṇḍakavatthu ^47

> [!TIP]- Links to [[mv1-brahmali-pali#^47|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch14|BMC Chapter 14]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-MV1.47" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


47.The Case of the Eunuch

109. Tena kho pana samayena aññataro paṇḍako bhikkhūsu pabbajito hoti. So dahare dahare bhikkhū upasaṅkamitvā evaṃ vadeti – ‘‘etha, maṃ āyasmanto dūsethā’’ti. Bhikkhū apasādenti – ‘‘nassa, paṇḍaka, vinassa, paṇḍaka, ko tayā attho’’ti. So bhikkhūhi apasādito mahante mahante moḷigalle sāmaṇere upasaṅkamitvā evaṃ vadeti – ‘‘etha, maṃ āvuso dūsethā’’ti. Sāmaṇerā apasādenti – ‘‘nassa, paṇḍaka, vinassa, paṇḍaka, ko tayā attho’’ti. So sāmaṇerehi apasādito hatthibhaṇḍe assabhaṇḍe upasaṅkamitvā evaṃ vadeti – ‘‘etha, maṃ, āvuso, dūsethā’’ti. Hatthibhaṇḍā assabhaṇḍā dūsesuṃ. Te ujjhāyanti khiyyanti vipācenti – ‘‘paṇḍakā ime samaṇā sakyaputtiyā. Yepi imesaṃ na paṇḍakā, tepi ime paṇḍake dūsenti. Evaṃ ime sabbeva abrahmacārino’’ti. Assosuṃ kho bhikkhū tesaṃ hatthibhaṇḍānaṃ assabhaṇḍānaṃ ujjhāyantānaṃ khiyyantānaṃ vipācentānaṃ. Atha kho te bhikkhū bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Paṇḍako, bhikkhave, anupasampanno na upasampādetabbo, upasampanno nāsetabboti.

109.Now at that time a certain eunuch had gone forth among the monks. He approached very young monks and said, “Come, venerables, defile me.” The monks rejected him, “Get lost, eunuch, perish, eunuch, what use are you?” Rejected by the monks, he then approached large, well-built novices and said, “Come, friends, defile me.” The novices rejected him, “Get lost, eunuch, perish, eunuch, what use are you?” Rejected by the novices, he then approached elephant keepers and horse keepers and said, “Come, friends, defile me.” The elephant keepers and horse keepers defiled him. They complained, criticized, and protested, “These Sakyan ascetics are eunuchs. Even those among them who are not eunuchs defile eunuchs. Thus, they are all unchaste.” The monks heard the complaints of the elephant keepers and horse keepers. Then those monks reported the matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, a eunuch who has not been ordained should not be ordained; one who has been ordained should be expelled.”

### 48. Theyyasaṃvāsakavatthu ^48

> [!TIP]- Links to [[mv1-brahmali-pali#^48|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch14|BMC Chapter 14]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-MV1.48" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


48.The Case of the Thief-Dweller

110. Tena kho pana samayena aññataro purāṇakulaputto khīṇakolañño sukhumālo hoti. Atha kho tassa purāṇakulaputtassa khīṇakolaññassa etadahosi – ‘‘ahaṃ kho sukhumālo, na paṭibalo anadhigataṃ vā bhogaṃ adhigantuṃ, adhigataṃ vā bhogaṃ phātiṃ kātuṃ. Kena nu kho ahaṃ upāyena sukhañca jīveyyaṃ, na ca kilameyya’’nti? Atha kho tassa purāṇakulaputtassa khīṇakolaññassa etadahosi – ‘‘ime kho samaṇā sakyaputtiyā sukhasīlā sukhasamācārā, subhojanāni bhuñjitvā nivātesu sayanesu sayanti. Yaṃnūnāhaṃ sāmaṃ pattacīvaraṃ paṭiyādetvā kesamassuṃ ohāretvā kāsāyāni vatthāni acchādetvā ārāmaṃ gantvā bhikkhūhi saddhiṃ saṃvaseyya’’nti. Atha kho so purāṇakulaputto khīṇakolañño sāmaṃ pattacīvaraṃ paṭiyādetvā kesamassuṃ ohāretvā kāsāyāni vatthāni acchādetvā ārāmaṃ gantvā bhikkhū abhivādeti. Bhikkhū evamāhaṃsu – ‘‘kativassosi tvaṃ, āvuso’’ti? Kiṃ etaṃ, āvuso, kativasso nāmāti? Ko pana te, āvuso, upajjhāyoti? Kiṃ etaṃ, āvuso, upajjhāyo nāmāti? Bhikkhū āyasmantaṃ upāliṃ etadavocuṃ – ‘‘iṅghāvuso upāli, imaṃ pabbajitaṃ anuyuñjāhī’’ti. Atha kho so purāṇakulaputto khīṇakolañño āyasmatā upālinā anuyuñjiyamāno etamatthaṃ ārocesi. Āyasmā upāli bhikkhūnaṃ etamatthaṃ ārocesi. Bhikkhū bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Theyyasaṃvāsako, bhikkhave, anupasampanno na upasampādetabbo, upasampanno nāsetabboti. Titthiyapakkantako, bhikkhave, anupasampanno na upasampādetabbo, upasampanno nāsetabboti.

110.Now at that time a certain clansman of an old family, whose family had declined, was accustomed to luxury. Then it occurred to that clansman of an old family, whose family had declined: “I am accustomed to luxury, not capable of acquiring unacquired wealth or increasing acquired wealth. By what means could I live happily without exertion?” Then it occurred to that clansman of an old family, whose family had declined: “These ascetics, the Sakyan sons, are easy in their habits and conduct; having eaten delicious meals, they sleep in sheltered resting places. Why don’t I myself prepare a bowl and robes, shave off my hair and beard, put on ochre robes, go to the monastery, and live with the monks?” Then that clansman of an old family, whose family had declined, prepared a bowl and robes himself, shaved off his hair and beard, put on ochre robes, went to the monastery, and paid homage to the monks. The monks said to him: “How many years [ordained] are you, friend?” “What is this, friend, called ‘how many years [ordained]’?” “Then who is your preceptor, friend?” “What is this, friend, called ‘preceptor’?” The monks said to Venerable Upāli: “Come, friend Upāli, investigate this one who has gone forth.” Then that clansman of an old family, whose family had declined, being investigated by Venerable Upāli, explained the matter. Venerable Upāli informed the monks of the matter. The monks reported the matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, a thief-dweller who has not been ordained should not be ordained; one who has been ordained should be expelled. Monks, one who has deserted to another sect who has not been ordained should not be ordained; one who has been ordained should be expelled.”

### 49. Tiracchānagatavatthu ^49

> [!TIP]- Links to [[mv1-brahmali-pali#^49|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch14|BMC Chapter 14]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-MV1.49" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


49.The Account of One Born as an Animal

111. Tena kho pana samayena aññataro nāgo nāgayoniyā aṭṭīyati harāyati jigucchati. Atha kho tassa nāgassa etadahosi – ‘‘kena nu kho ahaṃ upāyena nāgayoniyā ca parimucceyyaṃ khippañca manussattaṃ paṭilabheyya’’nti. Atha kho tassa nāgassa etadahosi – ‘‘ime kho samaṇā sakyaputtiyā dhammacārino samacārino brahmacārino saccavādino sīlavanto kalyāṇadhammā. Sace kho ahaṃ samaṇesu sakyaputtiyesu pabbajeyyaṃ, evāhaṃ nāgayoniyā ca parimucceyyaṃ, khippañca manussattaṃ paṭilabheyya’’nti. Atha kho so nāgo māṇavakavaṇṇena bhikkhū upasaṅkamitvā pabbajjaṃ yāci. Taṃ bhikkhū pabbājesuṃ, upasampādesuṃ. Tena kho pana samayena so nāgo aññatarena bhikkhunā saddhiṃ paccantime vihāre paṭivasati. Atha kho so bhikkhu rattiyā paccūsasamayaṃ paccuṭṭhāya ajjhokāse caṅkamati. Atha kho so nāgo tassa bhikkhuno nikkhante vissaṭṭho niddaṃ okkami. Sabbo vihāro ahinā puṇṇo, vātapānehi bhogā nikkhantā honti. Atha kho so bhikkhu vihāraṃ pavisissāmīti kavāṭaṃ paṇāmento addasa sabbaṃ vihāraṃ ahinā puṇṇaṃ, vātapānehi bhoge nikkhante, disvāna bhīto vissaramakāsi. Bhikkhū upadhāvitvā taṃ bhikkhuṃ etadavocuṃ – ‘‘kissa tvaṃ, āvuso, vissaramakāsī’’ti? ‘‘Ayaṃ, āvuso, sabbo vihāro ahinā puṇṇo, vātapānehi bhogā nikkhantā’’ti. Atha kho so nāgo tena saddena paṭibujjhitvā sake āsane nisīdi. Bhikkhū evamāhaṃsu – ‘‘kosi tvaṃ, āvuso’’ti? ‘‘Ahaṃ, bhante, nāgo’’ti. ‘‘Kissa pana tvaṃ, āvuso, evarūpaṃ akāsī’’ti? Atha kho so nāgo bhikkhūnaṃ etamatthaṃ ārocesi. Bhikkhū bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Atha kho bhagavā etasmiṃ nidāne etasmiṃ pakaraṇe bhikkhusaṅghaṃ sannipātāpetvā taṃ nāgaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘tumhe khottha nāgā aviruḷhidhammā imasmiṃ dhammavinaye. Gaccha tvaṃ, nāga, tattheva cātuddase pannarase aṭṭhamiyā ca pakkhassa uposathaṃ upavasa, evaṃ tvaṃ nāgayoniyā ca parimuccissasi, khippañca manussattaṃ paṭilabhissasī’’ti. Atha kho so nāgo aviruḷhidhammo kirāhaṃ imasmiṃ dhammavinayeti dukkhī dummano assūni pavattayamāno vissaraṃ katvā pakkāmi. Atha kho bhagavā bhikkhū āmantesi – ‘‘dveme, bhikkhave, paccayā nāgassa sabhāvapātukammāya. Yadā ca sajātiyā methunaṃ dhammaṃ paṭisevati, yadā ca vissaṭṭho niddaṃ okkamati – ime kho, bhikkhave, dve paccayā nāgassa sabhāvapātukammāya. Tiracchānagato, bhikkhave, anupasampanno na upasampādetabbo, upasampanno nāsetabbo’’ti.

111.Now at that time, a certain nāga was distressed, ashamed, and disgusted with his nāga existence. Then it occurred to that nāga: "By what means could I be freed from this nāga existence and quickly attain human birth?" Then it occurred to that nāga: "These ascetics, the Sons of the Sakyans, are righteous in conduct, harmonious in conduct, living the holy life, truthful, virtuous, and of good character. If I were to go forth among the ascetics, the Sons of the Sakyans, I might be freed from this nāga existence and quickly attain human birth." Then that nāga, in the guise of a young man, approached the monks and requested ordination. The monks ordained him and gave him the full ordination. Now at that time, that nāga was dwelling in a remote monastery together with a certain monk. Then that monk, having risen at dawn, was walking back and forth in the open air. Then, when that monk had departed, the nāga, having relaxed, fell into deep sleep. The entire monastery was filled with a snake, its coils protruding through the windows. Then that monk, thinking, "I will enter the monastery," pushed open the door and saw the entire monastery filled with a snake, its coils protruding through the windows. Seeing this, terrified, he made a loud, unseemly noise. The monks came running and said to that monk, "Why did you make a loud, unseemly noise, friend?" "Friend, this entire monastery is filled with a snake, its coils protruding through the windows!" Then that nāga, awakened by the noise, sat down in his own seat. The monks asked, "Who are you, friend?" "I am a nāga, venerable sir." "But why, friend, did you do such a thing?" Then that nāga explained the matter to the monks. The monks reported the matter to the Blessed One. Then the Blessed One, having assembled the Sangha of monks on this occasion, addressed that nāga: "You nāgas are incapable of growth in this Dhamma and Discipline. Go, nāga, observe the Uposatha there on the fourteenth, fifteenth, and eighth day of the fortnight. Thus you will be freed from this nāga existence and quickly attain human birth." Then that nāga, thinking, "I am indeed incapable of growth in this Dhamma and Discipline," sorrowful and distressed, shedding tears, made a loud, unseemly noise and departed. Then the Blessed One addressed the monks: "Monks, there are two conditions for a nāga’s true nature to be revealed: when he engages in sexual intercourse with his own kind, and when he is relaxed and falls into deep sleep. These are the two conditions for a nāga’s true nature to be revealed. Monks, one born as an animal, being unordained, should not be given the full ordination; if ordained, he should be expelled."

### 50. Mātughātakavatthu ^50

> [!TIP]- Links to [[mv1-brahmali-pali#^50|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch14|BMC Chapter 14]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-MV1.50" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


50.The Account of Matricide

112. Tena kho pana samayena aññataro māṇavako mātaraṃ jīvitā voropesi. So tena pāpakena kammena aṭṭīyati harāyati jigucchati. Atha kho tassa māṇavakassa etadahosi – ‘‘kena nu kho ahaṃ upāyena imassa pāpakassa kammassa nikkhantiṃ kareyya’’nti? Atha kho tassa māṇavakassa etadahosi – ‘‘ime kho samaṇā sakyaputtiyā dhammacārino samacārino brahmacārino saccavādino sīlavanto kalyāṇadhammā. Sace kho ahaṃ samaṇesu sakyaputtiyesu pabbajeyyaṃ, evāhaṃ imassa pāpakassa kammassa nikkhantiṃ kareyya’’nti. Atha kho so māṇavako bhikkhū upasaṅkamitvā pabbajjaṃ yāci. Bhikkhū āyasmantaṃ upāliṃ etadavocuṃ – ‘‘pubbepi kho, āvuso upāli, nāgo māṇavakavaṇṇena bhikkhūsu pabbajito. Iṅghāvuso upāli, imaṃ māṇavakaṃ anuyuñjāhī’’ti. Atha kho so māṇavako āyasmatā upālinā anuyuñjīyamāno etamatthaṃ ārocesi. Āyasmā upāli bhikkhūnaṃ etamatthaṃ ārocesi. Bhikkhū bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ…pe… mātughātako, bhikkhave, anupasampanno na upasampādetabbo, upasampanno nāsetabboti.

112.Now at that time, a certain young man deprived his mother of life. He was troubled, distressed, and disgusted by that evil deed. Then it occurred to him: "By what means could I make an expiation for this evil deed?" Then it occurred to him: "These ascetics, the Sons of the Sakyans, are practitioners of the Dhamma, practitioners of righteous conduct, practitioners of the holy life, truthful, virtuous, and of good character. If I were to go forth among the ascetics, the Sons of the Sakyans, I could make an expiation for this evil deed." Then that young man approached the monks and requested ordination. The monks said to Venerable Upāli: "Friend Upāli, in the past, a nāga went forth among the monks in the guise of a young man. Come, friend Upāli, question this young man." Then, being questioned by Venerable Upāli, that young man disclosed the matter. Venerable Upāli reported the matter to the monks. The monks reported the matter to the Blessed One… "Monks, a matricide, being unordained, should not be given the full ordination; if ordained, he should be expelled."

### 51. Pitughātakavatthu ^51

> [!TIP]- Links to [[mv1-brahmali-pali#^51|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch14|BMC Chapter 14]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-MV1.51" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


51.The Case of Patricide

113. Tena kho pana samayena aññataro māṇavako pitaraṃ jīvitā voropesi. So tena pāpakena kammena aṭṭīyati harāyati jigucchati. Atha kho tassa māṇavakassa etadahosi ‘‘kena nu kho ahaṃ upāyena imassa pāpakassa kammassa nikkhantiṃ kareyya’’nti. Atha kho tassa māṇavakassa etadahosi ‘‘ime kho samaṇā sakyaputtiyā dhammacārino samacārino brahmacārino saccavādino sīlavanto kalyāṇadhammā, sace kho ahaṃ samaṇesu sakyaputtiyesu pabbajeyyaṃ, evāhaṃ imassa pāpakassa kammassa nikkhantiṃ kareyya’’nti. Atha kho so māṇavako bhikkhū upasaṅkamitvā pabbajjaṃ yāci. Bhikkhū āyasmantaṃ upāliṃ etadavocuṃ – ‘‘pubbepi kho, āvuso upāli, nāgo māṇavakavaṇṇena bhikkhūsu pabbajito, iṅghāvuso, upāli, imaṃ māṇavakaṃ anuyuñjāhī’’ti. Atha kho so māṇavako āyasmatā upālinā anuyuñjīyamāno etamatthaṃ ārocesi. Āyasmā upāli bhikkhūnaṃ etamatthaṃ ārocesi. Bhikkhū bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Pitughātako, bhikkhave, anupasampanno na upasampādetabbo, upasampanno nāsetabboti.

113.At that time, a certain young man deprived his father of life. He was troubled, ashamed, and disgusted by that evil deed. Then it occurred to the young man: "By what means could I make amends for this evil deed?" Then it occurred to the young man: "These recluses, the Sakyan sons, are practitioners of the Dhamma, of even conduct, followers of the holy life, truthful, virtuous, and of good qualities. If I were to go forth among the recluses, the Sakyan sons, I could make amends for this evil deed." Then that young man approached the bhikkhus and requested ordination. The bhikkhus said to Venerable Upāli: "Friend Upāli, in the past a Nāga also went forth among the bhikkhus in the guise of a young man. Come, friend Upāli, question this young man." Then, being questioned by Venerable Upāli, that young man disclosed the matter. Venerable Upāli reported the matter to the bhikkhus. The bhikkhus reported the matter to the Blessed One. "Bhikkhus, a patricide, being unordained, should not be given the higher ordination; if he has been ordained, he should be expelled."

### 52. Arahantaghātakavatthu ^52

> [!TIP]- Links to [[mv1-brahmali-pali#^52|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch14|BMC Chapter 14]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-MV1.52" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


52.The Case of the Slayer of an Arahant

114. Tena kho pana samayena sambahulā bhikkhū sāketā sāvatthiṃ addhānamaggappaṭipannā honti. Antarāmagge corā nikkhamitvā ekacce bhikkhū acchindiṃsu, ekacce bhikkhū haniṃsu. Sāvatthiyā rājabhaṭā nikkhamitvā ekacce core aggahesuṃ, ekacce corā palāyiṃsu. Ye te palāyiṃsu te bhikkhūsu pabbajiṃsu, ye te gahitā te vadhāya oniyyanti. Addasaṃsu kho te palāyitvā pabbajitā te core vadhāya oniyyamāne, disvāna evamāhaṃsu – ‘‘sādhu kho mayaṃ palāyimhā, sacā ca [sace ca, sacajja (aṭṭhakathāyaṃ pāṭhantarā)] mayaṃ gayheyyāma [gaṇheyyāma (ka.)], mayampi evameva haññeyyāmā’’ti. Bhikkhū evamāhaṃsu – ‘‘kiṃ pana tumhe, āvuso, akatthā’’ti? Atha kho te pabbajitā bhikkhūnaṃ etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Bhikkhū bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Arahanto ete, bhikkhave, bhikkhū. Arahantaghātako, bhikkhave, anupasampanno na upasampādetabbo, upasampanno nāsetabboti.

114.At that time, a number of bhikkhus were traveling on the road from Sāketa to Sāvatthī. Along the way, bandits emerged and robbed some bhikkhus, and killed others. Royal officers from Sāvatthī went out and captured some of the bandits, while others fled. Those who fled then went forth among the bhikkhus, while those who were captured were being led away for execution. Those who had fled and gone forth saw those bandits being led away for execution, and having seen them, said: "It is good that we fled, for if we had been captured, we too would be killed in this way." The bhikkhus said to them, "What is this that you have done, friends?" Then those who had gone forth reported this matter to the bhikkhus. The bhikkhus reported this matter to the Blessed One. "Bhikkhus, these bhikkhus are arahants. Bhikkhus, one who has killed an arahant, being unordained, should not be given the higher ordination; if he has been ordained, he should be expelled."

### 53. Bhikkhunīdūsakavatthu ^53

> [!TIP]- Links to [[mv1-brahmali-pali#^53|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch14|BMC Chapter 14]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-MV1.53" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


53.The Case of a Bhikkhuni's Abuser

115. Tena kho pana samayena sambahulā bhikkhuniyo sāketā sāvatthiṃ addhānamaggappaṭipannā honti. Antarāmagge corā nikkhamitvā ekaccā bhikkhuniyo acchindiṃsu, ekaccā bhikkhuniyo dūsesuṃ. Sāvatthiyā rājabhaṭā nikkhamitvā ekacce core aggahesuṃ, ekacce corā palāyiṃsu. Ye te palāyiṃsu, te bhikkhūsu pabbajiṃsu. Ye te gahitā, te vadhāya oniyyanti. Addasaṃsu kho te palāyitvā pabbajitā te core vadhāya oniyyamāne, disvāna evamāhaṃsu ‘‘sādhu kho mayaṃ palāyimhā, sacā ca mayaṃ gayheyyāma, mayampi evameva haññeyyāmā’’ti. Bhikkhū evamāhaṃsu ‘‘kiṃ pana tumhe, āvuso, akatthā’’ti. Atha kho te pabbajitā bhikkhūnaṃ etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Bhikkhū bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Bhikkhunidūsako, bhikkhave, anupasampanno na upasampādetabbo, upasampanno nāsetabboti. Saṅghabhedako, bhikkhave, anupasampanno na upasampādetabbo, upasampanno nāsetabboti. Lohituppādako, bhikkhave, anupasampanno na upasampādetabbo, upasampanno nāsetabboti.

115.At that time, a number of bhikkhunis were traveling on the road from Sāketa to Sāvatthī. On the way, bandits emerged and robbed some bhikkhunis, and violated others. Royal officers from Sāvatthī went out and captured some of the bandits, while others fled. Those who fled then went forth among the bhikkhus. Those who were captured were being led away for execution. Those who had fled and gone forth saw those bandits being led away for execution, and having seen them, said: "It is good that we fled, for if we had been captured, we too would be killed in this way." The bhikkhus said to them, "What is this that you have done, friends?" Then those who had gone forth reported this matter to the bhikkhus. The bhikkhus reported this matter to the Blessed One. "Bhikkhus, one who has violated a bhikkhuni, being unordained, should not be given the higher ordination; if he has been ordained, he should be expelled. Bhikkhus, one who has created a schism in the Sangha, being unordained, should not be given the higher ordination; if he has been ordained, he should be expelled. Bhikkhus, one who has drawn blood from a Tathāgata, being unordained, should not be given the higher ordination; if he has been ordained, he should be expelled."

### 54. Ubhatobyañjanakavatthu ^54

> [!TIP]- Links to [[mv1-brahmali-pali#^54|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch14|BMC Chapter 14]] and the following cites:

> ```query
