> ```


54.The Case of the Hermaphrodite

116. Tena kho pana samayena aññataro ubhatobyañjanako bhikkhūsu pabbajito hoti. So karotipi kārāpetipi. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Ubhatobyañjanako, bhikkhave, anupasampanno na upasampādetabbo, upasampanno nāsetabboti.

116.At that time, a certain hermaphrodite had gone forth among the bhikkhus. He both performed (sexual acts) and had them performed (on him). They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, a hermaphrodite who has not been given the higher ordination should not be given the higher ordination. If he has been given the higher ordination, he is to be expelled.”

### 55. Anupajjhāyakādivatthūni ^55

> [!TIP]- Links to [[mv1-brahmali-pali#^55|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch14|BMC Chapter 14]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-MV1.55" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


55.Cases of One Without a Preceptor, and So Forth

117. Tena kho pana samayena bhikkhū anupajjhāyakaṃ upasampādenti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Na, bhikkhave, anupajjhāyako upasampādetabbo. Yo upasampādeyya, āpatti dukkaṭassāti.

117.At that time, bhikkhus were giving the higher ordination to one without a preceptor. They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, one without a preceptor should not be given the higher ordination. Whoever gives the higher ordination (to such a person) incurs an offense of wrong-doing.”

Tena kho pana samayena bhikkhū saṅghena upajjhāyena upasampādenti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Na, bhikkhave, saṅghena upajjhāyena upasampādetabbo. Yo upasampādeyya, āpatti dukkaṭassāti.

At that time, bhikkhus were giving the higher ordination with the Saṅgha as the preceptor. They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, one should not be given the higher ordination with the Saṅgha as the preceptor. Whoever gives the higher ordination (to such a person) incurs an offense of wrong-doing.”

Tena kho pana samayena bhikkhū gaṇena upajjhāyena upasampādenti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Na, bhikkhave, gaṇena upajjhāyena upasampādetabbo. Yo upasampādeyya, āpatti dukkaṭassāti.

At that time, bhikkhus were giving the higher ordination with a group as the preceptor. They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, one should not be given the higher ordination with a group as the preceptor. Whoever gives the higher ordination (to such a person) incurs an offense of wrong-doing.”

Tena kho pana samayena bhikkhū paṇḍakupajjhāyena upasampādenti…pe… theyyasaṃvāsakupajjhāyena upasampādenti…pe… titthiyapakkantakupajjhāyena upasampādenti …pe… tiracchānagatupajjhāyena upasampādenti…pe… mātughātakupajjhāyena upasampādenti…pe… pitughātakupajjhāyena upasampādenti…pe… arahantaghātakupajjhāyena upasampādenti…pe… bhikkhunidūsakupajjhāyena upasampādenti…pe… saṅghabhedakupajjhāyena upasampādenti…pe… lohituppādakupajjhāyena upasampādenti…pe… ubhatobyañjanakupajjhāyena upasampādenti bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Na, bhikkhave, paṇḍakupajjhāyena upasampādetabbo…pe… na, bhikkhave, theyyasaṃvāsakupajjhāyena upasampādetabbo…pe… na, bhikkhave, titthiyapakkantakupajjhāyena upasampādetabbo…pe… na, bhikkhave, tiracchānagatupajjhāyena upasampādetabbo…pe… na, bhikkhave, mātughātakupajjhāyena upasampādetabbo …pe… na, bhikkhave, pitughātakupajjhāyena upasampādetabbo…pe… na, bhikkhave, arahantaghātakupajjhāyena upasampādetabbo…pe… na, bhikkhave, bhikkhunidūsakupajjhāyena upasampādetabbo …pe… na, bhikkhave, saṅghabhedakupajjhāyena upasampādetabbo…pe… na, bhikkhave, lohituppādakupajjhāyena upasampādetabbo…pe… na, bhikkhave, ubhatobyañjanakupajjhāyena upasampādetabbo. Yo upasampādeyya, āpatti dukkaṭassāti.

At that time, bhikkhus were giving the higher ordination with a eunuch as the preceptor … with a thief-monk as the preceptor … with one who had deserted to another sect as the preceptor … with an animal as the preceptor … with a matricide as the preceptor … with a patricide as the preceptor … with a murderer of an arahant as the preceptor … with a defiler of a bhikkhuni as the preceptor … with a schismatic as the preceptor … with one who has shed blood as the preceptor … with a hermaphrodite as the preceptor. They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, one should not be given the higher ordination with a eunuch as the preceptor … with a thief-monk as the preceptor … with one who has deserted to another sect as the preceptor … with an animal as the preceptor … with a matricide as the preceptor … with a patricide as the preceptor … with a murderer of an arahant as the preceptor … with a defiler of a bhikkhuni as the preceptor … with a schismatic as the preceptor … with one who has shed blood as the preceptor … with a hermaphrodite as the preceptor. Whoever gives the higher ordination (to such a person) incurs an offense of wrong-doing.”

### 56. Apattakādivatthu ^56

> [!TIP]- Links to [[mv1-brahmali-pali#^56|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch14|BMC Chapter 14]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-MV1.56" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


56.The Case of One Without a Bowl, and So Forth

118. Tena kho pana samayena bhikkhū apattakaṃ upasampādenti. Hatthesu piṇḍāya caranti. Manussā ujjhāyanti khiyyanti vipācenti – seyyathāpi titthiyāti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Na, bhikkhave, apattako upasampādetabbo. Yo upasampādeyya, āpatti dukkaṭassāti.

118.At that time, bhikkhus were giving the higher ordination to one without a bowl. They wandered for alms with food in their hands. People complained, criticized, and spread it about, saying, “Just like the sectarians!” They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, one without a bowl should not be given the higher ordination. Whoever gives the higher ordination (to such a person) incurs an offense of wrong-doing.”

Tena kho pana samayena bhikkhū acīvarakaṃ upasampādenti. Naggā piṇḍāya caranti. Manussā ujjhāyanti khiyyanti vipācenti – seyyathāpi titthiyāti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Na, bhikkhave, acīvarako upasampādetabbo. Yo upasampādeyya, āpatti dukkaṭassāti.

At that time, bhikkhus were giving the higher ordination to one without robes. They wandered for alms naked. People complained, criticized, and spread it about, saying, “Just like the sectarians!” They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, one without robes should not be given the higher ordination. Whoever gives the higher ordination (to such a person) incurs an offense of wrong-doing.”

Tena kho pana samayena bhikkhū apattacīvarakaṃ upasampādenti. Naggā hatthesu piṇḍāya caranti. Manussā ujjhāyanti khiyyanti vipācenti – seyyathāpi titthiyāti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Na, bhikkhave, apattacīvarako upasampādetabbo. Yo upasampādeyya, āpatti dukkaṭassāti.

At that time, bhikkhus were giving the higher ordination to one without a bowl and robes. They wandered for alms naked with food in their hands. People complained, criticized, and spread it about, saying, “Just like the sectarians!” They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, one without a bowl and robes should not be given the higher ordination. Whoever gives the higher ordination (to such a person) incurs an offense of wrong-doing.”

Tena kho pana samayena bhikkhū yācitakena pattena upasampādenti. Upasampanne pattaṃ paṭiharanti. Hatthesu piṇḍāya caranti. Manussā ujjhāyanti khiyyanti vipācenti – seyyathāpi titthiyāti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Na, bhikkhave, yācitakena pattena upasampādetabbo. Yo upasampādeyya, āpatti dukkaṭassāti.

At that time, bhikkhus were giving the higher ordination with a borrowed bowl. After the higher ordination, they took back the bowl. The newly ordained wandered for alms with food in their hands. People complained, criticized, and spread it about, saying, “Just like the sectarians!” They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, one should not be given the higher ordination with a borrowed bowl. Whoever gives the higher ordination (to such a person) incurs an offense of wrong-doing.”

Tena kho pana samayena bhikkhū yācitakena cīvarena upasampādenti. Upasampanne cīvaraṃ paṭiharanti. Naggā piṇḍāya caranti. Manussā ujjhāyanti khiyyanti vipācenti – seyyathāpi titthiyāti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Na, bhikkhave, yācitakena cīvarena upasampādetabbo. Yo upasampādeyya, āpatti dukkaṭassāti.

At that time, bhikkhus were giving the higher ordination with borrowed robes. After the higher ordination, they took back the robes. The newly ordained wandered for alms naked. People complained, criticized, and spread it about, saying, “Just like the sectarians!” They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, one should not be given the higher ordination with borrowed robes. Whoever gives the higher ordination (to such a person) incurs an offense of wrong-doing.”

Tena kho pana samayena bhikkhū yācitakena pattacīvarena upasampādenti. Upasampanne pattacīvaraṃ paṭiharanti. Naggā hatthesu piṇḍāya caranti. Manussā ujjhāyanti khiyyanti vipācenti – seyyathāpi titthiyāti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Na, bhikkhave, yācitakena pattacīvarena upasampādetabbo. Yo upasampādeyya, āpatti dukkaṭassāti.

At that time, bhikkhus were giving the higher ordination with a borrowed bowl and robes. After the higher ordination, they took back the bowl and robes. The newly ordained wandered for alms naked with food in their hands. People complained, criticized, and spread it about, saying, “Just like the sectarians!” They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, one should not be given the higher ordination with a borrowed bowl and robes. Whoever gives the higher ordination (to such a person) incurs an offense of wrong-doing.”

Naupasampādetabbekavīsativāro niṭṭhito.

The Section on the Twenty-One Grounds for Not Giving the Higher Ordination is Concluded.

### 57. Napabbājetabbadvattiṃsavāro ^57

> [!TIP]- Links to [[mv1-brahmali-pali#^57|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch14|BMC Chapter 14]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-MV1.57" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


57.The Section on the Thirty-two Grounds for Non-Ordination

119. Tena kho pana samayena bhikkhū hatthacchinnaṃ pabbājenti…pe… pādacchinnaṃ pabbājenti…pe… hatthapādacchinnaṃ pabbājenti…pe… kaṇṇacchinnaṃ pabbājenti…pe… nāsacchinnaṃ pabbājenti…pe… kaṇṇanāsacchinnaṃ pabbājenti…pe… aṅgulicchinnaṃ pabbājenti…pe… aḷacchinnaṃ pabbājenti…pe… kaṇḍaracchinnaṃ pabbājenti…pe… phaṇahatthakaṃ pabbājenti…pe… khujjaṃ pabbājenti…pe… vāmanaṃ pabbājenti…pe… galagaṇḍiṃ pabbājenti…pe… lakkhaṇāhataṃ pabbājenti…pe… kasāhataṃ pabbājenti…pe… likhitakaṃ pabbājenti…pe… sīpadiṃ pabbājenti…pe… pāparogiṃ pabbājenti…pe… parisadūsakaṃ pabbājenti…pe… kāṇaṃ pabbājenti…pe… kuṇiṃ pabbājenti…pe… khañjaṃ pabbājenti…pe… pakkhahataṃ pabbājenti…pe… chinniriyāpathaṃ pabbājenti…pe… jarādubbalaṃ pabbājenti…pe… andhaṃ pabbājenti…pe… mūgaṃ pabbājenti…pe… badhiraṃ pabbājenti…pe… andhamūgaṃ pabbājenti…pe… andhabadhiraṃ pabbājenti…pe… mūgabadhiraṃ pabbājenti…pe… andhamūgabadhiraṃ pabbājenti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ…pe… na, bhikkhave, hatthacchinno pabbājetabbo…pe… na, bhikkhave, pādacchinno pabbājetabbo…pe… na, bhikkhave, hatthapādacchinno pabbājetabbo…pe… na, bhikkhave, kaṇṇacchinno pabbājetabbo…pe… na, bhikkhave, nāsacchinno pabbājetabbo…pe… na, bhikkhave, kaṇṇanāsacchinno pabbājetabbo…pe… na, bhikkhave, aṅgulicchinno pabbājetabbo…pe… na, bhikkhave, aḷacchinno pabbājetabbo…pe… na, bhikkhave, kaṇḍaracchinno pabbājetabbo…pe… na, bhikkhave, phaṇahatthako pabbājetabbo…pe… na, bhikkhave, khujjo pabbājetabbo…pe… na, bhikkhave, vāmano pabbājetabbo…pe… na, bhikkhave, galagaṇḍī pabbājetabbo…pe… na, bhikkhave, lakkhaṇāhato pabbājetabbo…pe… na, bhikkhave, kasāhato pabbājetabbo…pe… na, bhikkhave, likhitako pabbājetabbo…pe… na, bhikkhave, sīpadī pabbājetabbo…pe… na, bhikkhave, pāparogī pabbājetabbo…pe… na, bhikkhave, parisadūsako pabbājetabbo…pe… na, bhikkhave, kāṇo pabbājetabbo…pe… na, bhikkhave, kuṇī pabbājetabbo…pe… na, bhikkhave, khañjo pabbājetabbo…pe… na, bhikkhave, pakkhahato pabbājetabbo…pe… na, bhikkhave, chinniriyāpatho pabbājetabbo…pe… na, bhikkhave, jarādubbalo pabbājetabbo…pe… na, bhikkhave, andho pabbājetabbo…pe… na, bhikkhave, mūgo pabbājetabbo…pe… na, bhikkhave, badhiro pabbājetabbo…pe… na, bhikkhave, andhamūgo pabbājetabbo…pe… na, bhikkhave, andhabadhiro pabbājetabbo…pe… na, bhikkhave, mūgabadhiro pabbājetabbo…pe… na, bhikkhave, andhamūgabadhiro pabbājetabbo. Yo pabbājeyya, āpatti dukkaṭassāti.

119.At that time, monks were ordaining those with hands cut off… those with feet cut off… those with both hands and feet cut off… those with ears cut off… those with noses cut off… those with both ears and noses cut off… those with fingers cut off… those with thumbs cut off… those with tendons cut off… those with webbed hands… the hunchbacked… the dwarfed… those with goiters… those branded… those whipped… those tattooed… those with elephantiasis… those with chronic diseases… those who corrupt the Sangha… the one-eyed… the crippled… the lame… the paralyzed… one who crawls on his buttocks… the aged and feeble… the blind… the mute… the deaf… the blind and mute… the blind and deaf… the mute and deaf… the blind, mute, and deaf. They reported this matter to the Blessed One. [He said:] "Monks, one whose hand is cut off should not be ordained… one whose foot is cut off should not be ordained… one whose both hands and feet are cut off should not be ordained… one whose ear is cut off should not be ordained… one whose nose is cut off should not be ordained… one whose both ears and nose are cut off should not be ordained… one whose finger is cut off should not be ordained… one whose thumb is cut off should not be ordained… one whose tendon is cut off should not be ordained… one with webbed hands should not be ordained… the hunchbacked should not be ordained… the dwarfed should not be ordained… one with a goiter should not be ordained… one who is branded should not be ordained… one who is whipped should not be ordained… one who is tattooed should not be ordained… one with elephantiasis should not be ordained… one with a chronic disease should not be ordained… one who corrupts the Sangha should not be ordained… the one-eyed should not be ordained… the crippled should not be ordained… the lame should not be ordained… the paralyzed should not be ordained… one who crawls on his buttocks should not be ordained… the aged and feeble should not be ordained… the blind should not be ordained… the mute should not be ordained… the deaf should not be ordained… the blind and mute should not be ordained… the blind and deaf should not be ordained… the mute and deaf should not be ordained… the blind, mute, and deaf should not be ordained. Whoever ordains them commits an offense of wrong conduct."

Napabbājetabbadvattiṃsavāro niṭṭhito.

The Section on the Thirty-two Grounds for Non-Ordination is completed.

Dāyajjabhāṇavāro niṭṭhito navamo.

The ninth chapter, the Recitation on Inheritance, is completed.

### 58. Alajjīnissayavatthūni ^58

> [!TIP]- Links to [[mv1-brahmali-pali#^58|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch14|BMC Chapter 14]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-MV1.58" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


58.Matters Concerning Dependence on the Shameless

120. Tena kho pana samayena chabbaggiyā bhikkhū alajjīnaṃ nissayaṃ denti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Na, bhikkhave, alajjīnaṃ nissayo dātabbo. Yo dadeyya, āpatti dukkaṭassāti.

120.At that time, the group-of-six monks gave dependence to the shameless. They reported this matter to the Blessed One. [He said:] "Monks, dependence should not be given to the shameless. Whoever gives it commits an offense of wrong conduct."

Tena kho pana samayena bhikkhū alajjīnaṃ nissāya vasanti. Tepi nacirasseva alajjino honti pāpakābhikkhū. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Na, bhikkhave, alajjīnaṃ nissāya vatthabbaṃ. Yo vaseyya, āpatti dukkaṭassāti.

At that time, monks lived in dependence on the shameless. Soon, they too became shameless and bad monks. They reported this matter to the Blessed One. [He said:] "Monks, one should not live in dependence on the shameless. Whoever lives thus commits an offense of wrong conduct."

Atha kho bhikkhūnaṃ etadahosi – ‘‘bhagavatā paññattaṃ ‘na alajjīnaṃ nissayo dātabbo, na alajjīnaṃ nissāya vatthabba’nti. Kathaṃ nu kho mayaṃ jāneyyāma lajjiṃ vā alajjiṃ vā’’ti? Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, catūhapañcāhaṃ āgametuṃ yāva bhikkhusabhāgataṃ jānāmīti.

Then the monks had this thought: "The Blessed One has laid down: 'Dependence should not be given to the shameless, nor should one live in dependence on the shameless.' But how can we know who is scrupulous and who is unscrupulous?" They reported this matter to the Blessed One. [He said:] "I allow, monks, to wait for four or five days until you know the monk's scrupulousness."

### 59. Gamikādinissayavatthūni ^59

> [!TIP]- Links to [[mv1-brahmali-pali#^59|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch14|BMC Chapter 14]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-MV1.59" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


59.Matters Concerning Dependence, Beginning with Travelers

121. Tena kho pana samayena aññataro bhikkhu kosalesu janapade addhānamaggappaṭipanno hoti. Atha kho tassa bhikkhuno etadahosi – ‘‘bhagavatā paññattaṃ ‘na anissitena vatthabba’nti. Ahañcamhi nissayakaraṇīyo addhānamaggappaṭipanno, kathaṃ nu kho mayā paṭipajjitabba’’nti? Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, addhānamaggappaṭipannena bhikkhunā nissayaṃ alabhamānena anissitena vatthunti.

121.At that time, a certain bhikkhu was traveling on a road in the Kosala country. Then it occurred to that bhikkhu: “The Blessed One has laid down, ‘One should not dwell without dependence.’ But I am one who needs to take dependence, and I am traveling on a road. How then should I proceed?” They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, I allow a bhikkhu who is traveling on a road and is unable to obtain dependence to dwell without dependence.”

Tena kho pana samayena dve bhikkhū kosalesu janapade addhānamaggappaṭipannā honti. Te aññataraṃ āvāsaṃ upagacchiṃsu. Tattha eko bhikkhu gilāno hoti. Atha kho tassa gilānassa bhikkhuno etadahosi – ‘‘bhagavatā paññattaṃ ‘na anissitena vatthabba’nti. Ahañcamhi nissayakaraṇīyo gilāno, kathaṃ nu kho mayā paṭipajjitabba’’nti? Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, gilānena bhikkhunā nissayaṃ alabhamānena anissitena vatthunti.

At that time, two bhikkhus were traveling along a road in the Kosala country. They approached a certain monastery. There, one bhikkhu was ill. Then it occurred to that sick bhikkhu: “The Blessed One has laid down, ‘One should not dwell without dependence.’ But I am one who needs to take dependence, and I am ill. How then should I proceed?” They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, I allow a sick bhikkhu who is unable to obtain dependence to dwell without dependence.”

Atha kho tassa gilānupaṭṭhākassa bhikkhuno etadahosi – ‘‘bhagavatā paññattaṃ ‘na anissitena vatthabba’nti. Ahañcamhi nissayakaraṇīyo, ayañca bhikkhu gilāno, kathaṃ nu kho mayā paṭipajjitabba’’nti? Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, gilānupaṭṭhākena bhikkhunā nissayaṃ alabhamānena yāciyamānena anissitena vatthunti.

Then it occurred to the bhikkhu attending to the sick one: “The Blessed One has laid down, ‘One should not dwell without dependence.’ But I am one who needs to take dependence, and this bhikkhu is ill. How then should I proceed?” They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, I allow a bhikkhu attending to a sick one, if he is unable to obtain dependence, to dwell without dependence when requested [by the sick bhikkhu].”

Tena kho pana samayena aññataro bhikkhu araññe viharati. Tassa ca tasmiṃ senāsane phāsu hoti. Atha kho tassa bhikkhuno etadahosi – ‘‘bhagavatā paññattaṃ ‘na anissitena vatthabba’nti. Ahañcamhi nissayakaraṇīyo araññe viharāmi, mayhañca imasmiṃ senāsane phāsu hoti, kathaṃ nu kho mayā paṭipajjitabba’’nti? Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, āraññikena bhikkhunā phāsuvihāraṃ sallakkhentena nissayaṃ alabhamānena anissitena vatthuṃ – yadā patirūpo nissayadāyako āgacchissati, tadā tassa nissāya vasissāmīti.

At that time, a certain bhikkhu was dwelling in the forest. And he was comfortable in that lodging. Then it occurred to that bhikkhu: “The Blessed One has laid down, ‘One should not dwell without dependence.’ But I am one who needs to take dependence, and I dwell in the forest, and I am comfortable in this lodging. How then should I proceed?” They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, I allow a forest-dwelling bhikkhu, assessing his comfortable dwelling and being unable to obtain dependence, to dwell without dependence—thinking, ‘When a suitable preceptor comes, then I will dwell in dependence on that preceptor.’”

### 60. Gottena anussāvanānujānanā ^60

> [!TIP]- Links to [[mv1-brahmali-pali#^60|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch14|BMC Chapter 14]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-MV1.60" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


60.Permission to Announce by Clan Name

122. Tena kho pana samayena āyasmato mahākassapassa upasampadāpekkho hoti. Atha kho āyasmā mahākassapo āyasmato ānandassa santike dūtaṃ pāhesi – āgacchatu ānando imaṃ anussāvessatūti [anussāvessatīti (syā.)]. Āyasmā ānando evamāha – ‘‘nāhaṃ ussahāmi therassa nāmaṃ gahetuṃ, garu me thero’’ti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, gottenapi anussāvetunti.

122.At that time, Venerable Mahākassapa had a candidate for higher ordination. Then Venerable Mahākassapa sent a messenger to Venerable Ānanda, saying, “Let Ānanda come and make the announcement for this one.” Venerable Ānanda replied, “I do not dare to call the elder by name, for the elder is revered by me.” They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, I allow the announcement to be made even by clan name.”

### 61. Dveupasampadāpekkhādivatthu ^61

> [!TIP]- Links to [[mv1-brahmali-pali#^61|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch14|BMC Chapter 14]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-MV1.61" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


61.Matters Concerning Two Candidates for Higher Ordination, and So Forth

123. Tena kho pana samayena āyasmato mahākassapassa dve upasampadāpekkhā honti. Te vivadanti – ahaṃ paṭhamaṃ upasampajjissāmi, ahaṃ paṭhamaṃ upasampajjissāmīti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, dve ekānussāvane kātunti.

123.At that time, Venerable Mahākassapa had two candidates for higher ordination. They argued, “I will receive the higher ordination first!” “I will receive the higher ordination first!” They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, I allow two to be ordained with a single announcement.”

Tena kho pana samayena sambahulānaṃ therānaṃ upasampadāpekkhā honti. Te vivadanti – ahaṃ paṭhamaṃ upasampajjissāmi, ahaṃ paṭhamaṃ upasampajjissāmīti. Therā evamāhaṃsu – ‘‘handa, mayaṃ, āvuso, sabbeva ekānussāvane karomā’’ti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, dve tayo ekānussāvane kātuṃ, tañca kho ekena upajjhāyena, na tveva nānupajjhāyenāti.

At that time, many elders had candidates for higher ordination. They argued, “I will receive the higher ordination first!” “I will receive the higher ordination first!” The elders said, “Come, friends, let us all make a single announcement.” They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, I allow a single announcement to be made for two or three [candidates], but with one preceptor, and certainly not with different preceptors.”

### 62. Gabbhavīsūpasampadānujānanā ^62

> [!TIP]- Links to [[mv1-brahmali-pali#^62|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch14|BMC Chapter 14]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-MV1.62" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


62.Authorization for the Higher Ordination of a Womb-Dweller

124. Tena kho pana samayena āyasmā kumārakassapo gabbhavīso upasampanno ahosi. Atha kho āyasmato kumārakassapassa etadahosi – ‘‘bhagavatā paññattaṃ ‘na ūnavīsativasso puggalo upasampādetabbo’ti. Ahañcamhi gabbhavīso upasampanno. Upasampanno nu khomhi, nanu kho upasampanno’’ti? Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Yaṃ, bhikkhave, mātukucchismiṃ paṭhamaṃ cittaṃ uppannaṃ, paṭhamaṃ viññāṇaṃ pātubhūtaṃ, tadupādāya sāvassa jāti. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, gabbhavīsaṃ upasampādetunti.

124.At that time, Venerable Kumārakassapa had received the higher ordination as a womb-dweller. Then Venerable Kumārakassapa thought: “The Blessed One has laid down the rule: ‘A person under twenty years of age should not be given the higher ordination.’ But I received the higher ordination as a womb-dweller. Have I received the higher ordination, or have I not received it?” They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, the birth of a person is reckoned from the moment the first thought arises in the mother’s womb, when the first consciousness appears. I allow, monks, that a womb-dweller may be given the higher ordination.”

### 63. Upasampadāvidhi ^63

> [!TIP]- Links to [[mv1-brahmali-pali#^63|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch14|BMC Chapter 14]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-MV1.63" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


63.The Procedure for Higher Ordination

125. Tena kho pana samayena upasampannā dissanti kuṭṭhikāpi gaṇḍikāpi kilāsikāpi sosikāpi apamārikāpi. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, upasampādentena terasa [tassa (ka.)] antarāyike dhamme pucchituṃ. Evañca pana, bhikkhave, pucchitabbo – ‘‘santi te evarūpā ābādhā – kuṭṭhaṃ, gaṇḍo, kilāso, soso, apamāro? Manussosi? Purisosi? Bhujissosi? Aṇaṇosi? Nasi rājabhaṭo? Anuññātosi mātāpitūhi? Paripuṇṇavīsativassosi? Paripuṇṇaṃ te pattacīvaraṃ? Kiṃnāmosi? Konāmo te upajjhāyo’’ti?

125.Now at that time, monks who had received the higher ordination were seen to be suffering from leprosy, boils, skin disease, consumption, and epilepsy. They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “I allow, monks, that the one giving the higher ordination may ask about the thirteen obstructive factors. And, monks, he should be asked in this way: ‘Do you have such diseases as leprosy, boils, skin disease, consumption, or epilepsy? Are you a human being? Are you a male? Are you free? Are you debtless? Are you not a royal servant? Are you permitted by your parents? Are you fully twenty years of age? Are your bowl and robes complete? What is your name? What is the name of your preceptor?’”

Tena kho pana samayena bhikkhū ananusiṭṭhe upasampadāpekkhe antarāyike dhamme pucchanti. Upasampadāpekkhā vitthāyanti, maṅkū honti, na sakkonti vissajjetuṃ. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, paṭhamaṃ anusāsitvā pacchā antarāyike dhamme pucchitunti.

At that time, monks were questioning candidates for higher ordination about the obstructive factors without first instructing them. The candidates for higher ordination became bewildered, embarrassed, and unable to answer. They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “I allow, monks, that they should first be instructed and then questioned about the obstructive factors.”

Tattheva saṅghamajjhe anusāsanti. Upasampadāpekkhā tatheva vitthāyanti, maṅkū honti, na sakkonti vissajjetuṃ. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, ekamantaṃ anusāsitvā saṅghamajjhe antarāyike dhamme pucchituṃ. Evañca pana, bhikkhave, anusāsitabbo –

There, in the midst of the Saṅgha, they instructed them. The candidates for higher ordination became bewildered, embarrassed, and unable to answer. They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “I allow, monks, after instructing him privately, to question him in the midst of the Saṅgha about the obstructive factors. And, monks, he should be instructed in this way:

126. Paṭhamaṃ upajjhaṃ gāhāpetabbo. Upajjhaṃ gāhāpetvā pattacīvaraṃ ācikkhitabbaṃ – ayaṃ te patto, ayaṃ saṅghāṭi, ayaṃ uttarāsaṅgo, ayaṃ antaravāsako. Gaccha, amumhi okāse tiṭṭhāhīti.

126.First, he should be made to take a preceptor. Having made him take a preceptor, his bowl and robes should be pointed out: ‘This is your bowl, this is the outer robe, this is the upper robe, this is the lower robe. Go, stand in that place.’

Bālā abyattā anusāsanti. Duranusiṭṭhā upasampadāpekkhā vitthāyanti, maṅkū honti, na sakkonti vissajjetuṃ. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Na, bhikkhave, bālena abyattena anusāsitabbo. Yo anusāseyya, āpatti dukkaṭassa. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, byattena bhikkhunā paṭibalena anusāsitunti.

Fools and the incompetent instructed. Poorly instructed, the candidates for higher ordination became bewildered, embarrassed, and unable to answer. They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, a fool or an incompetent person should not instruct. Whoever instructs incurs an offense of wrong-doing. I allow, monks, that a competent and capable monk should instruct.”

Asammatā anusāsanti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Na, bhikkhave, asammatena anusāsitabbo. Yo anusāseyya, āpatti dukkaṭassa. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, sammatena anusāsituṃ. Evañca pana, bhikkhave, sammannitabbo [sammanitabbo (ka.)] – attanā vā [attanāva (syā.)] attānaṃ sammannitabbaṃ, parena vā paro sammannitabbo.

Unauthorized persons instructed. They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, an unauthorized person should not instruct. Whoever instructs incurs an offense of wrong-doing. I allow, monks, that an authorized person should instruct. And, monks, authorization should be conferred in this way: either one authorizes oneself, or another authorizes another.”

Kathañca attanāva attānaṃ sammannitabbaṃ? Byattena bhikkhunā paṭibalena saṅgho ñāpetabbo – ‘‘suṇātu me, bhante, saṅgho. Itthannāmo itthannāmassa āyasmato upasampadāpekkho. Yadi saṅghassa pattakallaṃ, ahaṃ itthannāmaṃ anusāseyya’’nti. Evaṃ attanāva attānaṃ sammannitabbaṃ.

And how is one to authorize oneself? A competent and capable monk should inform the Saṅgha: “Venerable sirs, may the Saṅgha hear me. So-and-so is a candidate for higher ordination under the Venerable So-and-so. If it is agreeable to the Saṅgha, I would instruct So-and-so.” In this way, one authorizes oneself.

Kathañca pana parena paro sammannitabbo? Byattena bhikkhunā paṭibalena saṅgho ñāpetabbo – ‘‘suṇātu me, bhante, saṅgho. Itthannāmo itthannāmassa āyasmato upasampadāpekkho. Yadi saṅghassa pattakallaṃ, itthannāmo itthannāmaṃ anusāseyyā’’ti. Evaṃ parena paro sammannitabbo.

And how is another to be authorized by another? A competent and capable monk should inform the Saṅgha: “Venerable sirs, may the Saṅgha hear me. So-and-so is a candidate for higher ordination under the Venerable So-and-so. If it is agreeable to the Saṅgha, So-and-so would instruct So-and-so.” In this way, another is authorized by another.

Tena sammatena bhikkhunā upasampadāpekkho upasaṅkamitvā evamassa vacanīyo – ‘‘suṇasi, itthannāma, ayaṃ te saccakālo bhūtakālo. Yaṃ jātaṃ taṃ saṅghamajjhe pucchante santaṃ atthīti vattabbaṃ, asantaṃ natthī’’ti vattabbaṃ. Mā kho vitthāyi, mā kho maṅku ahosi. Evaṃ taṃ pucchissanti – ‘‘santi te evarūpā ābādhā – kuṭṭhaṃ, gaṇḍo, kilāso, soso, apamāro? Manussosi? Purisosi? Bhujissosi? Aṇaṇosi? Nasi rājabhaṭo? Anuññātosi mātāpitūhi? Paripuṇṇavīsativassosi? Paripuṇṇaṃ te pattacīvaraṃ? Kiṃnāmosi? Konāmo te upajjhāyo’’ti?

The authorized monk should approach the candidate for higher ordination and say to him: ‘Listen, So-and-so, this is your time for truth, your time for what is real. When asked in the midst of the Saṅgha about what exists, you should say, “It exists”; about what does not exist, you should say, “It does not exist.” Do not be bewildered, do not be embarrassed. They will ask you: “Do you have any such diseases—leprosy, boils, skin disease, consumption, or epilepsy? Are you a human being? Are you a male? Are you free? Are you debtless? Are you not a royal servant? Are you permitted by your parents? Are you fully twenty years of age? Are your bowl and robes complete? What is your name? What is the name of your preceptor?”’

Ekato āgacchanti. Na, bhikkhave, ekato āgantabbaṃ. Anusāsakena paṭhamataraṃ āgantvā saṅgho ñāpetabbo – ‘‘suṇātu me, bhante, saṅgho. Itthannāmo itthannāmassa āyasmato upasampadāpekkho. Anusiṭṭho so mayā. Yadi saṅghassa pattakallaṃ, itthannāmo āgaccheyyā’’ti. Āgacchāhīti vattabbo.

They arrived together. “Monks, they should not come together. The instructor should come earlier and inform the Saṅgha: ‘Venerable sirs, may the Saṅgha hear me. So-and-so is a candidate for higher ordination under the Venerable So-and-so. I have instructed him. If it is agreeable to the Saṅgha, So-and-so may come.’ He should be told: ‘Come!’”

Ekaṃsaṃ uttarāsaṅgaṃ kārāpetvā bhikkhūnaṃ pāde vandāpetvā ukkuṭikaṃ nisīdāpetvā añjaliṃ paggaṇhāpetvā upasampadaṃ yācāpetabbo – ‘‘saṅghaṃ, bhante, upasampadaṃ yācāmi. Ullumpatu maṃ, bhante, saṅgho anukampaṃ upādāya. Dutiyampi, bhante, saṅghaṃ upasampadaṃ yācāmi. Ullumpatu maṃ, bhante, saṅgho anukampaṃ upādāya. Tatiyampi, bhante, saṅghaṃ upasampadaṃ yācāmi. Ullumpatu maṃ, bhante, saṅgho anukampaṃ upādāyā’’ti. Byattena bhikkhunā paṭibalena saṅgho ñāpetabbo –

Having had him arrange his upper robe over one shoulder, had him worship the monks’ feet, had him sit in a squatting position, and had him raise his hands in añjali, he should be made to request the higher ordination: ‘Venerable sirs, I request the Saṅgha for the higher ordination. Lift me up, venerable sirs, out of compassion. For the second time, venerable sirs, I request the Saṅgha for the higher ordination. Lift me up, venerable sirs, out of compassion. For the third time, venerable sirs, I request the Saṅgha for the higher ordination. Lift me up, venerable sirs, out of compassion.’ Then a competent and capable monk should inform the Saṅgha:

‘‘Suṇātu me, bhante, saṅgho. Ayaṃ itthannāmo itthannāmassa āyasmato upasampadāpekkho. Yadi saṅghassa pattakallaṃ, ahaṃ itthannāmaṃ antarāyike dhamme puccheyya’’nti? Suṇasi, itthannāma, ayaṃ te saccakālo bhūtakālo. Yaṃ jātaṃ taṃ pucchāmi. Santaṃ atthīti vattabbaṃ, asantaṃ natthīti vattabbaṃ. Santi te evarūpā ābādhā – kuṭṭhaṃ gaṇḍo kileso soso apamāro, manussosi, purisosi, bhujissosi, aṇaṇosi, nasi rājabhaṭo, anuññātosi mātāpitūhi, paripuṇṇavīsativassosi, paripuṇṇaṃ te pattacīvaraṃ, kiṃnāmosi, konāmo te upajjhāyoti? Byattena bhikkhunā paṭibalena saṅgho ñāpetabbo –

“Venerable sirs, may the Saṅgha hear me. This So-and-so is a candidate for higher ordination under the Venerable So-and-so. If it is agreeable to the Saṅgha, I would question So-and-so about the obstructive factors.” “Do you hear, So-and-so? This is your time for truth, your time for what is real. I will ask you about what exists. If it exists, you should say, ‘It exists’; if it does not exist, you should say, ‘It does not exist.’ Do you have any of these diseases—leprosy, boils, skin disease, consumption, epilepsy? Are you a human being? Are you a male? Are you free? Are you debtless? Are you not a royal servant? Are you permitted by your parents? Are you fully twenty years of age? Are your bowl and robes complete? What is your name? What is the name of your preceptor?” A competent and capable monk should inform the Saṅgha:

127. ‘‘Suṇātu me, bhante, saṅgho. Ayaṃ itthannāmo itthannāmassa āyasmato upasampadāpekkho, parisuddho antarāyikehi dhammehi, paripuṇṇassa pattacīvaraṃ. Itthannāmo saṅghaṃ upasampadaṃ yācati itthannāmena upajjhāyena. Yadi saṅghassa pattakallaṃ, saṅgho itthannāmaṃ upasampādeyya itthannāmena upajjhāyena. Esā ñatti.

127.“Venerable sirs, may the Saṅgha hear me. This So-and-so is a candidate for higher ordination under the Venerable So-and-so, is purified of the obstructive factors, and his bowl and robes are complete. So-and-so requests higher ordination from the Saṅgha with So-and-so as preceptor. If it is agreeable to the Saṅgha, the Saṅgha would confer higher ordination on So-and-so with So-and-so as preceptor. This is the motion.”

‘‘Suṇātu me, bhante, saṅgho. Ayaṃ itthannāmo itthannāmassa āyasmato upasampadāpekkho, parisuddho antarāyikehi dhammehi, paripuṇṇassa pattacīvaraṃ. Itthannāmo saṅghaṃ upasampadaṃ yācati itthannāmena upajjhāyena. Saṅgho itthannāmaṃ upasampādeti itthannāmena upajjhāyena. Yassāyasmato khamati itthannāmassa upasampadā itthannāmena upajjhāyena, so tuṇhassa; yassa nakkhamati, so bhāseyya.

“Venerable sirs, may the Saṅgha hear me. This So-and-so is a candidate for higher ordination under the Venerable So-and-so, is purified of the obstructive factors, and his bowl and robes are complete. So-and-so requests higher ordination from the Saṅgha with So-and-so as preceptor. The Saṅgha confers higher ordination on So-and-so with So-and-so as preceptor. If the higher ordination of So-and-so with So-and-so as preceptor is agreeable to any venerable one, he should be silent; if not, he should speak.”

‘‘Dutiyampi etamatthaṃ vadāmi – suṇātu me, bhante, saṅgho. Ayaṃ itthannāmo itthannāmassa āyasmato upasampadāpekkho, parisuddho antarāyikehi dhammehi, paripuṇṇassa pattacīvaraṃ. Itthannāmo saṅghaṃ upasampadaṃ yācati itthannāmena upajjhāyena. Saṅgho itthannāmaṃ upasampādeti itthannāmena upajjhāyena. Yassāyasmato khamati itthannāmassa upasampadā itthannāmena upajjhāyena, so tuṇhassa; yassa nakkhamati, so bhāseyya.

For the second time, I speak on this matter: May the Sangha, Venerable Sirs, listen to me. This person, named so-and-so, is an aspirant for higher ordination under the Venerable so-and-so; he is purified of obstructive qualities, and his bowl and robes are complete. So-and-so requests higher ordination from the Sangha with so-and-so as preceptor. The Sangha confers higher ordination upon so-and-so with so-and-so as preceptor. Any venerable one who approves of the higher ordination of so-and-so with so-and-so as preceptor should remain silent; any who does not approve should speak.

‘‘Tatiyampi etamatthaṃ vadāmi – suṇātu me, bhante, saṅgho. Ayaṃ itthannāmo itthannāmassa āyasmato upasampadāpekkho, parisuddho antarāyikehi dhammehi, paripuṇṇassa pattacīvaraṃ. Itthannāmo saṅghaṃ upasampadaṃ yācati itthannāmena upajjhāyena. Saṅgho itthannāmaṃ upasampādeti itthannāmena upajjhāyena. Yassāyasmato khamati itthannāmassa upasampadā itthannāmena upajjhāyena, so tuṇhassa; yassa nakkhamati, so bhāseyya.

For the third time, I speak on this matter: May the Sangha, Venerable Sirs, listen to me. This person, named so-and-so, is an aspirant for higher ordination under the Venerable so-and-so; he is purified of obstructive qualities, and his bowl and robes are complete. So-and-so requests higher ordination from the Sangha with so-and-so as preceptor. The Sangha confers higher ordination upon so-and-so with so-and-so as preceptor. Any venerable one who approves of the higher ordination of so-and-so with so-and-so as preceptor should remain silent; any who does not approve should speak.

‘‘Upasampanno saṅghena itthannāmo itthannāmena upajjhāyena. Khamati saṅghassa, tasmā tuṇhī, evametaṃ dhārayāmī’’ti.

So-and-so has received higher ordination from the Sangha with so-and-so as preceptor. The Sangha approves of this, and therefore it is silent. Thus I record it.

Upasampadākammaṃ niṭṭhitaṃ.

The higher ordination procedure is concluded.

### 64. Cattāro nissayā ^64

> [!TIP]- Links to [[mv1-brahmali-pali#^64|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch14|BMC Chapter 14]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-MV1.64" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


64.The Four Supports

128. Tāvadeva chāyā metabbā, utuppamāṇaṃ ācikkhitabbaṃ, divasabhāgo ācikkhitabbo, saṅgīti ācikkhitabbā, cattāro nissayā ācikkhitabbā [ācikkhitabbā, cattāri akaraṇīyāni ācikkhitabbāni. (ka.)] –

128.Immediately after, the shadow should be measured, the season should be announced, the division of the day should be announced, the instruction regarding the gains should be announced, and the four supports should be announced.

‘‘Piṇḍiyālopabhojanaṃ nissāya pabbajjā. Tattha te yāvajīvaṃ ussāho karaṇīyo. Atirekalābho – saṅghabhattaṃ, uddesabhattaṃ, nimantanaṃ, salākabhattaṃ, pakkhikaṃ, uposathikaṃ, pāṭipadikaṃ.

The going forth is dependent on almsfood. In this, you should strive for as long as you live. Extra gains are: community meals, designated meals, invitations, ticket meals, fortnightly meals, Uposatha meals, and first-day-of-the-month meals.

‘‘Paṃsukūlacīvaraṃ nissāya pabbajjā. Tattha te yāvajīvaṃ ussāho karaṇīyo. Atirekalābho – khomaṃ, kappāsikaṃ, koseyyaṃ, kambalaṃ, sāṇaṃ, bhaṅgaṃ.

The going forth is dependent on robes made of rags. In this, you should strive for as long as you live. Extra gains are: linen, cotton, silk, wool, coarse cloth, and hemp.

‘‘Rukkhamūlasenāsanaṃ nissāya pabbajjā. Tattha te yāvajīvaṃ ussāho karaṇīyo. Atirekalābho – vihāro, aḍḍhayogo, pāsādo, hammiyaṃ, guhā.

The going forth is dependent on lodging at the root of a tree. In this, you should strive for as long as you live. Extra gains are: a monastery, an attic, a palatial building, a mansion, and a cave.

‘‘Pūtimuttabhesajjaṃ nissāya pabbajjā. Tattha te yāvajīvaṃ ussāho karaṇīyo. Atirekalābho – sappi, navanītaṃ, telaṃ, madhu, phāṇita’’nti.

The going forth is dependent on putrid urine as medicine. In this, you should strive for as long as you live. Extra gains are: ghee, fresh butter, oil, honey, and molasses.

Cattāro nissayā niṭṭhitā.

The four supports are concluded.

### 65. Cattāri akaraṇīyāni ^65

> [!TIP]- Links to [[mv1-brahmali-pali#^65|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch14|BMC Chapter 14]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-MV1.65" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


65.Four Things Not to Be Done

129. Tena kho pana samayena bhikkhū aññataraṃ bhikkhuṃ upasampādetvā ekakaṃ ohāya pakkamiṃsu. So pacchā ekakova āgacchanto antarāmagge purāṇadutiyikāya samāgañchi. Sā evamāha – ‘‘kiṃdāni pabbajitosī’’ti? ‘‘Āma, pabbajitomhī’’ti. ‘‘Dullabho kho pabbajitānaṃ methuno dhammo; ehi, methunaṃ dhammaṃ paṭisevā’’ti. So tassā methunaṃ dhammaṃ paṭisevitvā cirena agamāsi. Bhikkhū evamāhaṃsu – ‘‘kissa tvaṃ, āvuso, evaṃ ciraṃ akāsī’’ti? Atha kho so bhikkhu bhikkhūnaṃ etamatthaṃ ārocesi. Bhikkhū bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, upasampādetvā dutiyaṃ dātuṃ, cattāri ca akaraṇīyāni ācikkhituṃ –

129.Now at that time, some bhikkhus, having given higher ordination to a certain bhikkhu, left him alone and departed. Later, as he was returning alone, he met his former female companion on the way. She said to him: 'Have you now gone forth?' 'Yes, I have gone forth.' 'Sexual intercourse is indeed difficult to obtain for those gone forth. Come, let us engage in sexual intercourse.' He engaged in sexual intercourse with her and arrived after a long time. The bhikkhus asked him: 'Friend, why have you been so long?' Then that bhikkhu told the bhikkhus about this matter. The bhikkhus told the Blessed One about this matter. 'Bhikkhus, I allow that after higher ordination, a second [bhikkhu] should be given [as a companion], and the four prohibitions should be taught.'

‘‘Upasampannena bhikkhunā methuno dhammo na paṭisevitabbo, antamaso tiracchānagatāyapi. Yo bhikkhu methunaṃ dhammaṃ paṭisevati, assamaṇo hoti asakyaputtiyo. Seyyathāpi nāma puriso sīsacchinno abhabbo tena sarīrabandhanena jīvituṃ, evameva bhikkhu methunaṃ dhammaṃ paṭisevitvā assamaṇo hoti asakyaputtiyo. Taṃ te yāvajīvaṃ akaraṇīyaṃ.

A bhikkhu who has received higher ordination should not engage in sexual intercourse, even with an animal. Any bhikkhu who engages in sexual intercourse is no longer a recluse, no longer a son of the Sakyan. Just as a person whose head has been cut off is unable to live with that body, so too a bhikkhu who engages in sexual intercourse is no longer a recluse, no longer a son of the Sakyan. This is a prohibition for you for as long as you live.

‘‘Upasampannena bhikkhunā adinnaṃ theyyasaṅkhātaṃ na ādātabbaṃ, antamaso tiṇasalākaṃ upādāya. Yo bhikkhu pādaṃ vā pādārahaṃ vā atirekapādaṃ vā adinnaṃ theyyasaṅkhātaṃ ādiyati, assamaṇo hoti asakyaputtiyo. Seyyathāpi nāma paṇḍupalāso bandhanā pamutto abhabbo haritatthāya, evameva bhikkhu pādaṃ vā pādārahaṃ vā atirekapādaṃ vā adinnaṃ theyyasaṅkhātaṃ ādiyitvā assamaṇo hoti asakyaputtiyo. Taṃ te yāvajīvaṃ akaraṇīyaṃ.

A bhikkhu who has received higher ordination should not take what is not given, with the intention of theft, not even so much as a blade of grass. Any bhikkhu who takes what is not given, with the intention of theft—whether worth a pāda, worth what deserves a pāda, or more than a pāda—is no longer a recluse, no longer a son of the Sakyan. Just as a yellow leaf fallen from its stalk is incapable of becoming green again, so too a bhikkhu who takes what is not given, with the intention of theft—whether worth a pāda, worth what deserves a pāda, or more than a pāda—is no longer a recluse, no longer a son of the Sakyan. This is a prohibition for you for as long as you live.

‘‘Upasampannena bhikkhunā sañcicca pāṇo jīvitā na voropetabbo, antamaso kunthakipillikaṃ upādāya. Yo bhikkhu sañcicca manussaviggahaṃ jīvitā voropeti, antamaso gabbhapātanaṃ upādāya, assamaṇo hoti asakyaputtiyo. Seyyathāpi nāma puthusilā dvedhā bhinnā appaṭisandhikā hoti, evameva bhikkhu sañcicca manussaviggahaṃ jīvitā voropetvā assamaṇo hoti asakyaputtiyo. Taṃ te yāvajīvaṃ akaraṇīyaṃ.

A bhikkhu who has received higher ordination should not intentionally deprive a living being of life, even so much as a worm or an ant. Any bhikkhu who intentionally deprives a human being of life, even by causing an abortion, is no longer a recluse, no longer a son of the Sakyan. Just as a large rock split in two cannot be rejoined, so too a bhikkhu who intentionally deprives a human being of life is no longer a recluse, no longer a son of the Sakyan. This is a prohibition for you for as long as you live.

‘‘Upasampannena bhikkhunā uttarimanussadhammo na ullapitabbo, antamaso ‘suññāgāre abhiramāmī’ti. Yo bhikkhu pāpiccho icchāpakato asantaṃ abhūtaṃ uttarimanussadhammaṃ ullapati jhānaṃ vā vimokkhaṃ vā samādhiṃ vā samāpattiṃ vā maggaṃ vā phalaṃ vā, assamaṇo hoti asakyaputtiyo. Seyyathāpi nāma tālo matthakacchinno abhabbo puna viruḷhiyā, evameva bhikkhu pāpiccho icchāpakato asantaṃ abhūtaṃ uttarimanussadhammaṃ ullapitvā assamaṇo hoti asakyaputtiyo. Taṃ te yāvajīvaṃ akaraṇīya’’nti.

A bhikkhu who has received higher ordination should not boast of a superhuman state (uttarimanussadhammo), even by saying, ‘I delight in an empty dwelling.’ Any bhikkhu who, wishing for evil and overcome by desires, falsely claims a superhuman state that is not and does not exist—such as jhāna, liberation, concentration, attainment, path, or fruition—is no longer a recluse, no longer a son of the Sakyan. Just as a palm tree whose crown has been cut off is incapable of growing again, so too a bhikkhu who, wishing for evil and overcome by desires, falsely claims a superhuman state that is not and does not exist, is no longer a recluse, no longer a son of the Sakyan. This is a prohibition for you for as long as you live.

Cattāri akaraṇīyāni niṭṭhitāni.

The four prohibitions are concluded.

### 66. Āpattiyā adassane ukkhittakavatthūni ^66

> [!TIP]- Links to [[mv1-brahmali-pali#^66|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch14|BMC Chapter 14]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-MV1.66" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


66.The grounds for suspension for not acknowledging an offense.

130. Tena kho pana samayena aññataro bhikkhu āpattiyā adassane ukkhittako vibbhami. So puna paccāgantvā bhikkhū upasampadaṃ yāci. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ.

130.At that time, a certain monk who had been suspended for not acknowledging an offense strayed. Later, he returned and asked the monks for full ordination. They reported the matter to the Blessed One.

Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu āpattiyā adassane ukkhittako vibbhamati. So puna paccāgantvā bhikkhū upasampadaṃ yācati. So evamassa vacanīyo – ‘‘passissasi taṃ āpatti’’nti? Sacāhaṃ passissāmīti, pabbājetabbo. Sacāhaṃ na passissāmīti, na pabbājetabbo. Pabbājetvā vattabbo – ‘‘passissasi taṃ āpatti’’nti? Sacāhaṃ passissāmīti, upasampādetabbo. Sacāhaṃ na passissāmīti, na upasampādetabbo. Upasampādetvā vattabbo – ‘‘passissasi taṃ āpatti’’nti? Sacāhaṃ passissāmīti, osāretabbo. Sacāhaṃ na passissāmīti, na osāretabbo. Osāretvā vattabbo – ‘‘passasi [passāhi (sī.)] taṃ āpatti’’nti? Sace passati, iccetaṃ kusalaṃ. No ce passati, labbhamānāya sāmaggiyā puna ukkhipitabbo. Alabbhamānāya sāmaggiyā anāpatti sambhoge saṃvāse.

Here, monks, a monk who has been suspended for not seeing an offense wanders about. Later, he returns and asks the monks for full ordination. He should be told, ‘Will you see that offense?’ If he says, ‘I will see it,’ he should be given the going forth. If he says, ‘I will not see it,’ he should not be given the going forth. After giving him the going forth, he should be told, ‘Will you see that offense?’ If he says, ‘I will see it,’ he should be given full ordination. If he says, ‘I will not see it,’ he should not be given full ordination. After giving him full ordination, he should be told, ‘Will you see that offense?’ If he says, ‘I will see it,’ he should be reinstated. If he says, ‘I will not see it,’ he should not be reinstated. After reinstating him, he should be told, ‘Do you see that offense?’ If he sees it, that is skillful. If he does not see it, if the Saṅgha is in harmony, he should be suspended again. If the Saṅgha is not in harmony, there is no offense in communal living and association.

Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu āpattiyā appaṭikamme ukkhittako vibbhamati. So puna paccāgantvā bhikkhū upasampadaṃ yācati. So evamassa vacanīyo – ‘‘paṭikarissasi taṃ āpatti’’nti? Sacāhaṃ paṭikarissāmīti, pabbājetabbo. Sacāhaṃ na paṭikarissāmīti, na pabbājetabbo. Pabbājetvā vattabbo – ‘‘paṭikarissasi taṃ āpatti’’nti? Sacāhaṃ paṭikarissāmīti, upasampādetabbo. Sacāhaṃ na paṭikarissāmīti, na upasampādetabbo. Upasampādetvā vattabbo – ‘‘paṭikarissasi taṃ āpatti’’nti? Sacāhaṃ paṭikarissāmīti, osāretabbo. Sacāhaṃ na paṭikarissāmīti, na osāretabbo. Osāretvā vattabbo – ‘‘paṭikarohi taṃ āpatti’’nti. Sace paṭikaroti, iccetaṃ kusalaṃ. No ce paṭikaroti labbhamānāya sāmaggiyā puna ukkhipitabbo. Alabbhamānāya sāmaggiyā anāpatti sambhoge saṃvāse.

Here, monks, a monk who has been suspended for not making amends for an offense wanders about. Later, he returns and asks the monks for full ordination. He should be told, ‘Will you make amends for that offense?’ If he says, ‘I will make amends,’ he should be given the going forth. If he says, ‘I will not make amends,’ he should not be given the going forth. After giving him the going forth, he should be told, ‘Will you make amends for that offense?’ If he says, ‘I will make amends,’ he should be given full ordination. If he says, ‘I will not make amends,’ he should not be given full ordination. After giving him full ordination, he should be told, ‘Will you make amends for that offense?’ If he says, ‘I will make amends,’ he should be reinstated. If he says, ‘I will not make amends,’ he should not be reinstated. After reinstating him, he should be told, ‘Make amends for that offense.’ If he makes amends, that is skillful. If he does not make amends, if the Saṅgha is in harmony, he should be suspended again. If the Saṅgha is not in harmony, there is no offense in communal living and association.

Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā appaṭinissagge ukkhittako vibbhamati. So puna paccāgantvā bhikkhū upasampadaṃ yācati. So evamassa vacanīyo – ‘‘paṭinissajjissasi taṃ pāpikaṃ diṭṭhi’’nti? Sacāhaṃ paṭinissajjissāmīti, pabbājetabbo. Sacāhaṃ na paṭinissajjissāmīti, na pabbājetabbo. Pabbājetvā vattabbo – ‘‘paṭinissajjissasi taṃ pāpikaṃ diṭṭhi’’nti? Sacāhaṃ paṭinissajjissāmīti, upasampādetabbo. Sacāhaṃ na paṭinissajjissāmīti, na upasampādetabbo. Upasampādetvā vattabbo – ‘‘paṭinissajjissasi taṃ pāpikaṃ diṭṭhi’’nti? Sacāhaṃ paṭinissajjissāmīti, osāretabbo. Sacāhaṃ na paṭinissajjissāmīti, na osāretabbo. Osāretvā vattabbo – ‘‘paṭinissajjehi taṃ pāpikaṃ diṭṭhi’’nti. Sace paṭinissajjati, iccetaṃ kusalaṃ. No ce paṭinissajjati, labbhamānāya sāmaggiyā puna ukkhipitabbo. Alabbhamānāya sāmaggiyā anāpatti sambhoge saṃvāseti.

Here, monks, a monk who has been suspended for not giving up a wrong view wanders about. Later, he returns and asks the monks for full ordination. He should be told, ‘Will you give up that wrong view?’ If he says, ‘I will give it up,’ he should be given the going forth. If he says, ‘I will not give it up,’ he should not be given the going forth. After giving him the going forth, he should be told, ‘Will you give up that wrong view?’ If he says, ‘I will give it up,’ he should be given full ordination. If he says, ‘I will not give it up,’ he should not be given full ordination. After giving him full ordination, he should be told, ‘Will you give up that wrong view?’ If he says, ‘I will give it up,’ he should be reinstated. If he says, ‘I will not give it up,’ he should not be reinstated. After reinstating him, he should be told, ‘Give up that wrong view.’ If he gives it up, that is skillful. If he does not give it up, if the Saṅgha is in harmony, he should be suspended again. If the Saṅgha is not in harmony, there is no offense in communal living and association.

Mahākhandhako paṭhamo.

The Great Section, the First.

### 67. Tassuddānaṃ ^67

> [!TIP]- Links to [[mv1-brahmali-pali#^67|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch14|BMC Chapter 14]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-MV1.67" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


67.Summary

131.

Vinayamhi mahatthesu, pesalānaṃ sukhāvahe;Niggahānañca pāpicche, lajjīnaṃ paggahesu ca.

In the Vinaya, for those of great purpose, for the virtuous, bringing welfare; and for restraining those with evil wishes, and for supporting the conscientious.

Sāsanādhāraṇe ceva, sabbaññujinagocare;Anaññavisaye kheme, supaññatte asaṃsaye.

And in upholding the Dispensation, in the domain of the All-knowing Conqueror; in the secure realm with no other object, in the well-proclaimed, free from doubt.

Khandhake vinaye ceva, parivāre ca mātike;Yathātthakārī kusalo, paṭipajjati yoniso.

In the Khandhakas, in the Vinaya, and in the Parivāra and the Mātikā; skillfully acting in accordance with the meaning, one proceeds systematically.

Yo gavaṃ na vijānāti, na so rakkhati gogaṇaṃ;Evaṃ sīlaṃ ajānanto, kiṃ so rakkheyya saṃvaraṃ.

One who does not understand cows does not protect the herd; so too, one who does not understand virtue, how can they guard restraint?

Pamuṭṭhamhi ca suttante, abhidhamme ca tāvade;Vinaye avinaṭṭhamhi, puna tiṭṭhati sāsanaṃ.

When the Suttantas are forgotten, and likewise the Abhidhamma, but when the Vinaya is not lost, the Dispensation stands again.

Tasmā saṅgāhaṇāhetuṃ [saṅgāhanāhetuṃ (ka.)], uddānaṃ anupubbaso;Pavakkhāmi yathāñāyaṃ, suṇātha mama bhāsato.

Therefore, for the sake of compilation, I will declare the summary in due order according to the proper method; listen to me as I speak.

Vatthu nidānaṃ āpatti, nayā peyyālameva ca;Dukkaraṃ taṃ asesetuṃ, nayato taṃ vijānathāti.

The basis, the cause, the offense, the methods, and the abbreviated forms as well; it is difficult to exhaust them all, know them by the method.

Bodhi rājāyatanañca, ajapālo sahampati;Brahmā āḷāro udako, bhikkhu ca upako isi.

The Bodhi tree, the Rājāyatana tree, the goatherd, Sahampati Brahmā; Brahmā, Āḷāra, Uddaka, and the monk Upaka, the seer.

Koṇḍañño vappo bhaddiyo, mahānāmo ca assaji;Yaso cattāro paññāsa, sabbe pesesi so disā.

Koṇḍañña, Vappa, Bhaddiya, Mahānāma, and Assaji; and Yasa with his fifty-four companions – all these he sent in different directions.

Vatthu mārehi tiṃsā ca, uruvelaṃ tayo jaṭī;Agyāgāraṃ mahārājā, sakko brahmā ca kevalā.

The incident, thirty with Māra, Uruvelā, the three matted-hair ascetics; the fire hall, the great king, Sakka, and Brahmā, entirely.

Paṃsukūlaṃ pokkharaṇī, silā ca kakudho silā;Jambu ambo ca āmalo, pāripupphañca āhari.

The rag-robe, the lotus pond, and the stone, and the hump on the stone; the rose apple, the mango, and the emblic myrobalan, and the coral tree flower were brought.

Phāliyantu ujjalantu, vijjhāyantu ca kassapa;Nimujjanti mukhī megho, gayā laṭṭhi ca māgadho.

May they split, may they blaze, and may they be extinguished, O Kassapa; faces sink, the cloud, and the Gayā staff, and the Magadhan.

Upatisso kolito ca, abhiññātā ca pabbajuṃ;Dunnivatthā paṇāmanā, kiso lūkho ca brāhmaṇo.

Upatissa and Kolita, well-known, went forth; poorly clad, paying homage, lean and rough was the brahmin.

Anācāraṃ ācarati, udaraṃ māṇavo gaṇo;Vassaṃ bālehi pakkanto, dasa vassāni nissayo.

He behaves improperly, the group of boys with swollen bellies; the rains residence was abandoned by the fools, a dependence of ten years.

Na vattanti paṇāmetuṃ, bālā passaddhi pañca cha;Yo so añño ca naggo ca, acchinnajaṭilasākiyo.

They do not succeed in dismissing, the fools, tranquility, five, six; that other one, naked, and the uncut matted-hair Sakyan.

Magadhesu pañcābādhā, eko rājā [bhaṭo coro (syā.)] ca aṅguli;Māgadho ca anuññāsi, kārā likhi kasāhato.

Among the Magadhans, five diseases, one king, and Anguli; and the Magadhan permitted, the prison, the writing, the one struck by a whip.

Lakkhaṇā iṇā dāso ca, bhaṇḍuko upāli ahi;Saddhaṃ kulaṃ kaṇṭako ca, āhundarikameva ca.

The marks, debt, and a slave, Bhaṇḍuka, Upāli, a snake; a faithful family, and a thorn, and a container of ghee.

Vatthumhi dārako sikkhā, viharanti ca kiṃ nu kho;Sabbaṃ mukhaṃ upajjhāye, apalāḷana kaṇṭako.

The boy in the story, the training, and what do they dwell upon? All the mouth belongs to the preceptor; the thorn of not pampering.

Paṇḍako theyyapakkanto, ahi ca mātarī pitā;Arahantabhikkhunībhedā, ruhirena ca byañjanaṃ.

The eunuch, the thief who went forth, and a snake, mother, father; the schism of an arahant bhikkhuni, and the mark with blood.

Anupajjhāyasaṅghena, gaṇapaṇḍakapattako;Acīvaraṃ tadubhayaṃ, yācitenapi ye tayo.

By the Sangha without a preceptor, the group, the eunuch, the bowl; without robes, those two, and those three who begged.

Hatthā pādā hatthapādā, kaṇṇā nāsā tadūbhayaṃ;Aṅguliaḷakaṇḍaraṃ, phaṇaṃ khujjañca vāmanaṃ.

Hands, feet, hands and feet, ears, noses, and both; fingers, teeth, the neck, the crest, the hunchback, and the dwarf.

Galagaṇḍī lakkhaṇā ceva, kasā likhitasīpadī;Pāpaparisadūsī ca, kāṇaṃ kuṇi tatheva ca.

The goiter, and the marks, the whip-scarred, the elephant-footed; and the defiler of the evil assembly, the one-eyed, the crippled, and likewise.

Khañjaṃ pakkhahatañceva, sacchinnairiyāpathaṃ;Jarāndhamūgabadhiraṃ, andhamūgañca yaṃ tahiṃ.

The lame, and the one with a paralyzed side, the one with impaired movement; the aged, the blind, the mute, the deaf, and the blind and mute, which is there.

Andhabadhiraṃ yaṃ vuttaṃ, mūgabadhirameva ca;Andhamūgabadhirañca, alajjīnañca nissayaṃ.

The blind and deaf, as was said, and the mute and deaf as well; and the blind, mute, and deaf, and the dependence on the shameless.

Vatthabbañca tathāddhānaṃ, yācamānena lakkhaṇā [pekkhanā (sabbattha)];Āgacchatu vivadanti, ekupajjhāyena kassapo.

And what should be dwelt upon, likewise the duration; the marks being requested, let him come, they dispute, Kassapa with one preceptor.

Dissanti upasampannā, ābādhehi ca pīḷitā;Ananusiṭṭhā vitthenti, tattheva anusāsanā.

They are seen, fully ordained, and afflicted by illnesses; uninstructed, they wander; and there is instruction.

Saṅghepi ca atho bālā, asammatā ca ekato;Ullumpatupasampadā, nissayo ekako tayoti.

And in the Sangha too, then, fools, and those not agreed upon, and alone; lifting up, full ordination, dependence, one, three.

Imamhi khandhake vatthūni ekasatañca dvāsattati.

In this Khandhaka, there are one hundred and seventy-two topics.

Mahākhandhako niṭṭhito.

The Mahākhandhaka is concluded.
